#THE BOOK OF JUDGES & RUTH

The book of Judges is the seventh book in the [King James]{.class-1} Bible and the second of the "historical" books. In the Hebrew Bible, it is part of the [Nabhim,]{.class-1} what Christ called ["the prophets"]{.class-0} (Luke 24:44).

Judges covers the history of Israel after the death of Joshua to a point just before the birth of Samuel. The events of the book take place over a period of about 300 years. Ussher's chronology gives the dates from 1425--1120 B.C.

That being said, what you need to keep in mind is that the events recorded in the book are [not chronologically consecutive.]{.class-1} The first verse starts out with the death of Joshua, but in chapter 1, you have the conquest of Debir by Caleb and Othniel which was covered back in Joshua 15. In chapter 2, Joshua is alive, and his death is recorded again in verse 8. Before the first judges show up in chapter 3, the whole generation that served with Joshua in the conquest of Canaan had died out (Judg. 2:10); that included Eleazar the high priest (Josh. 24:33). But at the end of Judges, Eleazar's son Phinehas is the high priest (Judg. 20:28). Well, Phinehas didn't live to be over 300 years old, those events in chapters 17--21 took place between chapters 2 and 3.

Judges has 21 chapters, 618 verses, and 18,966 words. Unlike Genesis--Joshua, there is no indication of exactly who wrote the book. The most probable author is Samuel (1 Chron. 29:29), but there are other possible authors mentioned in Scripture. There are ["Nathan the prophet"]{.class-0} and ["Gad the seer"]{.class-0} (1 Chron. 29:29). There is ["Ahijah the Shilonite"]{.class-0} and ["Iddo the seer"]{.class-0} (2 Chron. 9:29). There is ["Shemaiah the prophet"]{.class-0} (2 Chron. 12:15). Joshua could even have written some of the material in the first two chapters (Josh. 18:9, 24:26).

But it is also altogether possible that the book is the firsthand accounts of people who lived through the events and wrote them down; those written accounts by several anonymous authors were later on collected into one book and preserved by the Levites (Mal. 2:4--7; Ezra 7:6). This is highly likely, since unlike the so-called "scriptures" of other religions (e.g., Mohammed's [Koran]{.class-1}), the Bible is the eyewitness accounts of actual, historical events (see our comments on Luke 1:2 in that Commentary). The Bible is [not]{.class-1} "supra-history"; i.e., fables and legends purporting to be history in order to teach moral lessons. Whatever "moral lessons" the Bible teaches are based on [real]{.class-1} history. So what you are about to read in the book of Judges are actual, historical events that really took place. The Bible is primarily a [history]{.class-1} book, not a "religious" book.

Something to note in regards to the authorship of the book of Judges is that whoever wrote it [never claimed to be inspired.]{.class-1} For that matter, neither did the authors of Ruth, 1 & 2 Kings, 1 & 2 Chronicles, Ecclesiastes, or Song of Solomon. The reason this is noteworthy to the Bible believer is that one of the main objections to the authority of the [Authorized Version]{.class-1} is that it could not have been ["given by inspiration of God"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 3:16) since its translators did not claim that for their work. Using such logic, one could say that Matthew, Mark, Luke, John, and Acts weren't ["given by inspiration"]{.class-0} either since the authors of those books never claimed to be "inspired."

Now the book is called "Judges" because at this time judges ruled over Israel. The key verse to the whole book is the last verse, which sums up the situation of those days.

["In those days there was no king in Israel: every man did that which was right in his own eyes"]{.class-0} (21:25).

Israel was in [total anarchy.]{.class-1} The great leaders Moses and Joshua were dead. There was no one leader over all twelve tribes who went by the Book as Joshua was commanded to do (see our remarks under Josh. 1:8 in that Commentary). And as we shall see in chapters 17--19, and in the case of Jephthah in chapter 11, the Levites were not fulfilling their God-given responsibility to teach the Law to the people (see Deut. 33:10 and our comments on Mal. 2:6--7 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class-1} Vol. II). So every Israelite was doing what he thought was right, and Paul tells us in the third chapter of Romans:

["There is none righteous, no not one: There is none that understandeth, there is none that seeketh after God. They are all gone out of the way, they are together become unprofitable; there is none that doeth good, no, not one"]{.class-0} (Rom. 3:10--12).

Apart from the written revelation of God in His word, there is no absolute standard of truth or morality (see John 17:17; 2 Pet. 1:17--20). And although God has put His law in the hearts and consciences of every man, woman, and child on earth (Rom. 2:15), ["The heart is deceitful above all things, and desperately wicked"]{.class-0} (Jer. 17:9), and man's conscience can be ["defiled"]{.class-0} (Tit. 1:15) until it is ["seared"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 4:2) to the point where it is practically dead.

That is where America is today. Having dumped the Bible for TV, radio, magazines, and newspapers, it no longer has any standard of absolute truth by which to judge anything. With no absolute standard, the standard of judgment becomes the opinions and preferences of the majority---mob rule. This eventually leads to appeasing the baser instincts of the flesh. So although you have a Constitution over this nation which was based on the Bible, the government of this country is run by men who are doing what every man thinks is ["right in his own eyes."]{.class-0} What they think is "right" is Socialism, drug use, sex perversion, jungle morals, drunkenness, fornication, pornography, jungle music, bestiality, vulgarity, and abortion.

The great theme of the book of Judges is the [Law of Human Collapse,]{.class-1} and it is just as firmly established as the Law of Gravity and the Second Law of Thermodynamics (the Law of Entropy). The Law of Human Collapse is that, left to his own machinations, "man" lapses into spiritual and moral decline. Advances in technology do not change that established fact, and in nearly all cases, they only make it worse. According to the infallible record of human history in ["the scripture of truth"]{.class-0} (Dan. 10:21), [all dispensations end in apostasy.]{.class-1}

Given a perfect environment with perfect marital relations, "man" produces [disobedience]{.class-1} (Gen. 2--3). In family relationships, he produces [envy, hatred, and murder]{.class-1} (Gen. 4). Given long life and "aid from other space," he produces [bestiality and the genocide of the human race]{.class-1} (Gen. 6--7). Given boundless property and social unity, he produces [rebellion and totalitarianism]{.class-1} (Gen. 11). Given the revealed, written Law of God to give spiritual light (Exod. 20; Deut. 4), he produces [idolatry]{.class-1} (Exod. 32) and [self-exaltation]{.class-1} (Num. 11--16). Given religious leaders (Moses, Joshua, David, Solomon, the prophets) and a complete Old Testament (Law, Prophets, and Wisdom books), he [murders God's Son at Golgotha.]{.class-1} Given a complete New Testament and over 2,000 years of "grace," he produces [a worldwide dictator who is Satan incarnate]{.class-1} and [a Tribulation which wipes out more than three billion people.]{.class-1} And finally, given 1,000 years of no Devil, of international peace and righteousness, with God in the flesh visibly on the throne at Jerusalem and a couple of billion perfect replicas of Him walking around on this earth (Phil. 3:21; 1 John 3:1--2), "man" produces the [final rebellion,]{.class-1} the [White Throne Judgment,]{.class-1} and the [Lake of Fire.]{.class-1}

All of that shows you that Darwin was [out of his mind.]{.class-1} The story of human history is not "upward and onward"; it's down to the gutter until you are pulled out of it by God. Watches don't run up; they run down. It requires intervention from an outside source to keep a watch running; someone has to wind it up. That's very simple, but it's a great truth.

You take your case. The Bible says you ["were dead in trespasses and sins"]{.class-0} (Eph. 2:1). What does God do? He steps in there with the Holy Spirit and the New Birth, and He "winds you up." When He does that, immediately you start "running down" again. The flesh asserts itself; the world demands conformity; the Devil fights you every step of the way to prevent you from living out what God has put in you. What do you need? You need another infusion of divine energy to get you up and running again. That is accomplished by the Holy Spirit with the word of God and prayer.

You leave that Book on the shelf unread and don't seek God in prayer, and the Holy Spirit who dwells inside you as a Christian won't do "nuthin'." Oh, He doesn't leave you or forsake you (Heb. 13:5). He'll get you to Heaven even if He has to turn you over to Satan for the destruction of your flesh so that ["the spirit may be saved in the day of the Lord Jesus"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 5:5). But when it comes to the fulness of the Christian life, you are dead in the sense of being unfruitful for Him (see our comments on Luke 8:14 and Eph. 5:14 in their respective Commentaries).

So Judges is a vivid illustration of the Law of Human Collapse. Unless God intervenes and helps man, "man" is [hopeless.]{.class-1} I know that's contrary to everything you learn in school and College; the NEA won't teach you that. It is not to be found in [Time, Life, Look, People, Newsweek,]{.class-1} or [U.S. News and World Report.]{.class-1} The Associated Press and the newscasts on TV won't tell you that. [National Geographic]{.class-1} and [Nature]{.class-1} magazines haven't got it. They are all just outlets for Marxist, evolutionary propaganda. They all teach that man came up from a monkey and keeps going higher and higher, but the truth is, if God doesn't "monkey" with you, you are headed back to the jungle with the monkeys. It's [back to the Bible or back to the jungle.]{.class-1}

So in Judges, you have Israel falling into sin and idolatry, and God intervening by sending men called "judges" to straighten them out. In the outstanding cases given in the book, the judges deliver the people from the heathen nations God sent in to punish them for their idolatry (2:16). This places the [doctrinal]{.class-1} application on the [Second Advent of Jesus Christ.]{.class-1}

["For I would not, brethren, that ye should be ignorant of this mystery, lest ye should be wise in your own conceits; that blindness in part is happened to Israel, until the fulness of the Gentiles be come in. And so all Israel shall be saved: as it is written, There shall come out of Zion the Deliverer, and shall turn away ungodliness from Jacob"]{.class-0} (Rom. 11:25--26).

When Jesus Christ returns in power, Israel is back in the land in unbelief just as they were in the book of Judges (Zech. 12:10). They are involved in idolatry just as they were in the book of Judges (Matt. 24:15). The heathen nations are oppressing them just as you read in the book of Judges (Zech. 14:2). And when the Lord Jesus Christ returns, He returns as a judge to deliver Israel both physically and spiritually (Joel 2:32, 3:21; Isa. 45:17; Jer. 31:31--34; Ezek. 34:22--28, 37:21--28). So the judges are types of Christ at His Second Coming, and this will be especially evident when we get to Deborah's song in chapter 5.

So here we enter into our study of the book of Judges. It is a perfect picture of America in its later stages of apostasy. It is a warning to the Christian who gives place to the Devil and the desires of the flesh in his life. And it shows us what will take place in the near future at the return of our Lord.

As is our practice in these Commentaries, we will not entertain the judgments of men, be they saved or lost, Fundamental or Liberal, on the God-honored text of the [Authorized Version.]{.class-1} Rather than sitting in judgment on God's word, we will let it judge us (Heb. 4:12--13). We will consult ["the Judge of all"]{.class-0} (Heb. 12:23) and let Him teach us the ["judgments"]{.class-0} in His Book (Psa. 119:108).

[]{#section-0_1_6271893c8f348ade_708b.xhtml}

Chapter 1

1:1 Now after the death of Joshua it came to pass, that the children of Israel asked the LORD, saying, Who shall go up for us against the Canaanites first, to fight against them?

2 And the LORD said, Judah shall go up: behold, I have delivered the land into his hand.

3 And Judah said unto Simeon his brother, Come up with me into my lot, that we may fight against the Canaanites; and I likewise will go with thee into thy lot. So Simeon went with him.

4 And Judah went up; and the LORD delivered the Canaanites and the Perizzites into their hand: and they slew of them in Bezek ten thousand men.

5 And they found Adonibezek in Bezek: and they fought against him, and they slew the Canaanites and the Perizzites.

6 But Adonibezek fled; and they pursued after him, and caught him, and cut off his thumbs and his great toes.

7 And Adonibezek said, Threescore and ten kings, having their thumbs and their great toes cut off, gathered their meat under my table: as I have done, so God hath requited me. And they brought him to Jerusalem, and there he died.

8 Now the children of Judah had fought against Jerusalem, and had taken it, and smitten it with the edge of the sword, and set the city on fire.

Judges starts out much as Joshua started out in the first verse.

Joshua 1:1---["Now after the death of Moses the servant of the LORD it came to pass . . . ."]{.class-0}

Judges 1:1---["Now after the death of Joshua it came to pass . . . ."]{.class-0}

And what ["came to pass"]{.class-0} marks the difference between the two books. What follows the death of Moses is [victory;]{.class-1} what follows the death of Joshua is [defeat.]{.class-1} The reasons for the difference is the [lack of faith]{.class-1} on the people's part in the book of Judges and [not getting rid of their idols]{.class-1} back in Joshua 24 (see our remarks on the subject in that Commentary).

For the lack of faith, compare verse 2 to verse 19.

Verse 2---["And the LORD said, Judah shall go up: behold, I have delivered the land into his hand."]{.class-0}

Verse 19---["And the LORD was with Judah; and he drave out the inhabitants of the mountain; but could not drive out the inhabitants of the valley, because they had chariots of iron."]{.class-0}

Well, if God told them they would take the land and they didn't take part of it, who made the mistake---God or Judah? Obviously the problem wasn't with the promises of God; it was with [Judah's faith.]{.class-1} They lacked the faith to follow completely through on what God said He would do. That is why the contrast is made with Caleb in verses 10, 20. Caleb had problems worse than valley dwellers with iron chariots; he had giants entrenched on high ground. Yet Caleb claimed the promise God had made to him 45 years earlier, and at 85 years old, he was able to defeat those giants (see our remarks under Josh. 14:9--12 in that Commentary).

Back to verse 1: ["the children of Israel asked the LORD."]{.class-0} Joshua is dead, and no one replaced him as leader of the twelve tribes. Now the tribes come together to inquire of the Lord.

The process is described in Numbers 27:21, where it is a reference to Joshua. Here, the leaders of the tribes would come together at the Tabernacle and stand before the high priest. The high priest wore an "ephod," a kind of a T-shirt, with a breastplate tied to it. On that breastplate were twelve stones, each stone representing one of the twelve tribes of Israel. You can read all about it in Exodus 28, and we commented quite extensively on it in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Exodus.]{.class-1}

On that breastplate was also something called "Urim and Thummim," which means "lights and perfections." No one knows exactly what it was, but the implication is that when someone came to the high priest to inquire of the Lord, those stones in that breastplate would light up like the numbers representing letters on a telephone dial and spell out the message from God.

The answer given the children of Israel here is that Judah would be the first tribe to go up and drive the remaining Canaanites out of its territory. We discussed the reason Judah was given the precedence under our remarks on Joshua 15:1 in that Commentary, which see. Briefly here, 1 Chronicles 5:2 says, ["Judah prevailed above his brethren"]{.class-0} because that was the tribe the Lord picked to bring forth Christ (Gen. 49:10).

Now, after being told he was to go up first, Judah asks Simeon to go up with him (vs. 3). That's the first sign of weakness in Judah's faith. There was nothing technically "wrong" with it, and God doesn't condemn them for it, but it is indicative of the fact that they were worried they wouldn't be able to handle those Canaanites by themselves. What Judah forgot---and this was the lack of faith that caused them not to be able to drive out ["the inhabitants of the valley"]{.class-0} in verse 19---was that [God]{.class-1} was with them in the battle.

["When thou goest out to battle against thine enemies, and seest horses, and chariots, and a people more than thou ]{.class-0}\[as they did in vs. 19 here in Judg. 1\][, be not afraid of them: for the LORD thy God is with thee . . . the LORD your God is he that goeth with you, to fight for you against your enemies, to save you"]{.class-0} (Deut. 20:1, 4).

Judah didn't need Simeon; all they needed was to rely on God to help them beat those Canaanites. Remember that, Christian, when you go up against sin and the Devil in your life. There's nothing wrong with enlisting the aid of other believers in prayer and accountability, but that's [not]{.class-1} on what you should rely. Your faith should be in God, in the Holy Ghost who lives in you and will give you the power, if you trust Him, to put down your flesh and resist the Devil.

Paul said, ["If God be for us, who can be against us"]{.class-0} (Rom. 8:31). Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "One man and God make a majority." John writes, ["Ye are of God, little children, and have overcome them: because greater is he that is in you, than he that is in the world"]{.class-0} (1 John 4:4). Victory is to be found in Christ and in His Holy Spirit in you.

Now there are reasons Judah seeks Simeon's help. First is the fact that Simeon's inheritance fell within the inheritance of Judah (see Josh. 19:1 and our comments on the verse in that Commentary). But Simeon was quite a character. It was Simeon, along with his brother Levi, who slaughtered the Hivites responsible for raping their sister Dinah in Genesis 34. Because of their cruelty and anger, God scattered both tribes in Israel so that neither one had a regular inheritance like the other tribes (Gen. 49:5--7).

Simeon was a rough character. When the tribes came out to David at Ziklag to make him King, Simeon was one of only two tribes (the other was Ephraim) whose men were called ["mighty men of valour"]{.class-0} (1 Chron. 12:25). So Simeon may have been a small tribe, but they were tough when it came to fighting and war. You will notice that there is no record in Joshua 19 or Judges 1 of Simeon's failure to drive out heathen nations among them. Simeon slaughters his group. So Simeon is a strong military tribe, which is why Judah asks for their help.

Verse 4: ["And Judah went up; and the LORD delivered the Canaanites and the Perizzites into their hand: and they slew of them in Bezek ten thousand men."]{.class-0} So the initial campaign is successful. They take Bezek, a mountainous area in Judah (notice ["my lot"]{.class-0} in reference to Judah in vs. 3). Some expositors make this a different ["Bezek"]{.class-0} from the one in 1 Samuel 11:8 where Saul numbered Israel and Judah to go fight Nahash the Ammonite at Jabeshgilead; they place that one in Mt. Ephraim northeast of Shechem. Whether that is so or not, I don't know, but this one is in Judah.

["Adonibezek"]{.class-0} (vs. 5) is [not]{.class-1} the ["Adonizedek"]{.class-0} of Jerusalem who led the southern confederation against Joshua, despite the fact that Jerusalem shows up in verses 7--8. Adonibezek was not the King of Jerusalem. His name means "Lord of Bezek"; so he was the King of Bezek, not Jerusalem.

Now Adonibezek was a mean rascal. He had conquered seventy Kings of other cities in Canaan, and he kept those Kings as "war trophies." He would cut off the thumbs on both hands and the big toes on both feet. That would put a fellow in a bad way. The big toe gives you balance as you walk, and that opposable thumb allows you to pick up things. Without their big toes and thumbs, those seventy Kings were reduced to an animal state where they had to crawl around on the floor and gather their food with just their four fingers (which is a difficult thing to do). That's why Adonibezek said those humiliated Kings ["gathered their meat UNDER my table"]{.class-0} (vs. 7).

The men of Judah and Simeon caught Adonibezek and did the same thing to him that he had done to those seventy Kings he had captured. And do you know what that lost heathen King said? He said, ["as I have done, so GOD HATH REQUITED ME."]{.class-0} That bird had more sense of the law of sowing and reaping than some Christians have. The law is:

["Be not deceived; God is not mocked: for whatsoever a man soweth, that shall he also reap. For he that soweth to his flesh shall of the flesh reap corruption; but he that soweth to the Spirit shall of the Spirit reap life everlasting"]{.class-0} (Gal. 6:7--8).

Modern Christians read an account like this, and they think, "What a cruel thing for those Israelites to do. They cut off that poor fellow's thumbs and big toes; that's a terrible thing." In other words, most Christians today are [humanists]{.class-1} in their approach to Scripture. The reason a lot of professing Christians have given up the doctrine of Hell---or at least the [fire]{.class-1} part (like Billy Graham)---is because they figure they wouldn't consign anyone to burn forever and God is better than they are, so God won't burn any sinner forever.

What they don't figure into their reasoning is the [nature of God.]{.class-1} Unlike you, God is [absolutely holy.]{.class-1} He's ["a consuming fire"]{.class-0} (Heb. 12:29). God's love and mercy are one part of His nature; His [jealousy, holiness,]{.class-1} and [wrath]{.class-1} are the other side of the coin. You have to have [both:]{.class-1} positive and negative. If God loves everybody and everything indiscriminately, He's a [perverted Deity.]{.class-1} Any God who loves Adolf Hitler, Joseph Stalin, Charlie Manson, Mao Tse-Tung, Bloody Mary, and Nero in the same way and to the same extent He loves Gen. William Booth, John Wesley, George Mueller, Gladys Aylward, Mary Slessor, Amy Carmichael, and William Carey is a twisted God. If you love your garden, you are going to hate weeds; if you love your wife and children, you are going to hate anyone who tries to do them harm.

What modern Christians don't seem to get is that God's love is found in [one person:]{.class-1} Jesus Christ (Rom. 8:39); it is found in [one place:]{.class-1} at Calvary (Rom. 5:8). Just because God is good, merciful, and longsuffering to a sinner doesn't mean He loves him enough to keep him out of Hell if that sinner rejects the payment God requires for that sinner's sins.

Adonibezek doesn't look at things the way this modern bunch does. He figured he "dished it out" seventy times so it was his turn to "take it." The old saying is: "What goes around, comes around."

The thief on the cross who got saved said to his buddy, ["Dost not thou fear God, seeing thou art in the same condemnation? AND WE INDEED JUSTLY; FOR WE RECEIVE THE DUE REWARD OF OUR DEEDS"]{.class-0} (Luke 23:40--41). He said, "We're getting exactly what we had coming for our crimes," and he was suffering one of the most horrific forms of execution devised by man. Sometimes the heathen know more than you think they know.

In verses 7--8, up shows the ["cup of trembling"]{.class-0} that God will use to destroy the United Nations---[Jerusalem]{.class-1} (Zech. 12:2). The word means "city of peace." That's God's idea of a joke. The first time it shows up in the Scriptures, it is called ["Salem"]{.class-0} (Gen. 14:18)---"peace." It appears in the context of the first recorded [war]{.class-1} (Gen. 14:2). The first time its full name appears (Josh. 10:1), it is given in the context of a [battle]{.class-1} (Josh. 10:4).

But there is a reason that city is called "the city of peace." When ["The Prince of Peace"]{.class-0} (Isa. 9:6) finally brings "peace on earth" (Luke 2:14), He brings it right there at that city (Hag. 2:9), and He does it by putting down all opposition in battle (Psa. 76:2--3; Mic. 5:2--5). So when you ["Pray for the peace of Jerusalem"]{.class-0} (Psa. 122:6), you are praying for the return of Jesus Christ. In the meantime, Jerusalem is ["a burdensome stone"]{.class-0} to shred every member State in the UN to ribbons (Zech. 12:3).

Now the conquest of Jerusalem mentioned in verse 8 obviously takes place before the battle of verses 4--6, for the text says ["the children of Judah HAD fought against Jerusalem, and HAD taken it."]{.class-0} Although you have the defeat of the [King]{.class-1} of Jerusalem in Joshua 10, the conquest of the [city]{.class-1} is not given in the book of Joshua. Most likely, though, verse 8 takes place before the death of Joshua, for what follows in verses 9--15 is recorded originally in Joshua 15:13--19.

9 And afterward the children of Judah went down to fight against the Canaanites, that dwelt in the mountain, and in the south, and in the valley.

10 And Judah went against the Canaanites that dwelt in Hebron: (now the name of Hebron before was Kirjatharba:) and they slew Sheshai, and Ahiman, and Talmai.

11 And from thence he went against the inhabitants of Debir: and the name of Debir before was Kirjathsepher:

12 And Caleb said, He that smiteth Kirjathsepher, and taketh it, to him will I give Achsah my daughter to wife.

13 And Othniel the son of Kenaz, Caleb's younger brother, took it: and he gave him Achsah his daughter to wife.

14 And it came to pass, when she came to him, that she moved him to ask of her father a field: and she lighted from off her ass; and Caleb said unto her, What wilt thou?

15 And she said unto him, Give me a blessing: for thou hast given me a south land; give me also springs of water. And Caleb gave her the upper springs and the nether springs.

We have commented on the passage under our remarks under Joshua 15:13--19 in that Commentary, which see. Briefly here, the student of the Scriptures should be reminded that people and places in the Bible can have more than one name. In the two examples in this passage (Hebron and Debir), they both have [three]{.class-1} names. Hebron was not only known as "Hebron," it was also known as ["Mamre"]{.class-0} (Gen. 23:19) and ["Kirjatharba"]{.class-0} (vs. 10 here). Debir was called ["Kirjathsepher"]{.class-0} (vs. 11) and ["Kirjathsannah"]{.class-0} (Josh. 15:42).

That is nothing unusual. Istanbul used to be Constantinople, and before that it was Byzantium. So remember that the next time you hear some infidel or apostate talking about contradictions in your Bible; some of those so-called "contradictions" can be explained by something as simple as different names for the same place or the same person.

The great practical lesson of the passage is [prayer.]{.class-1} Achsah had gotten some land from her daddy for a wedding present, but she didn't think much of it because it was arid. Now she could have sat around and complained about it and bemoaned the fact that her father thought so little of her to give her such poor land. Instead, she went to Caleb and asked for ["springs of water"]{.class-0} (vs. 15). The spiritual lesson for the New Testament believer is if you want something from God, [ask for it.]{.class-1} James said, ["ye have not, because ye ask not"]{.class-0} (James 4:2). Your Saviour [commanded]{.class-1} you to ask (Luke 11:9) and to ask [in His name]{.class-1} (John 16:24). Of course, that's not an unconditional promise that you'll get everything you want. There are stipulations, such as asking [in God's will ]{.class-1}and [for His glory]{.class-1} (2 Cor. 12:7--9) and not asking in order to ["consume it upon your lusts"]{.class-0} (James 4:3). But one thing's for sure, if you don't ask, you're not likely to get it.

I was talking to a lady one time about our school situation here at PBI. We're not like Pensacola Christian College, with all the classrooms, the dormitories, all kinds of parking spaces, a swimming pool, a dining hall, etc. All we have is a two-story tin building, our old church building, and a parking lot that looks like a minefield. That lady said to me, "If you want bigger facilities, why don't you ask God for the Holiday Inn down the road?"

I drove down there and looked the place over, and sure enough, it had everything we needed: plenty of rooms for dorms and classrooms, restaurant facilities for a cafeteria, and a nice, big parking lot. I told that sister, "Yeah, the whole thing is laid out right there."

"Why don't you ask God for it, then?" she asked.

"That would be silly," I said.

"Well, silly or not," she replied, "how do you know what God will give you if you don't ask."

I got to thinking about what that sister said to me, and I thought to myself, "Wouldn't it be a dumb thing for me to get up to Heaven and find out that I could have had that Holiday Inn and I was too stupid to ask for it?" So you know what I did? [I asked for it.]{.class-1}

You say, "Did you get it?" No, I didn't, but I have not forgotten the lesson I learned. I am not going to get up to Heaven and have God accuse me of not asking when He commanded me to do so. There are enough hindrances to prayer without not asking.

Brethren, the key to asking for something in prayer is what Jesus called ["importunity"]{.class-0} (Luke 11:8): [persistence in prayer.]{.class-1} Jesus told two parables about it: The Importunate Friend (Luke 11:5--8) and The Unjust Judge (Luke 18:1--8). The man kept asking for bread until his buddy got out of bed and gave it to him; the widow woman kept crying to the unjust judge for vengeance against her enemy until the unjust judge gave her what she wanted just to get her off his back. The lesson Jesus was trying to teach us is to keep on praying about a thing until you get a definite answer from God. Even Paul didn't let a "no" answer stop him the first time (2 Cor. 12:8).

A great example of asking in prayer and importunity in prayer was George Mueller. George Mueller would never ask anything of any man but God. He managed to pray in, in a lifetime, [two-and-a-half million dollars]{.class-1} and enough food to raise [ten thousand]{.class-1} orphans. Mueller said, "It is not enough to [begin]{.class-1} to pray, nor to pray [aright;]{.class-1} nor is it enough to continue [for a time]{.class-1} to pray; but we must [patiently, believingly continue in prayer, until we obtain an answer."]{.class-1}

George Mueller once began to pray for five of his friends to get saved; he prayed every day for those five men. The first one got saved after [several months]{.class-1} of prayer. Two others trusted Christ [ten years]{.class-1} after George began praying for them. The fourth man didn't get saved until [25 years]{.class-1} of prayer. Mueller prayed for that last fellow for[ 52 years,]{.class-1} and George prayed for him until the day that he (i.e., George Mueller) died. But it wasn't long after George's funeral that his last friend got saved. That's [persistence]{.class-1} in prayer.

With that sublime lesson from the story of Achsah in mind, consider the crass, vulgar rendering of the [New English Bible]{.class-1} in verse 14. Instead of Achsah lighting ["from off her ass"]{.class-0} to talk to her father, the [NEB]{.class-1} has her [breaking wind]{.class-1} (["As she sat on the ass, she broke wind, and Caleb said, 'What did you mean by that?'"]{.class-1}).

This "unique" translation was the work of a conceited fool named Godfrey Rolles Driver, Professor of Semitic Philology at Oxford University and head ("Covener") of the Old Testament Committee for the [NEB.]{.class-1} He [insisted]{.class-1} the reading be put in there---even though [no other]{.class-1} translation in [any other]{.class-1} language translates it that way---because of an obscure [Akkadian]{.class-1} (NOT Hebrew) word which had nothing to do with anything in the Hebrew text of Judges 1:14. Just because a man can read Akkadian, Arabic, Aramaic, Hebrew, and Syriac doesn't mean he has the sense of a five-year-old Ubangi when it comes to understanding or giving you [what God said]{.class-1}---in ANY language.

16 And the children of the Kenite, Moses' father in law, went up out of the city of palm trees with the children of Judah into the wilderness of Judah, which lieth in the south of Arad; and they went and dwelt among the people.

17 And Judah went with Simeon his brother, and they slew the Canaanites that inhabited Zephath, and utterly destroyed it. And the name of the city was called Hormah.

18 Also Judah took Gaza with the coast thereof, and Askelon with the coast thereof, and Ekron with the coast thereof.

19 And the LORD was with Judah; and he drave out the inhabitants of the mountain; but could not drive out the inhabitants of the valley, because they had chariots of iron.

20 And they gave Hebron unto Caleb, as Moses said: and he expelled thence the three sons of Anak.

21 And the children of Benjamin did not drive out the Jebusites that inhabited Jerusalem; but the Jebusites dwell with the children of Benjamin in Jerusalem unto this day.

["The Kenite"]{.class-0} of verse 16 is defined as ["Moses' father in law."]{.class-0} This would be the ["Hobab"]{.class-0} of 4:11. In Numbers 10:29, he is the son of a ["Midianite."]{.class-0} The word [Kenites]{.class-1} could be another name for the Midianites, but more likely it is the name of a tribe that lived in Midian (see Exod. 2:15--16, 3:1, 4:19, 18:1).

["The city of palm trees"]{.class-0} is another name for Jericho (Deut. 34:3; 2 Chron. 28:15). While this could be a [second]{.class-1} Jericho, it could also be the [fields and villages]{.class-1} associated with the city which were not destroyed when the walled fortress was brought down (see our comments on Josh. 21:11--12, 18:21 in that Commentary).

The Kenites end up settling in ["the south of Arad,"]{.class-0} which was in the southern part of Judah's territory (1 Sam. 27:10, 30:29) just north of Edom around where the Amalekites lived (1 Sam. 15:6).

Verse 17:[ "And Judah went with Simeon his brother."]{.class-0} This was the deal back in verse 3: if Simeon would help Judah clear out the Canaanites in Judah's territory, Judah would help Simeon take care of the Canaanites in Simeon's part.

The ["Hormah"]{.class-0} of verse 17 is not the same place which the Israelites destroyed in their wilderness wanderings back in Numbers 21:3. This is a city within Simeon's inheritance. The word means "utter destruction." The only thing the two "Hormahs" have in common is that they were both "wiped out" by the Jews.

The cities of verse 18 are Philistine cities (Josh. 13:3; 1 Sam. 6:17). This is one of those instances where Judah may have [taken]{.class-1} the cities, but they did not [possess]{.class-1} the cities (see our comments on Josh. 13:1 in that Commentary).

Verse 19 has a distinct division at the word ["but."]{.class-0} The first part of the verse is a statement of [fact;]{.class-1} the second part of the verse is an [excuse.]{.class-1} If ["the LORD was with Judah,"]{.class-0} they could have driven [anybody]{.class-1} out of [anywhere.]{.class-1} The problem wasn't with the Lord; it was with [Judah.]{.class-1} Look at 1 Kings 20:28.

["And there came a man of God, and spake unto the king of Israel, and said, Thus saith the LORD, Because the Syrians have said, The LORD is God of the hills, but he is not God of the valleys]{.class-0} \[i.e., God could give Israel the victory on the hills but not in the valleys\][, therefore will I deliver all this great multitude into thine hand, and ye shall know that I am the LORD."]{.class-0}

So the second part of verse 19 is Judah's alibi for their lack of faith. If you want to see how troubling those ["chariots of iron"]{.class-0} were to God, just look at chapter 4, verses 13--16. You think a God who made an atomic furnace like the sun is going to worry about your iron chariots or tanks or missiles or electromagnetic pulses?

Verse 20 is a repeat of the information given in verse 10, with the added detail that it was [Caleb]{.class-1} who ["slew Sheshai, and Ahiman, and Talmai."]{.class-0}

Verse 21 is the second mention of [partial obedience]{.class-1} on the part of the Israelites. Jerusalem was divided between the tribes of Judah and Benjamin (Josh. 15:8, 18:28), and neither tribe drove out the Jebusites in the city (see Josh. 15:63). This partial obedience leads to the disturbing events of chapters 19--21 here in Judges. Benjamin is singled out here because it is Benjamin that picks up the sodomy of the Jebusites in those chapters and nearly gets wiped out as a tribe of Israel. Benjamin's incomplete obedience nearly resulted in its [annihilation.]{.class-1}

Now there is a spiritual lesson here for the New Testament child of God. The Christian is commanded: ["mortify therefore your members which are upon the earth; fornication, uncleanness, inordinate affection, evil concupiscence, and covetousness, which is idolatry"]{.class-0} (Col. 3:5).

You are to [kill]{.class-1} the deeds of the sinful flesh in your life. If you do, you'll [live;]{.class-1} if you don't, you'll [die]{.class-1} (Rom. 8:13). That's because ["he that soweth to his flesh shall of the flesh reap corruption; but he that soweth to the Spirit shall of the Spirit reap life everlasting"]{.class-0} (Gal. 6:8). You will either kill the flesh, or it will [kill you.]{.class-1}

22 And the house of Joseph, they also went up against Bethel: and the LORD was with them.

23 And the house of Joseph sent to descry Bethel. (Now the name of the city before was Luz.)

24 And the spies saw a man come forth out of the city, and they said unto him, Shew us, we pray thee, the entrance into the city, and we will shew thee mercy.

25 And when he shewed them the entrance into the city, they smote the city with the edge of the sword; but they let go the man and all his family.

26 And the man went into the land of the Hittites, and built a city, and called the name thereof Luz: which is the name thereof unto this day.

As we discussed in our remarks on Joshua 18:1--5 in that Commentary (which see), the land of Israel was basically divided between Judah in the south and Joseph's tribes (Ephraim and Manasseh) in the north, with Benjamin as a "buffer zone" (Josh. 18:11). So here in Judges 1, you have Judah in verses 2--20 (with the tribe of Simeon that was scattered within Judah's borders), Benjamin in verse 21, Manasseh and Ephraim in verses 22--29, and the rest of the northern tribes in verses 30--36. Verse 22 introduces Joseph's two tribes.

["And the house of Joseph sent to descry Bethel"]{.class-0} (vs. 23). The city of Bethel belonged to Benjamin (Josh. 18:21--22), but it was taken by Ephraim and Manasseh. The word ["descry,"]{.class-0} as used here, means "to spy" (cf. Josh. 2:1, 14:7, 18:2). I know that's not a common term, but you could have figured it out without too much trouble. But one obscure word is no cause to make 36,000 ([NASV]{.class-1})--64,000 ([NIV]{.class-1}) changes in your Bible. A note in the margin will suffice, which is what we did in the [Ruckman Reference Bible;]{.class-1} we left the text alone.

["(Now the name of the city before was Luz.)"]{.class-65}[ It was here that Jacob spent a night as he fled from Esau and]{.class-66} had the vision of the[ ladder that ]{.class-22}["reached to heaven"]{.class-27}[; it was he who named the place ]{.class-22}["Bethel," "the house of God" ]{.class-27}(Gen. 28:17, 19). Of course, that would have meant nothing to the heathen people who lived in Luz and knew nothing of Jacob's vision, so for 400 years, the name remained Luz to all but the Hebrews who wrote of it. In this passage, the city ceases to be Luz and becomes the Hebrew city of Bethel.

Now in verses 24--25, there is a situation that seems to match Rahab's case in Joshua 2. The spies find a man from the city to collaborate with them and show them how to get in to take the city. For his help, they spare him and his family. The important difference between this man and Rahab was that [Rahab was a convert]{.class-1} (see our remarks under Josh. 2:8). This fellow [isn't.]{.class-1} When he and his family are spared in the destruction of the city, he leaves Israel (the only good thing in the story) and sets up his heathen city somewhere else (vs. 26). ["The land of the Hittites"]{.class-0} in verse 26 is located north of the Golan Heights.

["Which is the name thereof unto this day."]{.class-0} Whenever you read something like that in the Bible, it means at the time of the writing. Of course, after 3,400 years, most of the names of those places have changed.

27 Neither did Manasseh drive out the inhabitants of Bethshean and her towns, nor Taanach and her towns, nor the inhabitants of Dor and her towns, nor the inhabitants of Ibleam and her towns, nor the inhabitants of Megiddo and her towns: but the Canaanites would dwell in that land.

28 And it came to pass, when Israel was strong, that they put the Canaanites to tribute, and did not utterly drive them out.

29 Neither did Ephraim drive out the Canaanites that dwelt in Gezer; but the Canaanites dwelt in Gezer among them.

30 Neither did Zebulun drive out the inhabitants of Kitron, nor the inhabitants of Nahalol; but the Canaanites dwelt among them, and became tributaries.

31 Neither did Asher drive out the inhabitants of Accho, nor the inhabitants of Zidon, nor of Ahlab, nor of Achzib, nor of Helbah, nor of Aphik, nor of Rehob:

32 But the Asherites dwelt among the Canaanites, the inhabitants of the land: for they did not drive them out.

33 Neither did Naphtali drive out the inhabitants of Bethshemesh, nor the inhabitants of Bethanath; but he dwelt among the Canaanites, the inhabitants of the land: nevertheless the inhabitants of Bethshemesh and of Bethanath became tributaries unto them.

34 And the Amorites forced the children of Dan into the mountain: for they would not suffer them to come down to the valley:

35 But the Amorites would dwell in mount Heres in Aijalon, and in Shaalbim: yet the hand of the house of Joseph prevailed, so that they became tributaries.

36 And the coast of the Amorites was from the going up to Akrabbim, from the rock, and upward.

Now while sparing that fellow in Luz was indeed partial obedience to God's command to wipe out the inhabitants of the land, it didn't affect the Israelites like what follows. That man and his family [left the land.]{.class-1} What follows in verses 27 to the end of the chapter was what really brought ruin to the nation of Israel.

The passage is the account of the northern tribes not driving all the heathen peoples from their territories. Verses 27--29 record the incomplete obedience of the two tribes of Joseph and the compromise they made with the pagan nations they didn't destroy. This set the pattern for the rest of the northern tribes.

The command was to ["utterly destroy"]{.class-0} those heathen nations because if they didn't, those nations would lead Israel into worshiping other gods (Deut. 7:1--4), and that's exactly what happens in the next chapter here in Judges (2:11--12). Instead, the tribes compromise with the Gentile peoples that remained and put them under tribute. But [subjugation]{.class-1} and [taxation]{.class-1} are not [conversion.]{.class-1} Those heathens kept their idols and false gods and altars right there in the cities with the Israelites.

The lesson for the Christian is he is to be ruthless when it comes to sin in his life. Give it no quarter, because if you do, it will, eventually, get the upper hand.

The old-time preachers used to say, "Slay utterly." Wesley was real strong on that. What he meant was completely get rid of the sin in your life.

Now what starts out as a lack of faith, and then compromise, ends up with both the northern and the southern tribes going into captivity.

["For so it was, that the children of Israel had sinned against the LORD their God . . . and had feared other gods, And walked in the statutes of the heathen, whom the LORD cast out from before the children of Israel . . . And the LORD rejected all the seed of Israel, and afflicted them, and delivered them into the hand of spoilers, until he had cast them out of his sight"]{.class-0} (2 Kings 17:7--8, 20).

Those Jews didn't drive out all those heathen nations, so Israel and Judah ended up being driven out of the land themselves. The Assyrians came in and took the northern tribes captive, and Nebuchadnezzar came in and took Judah and Benjamin captive.

The lesson for the Christian is [don't try to "get along" with the world.]{.class-1} When you conform to the sinful world system (Rom. 12:2) and love this evil world (1 John 2:15--16) and are a friend to the wicked system of this world (James 4:4), you become God's [enemy]{.class-1} (James 4:4). You have been [delivered]{.class-1} from ["this present evil world"]{.class-0} (Gal. 1:4); you have been [crucified]{.class-1} to it (Gal. 6:14). You have in you the power to [overcome]{.class-1} it (1 John 5:4 --5). Why bring yourself back into bondage to it (Gal. 4:3, 9)? ["The rudiments of the world"]{.class-0} can [spoil]{.class-1} you (Col. 2:8), Christian; i.e., they can rob you of God's blessings.[ ]{.class-0}Being preoccupied with ["the cares of this world"]{.class-0} can cause you to be [unfruitful]{.class-1} (Mark 4:19). You have to trust God (1 John 5:4) and FIGHT (Eph. 6:12--13).

Back to Judges 1: ["And the Amorites forced the children of Dan into the mountain: for they would not suffer them to come down to the valley: But the Amorites would dwell in mount Heres in Aijalon, and in Shaalbim"]{.class-0} (vss. 34--35). Two things to notice in these verses. The first is ["the Amorites."]{.class-0} Those were the bunch that Israel whipped on the east side of Jordan (Num. 21:21--25, 32) and there in Joshua 10 (see vs. 1 in that chapter) with the five Kings. The people testify to this fact in Joshua 24:18 (which see).

What happened here? [Apostasy after the death of Joshua.]{.class-1} This apostasy manifests itself especially in the case of [Dan.]{.class-1} The tribe goes into complete apostasy for the next 800 years (18:30--31) and ends up laying the foundation for the [Roman Catholic Church]{.class-1} (17:10--13).

Chapter 2

2:1 And an angel of the LORD came up from Gilgal to Bochim, and said, I made you to go up out of Egypt, and have brought you unto the land which I sware unto your fathers; and I said, I will never break my covenant with you.

2 And ye shall make no league with the inhabitants of this land; ye shall throw down their altars: but ye have not obeyed my voice: why have ye done this?

3 Wherefore I also said, I will not drive them out from before you; but they shall be as thorns in your sides, and their gods shall be a snare unto you.

4 And it came to pass, when the angel of the LORD spake these words unto all the children of Israel, that the people lifted up their voice, and wept.

5 And they called the name of that place Bochim: and they sacrificed there unto the LORD.

Although the angel of verse 1 is only called ["AN angel of the LORD,"]{.class-0} it is obvious that this is actually THE Angel of the Lord (vs. 4), for he speaks as God in the first person in verses 1, 3:[ "I made you to go up out of Egypt ]{.class-0}\
[. . . the land which I sware unto your fathers . . . I said,  I will never break my covenant with you . . . . Wherefore I also said, I will not drive them out from before you."]{.class-0} That's not prefaced with "Thus saith the Lord"; it's the angel speaking directly as God.

["Gilgal"]{.class-0} is the first encampment of the Israelites after they crossed the Jordan (Josh. 4:19). It is where Joshua renewed the covenant God made with Abraham through circumcision (Gen. 17:10--14). During the forty years of wandering in the wilderness, none of the baby boys had been circumcised, so Joshua circumcised all the men who had grown up in that condition (Josh. 5:2--7). God called this uncircumcised state of the Jewish men ["the reproach of Egypt"]{.class-0} (Josh. 5:9). Joshua called the place where he carried out the circumcision ["Gilgal,"]{.class-0} which means "rolling," because it was at that place where God ["rolled away the reproach of Egypt"]{.class-0} from off the people (Josh. 5:9).

The Angel of the Lord goes ["from Gilgal to Bochim."]{.class-0} Now there is no indication of where ["Bochim"]{.class-0} is. The word itself means "weepers" (vss. 4--5). Verse 6 implies that what you read in verses 1--5 takes place in Joshua 24. [If ]{.class-1}that's the case, then Bochim is what those weeping Israelites called Shechem (Josh. 24:1).

["I made you to go up out of Egypt"]{.class-0}---a picture of Jesus Christ delivering you ["from this present evil world"]{.class-0} (Gal. 1:4). The Lord Jesus saved you as a believer and made you ["a new creature"]{.class-0} in Him (2 Cor. 5:17). As the song says: "the old man is dead." When some of you got saved, your former companions didn't recognize you.

Before I got saved, I was a drunken radio announcer who played drums in a dance band at night. After I got saved, the next time some of my old crowd saw me I was driving around in my car picking up kids for Vacation Bible School and telling them, "Get in the car with the bunny rabbit on the windshield" (each car had a picture of an animal on the windshield so the kids would know which vehicle to get in to go home). You talk about a "change," boy; Obama, Clinton, and the Democrats wouldn't know what to do with that kind of change.

When you got saved, you were spiritually separated from the world system under the control of Satan (2 Cor. 4:4) and separated from his kids (Eph. 2:1--6). Spiritually, the Lord ["brought you unto the land which I sware unto your fathers"]{.class-0}---a picture of salvation. Paul said God ["raised us up together, and made us sit together in heavenly places in Christ Jesus"]{.class-0} (Eph. 2:6).

["I said, I will never break my covenant with you"]{.class-0}---a spiritual picture of the eternal security of the believer. The promise to you is [nothing ]{.class-1}["shall be able to separate us from the love of God, which is in Christ Jesus our Lord"]{.class-0} (Rom. 8:39); it's ["I will NEVER leave thee, nor forsake thee"]{.class-0} (Heb. 13:5). You've been given [eternal]{.class-1} life, not [conditional]{.class-1} life.

Now when it comes to this covenant made with Israel, the thing to remember, in regards to the [nation]{.class-1} (not the individual), is that although there were conditions to Israel dwelling in the land (see Lev. 26:14--39; Deut. 28:15--68), the covenant God made with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob giving the land of Canaan to them and their descendants is [everlasting]{.class-1} (Gen. 17:7, 13, 19; 1 Chron. 16:13--18; Psa. 105:6--11). That covenant has [never]{.class-1} been negated and is as binding today as day and night (Jer. 32:25--26).

That means that contrary to the positions taken by the Muslim Brotherhood, the "Palestinian Authority" (news media "double speak" for the [Palestinian Liberation Organization]{.class-1}---a terrorist organizations responsible for the deaths of hundreds of innocent civilians), the UN, the EU, the Obama administration, and the [Roman Catholic Vatican State headed up by the Pope,]{.class-1} the land of Palestine---ALL of it---belongs to the JEW; not any Moslem, Roman Catholic, Arab "Palestinian," or "international" body. However God punishes His people, He will never break that covenant (Lev. 26:44). It is on the basis of that covenant that the Lord establishes a [new]{.class-1} covenant with the nation at His return (Jer. 31:31--34), and that covenant will be ["an everlasting covenant"]{.class-0} that will never be broken by either side (Ezek. 16:60--62).

Verse 2: ["And ye shall make no league with the inhabitants of this land]{.class-0} \[Deut. 7:2\][; ye shall throw down their altars]{.class-0} \[Deut. 12:3\][."]{.class-0} You are told in the New Testament:

["Be not unequally yoked together with unbelievers: for what fellowship hath righteousness with unrighteousness? ]{.class-0}\[none\][ and what communion hath light with darkness?]{.class-0} \[none\][ And what concord hath Christ with Belial?]{.class-0} \[none\][ or what part hath he that believeth with an infidel?]{.class-0} \[the answer should be [none,]{.class-1} but from listening to some of these professors at Fundamental Christian Colleges attack the Book, you might think otherwise\][ And what agreement hath the temple of God with idols?"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 6:14--16). There should be [no]{.class-1} agreement. You shouldn't be "getting along" with a lost world.

Now you may have to work with them and buy from them. I mean, be civil; you don't have to be an obnoxious jerk. But you don't have to like what they like, love what they love, or be interested in the same stuff they are. You don't adopt or honor their gods. When it comes to [your]{.class-1} car, [your]{.class-1} home, and [your]{.class-1} family, you [get rid]{.class-1} of their gods; you [break]{.class-1} them; you [throw them in the trash.]{.class-1}

["But ye have not obeyed my voice . . . Wherefore I also said, I will not drive them out from before you"]{.class-0} (vss. 2--3). Unlike the New Testament, the Old Testament promises were conditioned on [works.]{.class-1} So the application to the New Testament believer here would be to [service,]{.class-1} not to [salvation.]{.class-1} Your [rewards]{.class-1} and [blessings]{.class-1} as a believer are conditioned on your works, but when it comes to your eternal destiny, your works have nothing to do with it (Eph. 2:8--9). Salvation is a [free gift]{.class-1} (Rom. 5:15--18), but when it comes to an [inheritance]{.class-1} in Christ's kingdom, that's a different story.

If you are going to ["reign with him,"]{.class-0} you will have to [suffer]{.class-1} with Him (2 Tim. 2:12). If you want to ["inherit the kingdom of God"]{.class-0} ([not be saved]{.class-1}), you can't be involved in ["the works of the flesh"]{.class-0} (Gal. 5:19--21; 1 Cor. 6:9--10).

["But they shall be as thorns in your sides, and their gods shall be a snare unto you"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). That's good New Testament doctrine. Being a friend of the world can hurt you (James 4:4--6). Some Christians can be ensnared by Satan (1 Tim. 3:7) and be ["taken captive by him at his will"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 2:26) through sin (Prov. 29:6).

The picture here for the New Testament believer is what happens when he won't fight the sin in his life. The old-time Methodist evangelist Sam Jones used to say, "You keep just as many sins as you [want]{.class-1} to keep." In other words, whatever sin is in your life is the sin you [allow]{.class-1} to be there. If you hated it enough, you would fight it until you got rid of it. But the sin to which you give place is what harasses you and brings you down.

When it comes to the Israelites here, the problem was they wouldn't make any [negative]{.class-1} commitments to God (see our remarks under Josh. 24:16--24 in that Commentary). They promised to [serve God]{.class-1}---positive, but they wouldn't promise to [get rid of their idols---]{.class-1}negative. So if the "Gospel" you preach is [all positive,]{.class-1} you have [another gospel]{.class-1} (Gal. 1:8; 2 Cor. 11:4). The true Gospel is 75% [negative:]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-28}["Christ died ]{.class-0}\[negative\][ for our sins ]{.class-0}\[negative\][ . . . And that he was buried]{.class-0} \[negative\][, and that he rose again the third day according to the scriptures ]{.class-0}\[positive\]["]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 15:3--4).

Salvation requires both the positive [and]{.class-1} the negative. It is ["repentance toward God ]{.class-0}\[negative\][, and faith toward our Lord Jesus Christ]{.class-0} \[positive\]["]{.class-0} (Acts 20:21). Paul commended his Thessalonian converts because they ["turned to God from idols]{.class-0} \[negative\][ to serve the living and true God]{.class-0} \[positive\]["]{.class-0} (1 Thess. 1:9).

Every Christian should be an "iconoclast"---an [image breaker.]{.class-1} He should [kick]{.class-1} the world's "sacred cows." The world creates "gods" and "devils." The general rule of thumb is that if the world thinks a lot of it, God thinks it [stinks,]{.class-1} and if the world thinks it stinks, God thinks it's great (Luke 16:15; 2 Cor. 2:15--16). The world makes "gods" out of dope-heads, fornicators, and Marxists. Mark it down, when the world lifts up JFK, Martin Luther King Jr., Elvis Presley, Miley Cyrus, the Beatles, Frank Sinatra, "Lady Gaga," Slick Willie Clinton, Marilyn Monroe, and Pope John Paul II, that's a bunch no Christian should follow across the street. The Christian should kick 'em every chance he can because [those "cows" ain't sacred.]{.class-1}

6 And when Joshua had let the people go, the children of Israel went every man unto his inheritance to possess the land.

7 And the people served the LORD all the days of Joshua, and all the days of the elders that outlived Joshua, who had seen all the great works of the LORD, that he did for Israel.

8 And Joshua the son of Nun, the servant of the LORD, died, being an hundred and ten years old.

9 And they buried him in the border of his inheritance in Timnathheres, in the mount of Ephraim, on the north side of the hill Gaash.

10 And also all that generation were gathered unto their fathers: and there arose another generation after them, which knew not the LORD, nor yet the works which he had done for Israel.

11 And the children of Israel did evil in the sight of the LORD, and served Baalim:

12 And they forsook the LORD God of their fathers, which brought them out of the land of Egypt, and followed other gods, of the gods of the people that were round about them, and bowed themselves unto them, and provoked the LORD to anger.

13 And they forsook the LORD, and served Baal and Ashtaroth.

Verses 6--9 are a "recap" of Joshua 24:28--31, and we refer you to our comments on those verses in that Commentary. As long as Joshua was alive, and all the men who had served with Joshua and had seen what God had done in giving Israel the land, the people served God, but once that generation was gone, they lapsed into idolatry.

People tend to go by [sight,]{.class-1} not by [faith]{.class-1} (cf. 2 Cor. 5:7). The ones who [saw]{.class-1} what God did, they tended to stay right; then when the generation came up that never saw God do anything, they went all to pieces. People tend to have to [see]{.class-1} God [do]{.class-1} something before they really believe it.

That was Thomas' problem after the Resurrection. He skipped the Sunday night service where Jesus showed up to the other disciples, and when his buddies told him about the resurrected Christ, he said, ["Except I shall see in his hands the print of the nails, and put my finger into the print of the nails, and thrust my hand into his side, I will not believe"]{.class-0} (John 20:25). When Jesus did appear to Thomas, He told him, ["Thomas, because thou hast seen me, thou hast believed: blessed are they that have not seen, and yet have believed"]{.class-0} (John 20:29). The rule for the believer is supposed to be [faith, not sight]{.class-1} (2 Cor. 5:7); but that is not how most people operate.

Do you know why there are so many atheists in America today? It's because there have been several generations now who have never seen God [grow]{.class-1} anything. You won't find many farmers who are atheists; if you do, it is someone who has been messing with television or books by infidels. A farmer sees life come from a dead seed, and he knows he has nothing to do with that. That farmer can till the ground, fertilize it, plant the seed, water it if necessary (and many a farmer has been ruined by God shutting off the rain), and keep the weeds out; but unless [God]{.class-1} causes that seed to bring forth a plant and grow and bear fruit, that farmer has nothing. The psalmist wrote, ["He]{.class-0} \[i.e., God\][ causeth the grass to grow for the cattle, and herb for the service of man: that he may bring forth food out of the earth"]{.class-0} (Psa. 104:14).

You won't find many people raised up in the mountains who are atheists. That doesn't mean they're saved, but they realize there is a God (Theism). You can't see that snow in the Winter, everything coming back to life in the Spring, and those leaves in the Fall and not believe there is some higher Intelligence responsible for that wonder and majesty.

Atheism is a [city]{.class-1} thing, where the kid is raised around what [man]{.class-1} builds; it is an [educational]{.class-1} thing where the kid is trained in [man's]{.class-1} philosophy. But if that kid is out there in nature, he sees the One responsible for all that life and beauty that man could not do himself. I think every momma and daddy ought to give their child, around the time he or she is seven to twelve years old, a place out in the backyard to plant seeds and watch them grow. If they live in an apartment, give the kid a pot and some dirt, and let that boy or girl see God give life to something.

Even a sot drunk like Ulysses S. Grant could figure that out; he said the Bible was "the sheet anchor of your liberties . . . To the influence of THIS BOOK are we indebted for all the progress made in true civilization, and to this must we look as our guide in the future \[sorry, General, they dumped it back in 1963 for "sex education"\]. ['RIGHTEOUSNESS EXALTETH A NATION; BUT SIN IS A REPROACH TO ANY PEOPLE.']{.class-0}"

That wasn't "Ruckman" who said that; that was the commander of the Yankee forces during the Civil War and the eighteenth President of the United States. Do you know what the President who is on your twenty dollar bill (Andrew Jackson) said about the Bible? He said, "THAT BOOK, Sir, is the Rock upon which our republic rests." "Our republic" has gotten so far away from "THAT BOOK" that it is sunk down in the mire, the muck, and the quicksand; and it is about to go under for "the third time."

16 Nevertheless the LORD raised up judges, which delivered them out of the hand of those that spoiled them.

17 And yet they would not hearken unto their judges, but they went a whoring after other gods, and bowed themselves unto them: they turned quickly out of the way which their fathers walked in, obeying the commandments of the LORD; but they did not so.

18 And when the LORD raised them up judges, then the LORD was with the judge, and delivered them out of the hand of their enemies all the days of the judge: for it repented the LORD because of their groanings by reason of them that oppressed them and vexed them.

19 And it came to pass, when the judge was dead, that they returned, and corrupted themselves more than their fathers, in following other gods to serve them, and to bow down unto them; they ceased not from their own doings, nor from their stubborn way.

This is the pattern for the book of Judges, and it is consistent throughout. It is: 1. apostasy 2. repentance 3. deliverance 4. service (for as long as the judge lived) 5. apostasy again. And with number five, the cycle started over again. Verse 19 ends with: ["they ceased not from their own doings, nor from their stubborn way."]{.class-0}

["The LORD raised up judges"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). There are [seventeen]{.class-1} judges mentioned by name altogether between the books of Judges and 1 Samuel (eighteen if the ["Bedan"]{.class-0} of 1 Sam. 12:11 is not one of the judges given in the book of Judges). Thirteen are in Judges, and four are in 1 Samuel. The ones in Judges are: 1. Othniel, 2. Ehud, 3. Shamgar, 4. Deborah, 5. Barak, 6. Gideon, 7. Tola, 8. Jair, 9. Jephthah, 10. Ibzan, 11. Elon, 12. Abdon, 13. Samson. The four in the book of 1 Samuel are: Eli, Samuel, Joel, and Abiah.

["Which DELIVERED them out of the hand of those that spoiled them."]{.class-0} So the job of the judge was not only to bring the people back to keeping the Law of God, it was to physically deliver Israel from her enemies. So like Joshua, the judges were [military]{.class-1} leaders as well as [spiritual]{.class-1} leaders. As we stated in the Introduction, this is a picture of the Lord Jesus at His Second Advent.

["And so all Israel shall be saved: as it is written, There shall come out of Sion the Deliverer, and shall turn away ungodliness from Jacob"]{.class-0} (Rom. 11:26).

Paul's quoting Isaiah 59:20, and the Gentile nations coming against Israel at the end of the Tribulation is in the verse immediately proceeding it (Isa. 59:19 cf. Zech. 14:2--3). So as we saw in our study on Joshua (see the Introduction to that Commentary), the Second Advent will show up in type, and occasionally in direct prophecy, throughout the book.

Verse 17: ["but they went a whoring after other gods."]{.class-0} Idolatry is likened here to [sexual sin]{.class-1} (see our comments on vss. 11, 13 above). That's [literal]{.class-1} in the case of Baal worship (see Num. 25:1--2), and the application is made [spiritually]{.class-1} to the New Testament believer.

["Ye ADULTERERS and ADULTERESSES, know ye not that the FRIENDSHIP OF THE WORLD is enmity with God? whosoever therefore will be a friend of the world is the enemy of God"]{.class-0} (James 4:4).

When you get to fooling around with the sinful world system---[conforming]{.class-1} to it (Rom. 12:2) and [loving]{.class-1} it (1 John 2:15--16)---that's like a wife stepping out on her husband (see 2 Cor. 11:2--3).

Verse 18 says God sent the judges to deliver the people because ["it repented the LORD because of their groanings by reason of them that oppressed them and vexed them."]{.class-0} Here, as in Genesis 6:6 (see our comments on that verse in that Commentary), the word ["repented"]{.class-0} means God changed His mind about what He had done. ["Their groanings by reason of them that oppressed them"]{.class-0} were not merely groaning under an oppressive burden; those Jews were crying to the Lord in repentance (see 3:9, 15, 4:3, 6:7, 10:10, 15--16).

So while there are fixed points of prophecy of which the Lord will [never]{.class-1} repent (Num. 23:19), when it comes to judgment, repentance on the part of man can change God's mind (see Jon. 3:5--10; 1 Kings 21:29). Jesus expresses it this way in Revelation 2:16--["Repent; OR ELSE." "Or else"]{.class-0} what? ["Or else"]{.class-0} [you'll get what you had coming to you if you didn't repent.]{.class-1}

This is something John Calvin never could get. Calvin teaches that "repentance" is a gift from God given only to the [elect.]{.class-1} To the contrary, repentance was granted to people [as a group:]{.class-1} first to the [Jews]{.class-1} (Acts 5:31) and then to the [Gentiles]{.class-1} (Acts 11:18). Repentance isn't just a "gift," it's a [command.]{.class-1} And it's a command to every man, woman, and child on earth; not just "the elect."

["And the times of this ignorance God winked at; but now commandeth ALL MEN EVERYWHERE to repent"]{.class-0} (Acts 17:30).

Are you lost? Are you not one of "the elect"? Do you know what I would do if I were you? Well, I wouldn't sit around and wait for God to "unconditionally elect" me with "irresistible grace." Nor would I resign myself to Hell because I was under some "decree of reprobation." I would [repent as God commanded me]{.class-1} and exercise ["faith toward our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} (Acts 20:21) just as quick as I could, because Jesus said, ["him that cometh to me I will in no wise cast out"]{.class-0} (John 6:37).

["It repented the LORD because of their groanings by reason of them that oppressed them."]{.class-0} The immediate application in the context is to [God's people,]{.class-1} not the lost. God does not enjoy seeing His children oppressed and vexed by a lost world (see 2 Pet. 2:7--8); He doesn't get a "kick" out of hearing them groan under a burden of sin. It doesn't do a thing for Him to see the saints take a "lickin'" at the hands of the Devil. If the Lord had His "druthers," ["all should come to repentance"]{.class-0} (2 Pet. 3:9)---saved (Rev. 2:5) or lost (Acts 26:20).

["They ceased not from their own doings"]{.class-0} (vs. 19). That's the trouble we all have---SELF. Some of the "brethren" say about me, "Ruckman is his own worst enemy." I've got news for them---ANY MAN is his own worst enemy.

The greatest Christian who ever lived said, ["For that which I do I allow not: for what I would, that do I not; but what I hate, that do I . . . For the good that I would I do not: but the evil which I would not, that I do. Now if I do that I would not, it is no more I that do it, but sin that dwelleth in me. I find then a law, that, when I would do good, evil is present with me. For I delight in the law of God after the inward man: But I see another law in my members, warring against the law of my mind, and bringing me into captivity to the law of sin which is in my members" ]{.class-0}(Rom. 7:15, 19--23).

["Nor from their stubborn way."]{.class-0} Samuel said, ["stubbornness is as iniquity and idolatry"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 15:23). Stubbornness is wanting your own way to the point where neither God nor man can move you from it. You will either go your way or God's way, but it won't be both. The Lord said in Isaiah 55:8, ["For my thoughts are not your thoughts, neither are your ways my ways."]{.class-0} It has to be one or the other because they are [not the same.]{.class-1} If you want the victory over self, you have to ["yield yourselves unto God"]{.class-0} and [not]{.class-1} ["yield ye your members as instruments of unrighteousness unto sin"]{.class-0} (Rom. 6:13).

20 And the anger of the LORD was hot against Israel; and he said, Because that this people hath transgressed my covenant which I commanded their fathers, and have not hearkened unto my voice;

21 I also will not henceforth drive out any from before them of the nations which Joshua left when he died:

22 That through them I may prove Israel, whether they will keep the way of the LORD to walk therein, as their fathers did keep it, or not.

23 Therefore the LORD left those nations, without driving them out hastily; neither delivered he them into the hand of Joshua.

The passage gives you the reason God left some of the heathen people after Joshua conquered the land. Here it is given as a postscript to Israel's apostasy, but in the next chapter (3:1--7), it is given as the prelude. In other words, God left those heathen people to test the next generation of Israelites to see if they would follow the Lord on their own without a Moses or Joshua around to put the fear of God in them (Josh. 4:14), and [they failed the test.]{.class-1} Joshua had told them to put away their false gods they had kept as they conquered the cities of those heathen people (Josh 24:9--23). If they didn't, God wouldn't drive out the remnant of the heathen, and He would use them to punish His people for their idolatry (Josh. 23:11--13).

The same thing is true in the Christian life. When you get saved, God takes away some sins right away to encourage you in the fight, but others He leaves to see if you [will fight]{.class-1} and if you will [trust Him]{.class-1} to give you the victory. Every dog has just enough fleas to remind him he is a dog, and every Christian has just enough sins to remind him he is a sinner---albeit a [saved]{.class-1} sinner. The question is not will you sin as a believer. It's what do you do when you do sin; it's what are you doing to [resist]{.class-1} sin. The answers to those questions are found in 1 John 1 and Romans 6 (which see).

The thing to remember is that when God sends a test or trial your way, it's not for your defeat or humiliation. It's for your [good.]{.class-1}

["Who fed thee in the wilderness with manna, which thy fathers knew not, that he might humble thee, and that he might PROVE THEE, TO DO THEE GOOD AT THY LATTER END" ]{.class-0}(Deut. 8:16).

The New Testament promise is: ["And we know that all things work together for good to them that love God, to them who are the called according to his purpose"]{.class-0} (Rom. 8:28).

When God puts you through a trial, it's for your [benefit,]{.class-1} to make you a [better]{.class-1} Christian. Job said, ["But he knoweth the way that I take: when he hath tried me, I shall come forth as gold"]{.class-0} (Job 23:10). Gold is put through the refining process to [remove impurities.]{.class-1} When God leaves a sin in your life, it's for the purpose of [you overcoming it,]{.class-1} not it overcoming you. The struggle against the world, the flesh, and the Devil is to [purify you,]{.class-1} not enslave you to them. But it starts with you throwing out the "idols" in your life (2 Cor. 10:5), submitting yourself to God (James 4:7), yielding the members of your body to Him (Rom. 6:13), and then fighting ["the good fight of faith"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 6:12, 1:18; Eph. 6:10--13).

[]{#section-0_1_3264d4a21292d8b4_708d.xhtml}

Chapter 3

3:1 Now these are the nations which the LORD left, to prove Israel by them, even as many of Israel as had not known all the wars of Canaan;

2 Only that the generations of the children of Israel might know, to teach them war, at the least such as before knew nothing thereof;

3 Namely, five lords of the Philistines, and all the Canaanites, and the Sidonians, and the Hivites that dwelt in mount Lebanon, from mount Baalhermon unto the entering in of Hamath.

4 And they were to prove Israel by them, to know whether they would hearken unto the commandments of the LORD, which he commanded their fathers by the hand of Moses.

5 And the children of Israel dwelt among the Canaanites, Hittites, and Amorites, and Perizzites, and Hivites, and Jebusites:

6 And they took their daughters to be their wives, and gave their daughters to their sons, and served their gods.

7 And the children of Israel did evil in the sight of the LORD, and forgat the LORD their God, and served Baalim and the groves.

The passage is another synopsis of the apostasy of Israel. Notice again that it was [God]{.class-1} who left some of those heathen peoples there in Canaan. Not only did He do it as a [punishment]{.class-1} (see 2:23, 14), but also to [teach]{.class-1} the children of Israel something (vs. 2).

Liberals think war is the worst scourge on earth, and that the way to get rid of war is to bring everyone together in one big, happy family (the modern "buzz word" is "global community")---in other words, [integration.]{.class-1} But God ["is a man of war"]{.class-0} (Exod. 15:3), and He teaches His people[ "to war"]{.class-0} (Psa. 18:34, 144:1). That will continue until the\
"Commander-in-Chief" shows up to put down all opposition in battle (Rev. 19:11--16 cf. Isa. 2:4).

To carry out war effectively, it has to be [taught.]{.class-1} The German staff officers were trained at the Prussian [War College;]{.class-1} the Army, Navy, and Air Force here in the U.S. all have their own War Colleges. The Army post at Ft. Benning in Georgia has an Armor [School]{.class-1} and an Infantry [School.]{.class-1} You sit in a [classroom,]{.class-1} listen to [lectures from professors,]{.class-1} and take [exams.]{.class-1} There are "school solutions" you learn for different situations and terrains.

As a child of God who has been ["chosen . . . to be a soldier"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 2:4), a Christian should [learn to fight]{.class-1} spiritually. He should learn who his enemies are; he should learn his "Table of Equipment" (Eph. 6:10--17); he should learn techniques for dealing with the enemy and put them into practice. The problem with 90% of the churches in this country is that the individual believers in those congregations have never been taught how to fight (and I don't mean [each other]{.class-1}). They've been taught how to attend, how to give, and how to get along with folks; [but not how to fight.]{.class-1} You have to [fight]{.class-1} (1 Tim. 6:12).

"Sure I must FIGHT if I would reign---

Increase my courage, Lord!

I'll bear the toil, endure the pain,

Supported by Thy word."

I once asked Jimmy Stroud, the director of the Union Mission up in Memphis, Tennessee, what all the bums who came through his rescue mission had in common. He said, "None of them have ever won a battle in life." If you want to be a spiritual bum, I'll tell you how to do it. Just [don't fight back]{.class-1} when faced with opposition from the world, the flesh, and the Devil. Do nothing to stop the sin in your life. Just try to "get along" with everybody no matter what. That's the way to become a spiritual bum.

To try to please the wife, they [quit.]{.class-1} They get sick, they [quit.]{.class-1} They lose their job, they [quit.]{.class-1} They get a disease, they [quit.]{.class-1} They get insulted, they[ quit.]{.class-1} Their kids turn against them, they [quit.]{.class-1} They have some hard luck, they [quit.]{.class-1} [You can't quit;]{.class-1} you've got to fight!

There was always one player in the NFL I liked: it was Larry Csonka. I liked to watch him play. He had no grace or finesse at all. He had legs like a horse. I saw him once go through the line with three guys on him; he went five yards before they brought him down. He used to wear his helmet down low over his eyes; and someone asked him, "Why do you do that? You can't see where you're going." He said, "If I can't see where I'm going, they can't tell where I'm coming."

I used to watch him play, and I would yell at the TV screen, "Give the ball to Csonk; give it to Csonk!" I mean, you could count on him for three or four yards each play. If they had given it to him, he could have had first and ten within four plays through the whole game. He would bend his head over, double up, and those feet would go clomp, clomp, clomp right through the line.

That's the way to be as a Christian. Just plow through the opposition. If the enemy knocks you down, get up and go again. Keep on getting up and going forward until you reach the goal line (1 Cor. 9:24--26), but don't let the enemy just run roughshod over you. Make them pay for knocking you down.

Back to Judges 3, verse 3. God left those heathen people scattered all throughout Israel. The Philistines were down south in Judah, along the Mediterranean coast. Mt. Lebanon and Mt. Hermon are up north above Lake Huleh.

In verse 5, of the seven nations Joshua was commanded to wipe out in Joshua 3:10, only six are listed here. The [Girgashites]{.class-1} are missing here as they are from Joshua 9:1, and you can see our comments on that verse in that Commentary for the [possible]{.class-1} reason why.

Notice again the connection of [sex]{.class-1} to [idolatry]{.class-1} (see our remarks on 2:13) in verses 6--7. That's what happened at Baal-peor back in Numbers 25.
