When Balaam wasn't able to curse Israel, he taught Balak how to get God to curse them: have the Jewish boys marry the Moabite girls and have those Jews sign an agreement to raise the children in "the church." In the meantime, the girls put the "pressure" on the boys (if you know what I mean) to attend their "church." It's a [sex]{.class-1} job. That was called ["the doctrine of Balaam"]{.class-0} in Revelation 2:14.

"But I have a few things against thee, because thou hast there them that hold the doctrine of Balaam, who taught Balac to cast a stumblingblock before the children of Israel, TO EAT THINGS SACRIFICED UNTO IDOLS, AND TO COMMIT FORNICATION."

Verse 7: notice ["the groves."]{.class-0} The Israelites were forbidden to plant a grove of trees near the Brazen Altar at the Tabernacle (Deut. 16:21). The original planter of a grove was [Abraham]{.class-1} (Gen. 21:33), but that was [before the Law.]{.class-1} Also, no altar was mentioned in connection with Abraham's grove. The reason groves were forbidden under the Law was because by the time of Moses, the groves were connected with the [idols]{.class-1} in them (Exod. 34:13; Deut. 7:5, 12:3). The image in the middle of a grove of trees is still a common practice in the Roman Catholic Church to this day.

To make sure you won't associate the groves with Roman Catholic "veneration of images," the new "Bibles" either refuse to translate the Hebrew word [asherah]{.class-1} (to make the text more "accurate," of course; if the [AV]{.class-1} is accurate, they change the text to make it "clearer." Any excuse to [change what God said]{.class-1}---Rom. 1:25), or they translated the word as "idol(s)." The problem is, ["images"]{.class-0} and ["groves"]{.class-0} are [two separate things]{.class-1} in 1 Kings 14:23; 2 Kings 17:10, 23:14; 2 Chronicles 14:3, 24:18, 31:1, 34:3--4; and Isaiah 17:8, 27:9. While it is true that the word [asherah]{.class-1} can refer to images carved from the wood of a tree cut from a grove (2 Chron. 33:3 cf. 2 Kings 21:7), that still doesn't change the fact that the ["asherah"]{.class-1} were [living trees]{.class-1} that were [planted]{.class-1} (Deut. 16:21), not carved images that were set up.

8 Therefore the anger of the LORD was hot against Israel, and he sold them into the hand of Chushanrishathaim king of Mesopotamia: and the children of Israel served Chushanrishathaim eight years.

9 And when the children of Israel cried unto the LORD, the LORD raised up a deliverer to the children of Israel, who delivered them, even Othniel the son of Kenaz, Caleb's younger brother.

10 And the Spirit of the LORD came upon him, and he judged Israel, and went out to war: and the LORD delivered Chushanrishathaim king of Mesopotamia into his hand; and his hand prevailed against Chushanrishathaim.

11 And the land had rest forty years. And Othniel the son of Kenaz died.

This is the first of the heathen servitudes brought on Israel for their idolatry.[ "Chushanrishathaim"]{.class-0} is the second longest word in the Bible (["Mahershalalhashbaz"]{.class-0} in Isa. 8:1 is the longest). He was ["king of Mesopotamia"]{.class-0} (vs. 8). Mesopotamia is the land between the Tigris and Euphrates Rivers ([Meso]{.class-1}---"middle"; [potamia]{.class-1}---"river." Mesopotamia is the land in the middle of the rivers). Although it can refer to all the land from Syria in the north to Shinar in the south (Acts 7:2), the reference here is probably to the northern part in Syria (Gen. 24:10; Deut. 23:4).

In regards to Israel serving ["Chushanrishathaim eight years"]{.class-0} (vs. 8), one should recall the words of the Jewish leaders to Christ in John 8:33.

"They answered him, We be Abraham's seed, and were never in bondage to any man: how sayest thou, Ye shall be made free?"

["Never in bondage to any man"]{.class-0}?! What do you call this here?! The text says God ["sold them into the hand of Chushanrishathaim"]{.class-0}: they were [bondslaves.]{.class-1} They were in bondage to the Moabites (vss. 12--14), the Canaanites (4:2), the Midianites and the Amalekites (6:1--3), and the Philistines and Ammonites (10:7). Those are just the ones in [one book.]{.class-1} They don't include the Babylonians, the Persians, the Greeks, and the Romans (to whom the Jews were in bondage at the time of John 8). Awfully short memory there, wouldn't you say?

But the spiritual application made by Christ should not be lost in the irony of the ludicrous statement made by those Pharisees and Sadducees. Jesus said, ["Whosoever committeth sin is the servant of sin"]{.class-0} (John 8:34). That is where the application of verse 8 here in Judges 3 hits home for us.

The pattern of sin, repentance, deliverance, and sin is all too familiar to the believer. One minute we (and I include myself here, for this was my experience when I first got saved) are shouting on the mountain, and the next we are pouting in the valley. Of course, if you are in the word daily and consistent in your prayer life, that should stabilize after you have been saved a while. But if you do not reckon yourself dead to sin (Rom. 6:11), and if you are not yielding the members of your body ["as instruments of righteousness unto God"]{.class-0} (Rom. 6:13), you are not going to live a victorious Christian life; sin [will]{.class-1} ["have dominion over you"]{.class-0} in that case (cf. Rom. 6:14).

Back to Judges 3. The first judge raised up by God to deliver Israel was ["Othniel the son of Kenaz, Caleb's younger brother"]{.class-0} (vs. 9). This was Caleb's son-in-law from chapter 1 who gained Caleb's daughter in marriage by taking the city of Debir (see 1:11-13). So this is a man who learned faith and courage from his uncle and father-in-law (see Josh. 14:6--13 and comments in that Commentary).

["And the Spirit of the LORD came upon him"]{.class-0} (vs. 10). Two things about this part of the passage: the first is the word ["Spirit."]{.class-0} Some [King James Versions]{.class-1} (usually from the old Oxford text) don't capitalize the word, while the Cambridge editions do. Of course, now both publishers have tried to come together and standardize the two texts, so you don't often find such differences in Bibles published since around 2000 onward.

Nevertheless, some of the more zealous brethren consider a thing like that "s" not being capitalized there in verse 10 a "Satanic corruption," and it's nothing of the sort. Either way is correct.

You see, in the Old Testament, the Holy Spirit was not revealed as a [person.]{.class-1} Up until John 15, the Spirit was only revealed as an [influence]{.class-1} from God. In the Bible, you will find Holy Spirit given as ["holy spirit"]{.class-0} (Psa. 51:11), ["holy Spirit"]{.class-0} (Isa. 63:10--11; Eph. 1:13, 4:30; 1 Thess. 4:8), and, of course, ["Holy Spirit"]{.class-0} (Luke 11:13).

The second thing to note here is the Holy Spirit [coming on]{.class-1} Othniel. The teaching put forth by Scofield (see his notes on Mal. 2:15 \[ Holy Spirit, O.T. summary\] and Acts 2:4 \[Holy Spirit, N.T. summary\]) is that in the Old Testament, the Holy Spirit came [on]{.class-1} men, but [not in]{.class-1} them. This is the position taken by most Fundamentalists.

That is [not true.]{.class-1} The Holy Spirit did indeed come [into ]{.class-1}men. Bezaleel, the main craftsman chosen by God to make the Tabernacle, was ["filled . . . with the spirit of God"]{.class-0} (Exod. 31:3). The Holy Spirit was said to be ["in"]{.class-0} both Joseph (Gen. 41:38) and Daniel (Dan. 4:9). Isaiah 63:11 says the Holy Spirit was ["within"]{.class-0} Moses. As a matter of fact, 1 Peter 1:10--11 says the Holy Spirit ["was in"]{.class-0} all the Old Testament prophets.

With such clear statements in the Scriptures, why do Fundamentalists take the Scofield position? The reason is that the Fundamentalists believe that people were saved in the Old Testament the same way they are saved in the New Testament. Pure, unadulterated [horse feathers!]{.class-1} Nobody was born again in the Old Testament; no one was redeemed permanently from all sin; no one was justified solely by faith without works involved (not even Abraham---James 2:21; see our comments on Rom.4:2 in that Commentary). Old Testament saints weren't adopted, they weren't spiritually circumcised, they weren't predestinated to Christ's image, and if all that were not enough, they didn't even go to the same place you go when you die as a Christian. How could they possibly be the same?

The Fundamentalists say, "In the Old Testament they looked forward to the cross; in the New Testament we look back to the cross." Standard [baloney.]{.class-1} Of course the atonement of Christ was prophesied all through the Old Testament, but you understand that because you have a complete Bible in your hands. [They didn't.]{.class-1} Those Old Testament prophets didn't even [understand]{.class-1} the prophecies they made about "the cross" (1 Pet. 1:10--12). Listen, people, if the disciples who walked with Jesus and were personally taught by Him for three years didn't understand "the cross," what makes you think Abraham, Moses, David, Isaiah, et al., would when they had less revelation on the subject than the apostles had before the Resurrection (see our comments on Luke 18:34 in that Commentary)?

Having taken such a position, the Fundamentalists have no choice but to hold to Scofield's teachings on the subject, because in the Old Testament, the Holy Spirit [can]{.class-1} (and [does]{.class-1}) [leave]{.class-1} a person. He could have left David (Psa. 51:11); He did leave Saul and never came back (1 Sam. 16:14); He left Samson but did come back (Judg. 16:20, 28--30; Heb. 11:32). That being the case, the Fundamentalists figure this: well, in the New Testament, once the Holy Spirit comes to dwell in a believer, He won't leave (Eph. 1:13--14, 4:30; Heb. 13:5); so the Holy Spirit only comes "on" someone in the Old Testament, which is why He can leave him. Unfortunately, such a position completely contradicts the clear statements of Scripture (see remarks above).

The truth is that the Holy Spirit did not indwell the Old Testament believers in the [same way]{.class-1} He indwells believers today. When the Holy Spirit comes to live in your body as a New Testament believer (1 Cor. 6:19), He makes you [one with Jesus Christ]{.class-1} (1 Cor. 12:12--13). He is the guarantee you will make it to Heaven to be just like your Saviour (2 Cor. 1:22, 5:5). In the Old Testament, Jesus Christ hadn't come yet, He hadn't died for anyone's sins, and He hadn't risen from the dead. So the ministry of the Holy Spirit in indwelling Old Testament believers was different from His ministry in indwelling the born-again child of God in the New Testament, and the difference is found in the [finished atonement of Jesus Christ.]{.class-1}

Verse 11 gives you a "preview" of the long amount of time covered by the events in the book of Judges. Between verse 10 and verse 12, [forty years]{.class-1} have passed. You will see the same thing in verse 30: between the time of Ehud and the beginning of chapter 4, [eighty years]{.class-1} pass. So before you get out of chapter 3, over 120 years have gone by (see vss. 8, 14).

12 And the children of Israel did evil again in the sight of the LORD: and the LORD strengthened Eglon the king of Moab against Israel, because they had done evil in the sight of the LORD.

13 And he gathered unto him the children of Ammon and Amalek, and went and smote Israel, and possessed the city of palm trees.

14 So the children of Israel served Eglon the king of Moab eighteen years.

["And the LORD strengthened Eglon the king of Moab against Israel, because they had done evil in the sight of the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 12). When a nation like America has enemies like Russia, Red China, North Korea, Iran, and Al-Qaeda, it is because that nation is [not living right.]{.class-1} If a country isn't doing right, God will raise up enemies against it. The New Testament deals with [individuals;]{.class-1} the Old Testament deals with [nations.]{.class-1} That is why America ignores the Old Testament. When a nation doesn't do right, the Lord will raise up enemies to fight against it.

Here, God raised up the [Moabites]{.class-1} on the east side of Jordan. The Moabite King, Eglon, enlists the help of the Ammonites and the Amalekites to fight against Israel. Moab and Ammon were the bastard children of Lot through incestuous relations with his daughters (Gen. 19:37--38); they were forbidden from becoming Jewish proselytes for ten generations (Deut. 23:3). Amalek was a grandson of Esau (Gen. 36:12); God swore continual war against the Amalekites until the very memory of them would be wiped out, because they fought against Israel in the wilderness when Moses led the people out of Egypt (Exod. 17:14--16).

We have already commented on ["the city of palm trees"]{.class-0} (vs. 13) under 1:16, which see. As we saw there, this is the city of Jericho, which was part of Benjamin's inheritance (Josh. 18:21), and it will be a Benjamite who delivers Israel out of the hand of Eglon (vs. 15).

15 But when the children of Israel cried unto the LORD, the LORD raised them up a deliverer, Ehud the son of Gera, a Benjamite, a man lefthanded: and by him the children of Israel sent a present unto Eglon the king of Moab.

16 But Ehud made him a dagger which had two edges, of a cubit length; and he did gird it under his raiment upon his right thigh.

17 And he brought the present unto Eglon king of Moab: and Eglon was a very fat man.

18 And when he had made an end to offer the present, he sent away the people that bare the present.

19 But he himself turned again from the quarries that were by Gilgal, and said, I have a secret errand unto thee, O king: who said, Keep silence. And all that stood by him went out from him.

20 And Ehud came unto him; and he was sitting in a summer parlour, which he had for himself alone. And Ehud said, I have a message from God unto thee. And he arose out of his seat.

21 And Ehud put forth his left hand, and took the dagger from his right thigh, and thrust it into his belly:

22 And the haft also went in after the blade; and the fat closed upon the blade, so that he could not draw the dagger out of his belly; and the dirt came out.

This is Ehud, the second judge. The Scriptures make a point of saying he was ["lefthanded"]{.class-0} (vs. 15). At this point, the expositors go off on a tangent with the "original Hebrew." This is best expressed in [The Treasury of Scripture Knowledge]{.class-1} (usually attributed to R. A. Torrey).

"Left handed: Heb. shut of his right hand. This Hebrew phrase intimates that, either through disease or disuse, he made little or no use of the right hand, but of his left only, and so was the less fit for war, because he would most likely wield a dagger awkwardly."

After that you can write B-A-L-O-N-E-Y. We are about to see how "awkwardly" Ehud wields a dagger. Lefthandedness, in this case, had nothing to do with "disease or disuse." It was an hereditary trait within the tribe of Benjamin, and far from making them "the less fit for war," it was an [advantage]{.class-1} to them. Judges 20:15--16 says the Benjamites had ["seven hundred chosen men lefthanded; every one could sling stones at AN HAIR BREADTH, AND NOT MISS."]{.class-0} You reckon such a skill would make them "fit for war"? And like many lefthanded people, a lot of those Benjamites were [ambidextrous]{.class-1} (1 Chron. 12:2). In fact, those lefthanded Benjamites were so "fit for war" that they whipped the combined armies of the other eleven tribes [twice]{.class-1} (Judg. 20:14--25).

"The less fit for war"? Hogwash! That's the kind of nonsense you get by going to the "original Hebrew" or the "original Greek" while ignoring the clear statements of Scripture in the language God gave you.

The advantage Ehud had in being lefthanded was that the Moabites weren't expecting it. A righthanded man would strap a weapon on his left side, and that would be the side searched by the King's guard. But being lefthanded, Ehud had his dagger strapped on his right side (vs. 16), and that wasn't searched.

["But Ehud made him a dagger which had two edges, of a cubit length"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). That's quite a "frog-sticker." It's a foot and a half long, the size of a short sword like the Roman legionnaires used.

The typology, of course, is obvious to the student of the Scriptures; it is a picture of the word of God.

["For the word of God is quick, and powerful, and sharper than any twoedged sword, piercing even to the dividing asunder of soul and spirit, and of the joints and marrow, and is a discerner of the thoughts and intents of the heart"]{.class-0} (Heb. 4:12).

The word of God is part of the Christian's armament (Eph. 6:17). He should carry it in his [hand]{.class-1} (Psa. 149:5--6) and in his [mouth]{.class-1} (Isa. 49:2). He is to use it to [draw blood]{.class-1} spiritually (Jer. 48:10).

One of the reasons people don't like the Bible is because it is a sword: it [cuts;]{.class-1} it [stabs.]{.class-1} Of course, it can be used either to cut out the gangrene and cancer or to gut you. How the sword works depends on [how it is received]{.class-1} (1 Thess. 2:13) and the [Lord's purpose]{.class-1} (Isa. 55:11), but the believer is to "strike true" with his sword and leave the results to God.

One time a preacher went to a fair. He was walking down the midway, looking at the carnival sideshows, and stopped to watch a knife-thrower. The knife-thrower threw twelve knives at his "beautiful assistant" up against a wall, completely outlining her body and never once hitting her. That preacher walked away from that praying, "Lord, help me never to preach like that."

The preaching of the word of God should be pointed; it should be convicting. The word [sermon]{.class-1} is from a Latin word that means "to thrust" or "to stab." If the preacher doesn't throw his "knife" so that it hits you where it hurts, spiritually, he is a failure as a preacher. Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "If a preacher don't make me feel mean, he's no good."

John Wesley would send his Methodist preachers out to preach in the town squares and the mining camps and the market places all over England. When they came back to report on how their preaching junket went, he would ask them two questions. He would ask, "Did anyone get saved?" If the preacher said no, Wesley would ask, "Then did anyone [get mad?"]{.class-1} Make them glad or make them sad or make them mad, but no one should walk away from a Bible sermon or Gospel presentation [neutral.]{.class-1} If you can't win a person to Christ, take out the sword and thrust it in and give the sinner something to think about and bother him as he goes away.

I remember one night sitting in a restaurant with a lawyer, witnessing to him. To get out of accepting Christ, he began to ask the typical infidel questions: Where did Cain get his wife? How could all the animals fit into the ark? You know, that kind of stuff. Whenever he would ask one of those questions, I would say, "That's easy," and open my Bible to the answer and make him read it. About the fourth time I did that, he put his hand on my Bible to try to shut it and said, "That's okay; that's okay." What was the problem? He wanted me to sheath the sword because I was cutting him to ribbons with it. Brethren, don't sheath the sword; it's the one weapon you've got that can judge the sinner no matter where he goes or what he does (Heb. 4:13; 2 Tim. 2:9). Don't let anyone intimidate you about the Book.

Now what's going on here is that Ehud is bringing tribute to Eglon and using it as an opportunity to get near the King so he can kill him. Verse 19 gives an indication that ["the city of palm trees"]{.class-0} of verse 13 is indeed the villages and fields connected with the Jericho destroyed by Joshua, for the place where Ehud brings the tribute to Eglon is near Gilgal, which was on the eastern border of Jericho (Josh. 4:19).

The commentators and expositors obsessed with the "original Hebrew" don't like the word ["quarries"]{.class-0} in verse 19 (and again in vs. 26) since the Hebrew word ([pesilim]{.class-1}) is translated as ["graven images"]{.class-0} in Deuteronomy 7:25. Accepting the [AV]{.class-1} as it stands in both passages, undoubtedly the ["quarries"]{.class-0} of Judges 3:19 are where the stone was cut to be graven into idols. The key to understanding passages like this is not "the originals"; it is [belief in the Book]{.class-1} (1 Thess. 2:13).

Under the pretense of delivering a secret communique to the King, Ehud gets Eglon alone in his ["summer parlour"]{.class-0} (vs. 20). The ["message from God"]{.class-0} turns out to be a [sword in the gut.]{.class-1} That was the "message" throughout the prophets. The ["message from God"]{.class-0} that Jeremiah delivered to the false prophets of his day was ["sword and famine"]{.class-0} (Jer. 14:15); it was Jehovah God who appointed ["the sword to slay"]{.class-0} (Jer. 15:3). The ["message from God"]{.class-0} to Jerusalem through Ezekiel was: ["I will bring the sword upon thee. I the LORD have spoken it"]{.class-0} (Ezek. 5:17). God said, ["When I bring the sword upon a land . . ."]{.class-0} (Ezek. 33:2). So Ehud wasn't exaggerating or being deceptive at all with Eglon when he said, ["I have a message from God unto thee,"]{.class-0} and then he thrust the dagger into his belly. God said, ["I have slain them by the words of my mouth"]{.class-0} (Hos. 6:5).

To understand what happens next, you have to go back up to verse 17 and pick up the description of Eglon's "physique." Verse 17 says, ["Eglon was a VERY FAT MAN."]{.class-0} That's an unkind thing to say; that's not in keeping with the "sweet spirit of Christ" that would never say anything bad about anyone. In fact, it's so unkind that the [Septuagint]{.class-1} ([Vaticanus]{.class-1} and [Alexandrinus,]{.class-1} both written over 300 years after the ascension of Christ) translates ["aish bria mad"]{.class-1} (Heb.---literally, "man fat very") as ["aner asteios sphodra"]{.class-1} (Gk.---literally, "man striking vehemently"), translated by Brenton as ["a very HANDSOME man."]{.class-1} The rendering is so absurd that no English translation picks up the [Septuagint's]{.class-1} reading.

Eglon is not just "fat," he is ["VERY fat."]{.class-0} He is so big that when Ehud thrusts the dagger into Eglon's belly, the fat swallows up the dagger, blade and haft (vs. 22), and Ehud can't draw it back out. With an eighteen-inch blade and another six inches or so for the haft, that dagger was a good two feet into that fellow. That shows you how ["very fat"]{.class-0} Eglon was.

While the dagger doesn't come out, something else does: ["and the dirt came out."]{.class-0} That's a polite way of saying [dung.]{.class-1} That blade went through Eglon's intestines, and the contents came out of the wound.

Now there are some great spiritual applications to be made in regards to using the word of God on the sinner. First, get alone with a sinner to deal with him like Ehud got alone with Eglon. A one-on-one "faceoff" is the best way to witness, if you can. That way, there are no "friends" there to "run interference" for the one with whom you are dealing.

When I was in the Army, I wasn't saved; in fact, I never met (to my knowledge) a real, openly professing Christian the entire time I was in. I just bet you, though, there were some in my barracks who were too intimidated to speak up. Knowing what I know now after dealing with hundreds of lost sinners from all walks of life, what I would recommend to any Christian in the Army, Navy, Air Force, Marines, or Coast Guard would be the first day in the barracks, just about the time things get quiet, to stand up and say, "Fellows, I have an announcement to make, and I know some of you will think I'm pretty stupid and a 'holy roller' for making it, and maybe I am. But I just want you fellows to know that I'm a Christian and love the Lord. I don't expect any of you to change your life for me, but if there are any other Christians here, I'd like to meet you and get to know you." I guarantee you that if there are any other Christians in that room, they will look you up later when their buddies aren't around so they can have some fellowship and encouragement in serving the Lord in what is becoming more and more a hostile environment.

I would do like Glen Schunk did back in World War II. Schunk was in the Army just like I was, but he was saved. He would get together with other Christians to pray for their unsaved buddies. They would pray for them by name for a while; then Glen would get with one of them alone and witness to him. When he led him to the Lord, he would bring the fellow into the prayer meeting, and then they would pray for one of that guy's unsaved buddies. Schunk started out with one like that; then two. It grew to ten, then twenty, then thirty, until there was a group of fifty or sixty Christians praying for their unsaved buddies.

That thing will work in a military setting or a factory or in most any kind of work environment. Find some Christians, get together, pray for a particular individual, then confront that individual one on one.

Be polite, like Ehud was, but [draw the sword.]{.class-1} Don't buy into the "friendship evangelism" of the "seeker sensitive" movement. You aren't going to win anybody to Jesus Christ merely by being sweet and kind and nice. It is the [Gospel]{.class-1} that ["is the power of God unto salvation"]{.class-0} (Rom. 1:16), and the Gospel is found in the incorruptible seed of the word of God (1 Pet. 1:23--25).

Draw the sword (Eph. 6:17) and draw blood (Jer. 48:10). Give them something like: ["except ye repent, ye shall all likewise perish"]{.class-0} (Luke 13:3) or ["how can ye escape the damnation of hell"]{.class-0} (Matt. 23:32) or ["it is appointed unto men once to die, but after this the judgment"]{.class-0} (Heb. 9:27). You don't have to be mean and nasty about it; just give it to them as a matter of fact and then turn around and walk out. The Holy Spirit will take up the work and shove that blade into their guts a little at a time. And remember, when [the word goes in, the dirt comes out]{.class-1} (John 15:3).

23 Then Ehud went forth through the porch, and shut the doors of the parlour upon him, and locked them.

24 When he was gone out, his servants came; and when they saw that, behold, the doors of the parlour were locked, they said, Surely he covereth his feet in his summer chamber.

25 And they tarried till they were ashamed: and, behold, he opened not the doors of the parlour; therefore they took a key, and opened them: and, behold, their lord was fallen down dead on the earth.

26 And Ehud escaped while they tarried, and passed beyond the quarries, and escaped unto Seirath.

27 And it came to pass, when he was come, that he blew a trumpet in the mountain of Ephraim, and the children of Israel went down with him from the mount, and he before them.

28 And he said unto them, Follow after me: for the LORD hath delivered your enemies the Moabites into your hand. And they went down after him, and took the fords of Jordan toward Moab, and suffered not a man to pass over.

29 And they slew of Moab at that time about ten thousand men, all lusty, and all men of valour; and there escaped not a man.

30 So Moab was subdued that day under the hand of Israel. And the land had rest fourscore years.

Ehud has just killed the King of the Moabites, the occupying army, and he is seeking now to make his escape. He locks the doors leading to the summer parlor where he had met privately with Eglon. He gets out and gets past the stone quarries by Gilgal (vs. 26 cf. vs. 19) to a place in Mt. Ephraim called ["Seirath"]{.class-0} (vss. 26--27).

Meanwhile, the King's servants are waiting outside the locked doors, figuring their master was taking a nap (["Surely he covereth his feet in his summer chamber"]{.class-0}---vs. 24 cf. 1 Sam. 24:3). The text says, ["they tarried till they were ashamed"]{.class-0} (vs. 25): they waited so long that they became ashamed of themselves for not making sure their master was all right. And of course, when they got a key and unlocked the door, they went in and found Eglon dead.

The spiritual application for the child of God is wasted time is lost opportunity. While you are standing around doing nothing, Christian, souls are passing into a Christless eternity.

Jesus told a parable about a householder who hired some men to work in his vineyard (Matt. 20:1--7). He hired some at six in the morning. He goes back to the marketplace at 9:00 a.m. and finds some men standing around doing nothing and hires them too. He does the same thing at noon and at three in the afternoon. Finally, at five in the evening, one hour before quitting time, he goes back to the marketplace and finds some more "lollygaggers." He says to them, ["Why stand ye here all the day idle?"]{.class-0} (Matt. 20:6), and ends up hiring them to work one hour. Why? Because the harvest had to come in before it was too late.

Christian, what's your excuse for not serving Jesus Christ? Is it because the work's unreasonable? No. The work may be hard, but it's not unreasonable. Paul called it ["your REASONABLE service"]{.class-0} (Rom. 12:1). Is the pay not right? Jesus said, ["whatsoever is RIGHT I will give you"]{.class-0} (Matt. 20:4), so it can't be that. You can't possibly have a problem with the employer; it's [Jesus Christ.]{.class-1} Can you think of a better employer than Him? I can't. Could it be you don't think the job is important enough? What could possibly be more important than rescuing lost sinners from Hell?

Back before World War I, there lived a young lady named Sadie Virginia Smithson. She came from a poor family in Johnson Falls, West Virginia. Sadie wanted to be a "somebody" in Johnson Falls, and all the high-class women in town belonged to a social club called the Laurel Literary Society. Sadie tried joining, but she got turned down because to join the Laurel Literary Society, a lady had to write something that got read publicly in one of the Society's meetings. So Sadie saved up her money to take a trip over to Europe so she could write something on "My Trip to Europe" that she would read to the Laurel Literary Society.

It took several years, but she finally made it over to Europe just in time for the start of World War I. She ended up on the Belgian border just as the Germans were coming through there like a cat through a wet paper bag. The car in which she was riding got lost and ended up by a wheat field where a battle had just taken place. There were dead and wounded men all around. One of the wounded near the car cried out for water, and she got out to go get some from a small creek they had passed not too far back. Her companions in the car were yelling at her to get back in the car so they could get out of there, but Sadie told them to go on without her.

All night long she was going around, giving men water, bandaging their wounds with strips of cloth from her dress, quoting Scripture to comfort them, taking messages from the dying to give to their loved ones later, and doing whatever she could. At dawn, an ambulance arrived with Belgian medics. The medical officer took one look at that poor bedraggled woman and said, "Who are you, and what in thunder are you doing here?"

Sadie replied, "I'm Sadie Virginia Smithson, and I've been holding hell back all night."

That doctor calmed down and said, "Well, Miss Sadie Virginia, I'm glad you held some of it back, for everybody else in the world was letting it loose last night."

As she was relating her story to someone on the sea voyage home, the person said, "The Laurel Literary Society will be glad to have you now." But Sadie was no longer interested in joining the Laurel Literary Society. She said, "I've been face to face with war and death and hell and God. Do you reckon any of those little old things matter now?" When asked what did matter, she replied, "Nothing but God and love and doing things for folks."

Christian, the most important thing you can do in this life is to do the job God wants you to do to the folks to whom He sends you. Don't stand around idle your entire life until it's too late.

Back to Judges 3. Ehud is up in the hill country of Mt. Ephraim and blows a trumpet to gather the Israelites to battle---a type of the return of the Lord Jesus Christ in power.

["Blow ye the trumpet in Zion, and sound an alarm in my holy mountain: let all the inhabitants of the land tremble: for the day of the LORD cometh, for it is nigh at hand"]{.class-0} (Joel 2:1).

["But I will send a fire upon Moab]{.class-0} \[which happens at the Second Advent---Judg. 5:5; Obad. 18; Isa. 34:8--10; Hab. 3:5; 2 Thess. 1:8\][, and it shall devour the palaces of Kerioth]{.class-0} \[the home of the Son of Perdition---John 17:12 cf. John 6:70--71. [Iscariot]{.class-1} means "man of Kerioth"\][: and Moab shall die with tumult, with shouting, and with the sound of the trumpet"]{.class-0} (Amos 2:2).

["The great day of the LORD is near . . . A day of trumpet and alarm against the fenced cities, and against the high towers"]{.class-0} (Zeph. 1:14, 16).

["And the LORD shall be seen over them, and his arrow shall go forth as the lightning: and the Lord GOD shall blow the trumpet, and shall go with whirlwinds of the south"]{.class-0} (Zech. 9:14).

Another picture of Christ is found in verse 28. Ehud tells those Israelites, ["Follow after me."]{.class-0} Obviously that's a type of Jesus telling His disciples, ["Follow me,"]{.class-0} and you can see our comments on that command under Luke 5:27 in that Commentary. In regards to the Second Advent, the cross-reference would be Revelation 19:14, where the armies of Heaven (see 2 Thess. 1:7) follow Christ at the Battle of Armageddon.

["The fords of Jordan"]{.class-0} in verse 28 would be the same fords the spies used to enter the land when they came to Jericho (see our comments on Josh. 2:7, 3:6 in that Commentary). The Israelites take the fords and prevent the Moabite army from retreating across Jordan to their homeland.

Now while the Moabites may have taken Jericho with the help of the Ammonites and Amalekites (vs. 13), the army they left in Canaan to occupy the land was the elite troops---["all lusty, and all men of valour"]{.class-0} (vs. 29). Once Israel got right with God, they were able to do what they weren't able to do back in verses 12--13: take on 10,000 elite Moabite troops and whip them. Why? Because back up in verse 12, ["the LORD strengthened Eglon the king of Moab against Israel, because they had done evil in the sight of the LORD."]{.class-0} Eighteen years later (vs. 14), once Israel had gotten right, the Lord delivered the Moabites into the hands of Israel (vs. 28).

When David took on the giant, he said, ["And all this assembly shall know that the LORD saveth not with sword and spear: for the battle is the LORD'S, and he will give you into our hands"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 17:47). Brethren, if God is against you, it doesn't matter how many Seals, Rangers, Green Berets, "Delta Force," tanks, automatic weapons, "RPGs," ICBMs, SAMs, Tomahawk missiles, or nuclear warheads you have. If the Lord is against you, [you are a dead duck.]{.class-1}

Brethren, the way this country has been living, the Lord has ["a controversy"]{.class-0} with it (Isa. 34:8; Jer. 25:31). Once ["the iniquity"]{.class-0} of this nation is ["full"]{.class-0} (see Gen. 15:16), then it's going to be "all she wrote" for the United States of America, and it won't matter how big your military is. God can bring it down with a rag-tag force that is under-manned, under-armed, under-clothed, under-fed, and under-financed. Why? Because it is [the Lord]{.class-1} who decides the outcome of a battle or a war, and He will decide it based on the [obedience]{.class-1} of a people to His [revealed word]{.class-1} and [His own purposes.]{.class-1}

31 And after him was Shamgar the son of Anath, which slew of the Philistines six hundred men with an ox goad: and he also delivered Israel.

The verse shows you that not all the judges in the book of Judges are consecutive. Ehud is operating in central Canaan against Moabites who have taken Jericho. While that is going on, the Philistines are invading Judah in the south, and God raises up ["Shamgar the son of Anath"]{.class-0} against them.

Shamgar has to use an ox goad as a weapon because the Philistines didn't allow the Israelites to make any weapons (see Judg. 5:6--8).

["Now there was no smith found throughout all the land of Israel: for the Philistines said, Lest the Hebrews make them swords or spears: But all the Israelites went down to the Philistines, to sharpen every man his share ]{.class-0}\[i.e., plowshares---Isa. 2:4\][, and his coulter, and his axe, and his mattock. Yet they had a file for the mattocks, and for the coulters, and for the forks ]{.class-0}\[pitchforks\][, and for the axes, and to sharpen the goads"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 13:21).

The ox goad is a formidable weapon. An ox goad is about eight feet long and can be two to three inches in diameter at the large end. It is comparable to a quarter staff in England or a Bo staff in the Orient, except it was filed down to a sharp point at the "business end" like a spear or javelin. In the Middle Ages, it came out as a pike, a staff with a spike and a hook at the end. The advantage of a weapon like the ox goad is that it gave the wielder "reach" that a sword did not. It could be used either as a spear or a club.

Like Ehud's twoedged dagger, Shamgar's ox goad is a picture of [the words]{.class-1} of God (not just the "word"---singular---of God or the Neo-orthodox "Word" of God).

["The words of the wise are as goads, and as nails fastened by the masters of assemblies, which are given from one shepherd"]{.class-0} (Eccl. 12:11).

As a tool, the ox goad is used by a man plowing with oxen. When the oxen come to a stop, the plowman takes that ox goad and jabs them in the rear to get them moving again. The picture is that of the Holy Spirit using the words of Scripture delivered by a preacher or witness to bring conviction.

["Now when they heard this ]{.class-0}\[i.e., the preaching of Peter\][, they were PRICKED in their heart"]{.class-0} (Acts 2:37).

When Jesus appeared to Saul of Tarsus on the road to Damascus, He said to him, ["it is hard for thee to kick against the PRICKS"]{.class-0} (Acts 9:5). Saul had heard Stephen preach there in Acts 7, and the Holy Spirit was using  Stephen's words to prick Saul's conscience about Jesus Christ.

The Christian is to ["preach the word,"]{.class-0} and he is to do it to ["reprove"]{.class-0} and ["rebuke"]{.class-0} first (NEGATIVE!) before he exhorts (positive)---see 2 Timothy 4:2. Use the ["ox goad"]{.class-0} to get the sinner moving---one way or another (see remarks under vs. 16).

[]{#section-0_1_7e3b2e784e945766_708e.xhtml}

Chapter 4

4:1 And the children of Israel again did evil in the sight of the LORD, when Ehud was dead.

2 And the LORD sold them into the hand of Jabin king of Canaan, that reigned in Hazor; the captain of whose host was Sisera, which dwelt in Harosheth of the Gentiles.

3 And the children of Israel cried unto the LORD: for he had nine hundred chariots of iron; and twenty years he mightily oppressed the children of Israel.

Once more the pattern of apostasy repeats itself. After the death of Ehud, Israel falls back into idolatry. This time, God brings in a Canaanite King from the north.

This is ["Jabin king of Canaan,"]{.class-0} whose capital was Hazor (vs. 2). It was ["Jabin king of Hazor"]{.class-0} who led the northern confederation against Joshua in Joshua 11:1. Of course, this is not the same person. What you have is either another King by the same name (see the two different Jeroboams who ruled over the northern kingdom of Israel in 1 Kings 12--14 and 2 Kings 14:23--24), or ["Jabin" ]{.class-0}was a title for the King of Hazor (like Caesar was to the Romans and Pharaoh was to the Egyptians).

Joshua had taken Hazor and killed all the inhabitants and burned down the city (Josh. 11:11). Obviously, though, the tribe of Naphtali, to whom the city was given (Josh. 19:32--36), had not gone in and "possessed" the city (see our comments on Josh 13:1 in that Commentary), so a bunch of Canaanites had come back in and taken over the city again. You will see the same thing again when we get to the Philistines in chapters 13--16.

["Hazor"]{.class-0} was located above the Sea of Galilee, up near, but just south of, Lake Huleh. ["Harosheth of the Gentiles"]{.class-0} was located further south at the base of Mt. Carmel at the entering in to the Valley of Megiddo.

Jabin kept the northern tribes "in line" with a cavalry of 900 iron chariots. These iron chariots not only had an iron carriage and iron wheels, they had iron blades that came out about three feet from the wheels and were curved like a scythe. Men have always been very clever in inventing ways to kill. Those chariots would go through a line of troops and cut them to shreds.

It was these ["chariots of iron"]{.class-0} that Manasseh, Ephraim, and Judah all used as an excuse for not driving the remaining heathen peoples out of their territories (Josh. 17:16; Judg. 1:19). But iron chariots are no problem for God Almighty. Joshua promised Manasseh and Ephraim that they would ["drive out the Canaanites, though they have iron chariots"]{.class-0} (Josh. 17:18). Of course, that could have been a conditional promise based on the Ephraimites and Manassites acting in faith on the promise of God. There is no record of those tribes fulfilling that promise; in fact, Judges 1:27--29 lists the heathen peoples Manasseh and Ephraim didn't drive out. But there was no reason that they, or Judah for that matter, couldn't have overcome the iron chariots, as we are about to see in this chapter.

Jabin's "enforcer" was Sisera (vs. 2). The text says, ["twenty years he mightily oppressed the children of Israel"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). This is the longest period of servitude yet (see 3:8, 14). Judges 2:19 tells us that each successive generation ["corrupted themselves MORE than their fathers."]{.class-0} So in these first four chapters, as the apostasy grew, so did the years of defeat and slavery.

4 And Deborah, a prophetess, the wife of Lapidoth, she judged Israel at that time.

5 And she dwelt under the palm tree of Deborah between Ramah and Bethel in mount Ephraim: and the children of Israel came up to her for judgment.

6 And she sent and called Barak the son of Abinoam out of Kedeshnaphtali, and said unto him, Hath not the LORD God of Israel commanded, saying, Go and draw toward mount Tabor, and take with thee ten thousand men of the children of Naphtali and of the children of Zebulun?

7 And I will draw unto thee to the river Kishon Sisera, the captain of Jabin's army, with his chariots and his multitude; and I will deliver him into thine hand.

8 And Barak said unto her, If thou wilt go with me, then I will go: but if thou wilt not go with me, then I will not go.

9 And she said, I will surely go with thee: notwithstanding the journey that thou takest shall not be for thine honour; for the LORD shall sell Sisera into the hand of a woman. And Deborah arose, and went with Barak to Kedesh.

Here is a [woman]{.class-1} God is using as a prophetess and judge. The implication is that Israel, at least in the northern tribes, has run out of [men.]{.class-1} The order is the man as the head of the woman and God as the head of the man (1 Cor. 11:3). But where God can't find a man, He'll use a woman, like He did with Esther (Esth. 4:14). If He can't get a man or a woman, He'll get Him a child, like He did with the little maid who witnessed to Naaman's wife about ["the prophet that is in Samaria"]{.class-0} (2 Kings 5:2--3). The old saying is the greatest ability is [availability;]{.class-1} after that, it's [dependability.]{.class-1}

One of the great shames of American Fundamentalism is the number of single women on the mission field. There is nothing wrong with a single woman going to the mission field, but where are the men?

The great "patron saint" of Southern Baptist missions is Lottie Moon. Whatever "women's lib" views she held about the role of women in mission work, she once wrote something very profound about the need of [men]{.class-1} on the mission field.

"It is odd that [a million Baptists]{.class-1} of the South can furnish only [three men for all China.]{.class-1} Odd that with five hundred \[Baptist\] preachers in the state of Virginia, we \[i.e., the Baptist church where she worked in China\] must rely on [a Presbyterian]{.class-1} to fill [a Baptist pulpit"]{.class-1} (Ruth Tucker, [From Jerusalem to Irian Jaya,]{.class-1} 2004, pg. 297).

If God can't get a man to go, He'll get a woman. If He can't get a woman, He'll get a child. If no men, women, or children are available to Him, He'll find some way to get the message out even if He has to use a ["jenny"]{.class-1} (a female ass---Num. 22:28) or [a rooster]{.class-1} (Mark 14:72) to do it.

First of all, Deborah is ["a prophetess"]{.class-0}; that is, she is a woman to whom God is giving messages to deliver to the children of Israel. Although there are examples in the Bible of [false]{.class-1} prophetesses (["Noadiah"]{.class-0} in Neh. 6:14 and ["Jezebel"]{.class-0} in Rev. 2:20), there are many more examples of [good]{.class-1} prophetesses. There is not only [Deborah]{.class-1} here, there is also [Miriam]{.class-1} (Exod. 15:20), [Huldah]{.class-1} (2 Kings 22:14), [Isaiah's wife]{.class-1} (Isa. 8:3), [Anna]{.class-1} (Luke 2:36), and [the daughters of]{.class-1} ["Philip the evangelist"]{.class-0} (Acts 21:8--9).

That is one of the ways you know the Jehovah of the Bible is not the Allah of the [Koran.]{.class-1} Allah never spoke to [any ]{.class-1}woman. The God of the Bible not only spoke to them directly (e.g., Gen. 16:7--13, 18:15, 25:22--23; Judg. 13:3--5), He would use them to prophesy. Any of the women mentioned above had more real revelation from God than Mohammed ever had. The first person in the New Testament to preach the good news of redemption was [a woman ]{.class-1}(Anna---Luke 2:36--38); [women]{.class-1} were the first ones to proclaim the resurrection of Jesus Christ (Matt. 28:5--8). Women have a prominence in the Bible they aren't given in Mohammed's [Koran.]{.class-1}

Second, Deborah was a [judge.]{.class-1} Normally, that's not good. The Lord said in Isaiah 3:12, ["As for my people, children are their oppressors, AND WOMEN RULE OVER THEM. O my people, they which lead thee cause thee to err, and destroy the way of thy paths."]{.class-0} But Deborah is the exception to the rule. She's not like Hillary Clinton, Nancy Pelosi, Barbara Boxer, Dianne Feinstein, Janet Reno, Ruth Bader Ginsburg, or Donna Shalala; she isn't a Lesbian trying to create a Socialistic State with "women's lib," "children's rights," or two sex perverts getting together and pretending they're "married." Deborah loves the Lord and believes the Book, and all her judgments are based on [what God said.]{.class-1}

Now in the New Testament, the role of women is clear. Women are to be in subjection to their husbands (1 Pet. 3:1), parents (Eph. 6:1--2), and pastors (1 Tim. 2:11). In the local church, a woman is not allowed to teach or be in a position of authority over men (1 Tim. 2:12). Every office in the local church is to be occupied by [men]{.class-1} (1 Tim. 3:1--2, 12). But women hold a position of [respect]{.class-1} in the church (Rom. 16:1--6; Phil. 4:3; 1 Tim. 5:2--3). Though not allowed to teach men, they can teach other women (Tit. 2:4) and children (2 Tim. 1:5 cf. 2 Tim. 3:15). In salvation, there is no difference between a man and a woman (Gal. 3:28), and of course, any Christian woman can witness for Jesus Christ (Acts 18:26).

Further, any saved woman can "prophesy" (1 Cor. 11:5). Any saved woman can speak up for Jesus Christ. Sister, if you know about the Rapture, the Judgment Seat of Christ, the Tribulation, the Second Advent, the Millennial reign of Christ, the White Throne Judgment, the New Jerusalem, the Lake of Fire, and [where you are going when you die,]{.class-1} you are more of a prophet than Mohammed ever thought of being.

Back to Judges 4:[ "And she dwelt under the palm tree of Deborah . . . and the children of Israel came up to her for judgment"]{.class-0} (vs. 5). Now Deborah didn't live under that palm tree; that's where she "held court." When any of the Israelites had a dispute to settle, they came to her to find out the mind of God on the matter (cf. Exod. 18:13--16).

But the responsibility for judgment shouldn't have had to lie with Deborah. Deuteronomy 17:8--11 says it was the [Levites]{.class-1} at the Tabernacle (and later on at the Temple) who were given the job of judging (see also Deut. 19:27). As we will see further when we get to chapters 17--18, the Levites are in apostasy right along with the rest of the tribes. That's why God has to get Him a woman.

Now Deborah was a judge, but she was not a deliverer. Usually the judge [was]{.class-1} the deliverer (2:18). But the deliverer is a type of [Christ]{.class-1} (Rom. 11:26), so Deborah isn't the one who delivers Israel out of the hands of Jabin and Sisera. As a woman, she could [never]{.class-1} be a type of ["the MAN Christ Jesus"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 2:5). So Deborah gets a [man]{.class-1} to deliver Israel: ["And she sent and called Barak the son of Abinoam"]{.class-0} (vs. 6). As we shall see in the next chapter (5:12), Barak [is]{.class-1} a type of Christ.

Barak was from ["Kedesh-naphtali,"]{.class-0} which was a city of refuge up north of Lake Huleh (Josh. 20:7, 21:32). The staging area for the attack was ["mount Tabor."]{.class-0} It is about eleven miles south and west of the Sea of Galilee, and east and north of the Kishon River where the battle was to be fought. The Kishon flows from Mt. Gilboa through the Valley of Megiddo to the Mediterranean Sea on the north side of Mt. Carmel.

The Israeli army was made up of men from the tribes of Zebulun and Naphtali (vs. 6). Judges 5:15--18 indicates that other tribes were called: Issachar sent its chief rulers (5:15); Reuben, the Gileadites on the east side of Jordan, Dan, and Asher sent no one (5:16--17). ["Zebulun and Naphtali"]{.class-0} represented the "lion's share" of the army that went out against Sisera (5:18).

Verse 8 shows you the character of the men at that time: ["And Barak said unto her, If thou wilt go with me, then I will go: but if thou wilt not go with me, then I will not go."]{.class-0} Imagine the leader of an army leaning on a woman like that: "if you go, I'll go, but if you don't, I'm staying home." But there is a little more to it than that. Barak recognizes the Lord is with Deborah and that she has communication with God. Barak is reacting somewhat like Moses did back in Exodus 33:15 when he told God, ["If thy presence go not with me, carry us not up hence."]{.class-0} Barak is saying to Deborah, "I want you to go with us so we'll have the Lord's guidance."

Deborah agrees to go with Barak, but she tells him, "You won't get the credit for beating Sisera"---["the LORD shall sell Sisera into the hand of a woman"]{.class-0} (vs. 9). Barak probably thought she meant herself, and he must have thought that was a small price to pay for whipping a force of 900 iron chariots. Deborah wasn't talking about herself, though. The ["woman"]{.class-0} turns out to be a [Gentile,]{.class-1} and we'll comment more on the prophetic significance of that when we get to Deborah's song in chapter 5.

10 And Barak called Zebulun and Naphtali to Kedesh; and he went up with ten thousand men at his feet: and Deborah went up with him.

11 Now Heber the Kenite, which was of the children of Hobab the father in law of Moses, had severed himself from the Kenites, and pitched his tent unto the plain of Zaanaim, which is by Kedesh.

12 And they shewed Sisera that Barak the son of Abinoam was gone up to mount Tabor.

13 And Sisera gathered together all his chariots, even nine hundred chariots of iron, and all the people that were with him, from Harosheth of the Gentiles unto the river of Kishon.

14 And Deborah said unto Barak, Up; for this is the day in which the LORD hath delivered Sisera into thine hand: is not the LORD gone out before thee? So Barak went down from mount Tabor, and ten thousand men after him.

15 And the LORD discomfited Sisera, and all his chariots, and all his host, with the edge of the sword before Barak; so that Sisera lighted down off his chariot, and fled away on his feet.

16 But Barak pursued after the chariots, and after the host, unto Harosheth of the Gentiles: and all the host of Sisera fell upon the edge of the sword; and there was not a man left.

Barak returns to Kedesh with Deborah (vs. 9), and from there, he musters his army from the tribes of Zebulun and Naphtali. (Note: Kedesh is north of Hazor, the city of Jabin, the King who was oppressing them.)

["Ten thousand men at his feet"]{.class-0} (vs. 10) doesn't mean they were bowing down to Barak (cf. 1 Sam. 25:24; 2 Kings 4:37; Matt. 18:29; Mark 5:22; Luke 17:16; Acts 10:25; Rev. 19:10). It means two things: they were [following]{.class-1} Barak into battle (cf. 3:28), and they were all [on foot.]{.class-1} Barak has an army of 10,000 footmen against a cavalry of 900 iron chariots. That's about eleven men against each chariot (not counting the rest of Sisera's army---vs. 13), and the chariots have twirling blades coming three feet out from the spokes of the wheels. Not very good odds from a human standpoint, but God promised to deliver Sisera and his host into the hands of Barak and his 10,000 men.

In verse 11, someone else enters the narrative: ["Heber the Kenite."]{.class-0} We have already commented on the Kenites and Hobab under 1:16 (which see). The Kenites had settled south in Judah (Judg. 1:16; 1 Sam. 27:10), near the Amalekites (1 Sam. 15:6). Heber ["had severed himself from the Kenites"]{.class-0}; i.e., he left and got away from them. He went to the completely opposite end of Canaan, up in the north. ["The plain of Zaanaim"]{.class-0} is north and west of Lake Huleh, near Kedesh.

Verse 12:[ "And they shewed Sisera that Barak ]{.class-0}\
[. . . was gone up to mount Tabor."]{.class-0} The only antecedent to the ["they"]{.class-0} of verse 12 would be ["Heber the Kenite"]{.class-0} in verse 11 and his ["house"]{.class-0} (vs. 17; i.e., his household). Heber becomes Jabin's "snitch." He sees Barak gathering an army at Kedesh and "rats him out" to the Canaanite King.

While Sisera has advanced intelligence, Barak has a greater "advance Force." [The Lord]{.class-1} went out before Barak (vs. 14). The Lord promised those Israelites that He would go before them like ["a consuming fire"]{.class-0} to destroy their enemies (Deut. 9:3). One time when David went up against the Philistines, the Lord told him that when he heard something moving through ["the tops of the mulberry trees"]{.class-0} that was the signal to attack because that was the Lord Himself going before David's troops ["to smite the host of the Philistines"]{.class-0} (2 Sam. 5:24).

The Spirit of the Lord would blow through there before the Israeli army and do all kinds of things to mess up the enemy. He would send swarms of hornets in there to sting the enemy (Exod. 23:28; Deut. 7:20; Josh. 24:12). No soldier, no matter how good he is, would be able to fight well with hornets stinging him all over his legs, his arms, his ears, the back of his neck, his cheeks, etc. Over in Joshua 10:11, God cast down great hailstones on the armies of the southern confederation. It would be pretty hard to hold the line with fifty-pound chunks of ice hitting you on the head.

Verse 15 says, ["the LORD discomfited Sisera, and all his chariots, and all his host."]{.class-0} You have to admit, stuff like stinging hornets and falling hailstones sure would make you "uncomfortable." Judges 5:21 says, ["The river of Kishon swept them away."]{.class-0} Sisera's chariots were swept away in a flood by the river. His heavily armored chariots and scythe blades on the wheels were useless in the attack by Barak and the Israelites. When Pharaoh sent his chariots after the children of Israel at the Red Sea, all God had to do was take the chariot wheels off, and the greatest army in the world, at that time, became absolutely impotent (Exod. 14:25).

17 Howbeit Sisera fled away on his feet to the tent of Jael the wife of Heber the Kenite: for there was peace between Jabin the king of Hazor and the house of Heber the Kenite.

18 And Jael went out to meet Sisera, and said unto him, Turn in, my lord, turn in to me; fear not. And when he had turned in unto her into the tent, she covered him with a mantle.

19 And he said unto her, Give me, I pray thee, a little water to drink; for I am thirsty. And she opened a bottle of milk, and gave him drink, and covered him.

20 Again he said unto her, Stand in the door of the tent, and it shall be, when any man doth come and enquire of thee, and say, Is there any man here? that thou shalt say, No.

21 Then Jael Heber's wife took a nail of the tent, and took an hammer in her hand, and went softly unto him, and smote the nail into his temples, and fastened it into the ground: for he was fast asleep and weary. So he died.

22 And, behold, as Barak pursued Sisera, Jael came out to meet him, and said unto him, Come, and I will shew thee the man whom thou seekest. And when he came into her tent, behold, Sisera lay dead, and the nail was in his temples.

23 So God subdued on that day Jabin the king of Canaan before the children of Israel.

24 And the hand of the children of Israel prospered, and prevailed against Jabin the king of Canaan, until they had destroyed Jabin king of Canaan.

While Barak routs the Canaanites back to ["Harosheth of the Gentiles"]{.class-0} and destroys them to a man (vs. 16), their brave commander flees on foot northward to where Heber was (vss. 15, 17). Since Heber is Jabin's "stoolie" (see our comments on vs. 12), Sisera figures he will be safe there.

Now[ "Jael the wife of Heber the Kenite"]{.class-0} is the woman who gets the credit for killing Sisera (see vs. 9). What you are about to read is the standard Hollywood plot where a woman betrays a man who trusts her (see also 16:4--21). You won't get around the Bible; it contains all the plots used in literature and theater. All that changes is the setting: sometimes it will be a gangster and his "moll"; sometimes it will be a knight and his "lady fair"; sometimes it will be a politician having an affair; sometimes it will be a "Mata Hari"; sometimes it will be a poor wife thinking she is saving her husband; etc. Those are just the variations on one plot. There are literally [dozens]{.class-1} of original plots in the Bible which are copied in novels, radio dramas, movies, and TV shows; they are just changed slightly in hopes you won't recognize from where they were plagiarized.

Jael goes out to meet Sisera and invites him into the tent with: ["Turn in, my lord, turn in to me, fear not"]{.class-0} (vs. 18). If Sisera had known what her intentions were, he would have had plenty to fear: she intended to [kill him.]{.class-1} There is no indication in Scripture as to [why]{.class-1} she wanted to kill him, except that she was loyal to Israel (see how she is eulogized by Deborah in 5:24).

One thing we do know is that Sisera did something unthinkable in Bedouin society. No man was ever to go into a woman's quarters without her husband or father present. Such a violation of Bedouin ethics was punishable by death, which is what Jael dispenses to Sisera.

Knowing that Sisera is about to drop on his feet from running for his life, Jael puts a mantle (a cloak-like garment) over him. When he asks for water, she gives him milk (it's called ["butter"]{.class-0} in 5:25 because it's [buttermilk]{.class-1}). Between the milk and the warm mantle, Sisera is about to fall asleep, but before he does, he asks Jael to [lie]{.class-1} if anybody comes by asking if there's a man there. So that's another breach of Bedouin morals. He's in a woman's bedroom, asking her to lie about it. Such a thing could have gotten her stoned for adultery if she had gone along with him and had gotten caught.

As Sisera is ["fast asleep and weary"]{.class-0} (vs. 21), Jael takes ["a nail of the tent"]{.class-0}---a tent peg about the size of a railroad spike---and hammers it through his temples into the ground. Jael gives Sisera a [deadly head wound,]{.class-1} marking him as a type of the [Antichrist.]{.class-1} God prophesied in Genesis 3:15 that the Seed of the woman would bruise the head of the seed of the serpent. That takes place at the Second Advent (Rom. 16:20 cf. Psa. 68:21, 110:5--6; Hab. 3:13). There are eighteen types of Antichrist in the Bible (see chap. 3 of our work [The Mark of the Beast]{.class-1}), and three of them receive [head wounds:]{.class-1} Sisera (here), Abimelech (Judg. 9:53), and Goliath (1 Sam. 17:49). So what you are reading here in Judges 4 is a type of the Second Advent of Jesus Christ, and we will get into that further in the next chapter.

With the death of his General, Sisera, Jabin the King of the Canaanites was subdued by God before Israel (vs. 23). Not only was his tyrannical hold over the northern tribes broken, they ended up killing him too (vs. 24). The lesson for the Christian in his spiritual warfare is that once you have gained a victory over a sin in your life, don't stop fighting it until you have the complete victory over it. If the Israelites had not followed up on their victory over Sisera, Jabin would have simply chosen another General, rebuilt his army, and swept through Galilee again, wreaking more havoc. The King had to be killed to end the threat. The flesh has to be crucified daily to keep Jesus on the throne of your heart (Gal. 5:24 cf. 1 Cor. 15:31).

Before closing this chapter, let's go back and pick up a couple of things we missed along the way. Note another type of the word of God in verse 21: ["a NAIL of the tent."]{.class-0}

["The words of the wise are as goads, and as NAILS fastened by the masters of assemblies, which are given from one shepherd"]{.class-0} (Eccl. 12:11).

We saw the goad back in chapter 3 (see our comments on vs. 31); here we have the nail. Nails are for securing things; the Christian is built up on the word of God (Acts 20:32). ["The masters of assemblies"]{.class-0} are faithful pastors and teachers given to the Body of Christ by the Good Shepherd (John 10:11, 14) for the perfecting and edification of its members (Eph. 4:11--12). The ["one shepherd"]{.class-0} is no more the Pope of Rome than Rocky Marciano was Tinkerbell (see Heb. 13:20; 1 Pet. 5:4).

The second thing we should notice is the New Testament commentary on Barak's "ministry." Ignoring Barak's genuine fear of obeying God in verse 8, the writer of Hebrews says ["Barak" "turned to flight the armies of the aliens" "through faith"]{.class-0} (Heb. 11:32--34). Neither Deborah nor Jael are mentioned in the New Testament; the great hero of faith in this story is, of all people, [Barak.]{.class-1}

You see that over and over again in the New Testament: the sins of the Old Testament saints are not mentioned. To read the New Testament, you would never know that Noah got drunk, Moses lost his temper and forfeited the chance to enter the Promised Land, Joshua forgot to pray over the visit of the Gibeonites, Abraham lied about his wife, Sarah laughed at the promise of God concerning the birth of Isaac, David committed adultery, etc. Why is that? Because the New Testament was instituted on [the blood of Christ]{.class-1} (Matt. 26:28), which was able to completely redeem the sins of the Old Testament saints (Heb. 9:15). In the Old Testament, sins may have been remitted (i.e., forgiven)---see Exodus 34:7; Romans 3:25---but they [weren't taken away]{.class-1} because ["it is not possible that the blood of bulls and goats should take away sins"]{.class-0} (Heb. 10:4). ["The blood of bulls and goats"]{.class-0} is the [only]{.class-1} blood Abel, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Aaron, David, or any other Old Testament saint had.

That's why any Conservative or Fundamental Bible teacher or scholar who tells you people were saved the same way in the Old Testament as they are in the New Testament is a [crazy nut;]{.class-1} he is crippled too high for crutches. In the New Testament, ["the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from ALL sin"]{.class-0} (1 John 1:7). The blood of the Old Testament sacrifices couldn't ["take away"]{.class-0} [any]{.class-1} sin (Heb. 10:11). It took Jesus Christ showing up and shedding His blood at Calvary to take away the sins of the Old Testament saints. And it's that blood that affords ["eternal redemption"]{.class-0} (Heb. 9:12) and free justification (Rom. 3:24--25) to [you]{.class-1} if you trust Christ.

[]{#section-0_1_64b80c62d3055370_708f.xhtml}

Chapter 5

5:1 Then sang Deborah and Barak the son of Abinoam on that day, saying,

2 Praise ye the LORD for the avenging of Israel, when the people willingly offered themselves.

3 Hear, O ye kings; give ear, O ye princes; I, even I, will sing unto the LORD; I will sing praise to the LORD God of Israel.

This is the song of ["Deborah and Barak"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). The song itself is thirty verses long, and the whole thing is on the [Second Advent of Jesus Christ]{.class-1} (the same thing is true of the first song recorded in the Bible---see our comments on Exod. 15 in that Commentary). Because of that, it is one of the most attacked chapters in the book of Judges. In the [NASV,]{.class-1} the text has been altered by the Lockman Foundation more than sixty times in 31 verses. Like many new versions, the ["New" King James Version]{.class-1} (which is NOT the [King James Version]{.class-1} or even an "edition" of it) prints the song like [poetry.]{.class-1} The [NKJV]{.class-1} does that over and over again: it prints prophetic Scriptures as poetry so you will not take the prophecy [literally.]{.class-1}

Verse 2 should warn you that you are not just dealing with "poetry"---["Praise ye the LORD for the AVENGING OF ISRAEL."]{.class-0}

["For it is the DAY OF THE LORD'S VENGEANCE, and the year of recompences for the controversy of Zion"]{.class-0} (Isa. 34:8).

["To proclaim the acceptable year of the LORD, and THE DAY OF VENGEANCE OF OUR GOD; to comfort all that mourn"]{.class-0} (Isa. 61:2).

["For THE DAY OF VENGEANCE is in mine heart, and the year of my redeemed is come"]{.class-0} (Isa. 63:4).

["For this is THE DAY OF THE LORD GOD OF HOSTS, A DAY OF VENGEANCE, THAT HE MAY AVENGE HIM OF HIS ADVERSARIES: and the sword shall devour, and it shall be satiate and made drunk with their blood: for the Lord GOD of hosts hath a sacrifice in the north country by the river Euphrates"]{.class-0} (Jer. 46:10).

["And I will execute VENGEANCE IN ANGER AND FURY UPON THE HEATHEN, such as they have not heard"]{.class-0} (Mic. 5:15).

["FOR THESE BE THE DAYS OF VENGEANCE, that all things which are written may be fulfilled"]{.class-0} (Luke 21:22).

["Rejoice over her, thou heaven, and ye holy apostles and prophets; FOR GOD HATH AVENGED YOU ON HER"]{.class-0} (Rev. 18:20).

["For true and righteous are his judgments: for he hath judged the great whore, which did corrupt the earth with her fornication, and HATH AVENGED THE BLOOD OF HIS SERVANTS at her hand"]{.class-0} (Rev. 19:2).

["And to you who are troubled rest with us, when the Lord Jesus shall be revealed from heaven with his mighty angels, In flaming fire TAKING VENGEANCE ON THEM THAT KNOW NOT GOD, and that obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} (2 Thess. 1:7--8).

That's not even a third of the passages in the Bible that deal with Jesus Christ [taking vengeance]{.class-1} on the UN at His return, especially in regards to the nation of Israel. That's why I have taught you that Barak's battle with Sisera (as well as Jael slaying Sisera) was a type of Christ's Second Coming to conquer the United Nations.

Look at verse 3: ["Hear, O ye KINGS]{.class-0} \[[plural!]{.class-1}\][; give ear, O ye princes ]{.class-0}\[plural\][."]{.class-0} You might get away with limiting those ["princes"]{.class-0} to just chapter 4 (see vs. 15 in this chapter), but what about those ["kings"]{.class-0}? There weren't any Kings---plural--- involved in Barak's battle with Sisera. There is only [one King]{.class-1} involved in the entire story, and that is ["Jabin king of Canaan"]{.class-0} (4:2), and he wasn't even there. But there will be at the Second Advent. Look at verse 19.

["The KINGS]{.class-0} \[plural\][ came and fought, then fought the kings of Canaan in Taanach by the waters of Megiddo; they took no gain of money."]{.class-0}

If you think that's a reference to the battle with Sisera, look at the next verse, verse 20.

"They fought FROM HEAVEN; THE STARS IN THEIR COURSES fought against Sisera."

Someone's coming down from upstairs (2 Thess. 1:7; Rev. 19:14) to fight multiple Kings in Megiddo---[the Battle of Armageddon!]{.class-1} In Revelation 16, we read,

["And the sixth angel poured out his vial upon the great river Euphrates; and the water thereof was dried up, that the way of THE KINGS OF THE EAST might be prepared. And I saw three unclean spirits like frogs come out of the mouth of the dragon, and out of the mouth of the beast, and out of the mouth of the false prophet. For they are the spirits of devils, working miracles, which go forth unto THE KINGS OF THE EARTH AND OF THE WHOLE WORLD, to gather them to the battle of the great day of God Almighty . . . . And he gathered them together into a place called in the Hebrew tongue ARMAGEDDON"]{.class-0} (Rev. 16:12--14, 16).

So what you are reading in Judges 5 is the same kind of thing you read in Psalm 149:6--9, 110:5--6, 21:8--9, etc. It's [prophecy]{.class-1} in the form of a [song.]{.class-1} Such writings should never be looked on as mere "poetry." Peter said that David was a [prophet]{.class-1} when he wrote his Messianic psalms (Acts 2:25--30). Here in Judges 5, Deborah is speaking as a [prophetess]{.class-1} and giving you a [Messianic song,]{.class-1} dealing with the coming of the Messiah in power.

4 LORD, when thou wentest out of Seir, when thou marchedst out of the field of Edom, the earth trembled, and the heavens dropped, the clouds also dropped water.

5 The mountains melted from before the LORD, even that Sinai from before the LORD God of Israel.

What you just read has absolutely nothing to do with Barak fighting Sisera at Megiddo. Seir, Edom, and Sinai are nowhere near Megiddo; they're south below the Dead Sea.

Seeing that the passage has nothing to do with anything in Judges 4, the major commentators make the verses a reference to the giving of the Law in Exodus 19--20. But Seir and Edom aren't even in Exodus 19--20; moreover with all the thundering, lightning, and clouds on Sinai (Exod. 19:16), nowhere in the Scriptures is it recorded that it [rained]{.class-1} at the giving of the Law. And despite the fact that Mt. Sinai was covered in smoke ["because the LORD descended upon it in fire,"]{.class-0} and despite the fact that ["the whole mount quaked greatly"]{.class-0} (Exod. 19:18), neither Sinai nor any other mountain ["melted from before the LORD"]{.class-0} in Exodus 19--20.

You see, people don't pay attention to what they read. They figure Deborah is just expressing Exodus 19:18, 20:18 and Deuteronomy 4:11--12, 5:22--25 in the highly figurative language of poetry. That's not what she's doing at all. She's describing the same event Moses described in Deuteronomy 33:2 (which see), which Enoch prophesied as the coming of the Lord ["to execute judgment"]{.class-0} on the ungodly (Jude 14--15).

What you are reading is one of the definitive passages on the Second Coming of Christ and the route He takes. Although He ends up at the Mount of Olives (Acts 1:11--12 cf. Zech. 14:3--4), that is not where He starts. According to Song of Solomon 2:8, when the Bridegroom returns, He comes ["leaping upon the mountains, skipping upon the hills."]{.class-0} Judges 5:4--5; Deuteronomy 33:2; and Habakkuk 3:3 give you ["the mountains."]{.class-0}

When Jesus Christ comes back, He hits Mt. Sinai first, then Mt. Seir, Mt. Teman, and Mt. Paran in Edom. As He does, Habakkuk 3:5 says ["burning coals]{.class-0} \[go\][ forth at his feet"]{.class-0}; that's how those ["mountains"]{.class-0} get ["melted from before the LORD"]{.class-0} here in verse 5 of Judges 5. He ends up turning the entire land of Edom into a [lake of fire]{.class-1} (Obad. 18; Isa. 34:5--10).

He goes up the King's Highway (Num. 20:17, 19; 21:22), crosses Jordan where Joshua crossed on dry ground, in the same place where He was baptized, and hits the Mount of Olives, splitting it in half (Zech. 14:4). He descends by the route He took into Jerusalem at His Triumphal Entry (Zech. 9:9--10 cf. Luke 19:37--38) and comes to the Eastern Gate, which was sealed shut by the Moslems in A.D. 1187 (see Ezek. 44:1--2) for the express purpose of preventing Jesus Christ from fulfilling Ezekiel 46:1--2 (which see). But if they think a concrete wall can stop the One who went down through 3,900 miles of solid rock and magma and came back out again (Eph. 4:9--10), they've got "another think" coming.

Christ goes right through that cemented gate without breaking a sweat (see John 20:19), enters the Temple, and goes into the Holy of Holies where the Antichrist went three-and-a-half years earlier (2 Thess. 2:3--4). He sits down on the Mercy Seat of the Ark of the Covenant and puts one arm on one cherub and one arm on the other cherub (the Ark being a picture of the throne of God---Isa. 6:1--2), and says, "Anybody got a problem with that?" [And nobody opens his yap]{.class-1} (Hab. 2:20).

Now that is "The Path of the Second Advent," and for further study on the subject, we refer you to our short work by that title (Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1989). The question arises, "Where does the Battle of Armageddon fit into this?" And my answer is, ["I'm not sure."]{.class-1} As I read some passages, I think Armageddon comes first (e.g., Isa. 63:1--4 cf. Rev. 14:18--20, 19:11--15), but other passages lead me to believe Sinai to Jerusalem comes first (e.g., Judg. 5). The scenario that would make the most sense would be taking out the Antichrist and his armies at Armageddon first, then coming down to Sinai and going up through Edom, rescuing the Jews in Selah-Petra before heading to Jerusalem. But until the Holy Spirit gives more illumination from the Scriptures on the subject, that is where we will have to leave it.

Back to verse 4: ["the heavens dropped, the clouds also dropped water."]{.class-0} That's another phenomenon connected with the Second Advent. It's called ["the latter rain"]{.class-0} (Joel 2:23). It's a big rainstorm that precedes Christ's Second Coming, and it's pictured by Elijah praying for rain in 1 Kings 18:41--45.

["Elijah was a man subject to like passions as we are, and he prayed earnestly that it might not rain: and it rained not on the earth by the space of three years and six months ]{.class-0}\[the length of the Great Tribulation---Rev. 11:2--3, 12:4, 13:5\][. And he prayed again, and the heaven gave rain, and the earth brought forth her fruit"]{.class-0} (James 5:17--18).

The ["latter rain"]{.class-0} is right in the context (James 5:7), followed by ["the coming of the Lord"]{.class-0} (James 5:8). The events of 1 Kings 17--18 are going to be [repeated]{.class-1} in the Tribulation.

["And I will give power unto my two witnesses, and they shall prophesy a thousand two hundred and threescore days . . . These have power to SHUT HEAVEN, THAT IT RAIN NOT IN THE DAYS OF THEIR PROPHECY"]{.class-0} (Rev. 11:3, 6).

Those two witnesses prophesy 1,260 days---three and a half years. During that time, they shut off the rain to an idolatrous King, just like Elijah did. And when their time ends, God sends former and latter rains down at the same time just before ["the great and the terrible day of the LORD"]{.class-0} (Joel 2:23--31).

6 In the days of Shamgar the son of Anath, in the days of Jael, the highways were unoccupied, and the travellers walked through byways.

7 The inhabitants of the villages ceased, they ceased in Israel, until that I Deborah arose, that I arose a mother in Israel.

The passage describes the decimation of the Jews during the Tribulation.[ "The highways were unoccupied"]{.class-0} (vs. 6). Why? The Jews are being hunted down by the Antichrist and killed.

["They hunt our steps, that we cannot go in our streets: our end is near, our days are fulfilled; for our end is come"]{.class-0} (Lam. 4:18).

When the Antichrist sets up his image in the temple at Jerusalem, the Lord Jesus tells those Jews to get out of town just as fast as they can get and flee to the mountains (Matt. 24:15--16). The mountains, in this case, happen to be the mountains in [Edom]{.class-1} (see our remarks under vss. 4--5); specifically, the rock city of Selah-Petra (2 Kings 14:7; see our comments on ["Selah"]{.class-0} under Psa. 3:2 in that Commentary).

As the remnant of Israel flees to Petra, the Antichrist tries to kill them before they reach the fortress (Lam. 4:19), and if it weren't for the miraculous protection of God (Rev. 12:15--16), they would be completely wiped out. As it stands, the Devil continues to make war on the Jews who make it there (Rev. 12:17; Lam. 5:9).

Right now in Israel, as of 2014, there are 6,102,000 Jews in the land, a little over the number that died in Hitler's Holocaust. I wouldn't be surprised that by the end of the Tribulation there would be less than 10,000 Jews left; that number could be as low as a thousand. I wouldn't be surprised if every single Jew living in Israel at the time of this writing would be killed in the Tribulation. It's a shame that you can't win thousands of them to Christ so they will miss that awful time (Jer. 30:7).

Right now, there are all kinds of literature circulating, by Catholics, Christians, and Jews alike, saying, "Don't witness to the Jews; don't try to win them to Christ; leave them alone; they're God's chosen people; they'll be all right." Not only is that damning to every Jew who winds up in Hell before the Rapture (see Luke 16:22--25), it condemns millions of Jews who will be living during that time to genocide. [As a nation,]{.class-1} those Jews are still God's people (Rom. 11:1--2), but as [individuals,]{.class-1} they still go to Hell like any Christ-rejecting sinner and, therefore, need the Gospel. You had better do whatever you can to get those people saved before it's too late one way or another.

Back to verse 7: ["until that I Deborah arose, that I arose a mother in Israel." "A mother in Israel"]{.class-0} isn't a reference to a [religious]{.class-1} title like the "Mother Superior" of a Catholic nunnery. It's a reference to a real mother who is well respected (see 2 Sam. 20:19). Deborah is a [married woman]{.class-1} (Judg. 4:4) with children. According to the Apostle to the Gentiles, the doctrine of "clerical celibacy" (male or female) is a [doctrine of devils]{.class-1} (1 Tim. 4:1--3).

8 They chose new gods; then was war in the gates: was there a shield or spear seen among forty thousand in Israel?

9 My heart is toward the governors of Israel, that offered themselves willingly among the people. Bless ye the LORD.

10 Speak, ye that ride on white asses, ye that sit in judgment, and walk by the way.
