11 They that are delivered from the noise of archers in the places of drawing water, there shall they rehearse the righteous acts of the LORD, even the righteous acts toward the inhabitants of his villages in Israel: then shall the people of the LORD go down to the gates.

["They chose new gods"]{.class-0} (vs. 8): historically a reference to the apostasy of Israel (see Deut. 32:16--17); prophetically a reference to the Antichrist and his image in the Tribulation (Rev. 13:4, 15). When the False Prophet sets up the image of the Antichrist in the Temple, and the Antichrist goes into the Holy of Holies and seats himself on the Mercy Seat of the Ark as God (2 Thess. 2:3--4), some of those Jews give in and apostatize, some fight and get slaughtered (["then was there war in the gates: was there a shield or spear seen among forty thousand in Israel?"]{.class-0}), and a few heed Christ's warning in Matthew 24:15--16 to flee.

We have already discussed the lack of weapons among the Israelites back under 3:31 (which see), which is why ["Shamgar"]{.class-0} shows up in verse 6. So that passage too is a picture of the Second Advent.

In verse 9, the judges of Israel are called ["the governors of Israel"]{.class-0}; they are the ones ["that ride on white asses"]{.class-0} in verse 10. Historically, that is a reference to the judges who served under the main judge (see Num. 11:16--17; Deut. 1:12--17, 16:18). Often, the other judges were relatives (usually sons) of the main judge (Judg. 10:3--4, 12:13--14; 1 Sam. 8:1--2). ["The governors of Israel"]{.class-0} who are specifically given are ["the princes of Issachar"]{.class-0} (vs. 15) and possibly the ["governors"]{.class-0} that ["come down" "out of Machir"]{.class-0} (vs. 14).

But ["ye that ride on white asses, ye that sit in judgment"]{.class-0} should alert you that more is going on here than Barak's battle with Sisera. When Jesus Christ returns to reign, there is someone sitting with Him in judgment.

["And Jesus said unto them]{.class-0} \[the twelve apostles---Matt. 19:27\][, Verily I say unto you, that ye which have followed me, in the regeneration when the Son of man shall sit in the throne of his glory, ye also shall sit upon twelve thrones, judging the twelve tribes of Israel"]{.class-0} (Matt. 19:28).

["And I saw thrones, and they that sat upon them, and judgment was given unto them: and I saw the souls of them that were beheaded for the witness of Jesus, and for the word of God, and which had not worshipped the beast, neither his image, neither had received his mark upon their foreheads, or in their hands; and they lived and reigned with Christ a thousand years"]{.class-0} (Rev. 20:4).

So when Jesus Christ returns, He comes back with two groups. One rides on ["white horses"]{.class-0} and are members of the Bride of Christ, ["clothed in fine linen, white and clean"]{.class-0} (Rev. 19:14 cf. Rev. 19:8). The other are ["governors of Israel,"]{.class-0} from the Gospels and the Tribulation, who ["ride on white asses."]{.class-0} Those two groups are said to be ["two armies"]{.class-0} in Song of Solomon 6:13, and you can read our comments on that verse in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Song of Solomon.]{.class-1}

Verse 11: ["They that are delivered from the noise of archers . . . ." "The noise of archers"]{.class-0} is a peculiar expression. Bows and arrows don't make that much noise. But do you know what a bow and arrows are called in 1 Samuel 20:40? They're called ["artillery"]{.class-0} (referring to a weapon that fires projectiles). Modern artillery [does]{.class-1} make a lot of noise.

You say, "Ruckman, are you really saying the Holy Spirit is talking about cannons, mortars, 75mm assault guns, rockets, etc.? Then why didn't He say what He meant and mean what He said?"

Well, think about it; if He had said, "the noise of the Howitzers," who in 1000 B.C., 586 B.C., A.D. 30, A.D. 70, A.D. 96, A.D. 180, A.D. 325, or A.D. 1000 would have known about what He was talking? If the Holy Spirit had said, "The Buicks will speed down the Interstate, and the Fords will crash into the Chevys at the intersections," who before A.D. 1900 would have understood all that? But anyone from 700 B.C.---A.D. 1900 could understand ["The chariots shall rage in the streets, they shall justle one against another in the broad ways"]{.class-0} (Nah. 2:4).

You see, people, the Bible wasn't just written to you up beyond 2014. It's a universal Book written to people in 1000 B.C., 750 B.C., A.D. 500, A.D. 1000, A.D. 1500, 1600, 1700, 1800, 1900, 2000, and [today.]{.class-1} The Holy Spirit gave you His words in inclusive language that anyone at anytime could understand.

["They that are delivered from the noise of archers IN THE PLACES OF DRAWING WATER . . . ."]{.class-0} Normally that would refer to wells down on earth (e.g., see John 4:11). But this is a reference to somebody upstairs (["then shall the people of the LORD GO DOWN TO the gates"]{.class-0}) who is going through a "dress rehearsal" (["there shall they rehearse the righteous acts of the LORD"]{.class-0}). Somebody at the end of the Tribulation is caught up away from the artillery fire (Rev. 6:4, 8, 12:17, 13:9), up through a body of water that is frozen at the top like ["a sea of glass"]{.class-0} (Job 38:30 cf. Rev. 4:6); and they are rehearsing what they are going to do when they come back with their Lord. You can read about it in Revelation 15:2--4 (which see).

12 Awake, awake, Deborah: awake, awake, utter a song: arise, Barak, and lead thy captivity captive, thou son of Abinoam.

13 Then he made him that remaineth have dominion over the nobles among the people: the LORD made me have dominion over the mighty.

In the context, ["Deborah"]{.class-0} is a picture of Israel (vs. 7). The "awakening" is a [resurrection]{.class-1} (Isa. 26:19). If you doubt that interpretation, look at the next part of the verse: ["arise, Barak, and LEAD THY CAPTIVITY CAPTIVE, thou son of Abinoam."]{.class-0}[ ]{.class-28}That's a reference to Jesus Christ taking the inhabitants of Paradise up to Heaven at His resurrection.

["Wherefore he saith, When he ascended up on high, he LED CAPTIVITY CAPTIVE, and gave gifts unto men. (Now that he ascended, what is it but that he also descended first into the lower parts of the earth? He that descended is the same also that ascended up far above all heavens, that he might fill all things.)"]{.class-0} (Eph. 4:8--10).

When Jesus Christ rose, He emptied "Abraham's Bosom," so in this age, when a saint dies, he goes up instead of down (2 Cor. 5:1--6 cf. Luke 16:22--26).

But in the Tribulation, when a saint dies at the hand of the Antichrist, he goes down again (Rev. 6:9--11). That is where those martyrs stay until ["after the tribulation"]{.class-0} when Christ raises them in a POST-Tribulation rapture (Matt. 24:29--31). That is NOT the pre-Tribulation Rapture of the Body of Christ. That is a rapture at the end of the Tribulation where Jews and Gentiles in [two separate bodies]{.class-1} (Rev. 7) are caught out, and when they are, those martyrs underneath the altar there in Revelation 6 are raised from the dead.

["Thy dead men shall live, together with my dead body shall they arise. AWAKE AND SING]{.class-0}[ ]{.class-44}[\[]{.class-32}Judg[. 5!\]]{.class-32}[,]{.class-44}[ ]{.class-32}[ye that dwell in the dust: for thy dew is as the dew of herbs, and the earth shall cast out the dead"]{.class-0} (Isa. 26:19).

Verse 13: ["Then he made him that remaineth have dominion over the nobles among the people: the LORD made me have dominion over the mighty."]{.class-0} The Tribulation martyrs beheaded by the Antichrist rule and reign ["with Christ a thousand years"]{.class-0} (Rev. 20:4). These are ["the saints of the most High"]{.class-0} that ["take . . . and possess the kingdom for ever"]{.class-0} (Dan. 7:18; see also Dan. 7:22, 27). The same ["reign"]{.class-0}[ ]{.class-1}is promised to you as a New Testament believer if you suffer for Christ now (2 Tim. 2:12).

14 Out of Ephraim was there a root of them against Amalek; after thee, Benjamin, among thy people; out of Machir came down governors, and out of Zebulun they that handle the pen of the writer.

15 And the princes of Issachar were with Deborah; even Issachar, and also Barak: he was sent on foot into the valley. For the divisions of Reuben there were great thoughts of heart.

16 Why abodest thou among the sheepfolds, to hear the bleatings of the flocks? For the divisions of Reuben there were great searchings of heart.

17 Gilead abode beyond Jordan: and why did Dan remain in ships? Asher continued on the sea shore, and abode in his breaches.

18 Zebulun and Naphtali were a people that jeoparded their lives unto the death in the high places of the field.

Now while verses 15--18 can deal historically with the battle in chapter 4, verse 14 [does not.]{.class-1} Amalek wasn't involved at all. The Amalekites dwelt in the extreme south of Palestine, near Edom. But God said He would ["have war with Amalek from generation to generation"]{.class-0} (Exod. 17:16). Saul was commanded to destroy them all in 1 Samuel 15, and he didn't do it. As a result, the descendants of the King whom Saul saved alive (Agag) lived, and one of them tries to destroy Israel in the book of Esther (see our comments on Esth. 3:1 in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther]{.class-1}). Haman turns out to be a type of the [Antichrist.]{.class-1}

So Amalek is connected somehow to the Antichrist in the Tribulation, and it is one of the nations confederate against Israel in the Tribulation---see Psalm 83:5--8. Notice two things in that passage: 1) God compares that confederation to [Sisera and Jabin]{.class-1} in Psalm 83:9. 2) All those nations in modern times are [Moslem.]{.class-1} So what you have in verse 14, as well as verses 15--18 here in Judges 5, is a prophetic reference to a Moslem confederation that comes against Israel at the Battle of Armageddon, and in some way, the Antichrist is connected (probably [racially]{.class-1}) to that confederation. You see that at present (i.e., at the time of this writing) with [Obama.]{.class-1} His father from Kenya was a Moslem, his grandfather was a Moslem, his great grandfather was a Moslem, etc.; and he is [against Israel.]{.class-1}

Now I must admit, outside of that, there's not much more I can say about the passage prophetically. I simply [don't know]{.class-1} ([Ich weiss nicht]{.class-1}---I don't know). There are just some things about the passage that haven't been revealed to me, or anybody else, yet.

For instance, take ["Ephraim"]{.class-0} in verse 14. It is not even listed among the twelve tribes in the Tribulation (Rev. 7:5--8); ["Joseph"]{.class-0} is substituted for it (see our remarks about Rev. 7:8 in that Commentary). Given the omission of Ephraim, what the tribe is doing here prophetically ["against Amalek"]{.class-0} is anyone's guess. The ["root,"]{.class-0} in connection with the Second Coming, is Jesus Christ, but He is from [Judah,]{.class-1} not Ephraim (Isa. 11:10; Rev. 5:5, 22:16). At this present time, the root of Ephraim ["is dried up"]{.class-0} (Hos. 9:16).

["After thee, Benjamin"]{.class-0} (vs. 14) is a battle cry (see Hos. 5:8). The tribes wanted to follow Benjamin in battle, and we saw why back under our comments on 3:15. ["Machir"]{.class-0} would be a reference to the half tribe of Manasseh that dwelt on the west side of Jordan (cf. vs. 17). Exactly what the ["governors"]{.class-0} of that tribe do in the Tribulation, I have no idea, but look at Psalm 80:1--2.

["Give ear, O Shepherd of Israel, thou that leadest Joseph like a flock; thou that dwellest between the cherubims, shine forth ]{.class-0}\[a prayer for the Second Advent---Isa. 60:1\][. Before EPHRAIM and BENJAMIN and MANASSEH stir up thy strength, and come and save us."]{.class-0}

There are three of the four tribes mentioned in Judges 5:14. Evidently, remnants of those three tribes are under particular attack by the Antichrist at the end of the Tribulation. Both Psalm 60:7 and 108:8 say, ["Gilead is mine, and Manasseh is mine]{.class-0} \[i.e., the tribe of Manasseh on both sides of Jordan\][; Ephraim also is the strength of mine head."]{.class-0} So although the tribe of Ephraim loses its place by name among the twelve tribes sealed in Revelation 7---due to its idolatry in Hoses 4:17---by the end of the Tribulation, a remnant has managed to "redeem itself" and regain its tribal identity in God's eyes.

["Out of Zebulun they that handle the pen of the writer."]{.class-0} According to the commentators and expositors, the tribe of Zebulun produced the "scholars" in Israel at that time, but what prophetic significance that has, I have no idea. The first of the apostles were chosen from the regions of Zebulun and Naphtali (Matt. 4:13--22), and three of the four wrote books of the New Testament (Peter, James, and John). But all of them combined didn't produce the material put out by the apostle from [Benjamin]{.class-1} (Phil. 3:4--5). What connection the tribe has in regards to the Jews at the Second Advent will remain a mystery until the Holy Spirit reveals it to someone.

Now the corrupt modern translations ([ASV, RSV, NASV, NIV, NKJV,]{.class-1} etc.) don't like ["the pen of the writer."]{.class-0}[ ]{.class-28}Being[ ]{.class-0}[religious evolutionists,]{.class-1} their translators and editors don't believe "pens and ink" existed in 1300 B.C., so they change the text to ["the marshal's]{.class-1} (or [commander's]{.class-1} or [lieutenant's]{.class-1} or [recruiter's]{.class-1} \[[NKJV]{.class-1}---it's just as corrupt as any Alexandrian text\])[ staff."]{.class-1} That little piece of infidelity is contrary to [history,]{.class-1} the [Hebrew text,]{.class-1} and the [Scriptures.]{.class-1}

Manuscripts have been found written with [pen and ink]{.class-1} as early as 1400 B.C. ([Halley's Bible Handbook,]{.class-1} 1965, pp. 44--55). The Hebrew word here ([shebet]{.class-1}) is a "scribe's stick," called a [stylus.]{.class-1} It can be used to write like an engraving tool (see Job 19:24) or as a pen. This time the [Septuagint]{.class-1} got it right: ["the scribe's pen of record." ]{.class-1}But we really didn't need any of that to tell us the men who put out the new translations were full of beans when they foisted their "marshal's staff" on their readership. You see, we had the words of the Holy Ghost that books were being written as far back as 1500 B.C. (see Exod. 17:14; Deut. 17:18, 31:19, 24; Josh. 24:26). Always take the words of God Almighty over "recognized scholarship."

Now verses 15--17 list the tribes which didn't help Barak in the battle in Judges 4. There may be some prophetic reference to the Second Advent (especially in regards to Dan---see our comments on Gen. 49:16--17 in that Commentary), but the passage is basically [historical]{.class-1} in nature. Reuben, the Gileadites, Dan, and Asher stayed put; they were obviously called but didn't come. The great exception is [Issachar]{.class-1} (vs. 15): their ["princes"]{.class-0}---the rulers, the bigshots---came to fight with Barak. (We have already commented on Barak's army being ["on foot"]{.class-0} under 4:10, which see.)

The eastern tribes---Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh---didn't come to the battle. Reuben stayed with his flocks (vs. 16). The sheep and cattle are what made them settle on the east side of Jordan to begin with (Num. 32:1--4). Moses thought it was an attempt to get out of fighting to take Canaan, and he made them promise that they wouldn't rest in their inheritance until the land was conquered (Num. 32:6--32). They fulfilled that commitment (Josh. 22:1--3), but when they were needed here, they stayed home. They were more concerned about their sheep than they were about their fellow Jews. The New Testament commentary is:

["For all seek their own, not the things which are Jesus Christ's"]{.class-0} (Phil. 2:21).

The Bible describes such people as ["greedy dogs"]{.class-0} (Isa. 56:11). The Christian is commanded:

["Look not every man on his own things, but every man also on the things of others"]{.class-0} (Phil. 2:4).

["Let no man seek his own, but every man another's wealth"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 10:24).

["Bear ye one another's burdens, and so fulfill the law of Christ"]{.class-0} (Gal. 6:2).

["We then that are strong ought to bear the infirmities of the weak, and not to please ourselves"]{.class-0} (Rom. 15:1).

Part of loving the brethren (1 John 3:14) is laying down your life for them and helping them out when they have a real need (1 John 3:16--18).

In verse 17, two tribes in the land were summoned to fight and didn't come: Dan and Asher. The ["ships"]{.class-0} of Dan were at Joppa (Josh. 19:46), a major seaport in Israel (Jon. 1:3; 2 Chron. 2:16; Ezra 3:7) even today. Asher's inheritance was along the seacoast. The ["breaches"]{.class-0} were where the mouths of rivers breached the coast; those were where the tribe's major cities were.

Verse 18 gives you the two main tribes that made up Barak's army (see 4:6, 10), but ["the high places of the field"]{.class-0} is definitely a "red flag" that you are reading more than history, as is evidenced by what follows in verses 19--22. Notice ["Megiddo"]{.class-0} in verse 19. That is where ["Armageddon"]{.class-0} (Rev. 16:16), "the hill of the crowded," is located; that is ["the high places of the field]{.class-0} \[the Valley of Megiddo, the plain of Esdraelon\][."]{.class-0}

19 The kings came and fought, then fought the kings of Canaan in Taanach by the waters of Megiddo; they took no gain of money.

20 They fought from heaven; the stars in their courses fought against Sisera.

21 The river of Kishon swept them away, that ancient river, the river Kishon. O my soul, thou hast trodden down strength.

22 Then were the horsehoofs broken by the means of the pransings, the pransings of their mighty ones.

["The KINGS]{.class-0} \[plural\][ came and fought, then fought the KINGS of Canaan in Taanach by the waters of Megiddo"]{.class-0} (vs. 19). Well, no, not in Judges 4 they didn't (see our comments on vs. 3). The multiple Kings are at the Second Advent.

["And I saw the beast, and THE KINGS OF THE EARTH, and their armies, gathered together to make WAR against him that sat on the horse, and against his army"]{.class-0} (Rev. 19:19).

Where do they fight? ["By the waters of MEGIDDO"]{.class-0}: that's ["Armageddon"]{.class-0} in Revelation 16:16---"the hill of Megiddo." ["Armageddon"]{.class-0} means "the hill of the crowded" because [200 million]{.class-1} UN troops show up to fight there (Rev. 9:16).

["They took no gain of money."]{.class-0} The Canaanites couldn't spoil the Israeli army; there was no profit from the war. That's what happened to those Kings there in Genesis 14: Abram went after them with ["his trained servants"]{.class-0} and got back everything they had taken in the battle against Sodom and the other cities of the plain down there below the Dead Sea (Gen. 14:14--16). At Armageddon, those Kings and their armies not only don't take any spoil, they get turned into a banquet for the buzzards (Rev. 19:17--18).

Now here's the opposing side at the Battle of Armageddon: ["They fought from heaven, the stars in their courses fought against Sisera"]{.class-0} (vs. 20). That has nothing to do with astrology like some of the modern infidels would have you believe. In that Bible, stars are not only a reference to the celestial bodies in the second heaven, they're also [angels]{.class-1} (Job 38:7; Rev. 1:20, 12:4, 7--9). Second Thessalonians 1:7 says that at the Second Advent, ["the Lord Jesus shall be revealed from heaven with his mighty angels."]{.class-0} Who are those ["mighty angels"]{.class-0}? They're [you]{.class-1} if you're saved. Jesus said that every saved person in this age is ["equal unto the angels; and are the children of God, being the children of the resurrection"]{.class-0} (Luke 20:36).

When you get saved by faith in Jesus Christ, you become a son of God (John 1:12): you are part of a spiritual "race," if you will, that takes the place of the sons of God that fell in the Old Testament (Job 38:7 cf. Gen. 6:2--4; Psa. 82:6--7; 2 Pet. 2:4; Jude 6). As a son of God, when Jesus Christ returns at the Rapture, you get a body like His body at His resurrection (1 John 3:1--3; Phil. 3:20--21). The glorified body you receive at the Rapture is likened to the celestial bodies of the stars (1 Cor. 15:40--49). So ["the stars"]{.class-0} that fight against the ["Sisera"]{.class-0} of the future (the Antichrist) are the ["armies" ]{.class-0}from ["heaven"]{.class-0} that follow Christ on ["white horses"]{.class-0} at His Second Coming (Rev. 19:4). Enoch prophesied about that 3,900 years before the birth of Christ.

["And Enoch also . . . prophesied of these, saying, Behold, the Lord cometh with ten thousands of his saints, To execute judgment upon all"]{.class-0} (Jude 14--15).

So Deuteronomy 33:2 has nothing to do with the giving of the Law at Sinai, like all the commentators and expositors would lead you to believe. Moses is talking about Christ's Second Advent, and not one commentator got it. I have 24 major commentaries in my office, and not one of them got Deuteronomy 33:2 or Judges 5:4--5 right. Par for the course.

Back to Judges 5: ["The river of Kishon swept them away"]{.class-0} (vs. 21). The Kishon is the river that flows through the Valley of Megiddo. But there is another reason the river shows up in the verse: ["O my soul, thou hast trodden down strength."]{.class-0} Literal in the case of Jesus Christ at the Second Advent. He "trods" on 200 million UN troops (Isa. 63:3; Mal. 4:3; Rev. 19:15) until the blood flows five feet deep for 1,280 miles (Rev. 14:20).

Verse 22: ["Then were the horsehoofs broken by the means of the pransings, the pransings of their mighty ones."]{.class-0} This is another verse that points to a future battle and not the one of Judges 4. The word ["pransings"]{.class-0} is typically used of [horses,]{.class-1} not people. So in this verse you have [two ]{.class-1}cavalries, not one calvary and an opposing infantry like in Judges 4. At the Battle of Armageddon, there is an earthly cavalry where the horses are mutant monsters (Rev. 9:17) and a heavenly cavalry of supernatural horses (Rev. 19:14). The ["white horses"]{.class-0} from Heaven are said to be ["horses of fire"]{.class-0} in the Old Testament (2 Kings 2:11, 6:17).

Joel 3:11, in speaking of the Second Advent, says, ["thither cause thy mighty ones]{.class-0} \[Judg. 5:22\][ to come down, O LORD]{.class-0} \[Rev. 19:14\][."]{.class-0} Back in Joel 2:4--5, the Holy Ghost describes those ["mighty ones"]{.class-0}:

["The appearance of them is as the appearance of horses; and as horsemen, so shall they run ]{.class-0}\[Rev. 19:14\][. Like the noise of chariots on the tops of mountains shall they leap, like the noise of a flame of fire]{.class-0} \[Judg. 5:5 cf. 2 Kings 2:11\][ that devoureth the stubble, as a strong people set in battle array]{.class-0} \[2 Kings 6:17\][."]{.class-0}

So the whole thing is laid out: Jesus Christ, the glorified armies from Heaven, the horses and chariots of fire. Do you see now why the scholars don't want you taking the passage too seriously? There is too much there that still awaits future application. They want you to think the Book is a volume of dry history or obscure Hebrew poetry and Greek prose that you have to come to them to understand. The last thing they want is for you to find out that you can know that Book, [without]{.class-1} Greek and [without]{.class-1} Hebrew, by just going to the Author and comparing Scripture with Scripture (1 Cor. 2:13).

23 Curse ye Meroz, said the angel of the LORD, curse ye bitterly the inhabitants thereof; because they came not to the help of the LORD, to the help of the LORD against the mighty.

24 Blessed above women shall Jael the wife of Heber the Kenite be, blessed shall she be above women in the tent.

I have given you the two verses together in this passage so you will see the contrast. In verse 23, you have a [cursed city]{.class-1}, and in verse 24 you have a [blessed woman. ]{.class-1}Historically, the ["Meroz"]{.class-0} of verse 23 is a city the Angel of the Lord cursed because its citizens wouldn't come to help Barak in the battle. R. A. Torrey, in the [Treasury of Scripture Knowledge,]{.class-1} has a sound observation to make on the passage [historically:]{.class-1}

"This city of Meroz seems to have been, at this time, a place of considerable importance, since something great was expected from it; but probably, after the angel of the Lord had pronounced this curse, it dwindled and like the fig-tree which Christ cursed, withered away; so that we never read of it after this in Scripture."

Having made the historical application, Torrey completely missed the [prophetic]{.class-1} significance; ditto Clarke, Henry, Gill, and Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown. I have 24 commentaries on my bookshelf, and not one connected what you are reading with what will take place in the next several years.

In Revelation 17--18, you have a [cursed city]{.class-1} (Babylon the Great) that is pictured as [a woman.]{.class-1} It stands in stark contrast to a [blessed city]{.class-1} in Revelation 21--22 (New Jerusalem) that is likened to [the Bride of Christ]{.class-1} (Rev. 21:2). So in the passage before us here in Judges 5, Meroz is a type of ["BABYLON THE GREAT, THE MOTHER OF HARLOTS"]{.class-0} in the Tribulation (Rev. 17:5), and Jael is a type of the Bride of Christ who returns with her Bridegroom at the Second Advent to bruise the head of the Antichrist (Rev. 19).

Now why is Jael ["blessed above women"]{.class-0} (vs. 24)? Because she kills Sisera, a type of the Antichrist. That is what Abimelech, another type of the Antichrist, is afraid of over in chapter 9, verse 54 here in Judges. So in mythology, you have groups of [warrior women:]{.class-1} in Greece they are the Amazons; in Germany they are the Valkyrie. They are types of the [Bride of Christ]{.class-1} (Eph. 5:25--32; Rev. 19:7--9) at the Second Advent. Song of Solomon 6:10 describes the Bride as ["terrible as AN ARMY with banners."]{.class-0} And not only does Jesus Christ as the Seed of the woman bruise the Serpent's seed (Gen. 3:15), Paul says God will ["bruise Satan"]{.class-0} under the [Church's]{.class-1} feet as well (Rom. 16:20).

Notice that Jael is ["blessed ABOVE women."]{.class-0} That means that any born-again child of God in the Body of Christ is [more blessed than Mary,]{.class-1} the mother of Jesus. Mary was only ["blessed . . . AMONG women"]{.class-0} (Luke 1:28, 42). When someone tried calling Mary ["blessed,"]{.class-0} [Jesus Christ corrected her immediately.]{.class-1}

["And it came to pass, as he spake these things, a certain woman of the company lifted up her voice, and said unto him, Blessed is the womb that bare thee, and the paps which thou hast sucked. But he said, YEA RATHER, BLESSED ARE THEY THAT HEAR THE WORD OF GOD, AND KEEP IT"]{.class-0} (Luke 11:27--28).

No Catholic should get too excited about Mary. She takes [second place]{.class-1} to anybody who trusts Jesus Christ for salvation by grace through faith [without works]{.class-1} (Eph. 2:8--9; Tit. 3:5).

25 He asked water, and she gave him milk; she brought forth butter in a lordly dish.

26 She put her hand to the nail, and her right hand to the workmen's hammer; and with the hammer she smote Sisera, she smote off his head, when she had pierced and stricken through his temples.

27 At her feet he bowed, he fell, he lay down: at her feet he bowed, he fell: where he bowed, there he fell down dead.

28 The mother of Sisera looked out at a window, and cried through the lattice, Why is his chariot so long in coming? why tarry the wheels of his chariots?

29 Her wise ladies answered her, yea, she returned answer to herself,

30 Have they not sped? have they not divided the prey; to every man a damsel or two; to Sisera a prey of divers colours, a prey of divers colours of needlework, of divers colours of needlework on both sides, meet for the necks of them that take the spoil?

31 So let all thine enemies perish, O LORD: but let them that love him be as the sun when he goeth forth in his might. And the land had rest forty years.

The rest of the chapter, with the exception of the last verse, goes back to the historical account of chapter 4. We have already commented on verse 25 back under our remarks on 4:19. The ["milk"]{.class-0} is the ["butter in a lordly dish"]{.class-0}: it's buttermilk.

This repetition and expansion of material is a common Hebrew literary device (see Gen. 41:32). God will give a general account of something and then go through the same thing a second time (and as in the life of Christ, [four]{.class-1} times) giving you more details. The classic example of this---which causes no end of confusion to religious Liberals ("higher" critics), agnostics, and atheists who would rather find fault with what God says than trust it for truth and salvation---is Genesis 1--2. Genesis 1 gives you a general account of creation, ending with the creation of man. Genesis 2 goes back and gives you the details of the creation of man; it's not a separate, conflicting account. The material is [supplementary;]{.class-1} i.e., it [completes]{.class-1} the information you're given about a thing.

Take, for instance, verse 26: ["she smote off his head, when she had pierced and stricken through his temples."]{.class-0} You didn't read about that in 4:21--22. That is additional information given here that [supplements]{.class-1} the account: it [completes]{.class-1} it. She cut off Sisera's head from his body after nailing the head to the ground; David did the same thing to Goliath after rocking his brains out (1 Sam. 17:49--51).

Verse 27 is not only self-explanatory; it is [emphatic.]{.class-1} He "bowed out"; he "kicked the bucket"; he "cashed in"; he "popped off"; [he dropped dead.]{.class-1}

Verse 28 is a lamentation attributed to Sisera's mother. ["Why is his chariot so long in coming? why tarry the wheels of his chariots?"]{.class-0} In other words, "Where's my boy?" There is many a mother who wondered what happened to her son in the South Pacific, in Korea, in Vietnam, in Iraq, in Afghanistan, etc.

But a mother's concern isn't confined to the battlefield or the combat zone. Many mothers worry about their boys after they have left for the ["far country"]{.class-0} (Luke 15:13). The old song goes:

"Where is my wandering boy tonight,

The boy of my tenderest care,

The boy that was once my joy and light,

The child of my love and prayer?"

He's out in the world wasting ["his substance with riotous living"]{.class-0} (Luke 15:13); that's where he is. Sometimes the prodigal comes home, and [sometimes he doesn't.]{.class-1}

I preached at a Christian youth camp one time on "The Prodigal Son." A fellow sat at the back of the auditorium with a Christian girl, hoping to "make time" with her afterwards. When I gave the invitation, she invited her boyfriend to go down and get saved. He said, "I've got a better idea. Let's you and me head for the far country." The young lady said, "I'm afraid we might not come back."

Sisera didn't make it back. He lay dead in a woman's tent, his head severed from his body.

["The lattice"]{.class-0} of verse 28 is connected with the Rapture (see our comments on Song of Sol 2:9 in that Commentary). In this case, it is probably connected with the post-Tribulation rapture of the Tribulation saints. In Revelation 14:14, the Lord Jesus Christ, as the Angel of the Lord, appears at some point prior to the Second Advent.

In the song, Sisera's mother is answered by ["her wise ladies"]{.class-0} (vs. 29), her "ladies-in-waiting." ["Have they not sped?"]{.class-0} (vs. 30). No, they were routed, and her boy fled for his life. ["Have they not divided the prey . . . ?"]{.class-0} No, they [became]{.class-1} prey.

The ["prey of divers colours of needlework"]{.class-0} is Joseph's ["coat of many colours"]{.class-0} (Gen. 37:3); it was a symbol of nobility (2 Sam. 13:18). In Sisera's case, it would be the symbol of a conquering hero (["meet for the necks of them that take the spoil"]{.class-0}). But Sisera didn't end his life as a conquering hero or even a brave man; he ended it as a [coward]{.class-1} who deserted his men.

Verse 31 shows you that the battle between Barak and Sisera is a [type]{.class-1} of a future conflict. ["So ]{.class-0}\[i.e., in the same way\][ let all thine enemies perish, O LORD."]{.class-0} [They will]{.class-1} (Psa. 83:1--9 cf. Zech. 14:1--3; Psa. 110:1--6; Rev. 19:15--21).

["But let them that love him be as the sun when he goeth forth in his might."]{.class-0} There is no doubt when that happens---it is at Christ's Second Advent.

["But unto you that fear my name shall the Sun of righteousness arise with healing in his wings; and ye shall go forth, and grow up as calves of the stall. And ye shall tread down the wicked; for they shall be ashes under the soles of your feet in the day that I shall do this, saith the LORD of hosts"]{.class-0} (Mal. 4:2--3).

["And at that time shall Michael stand up, the great prince which standeth for the children of thy people: and there shall be a time of trouble]{.class-0} \[Jer. 30:7\][, such as never was since there was a nation even to that same time ]{.class-0}\[Matt. 24:21\][: and at that time thy people shall be delivered, every one that shall be found written in the book. And many of them that sleep in the dust of the earth shall awake, some to everlasting life, and some to shame and everlasting contempt]{.class-0} \[John 5:28--29\][. And they that be wise shall shine as the brightness of the firmament; and they that turn many to righteousness as the stars for ever and ever"]{.class-0} (Dan. 12:1--3).

["The harvest is the end of the world; and the reapers are the angels . . . The Son of man shall send forth his angels, and they shall gather out of his kingdom all things that offend, and them which do iniquity . . . Then shall the righteous shine forth as the sun in the kingdom of their Father"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:39--43).

Judges 5 is about Christ's return in power, and if you want further study, then go to the companion passage in Psalm 68. It too is a prophecy in the form of a song. But the whole thing is there: the rain, Sinai, the Kings, leading ["captivity captive"]{.class-0} (Psa. 68:18), the tens of thousands of angelic hosts, wounding the head of the Antichrist, the whole thing. You can get our comments on that chapter in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Psalms,]{.class-1} Volume I.

["And the land had rest forty years,"]{.class-0} like it did after Othniel delivered Israel (see 3:11). Right now, those Jews are back in the land, but they're not "at rest." They're under constant attack from the "Palestinians" in Gaza, from the Lebanese and Syrians up north, from suicide bombers, and now from a possible nuclear strike from Iran. That means that even though [God]{.class-1} brought them back to the land (Isa. 11:11), they are still not right with Him. That will remain their condition until the Deliverer comes (Rom. 11:26--27; Zech. 12:10--11) and gives the land ["rest"]{.class-0} from its enemies (Heb. 4:9; Rev. 20:1--6).

[]{#section-0_1_85c79f89760d3f35_7090.xhtml}

Chapter 6

6:1 And the children of Israel did evil in the sight of the LORD: and the LORD delivered them into the hand of Midian seven years.

2 And the hand of Midian prevailed against Israel: and because of the Midianites the children of Israel made them the dens which are in the mountains, and caves, and strong holds.

3 And so it was, when Israel had sown, that the Midianites came up, and the Amalekites, and the children of the east, even they came up against them;

4 And they encamped against them, and destroyed the increase of the earth, till thou come unto Gaza, and left no sustenance for Israel, neither sheep, nor ox, nor ass.

5 For they came up with their cattle and their tents, and they came as grasshoppers for multitude; for both they and their camels were without number: and they entered into the land to destroy it.

Chapter five ended with ["forty years,"]{.class-0} and this chapter opens with ["seven years."]{.class-0} The peculiar phenomenon of [seven]{.class-1} and [forty]{.class-1} (usually in just that order) shows up time and again in the Old Testament. Sometimes the Scriptures are "forced" to come up with that combination; i.e., an account is put in the Scripture for no apparent reason other than to bring the numbers seven and forty together. Lo[ok up the following verses: Genesis 7:4; Genesis 25:17, 20; ]{.class-33}2 Kings 8:3, 9; 2 Kings 12:1; Numbers 13:22, 25.

Now I don't have all of this put together, but undoubtedly this has to do with the testing of Israel in the Tribulation (see Rev. 13:1--5). Seven is the number of years in Daniel's Seventieth Week (Dan. 7:25--27); forty is a time of probation or testing (Moses was on Sinai ["forty days and forty nights"]{.class-0} \[Exod. 24:18\]; Goliath challenged Israel forty days \[1 Sam. 17:16\]; Jesus Christ was tempted ["forty days and forty nights"]{.class-0} \[Matt. 4:2; Mark 1:13; Luke 4:2\]).

["And the children of Israel did evil in the sight of the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). Once more the cycle of apostasy, oppression, repentance, deliverance, and apostasy begins. This time, God sends in the [Midianites]{.class-1} to raid the crops and cattle of the Israelites (vss. 3--5). Once more this points to the oppression of Israel under the hands of the Antichrist (see our comments on James 5:4--7 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the General Epistles,]{.class-1} Vol. I).

Like the Ishmaelites, the Midianites were some of the rejected sons of Abraham.

["Then again Abraham took a wife, and her name was Keturah. And she bare him Zimran, and Jokshan, and Medan, and MIDIAN, and Ishbak, and Shuah ]{.class-0}\
[. . . . And Abraham gave all that he had unto Isaac. But unto the sons of the concubines, which Abraham had, Abraham gave gifts, and sent them away from Isaac his son, while he yet lived, eastward, unto the east country"]{.class-0} (Gen. 25:1--2, 5--6).

Notice that when Abraham sent away ["the sons of the concubines," ]{.class-0}he sent them to ["the east country."]{.class-0} Here in Judges 6, the Midianites come against Israel with ["the Amalekites" ]{.class-0}\[from the grandson of the rejected son of Isaac, Esau---Gen. 36:12\][, and the children of the east"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). So the implication is that the Midianites led a coalition of nations that had been ostracized by God from the Abrahamic Covenant.

You should remember that when you hear the Moslems referred to as "children of Abraham." Being a child of Abraham means nothing when it comes to the covenant God made with Abraham to give him the land of Canaan (Gen. 13:15--17). The command, [in both Testaments,]{.class-1} is: ["Cast out the bondwoman and her son: for the son of this bondwoman shall not be heir . . . with Isaac"]{.class-0} (Gen. 21:10 cf. Gal. 4:30). No Mohammedan or Arab or "Palestinian" has any right to the land of Israel. God gave that land not just to Abraham, not just to Isaac, but to Jacob and the twelve tribes from him as well (Gen. 28:3--4, 35:12; Exod. 6:3--8; Num. 26:53--55; Deut. 1:8, 5:31, 6:10, 7:13, 8:1, 9:23, 10:11, 11:9, 31, 12:10, 16:20, 19:8, 14, 28:11; etc.). The land doesn't belong to the Pope or any Catholic, Greek Orthodox, Protestant, or ["Israel of God"]{.class-0} (Gal. 6:16). It was promised to the [physical seed]{.class-1} of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. It was promised [unconditionally]{.class-1} (Gen. 15:12--18) and [eternally]{.class-1} (Psa. 105:9--11).

In this case, ["the east"]{.class-0} would be the land east of where Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh settled on the east side of Jordan. In Genesis 29:1--4, it is a reference to Mesopotamia; specifically Haran. Prophetically speaking, ["the children of the east"]{.class-0} will be ["the kings of the east"]{.class-0} that come against Israel in the Tribulation (Rev. 16:12).

["And because of the Midianites the children of Israel made them the dens which are in the mountains, and caves, and strong holds"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). There are caves all over Israel; one of the more famous locations is Engedi on the west side of the Dead Sea where the Qumran Caves of Dead Sea Scrolls fame are (1 Sam. 23:29, 24:1--3). David hid from Saul in a cave at Adullam (1 Sam. 22:1), which was thirteen miles west of Bethlehem. The ["dens"]{.class-0} and ["caves"]{.class-0} here are probably a reference to the ones located in Mt. Ephraim (1 Sam. 13:16, 14:22).

The ["strong holds" ]{.class-0}today would be the [bomb shelters]{.class-1} all over Israel. Since 1951, the Israeli government has required all residential and commercial buildings to have bomb shelters. Israelis have been under constant missile attacks from Lebanon and rocket attacks from the "Gaza Strip." Thanks to the inaction of Bush and Obama, they are about to face the threat of a nuclear Iran.

Verse 4: ["And they encamped against them, and destroyed the increase of the earth, till thou come unto Gaza."]{.class-0} The Midianites and Amalekites come in and take all the crops and all the cattle (["and left no sustenance for Israel, neither sheep, nor ox, nor ass"]{.class-0}). Verse 5 likens them to [grasshoppers,]{.class-1} because grasshoppers, like locusts, eat up all the crops. The Midianites and Amalekites pillage the land from the Jordan to Gaza by the seacoast.

["For both they and their camels were without number."]{.class-0} That is a figure of speech known as [hyperbole:]{.class-1} it is exaggeration for the purpose of emphasis or effect. Obviously the expression ["without number"]{.class-0} doesn't mean their number was endless or that there was no specific number to them, because there was (see 8:10). It means the number was so great that nobody bothered to try to count them as they were fleeing for their lives to the caves, dens, and strong holds.

Again, as in the case of Jabin and Sisera, what you are reading here is a picture of the Moslem confederation that comes against Israel in the Tribulation (see Psa. 83:4--12 and note especially vss. 9, 11 in that passage). Their goal is to destroy the nation (Psa. 83:4) and take the houses, buildings, and cities for themselves. The goal of the PLO (now called the "PA," the Palestinian Authority) has always been to drive Israel into the Mediterranean Sea and take all the land of Palestine for themselves (see chap. 11 of [Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt]{.class-1}).

6 And Israel was greatly impoverished because of the Midianites; and the children of Israel cried unto the LORD.

7 And it came to pass, when the children of Israel cried unto the LORD because of the Midianites,

8 That the LORD sent a prophet unto the children of Israel, which said unto them, Thus saith the LORD God of Israel, I brought you up from Egypt, and brought you forth out of the house of bondage;

9 And I delivered you out of the hand of the Egyptians, and out of the hand of all that oppressed you, and drave them out from before you, and gave you their land;

10 And I said unto you, I am the LORD your God; fear not the gods of the Amorites, in whose land ye dwell: but ye have not obeyed my voice.

Verse 6 is, unfortunately, the common practice of most people, saved or lost. When things are going well, the bills are all paid, the wife and kids are in good health, and you are getting ahead, you tend to relax, shut your Bible, quit praying, start messing with television and magazines, and maybe even be lax on your church attendance. Then the kids get sick or your wife threatens to leave you or you get laid off from your job; then it's, "God help me! God help me! God help me!" If God intervenes and bails you out, you straighten out for a while, and then the drift away begins all over again. Our attitude should be: ["Bless the LORD, O my soul, and forget not all his benefits"]{.class-0} (Psa. 103:2). Sadly, too often Christians do.

It's like the carpenter working up on a ten-story building, and he slides off the roof. As he falls toward the ground below, he screams, "Oh God, help me!" Suddenly, his overalls catch on a nail. Breathing a sigh of relief, he says, "That's all right, Lord; the nail's got me." That's how we are.

It took extreme poverty (["greatly impoverished"]{.class-0}---vs. 6) to drive the Israelites to repentance. David wrote, ["Before I was afflicted I went astray: but now have I kept thy word"]{.class-0} (Psa. 119:67). It is hard to acknowledge, but it is so: it is the [troubles]{.class-1} God sends our way that drive us to forsake sin and seek Him.

Verse 8 is the first mention of the word ["prophet"]{.class-0} since Deuteronomy 34:10. He is anonymous, like th[e prophets in 1 Kings 13:11, 20:13; 2 Kings 9:4; and]{.class-70} 2 Chronicles 25:15--16. It is not that there was no prophet, for Joshua prophesied about Jericho (see our comments on Josh. 6:26 in that Commentary). Back in chapter 4 here in Judges, God couldn't find a man to raise up as a prophet, so He got Him a woman as a prophetess (see our comments on 4:4). Now He is able to get Him a man.

The prophets were men God raised up out of nowhere, during times of declension and trouble, to take the Lord's side in a controversy against His people. They were never official religious figures. God hauled them out of the back end of nowhere and said, "Sic 'em!"

A good example of that is Amos. He said, ["I was no prophet, neither was I a prophet's son; but I was an herdman, and a gatherer of sycamore fruit: And the LORD took me as I followed the flock, and the LORD said unto me, Go, prophesy unto my people Israel"]{.class-0} (Amos 7:14--15). Elijah wasn't anybody special, just somebody from a small town in Gilead.

Now there are seven periods of prophecy in the Bible. The first would be from [Adam to Abraham.]{.class-1} God Himself gives the first prophecy in Genesis 3:15. Enoch prophesied (Jude 14--15); so did Noah (Gen. 9:25--27).

The second period is [Abraham to Moses;]{.class-1} both are called prophets (Gen. 20:7; Deut. 34:10). Jacob prophesied in Genesis 49, and God called Aaron Moses' prophet (Exod. 7:1).

The third period is from [Moses to Joel.]{.class-1} Remembering that the Prophets (Major and Minor) aren't in chronological order, Joel takes you up to the time of the Exile. This is the period of Samuel, David, and Elijah, as well as many others (e.g., Isaiah, Jeremiah, Jonah, et al.).

The fourth period is [Joel to Malachi]{.class-1} and covers the Exilic and post-Exilic periods of Israel's history. It would include Ezekiel and Daniel in the Major Prophets, and Haggai, Zechariah, and Malachi among the Minor Prophets. It goes to the end of the Old Testament and is followed by 400 "Silent Years" of no revelation or prophecy.

The fifth period is Christ on earth. He was the Prophet like unto Moses (Acts 3:23--26). This period would include, of course, the ministry of His forerunner, John the Baptist (Matt. 11:7--9). When Christ was born, the wise men brought Him myrrh (Matt. 2:11); myrrh represented Christ's office as a prophet.

The sixth period is from [Pentecost ]{.class-1}(Acts 2)[ to the Rapture:]{.class-1} it is the [Holy Spirit here on earth]{.class-1} in the Body of Christ in this age. Revelation 19:10 says, ["the testimony of Jesus is the spirit of prophecy."]{.class-0} If you have the Holy Ghost indwelling you (1 Cor. 6:19), you are a prophet who can tell for sure where you are going when you die (1 John 5:13; Phil. 1:21, 23; 2 Cor. 5:1--10).

The seventh and last period of prophecy is the Tribulation, with the two witnesses and the 144,000 (Rev. 1, 7). After that, there are no more prophets. In fact, in the Millennium, if a fellow tries prophesying, his parents are to [kill him]{.class-1} for lying (Zech. 13:1--3). Prophecy is [over ]{.class-1}in the Millennium.

Now you have people in this age that claim to be prophets, but they are no more prophets than they are apostles (Rev. 2:2). People are always curious about people like Nostradamus, Edgar Cayce, and Jeane Dixon. Nostradamus had some things that might apply to European history if you stretched them enough; anything he got right, he copied from the Old and New Testaments. Edgar Cayce was a "psychic healer" who couldn't prophesy a bunny rabbit out of a hole. Jeane Dixon would always reveal her prophecies [after]{.class-1} an event took place. She would "prophesy" things in such general terms that they could mean anything, and when something happened, she would say, "See, I was right." If I "prophesied" that some famous public figure would be assassinated, that wouldn't be anything; somebody somewhere is always getting killed by someone.

The Bible is not that way at all. It will give people [by name]{.class-1} (e.g., Josiah in 1 Kings 13:2 and Cyrus in Isa. 44:28, 45:1). It will give where they will be born (Mic. 5:2) and how they will die (Psa. 22:16) and why (Isa. 53:10).

Mohammed as a prophet is a joke. He couldn't make one historical prophecy that would take place after he died. The Bible could make 48 on one man, anywhere from 1,500--400 years before He was born, and have every single one of them come right through on the money. And Mohammed had no more idea of where he was going when he died ([Hadith,]{.class-1} Bukhari, Vol. V, no. 266) than he did about when "the Hour of Judgment" was coming ([Hadith,]{.class-1} Bukhari, Vol. II, no. 167). John could lay out history from his day to Eternity (Revelation).

Somebody said, "Martin Luther King Jr. was a prophet ahead of his time." That fellow was no prophet. He said he had "a dream"; what he had was a [nightmare.]{.class-1} He was just a [political Communist.]{.class-1} I've got a statement by Martin Luther King Jr.'s wife where she quoted him as saying, "I'm not concerned in the temperature of Hell or the furnishings of Heaven, but with the things men do here on earth" (Coretta Scott King, [My Life With Martin Luther King Jr.,]{.class-1} 1968). Jesus Christ's evaluation of Martin Luther King Jr., based on that one statement alone, would be: ["Get thee behind me, Satan . . . for thou savourest not the things that be of God, but those that be of men"]{.class-0} (Matt. 16:23). The Apostle Paul would add: ["Set your affection on things above, not on things on the earth"]{.class-0} (Col. 3:2). Martin Luther King Jr. was no prophet. A prophet would acknowledge that what God said in that Book is so (1 Cor. 14:37).

Now I have studied the prophets. I know some things about them. I admit that my study may not be exhaustive, but I know the basic characteristics that distinguish the prophets of God in the Bible from this modern bunch of professing prophets.

1\. [The prophets of the Bible thought all the trouble in this world is due to the sinful heart of man.]{.class-1} In that Book, man is [depraved.]{.class-1}

2\. [None of the prophets of the Bible are utopian.]{.class-1} None of them hold out any hope for "peace on earth" apart from the righteous rule of the Prince of peace. You won't find any [real]{.class-1} prophet in that Book trying to get everybody together in one big, happy "global community."

3\. [The messages of God's prophets are always based on a Biblical concept of God.]{.class-1} Not one prophet in the Book (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Ezekiel, Daniel, Hosea, Joel, Amos, Obadiah, et al.) held to the concept of God put forth by Martin Luther King Jr., Reinhold Niebuhr, Barth and Brunner, Rick Warren, Brian McLaren, Rob Bell, or the Liberals in the National Council and World Council of Churches. No Bible prophet speaks of God as a "wonderful, kind, beautiful, sharing, caring" grandfather up in Heaven who loves you no matter what and just wants to give everybody a big hug and kiss. The prophets' concept of God is a Deity who is absolutely holy and will judge you by His absolute standards of truth and righteousness; if you get along with Him at all, it's because of His mercy and grace to a lost, Hell-bound sinner.

4\. [The Bible's prophets all emphasize God's judgment on nations.]{.class-1} Any "prophet" who doesn't put emphasis on God judging whole groups of people for their idolatry, immorality, sex perversion, Bible-rejection, Christ-rejection, pride, conceit, rebellion, and wickedness, is [not]{.class-1} a prophet of God. Any prophet who prophesies of only good despite those things is a [false]{.class-1} prophet (Jer. 23). Whenever a natural disaster hits, this modern bunch of religious apostates ("Evangelical" or Liberal) would [never]{.class-1} attribute a thing like a hurricane or earthquake or mudslide or tsunami or tornado to the Lord (see Amos 4), and they would condemn and disassociate themselves with anyone who did. If any of them are saved (and some of them [are]{.class-1}), they are taking a position exactly opposite of the prophets of the Old Testament. They are not preaching ["all the counsel of God"]{.class-0} like the greatest missionary of the New Testament did (Acts 20:27).

When someone like Jeremiah Wright (Obama's pastor for [twenty years]{.class-1} before Obama ran for President) "damns" America because of its treatment of the "poor oppressed minorities," that's not a Bible prophet. The God of that Bible is a [segregationist]{.class-1} (Deut. 32:8; Acts 17:26). Jeremiah Wright will damn America for supposedly mistreating blacks while he has Louis Farrakhan, a Black Muslim who is the head of the "Nation of Islam," in. That's a professing "Christian" pastor letting someone speak from his pulpit who denies the Trinity, the Deity of Christ, the Holy Spirit, and the Vicarious Atonement. America may indeed be damned, but not for any reason put out by Wright and Farrakhan. That's the pot calling the kettle [black.]{.class-1}

[The message of a true prophet in the Bible is that the only hope for mankind is the Messiah coming to earth.]{.class-1} No prophet in that Book holds out any hope of "man" solving his own problems; no prophet in that Book even entertains the possibility of the government---ANY government (democracy, republic, Socialism, Communism, etc.)---solving your problems. And of course, science, philosophy, education, and religion are all poor jokes when it comes to solving the basic problems of mankind. The only hope for solving war, poverty, crime, disease, natural disasters, and [death]{.class-1} is [the return of Jesus Christ.]{.class-1}

In light of that, don't you find it "highly instructive" that you have never heard one Pope in the last 100 years (Pius XI, Pius XII, John XXIII, Paul VI, John Paul I, John Paul II, Benedict XVI, and "Francis") talk about the Second Coming of the Lord Jesus Christ? Here was John Paul II traveling all over the globe more than any other Pope, and not once did he open his yap about the return of the One he was supposed to be representing (the "Vicar" of Christ, remember?). He talked about "bread not guns," nuclear disarmament, international Socialism, and religious ecumenicism with Hindus, Buddhists, Tibetan Lamas, Moslems, and [snake worshippers;]{.class-1} but not once did he ever give a discourse on the [main theme of the Book---]{.class-1}the Second Coming of Jesus Christ. And you think a bird like that (see Rev. 18:2) is a prophet? Why, he couldn't prophesy his way out of a wet paper bag.

Now just as there are characteristics of true prophets of God, there are certain things that mark out false prophets. Here is what I call "the creed of the false prophet."

1\. [Science is the highest authority.]{.class-1} Whether you define science as a body of empirical facts arrived at by experimentation and observation or knowledge in general, science is [not]{.class-1} the highest authority. The Devil is the smartest being in the universe, and he is not the highest authority. So it is [not true]{.class-1} that science or knowledge---whether it be true or false---is the highest authority.

2\. [Peace is the highest ideal.]{.class-1} In Jeremiah 6:13--14, 8:10--11, preaching peace when there is none is the mark of a false prophet. Even if there were "peace" of a sort to be had, "peace," in and of itself, is [not]{.class-1} the highest ideal. [Righteousness]{.class-1} supersedes peace: it's [righteousness first,]{.class-1} then peace (Heb. 7:2; Psa. 72:2--3, 7, 85:10).

3\. [Nonconformity to the world is abnormal.]{.class-1} There's nothing wrong with you mentally if you don't conform to ["this present evil world"]{.class-0} (Gal. 1:4); in fact, your mind has been transformed and renewed by the Holy Ghost of God (Rom. 12:2). If you are "abnormal" for believing and reading the Bible, passing out tracts, and preaching on the streets, you are only "abnormal" to a lost world where "normal" is as rotten as Hell.

4\. [It is all right to criticize the Bible, but it is not all right to criticize someone's "faith."]{.class-1} That's a peculiar kind of thing. Changing the Bible and attacking the Scriptures are perfectly all right, but don't say anything bad about Catholics, Mormons, Charismatics, Seventh-day Adventists, Moslems, Buddhists, or Hindus. God said the false prophets ["have perverted the words of the living God"]{.class-0} (Jer. 23:36).

5\. [Capital punishment is unjust and cruel.]{.class-1} These thin-skinned girl scouts will get some sap-headed reporter to write or talk about how awful and terrible it is to watch a person fry on the "hot squat" (the electric chair) or get the deadly "cocktail" (lethal injection). Of course, they'll never give the details of how the criminal murdered his victims or the loss of victims' relatives. In that Book, God says if a person takes someone else's life, that person is to be killed. That's found [before the Law]{.class-1} (Gen. 9:6), [under the Law]{.class-1} (Num. 35:31), and [under grace]{.class-1} (Acts 25:11; Rom. 13:4). When you don't execute the murderer, you defile the land (Num. 35:31).

6\. [Guilt feelings are a mental problem.]{.class-1} That's the teaching of a false prophet. If you are guilty, feelings of guilt are the healthiest feelings you can have; the quicker you get a "guilt complex," the better off you will be. Guilt is that prick of conscience God has put in every man to convict him of sin. The answer to feelings of guilt is not to get rid of them by denial or self-justification. You need to come to Jesus Christ for forgiveness and get that of which you are guilty under the blood (1 John 1:7--9).

7\. [Your full punishment is in this life.]{.class-1} Listen, people, just as sure as there are good people who don't get their full reward in this life, there are guilty people who don't get their full punishment in this life. Do you think a faithful witness like Stephen or John the Baptist got all the good God had for either of them? Then what makes you think Hitler got all that was coming to him for the deaths of twelve million of his own citizens, or Stalin or Mao Tse-tung for that matter?

8\. And finally, [all truth is relative,]{.class-1} except for three things. All these fellows who say all truth is relative have [some absolutes.]{.class-1} They are the biggest bunch of hypocrites that ever lived. Their three "absolutes," which they will never compromise, are [evolution, integration,]{.class-1} and [ecumenicism.]{.class-1} You got here by random chance; race-mixing is not only proper but absolutely necessary; the whole world has to come together in one mongrelized pack that is neither black nor white, but only a tattletale gray. Those are religious "fundamentals" for false prophets.

The prophet here in verses 8--10 gives the same message as the Angel of the Lord in 2:1--3, and you can see our comments on that passage. Notice that the prophet falls short of promising deliverance, but it is evident that God does intend to do just that in what follows.

11 And there came an angel of the LORD, and sat under an oak which was in Ophrah, that pertained unto Joash the Abiezrite: and his son Gideon threshed wheat by the winepress, to hide it from the Midianites.

12 And the angel of the LORD appeared unto him, and said unto him, The LORD is with thee, thou mighty man of valour.

13 And Gideon said unto him, Oh my Lord, if the LORD be with us, why then is all this befallen us? and where be all his miracles which our fathers told us of, saying, Did not the LORD bring us up from Egypt? but now the LORD hath forsaken us, and delivered us into the hands of the Midianites.

14 And the LORD looked upon him, and said, Go in this thy might, and thou shalt save Israel from the hand of the Midianites: have not I sent thee?

15 And he said unto him, Oh my Lord, wherewith shall I save Israel? behold, my family is poor in Manasseh, and I am the least in my father's house.

16 And the LORD said unto him, Surely I will be with thee, and thou shalt smite the Midianites as one man.

17 And he said unto him, If now I have found grace in thy sight, then shew me a sign that thou talkest with me.

18 Depart not hence, I pray thee, until I come unto thee, and bring forth my present, and set it before thee. And he said, I will tarry until thou come again.

Again, this is not just ["AN angel of the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 11), but ["THE angel of the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 12), for as the Angel back in 2:1--3, He speaks in the first person, as God (vs. 16).

This is the same Angel that wrestled with Jacob at Peniel (vs. 22 cf. Gen. 32:24--30), and Hosea 12:4--5 defines that Angel as an appearance of Jehovah God. When Moses spoke with ["the LORD . . . face to face"]{.class-0} (Exod. 33:11 cf. Deut. 34:10), he was speaking to the Angel of the Lord, as Gideon was.

When God appeared to men in the Old Testament, this is how He did it. When John wrote ["No man hath seen God at any time"]{.class-0} (John 1:18; 1 John 4:12), he is referring to God's [essence,]{.class-1} His [soul.]{.class-1} The Lord told Moses, ["Thou canst not see my face: for there shall no man see me, and live"]{.class-0} (Exod. 33:20). So when Moses wrote about talking with God ["face to face"]{.class-0} (Exod. 33:11; Num. 14:14; Deut. 5:4, 34:10), he was referring to God appearing to men and speaking to them as the Angel of the Lord.

Notice the ["oak"]{.class-0} in verse 11. The oak holds a prominent place in Scripture and history, and you can see our comments on it under Joshua 24:26 in that Commentary. Undoubtedly it was an [oak]{.class-1}, not a dogwood tree, that was the wood of the cross on which Christ was crucified.

The ["Ophrah"]{.class-0} of verse 11 is a different one than that of Joshua 18:23, which belonged to Benjamin. This is ["Ophrah of the Abiezrites"]{.class-0} (vs. 24); ["the Abiezrites"]{.class-0} were part of the tribe of Manasseh (Josh. 17:2).

Now this is Gideon, the next judge. The Angel greets him as a ["mighty man of valour"]{.class-0} (vs. 12). That's ironic, considering what Gideon is doing in verse 11. Ordinarily, wheat is threshed on a "threshing floor," a flat place on the top of a hill where the wind can blow the winnowed chaff away. But here, Gideon is threshing wheat in a low place---beside a winepress. Verse 11 says he does that to hide from the Midianites what little wheat he is able to thresh. So this ["mighty man of valour"]{.class-0} is hiding because he's [scared.]{.class-1}

Verse 13: ["And Gideon said unto him, Oh my Lord, if the LORD be with us, why then is all this befallen us? and where be all his miracles which our fathers told us of, saying, Did not the LORD bring us up from Egypt? but now the LORD hath forsaken us and delivered us into the hands of the Midianites."]{.class-0} So the message of the prophet in verses 8--9 did not fall on deaf ears. Notice Gideon quotes the deliverance from Egypt but skips the idolatry of the Israelites from verse 10. The answer to ["why then is all this befallen us?"]{.class-0} was ["ye have not obeyed my voice."]{.class-0} When you get down to verse 25, you are going to find out that Gideon's own father had an idol in a grove. If God had ["forsaken"]{.class-0} them, it was because they had [forsaken Him first]{.class-1} (see Deut. 28:20; Judg. 2:12--13, 10:13; 1 Sam. 8:8; 2 Chron. 7:22).

That being said, Gideon knew something that was to his benefit: he knew Israel was in a mess and that only God could help. Blessed is the man who knows his true condition. That was Gideon's ["might"]{.class-0} in verse 14. Paul said, ["when I am weak, then am I strong"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 12:10). It's the ones who think they are strong that are weak (Prov. 16:18). If you are saved, it is because you realized your true condition (Rom. 3:23) and went to the only One who could do something about it (Rom. 3:24--27).

["Go in this thy might, and thou shalt save Israel"]{.class-0} (vs. 14). God is calling Gideon to deliver Israel. Immediately Gideon begins to [alibi]{.class-1} (vs. 15), as Moses did when God called him in Exodus 3--4: he is [poor]{.class-1} and ["the least in ]{.class-0}\[his\][ father's house."]{.class-0} But that is God's rule for service.

["For ye see your calling, brethren, how that not many wise men after the flesh, not many mighty, not many noble, are called: But God hath chosen the foolish things of the world to confound the wise; and God hath chosen the weak things of the world to confound the things which are mighty; And base things of the world, and things which are despised, hath God chosen, yea, and things which are not, to bring to nought thi]{.class-0}[ngs that are: That no flesh should glory in his presence"]{.class-71}[ ]{.class-45}(1 Cor. 1:26--29).

So far in this book, God has used a lefthanded man, an ox goad, a Gentile woman, a tent peg, and a man who wouldn't fight without a woman. If God can use such things, [He can use you.]{.class-1}

Now Gideon had seven qualifications which made him fit for service in God's eyes.

1\. He had conviction about his true state.

2\. He had ["no confidence in the flesh"]{.class-0} (cf. Phil. 3:3).

3\. He had an attentive ear to what God said.

4\. He was obedient in small things (see our comments on vss. 25--27).

5\. He had power for great things (see our comments on vs. 34).

6\. He was unafraid to criticize false religion (see our comments on vss. 27--32).

7\. He got the peace of God through grace (see our comments on vs. 17).

If you have those seven characteristics, you, like Gideon, will be equipped to serve God.

Back to Judges 6: ["And the LORD said unto him, Surely I will be with thee"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). That is what makes the difference between defeat and victory: the Lord being with you in your endeavor. When God wasn't with Israel, the Midianites and Amalekites were able to come in and loot them to the point of poverty, Sisera was able to oppress the northern tribes with his 900 iron chariots, a fat man was able to subjugate one of the toughest tribes in Israel. But when they repented and got right, God was ["with"]{.class-0} them; and they could defeat an elite force, overthrow armored cavalry with only infantry, and take on 600 men with a stick. But for all of that to happen, they had to [get on God's side first.]{.class-1}

During the Civil War, someone asked Abraham Lincoln whether he thought God was on his side. Lincoln replied that he wasn't so much concerned about which side God was on as he was about him being on God's side. That is a true statement. The most important thing for you as a Christian is to make sure that you and God are in fellowship. When that is settled, you don't have to worry about whatever you undertake to do, no matter what the outcome. If you are right with God, the Lord is with you, and you are invulnerable until you accomplish the purpose God has set for you.

Now I trust you understand that when I talk about God being with you, I am speaking of more than just the indwelling Holy Spirit of God. If you are a born-again child of God, you have the promise of your Saviour that He is ["with you alway, even unto the end of the world"]{.class-0} (Matt. 28:20). But that is not about what I'm talking. I'm talking about walking with God in fellowship like Enoch and Noah (1 John 1:6 cf. Gen. 5:24, 6:9). You are "with God" in the sense that you agree with and act according to what He says in His word. You take God's side in a controversy, even against your own self. You labor on His behalf (1 Cor. 3:9).

Verse 17: ["And he said unto him, If now I have found grace in thy sight, then shew me a sign that thou talkest with me."]{.class-0} This is a Jew asking for a sign because that's how his nation started (see our comments on 1 Cor. 1:22 in that Commentary). The ["sign"]{.class-0} here is not the test of the fleece; that comes later in the chapter (vss. 37--40). The ["sign,"]{.class-0} in the immediate context (vs. 21), is the miraculous acceptance of a sacrifice, similar to what you find [in Leviticus 9:24; 1 Chronicles 21:26; 2 Chronicles 7:1; ]{.class-45}1 Kings 18:38. The sign given to the ["evil and adulterous generation"]{.class-0} of Christ's day that God was speaking to them through Christ (Matt. 11:27; John 8:26, 28, 38, 12:50) was His death, burial, and resurrection (Matt. 12:39--40). Though never called a "sign" in regards to the Gentiles, Christ's resurrection is still the [confirmation]{.class-1} of His virgin birth and Deity (Rom. 1:3--4). We will discuss "signs" in regards to the will of God more when we get to verses 37--40.

19 And Gideon went in, and made ready a kid, and unleavened cakes of an ephah of flour: the flesh he put in a basket, and he put the broth in a pot, and brought it out unto him under the oak, and presented it.

20 And the angel of God said unto him, Take the flesh and the unleavened cakes, and lay them upon this rock, and pour out the broth. And he did so.

21 Then the angel of the LORD put forth the end of the staff that was in his hand, and touched the flesh and the unleavened cakes; and there rose up fire out of the rock, and consumed the flesh and the unleavened cakes. Then the angel of the LORD departed out of his sight.

The ["kid"]{.class-0} is ["made ready"]{.class-0} (vs. 19) as an offering (see 13:15--16), along with its accompanying ["meat offering"]{.class-0} (13:19 cf. Lev. 2). It was "seethed" (Exod. 29:31; i.e., [boiled]{.class-1}---Lev. 8:31) before being burned.

["An ephah"]{.class-0} is a little under a bushel. The whole ["ephah of flour"]{.class-0} wasn't used to make the ["unleavened cakes"]{.class-0} since the normal amount of flour used for a meat offering was ["a tenth part"]{.class-0} (Lev. 6:20; Num. 28:5). So when Gideon made ["unleavened cakes OF an ephah of flour,"]{.class-0} the word ["of"]{.class-0} there would mean "from," as in the expression ["of ]{.class-0}\[from\][ the tribe of Judah"]{.class-0} (see Exod. 31:2).

Verse 21 is from where the idea of a [lightning rod]{.class-1} comes. The "rod," in this case, is the Angel's [staff.]{.class-1} "Lightning" is presumed based on the fire falling from Heaven, as it did in the case of Elijah on Mt. Carmel (1 Kings 18:38).

22 And when Gideon perceived that he was an angel of the LORD, Gideon said, Alas, O Lord GOD! for because I have seen an angel of the LORD face to face.

23 And the LORD said unto him, Peace be unto thee; fear not: thou shalt not die.

24 Then Gideon built an altar there unto the LORD, and called it Jehovahshalom: unto this day it is yet in Ophrah of the Abiezrites.

With the Angel calling fire from Heaven and departing out of his sight (vs. 21), ["Gideon perceived"]{.class-0} that he had been speaking to the Angel of the Lord (vs. 22). Over in Judges 13, ["the angel of the LORD ascended in the flame of the altar"]{.class-0} (Judg. 13:20). You have to admit, that would help your "perception" a bit.

Gideon says, ["Alas, O Lord GOD! for because I have seen an angel of the LORD face to face"]{.class-0} (vs. 22) because seeing the Angel of the Lord was the equivalent of seeing the Lord, and God had told Moses, ["there shall no man see me, and live"]{.class-0} (Exod. 33:20). But as we discussed in our remarks on verse 11, there was a difference between seeing God in His unsheathed glory and His manifestation as the Angel of the Lord. The Angel of the Lord was a form God took so He could interact personally with His creation.

["Peace be unto thee"]{.class-0} (vs. 23). That's what Jesus said to the disciples at His resurrection (Luke 24:26; John 20:19, 21, 26). The resurrected body of Jesus Christ was called ["the angel of God"]{.class-0} by the Apostle Paul (Acts 27:23; Gal. 4:14), so the Angel of the Lord in the Old Testament was a preincarnate appearance of Jesus Christ that was like His glorified body after the Resurrection (John 17:5).

In response to the Lord's words in verse 22, Gideon builds an altar and calls it ["Jehovah-shalom"]{.class-0}---"the Lord is peace" or "the Lord send peace." Jesus said:

["Peace I leave with you, my peace I give unto you: not as the world giveth, give I unto you. Let not your heart be troubled, neither let it be afraid"]{.class-0} (John 14:27).

Faith in Jesus Christ gives us ["peace with God"]{.class-0} (Rom. 5:1). His Gospel is ["the gospel of peace"]{.class-0} (Rom. 10:15), for it reconciles us to God (Rom. 5:10; 2 Cor. 5:18, 20; Col. 1:20). The Kingdom of God is ["righteousness, and peace, and joy in the Holy Ghost"]{.class-0} (Rom. 14:17).[ "The fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace,"]{.class-0} etc. (Gal. 5:22). Jesus Christ is the personification of peace, [spiritually]{.class-1} now (Eph. 2:14) and [physically]{.class-1} at the Second Advent (Mic. 5:5). And as believers in Christ, we not only have ["peace with God"]{.class-0} but[ "the peace of God"]{.class-0} in our hearts (Phil. 4:7).

25 And it came to pass the same night, that the LORD said unto him, Take thy father's young bullock, even the second bullock of seven years old, and throw down the altar of Baal that thy father hath, and cut down the grove that is by it:

26 And build an altar unto the LORD thy God upon the top of this rock, in the ordered place, and take the second bullock, and offer a burnt sacrifice with the wood of the grove which thou shalt cut down.

27 Then Gideon took ten men of his servants, and did as the LORD had said unto him: and so it was, because he feared his father's household, and the men of the city, that he could not do it by day, that he did it by night.

28 And when the men of the city arose early in the morning, behold, the altar of Baal was cast down, and the grove was cut down that was by it, and the second bullock was offered upon the altar that was built.

29 And they said one to another, Who hath done this thing? And when they enquired and asked, they said, Gideon the son of Joash hath done this thing.

30 Then the men of the city said unto Joash, Bring out thy son, that he may die: because he hath cast down the altar of Baal, and because he hath cut down the grove that was by it.

31 And Joash said unto all that stood against him, Will ye plead for Baal? will ye save him? he that will plead for him, let him be put to death whilst it is yet morning: if he be a god, let him plead for himself, because one hath cast down his altar.

32 Therefore on that day he called him Jerubbaal, saying, Let Baal plead against him, because he hath thrown down his altar.

Now the Lord commands Gideon to ["throw down the altar of Baal that thy father hath, and cut down the grove that is by it."]{.class-0} We have discussed the groves under our remarks on 3:7 (which see). In place of Baal's altar, Gideon is to rear up an altar to the Lord and use the wood from the grove to make a burnt offering to God. (The ["this rock"]{.class-0} of vs. 26 is the same rock on which Gideon offered the kid and unleavened bread back in vs. 20.) The peculiar thing about the sacrifice was that it was to be ["the second bullock"]{.class-0} (vss. 25--26). The rule was the [firstborn]{.class-1} belonged to God (Exod. 13:2). Something has obviously gone wrong with the firstborn bullock for God to choose the second one.

Well, it could have been that the firstborn bullock had some ["blemish"]{.class-0} that prevented it from being offered to the Lord (see Lev. 1:3, 10, 3:1, 6, 4:3, 23, etc.). It could also have been that the Midianites took it (vs. 4). But far more likely is that Gideon's father had dedicated the firstborn bullock to Baal and it had been sacrificed.

Now look at the ["mighty man of valour"]{.class-0} in verse 27. He wouldn't go bust up the altar of Baal in broad daylight ["because he FEARED his father's household, and the men of the city."]{.class-0} Isn't it amazing what God sees in people?

The Holy Spirit put verse 27 there to show you how [human]{.class-1} the Bible's heroes are. How honest the Bible is, and how well God understands you and me. About the time you think you found someone you can "idolize," the Holy Spirit records some glaring error or fault to let you know that person is [just like you:]{.class-1} ["Elias was a man subject to like passions as we are"]{.class-0} (James 5:17).

Verse 27 should teach you two things. First, [you are not worth fifteen cents.]{.class-1} ["All flesh is as grass, and all the glory of man as the flower of grass"]{.class-0} (1 Pet. 1:24). ["Every man at his best state is altogether vanity"]{.class-0} (Psa. 39:5).

Second, you [shouldn't be discouraged]{.class-1} by what you just read. Sure you are no good in and of yourself. You need to get that, or what I am about to give you will be misapplied to your detriment. You are no good, but [God can still use you.]{.class-1} God can use a man who realizes he isn't worth anything and that the only way he can accomplish anything is [through the Lord.]{.class-1}

God sees the potential in a man that the man does not even realize himself. God looked at Gideon and saw a ["mighty man of valour"]{.class-0} rather than a scared bunny rabbit. Contrariwise, God knows what a man won't do, as well. When the Lord sent Samuel to get a King from among Jesse's sons, Samuel took one look at Jesse's oldest boy and thought for sure that he was ["the LORD'S anointed"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 16:6). But God told Samuel this: ["the LORD seeth not as man seeth; for man looketh on the outward appearance, but the LORD looketh on the heart"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 16:7).

You see, God knows the basic [character]{.class-1} of a man. Character isn't manifest through just individual acts. It shows through over a period of years. It takes years to develop a character, and God sees the "big picture."

You take Gideon. Gideon may have been scared, but did you notice that he did what God told him to do. ["Valour"]{.class-0} is another word for [courage.]{.class-1} Well, courage is not the absence of fear; it's being scared and going on anyway. Once Gideon was assured God wanted him to deliver Israel, he went into battle like a madman. He chased the Kings of the Midianites until he was so tired that he could hardly stand. But he stuck to the pursuit until he got them and killed them; then he came back and whipped the ones who wouldn't come out to help him. The fellow was tough, but you wouldn't figure it from what you've read so far.

Well, Gideon goes through[ ]{.class-0}with what God told him to do, but he does it under cover of darkness because he's scared. When the Baalites wake up the next morning, their statues of the "sacred heart of Jesus" and "Our Lady" are busted up and all the trees of the grove are cut down. In their place is a stone altar with the ashes of Joash's second bullock still smoldering on it.

Those Baalites have a "conniption." "Holy Mother of God!" "Who did this?!" "Religious bigotry!" "Heretic!"
