Then you had better have the proper sacrifice that God will accept (Heb. 10:10--14)---and I don't mean a jug of hooch and a starchy cookie (see our work on [The Mass]{.class-1}).

24 And the woman bare a son, and called his name Samson: and the child grew, and the LORD blessed him.

25 And the Spirit of the LORD began to move him at times in the camp of Dan between Zorah and Eshtaol.

This is Samson. His name means "man of the sun." This is a reference to ["the Sun of righteousness"]{.class-0} that arises ["with healing in his wings"]{.class-0} (Mal. 4:2; see also Matt. 13:43). So from his birth, Samson is marked as a type of Christ. Like Christ in His childhood, as Samson grows up, God blesses him (vs. 24 cf. Luke 2:52). This also sets Samuel and John the Baptist as types of Christ in that regard (1 Sam. 3:19; Luke 1:80).

["And the Spirit of the LORD began to move him at times in the camp of Dan"]{.class-0} (vs. 25). Although the nature of these "moves" is not revealed here, from what is given in chapters 14--16, these must have been feats of great strength. Comparing the ministry of the Holy Spirit in Samson with other judges in the book, the purpose of these moves was to prepare Samson to deliver Israel from the Philistines (see 3:10, 6:34, 11:29).

The trouble was, somewhere along the way, Samson lost sight of his purpose (see vs. 5). God ends up having to use Samson's lust to seek ["an occasion against the Philistines"]{.class-0} (14:4). In other words, if God had not worked out the circumstances of the next chapter to get Samson angry enough at the Philistines to do something about it, Samson would have gone along and fit right in with the world. He would have been an Old Testament version of Demas (2 Tim. 4:10; see also our remarks under Phile. 24 in that Commentary).

[]{#section-0_1_ecc8f570a0d25487_7098.xhtml}

Chapter 14

14:1 And Samson went down to Timnath, and saw a woman in Timnath of the daughters of the Philistines.

2 And he came up, and told his father and his mother, and said, I have seen a woman in Timnath of the daughters of the Philistines: now therefore get her for me to wife.

3 Then his father and his mother said unto him, Is there never a woman among the daughters of thy brethren, or among all my people, that thou goest to take a wife of the uncircumcised Philistines? And Samson said unto his father, Get her for me; for she pleaseth me well.

4 But his father and his mother knew not that it was of the LORD, that he sought an occasion against the Philistines: for at that time the Philistines had dominion over Israel.

["Timnath"]{.class-0} (vs. 1) is the ["Timnah"]{.class-0} of Joshua 15:57 and the ["Timnathah"]{.class-0} of Joshua 19:43. It was supposed to be a city shared by the tribes of Judah (Josh. 15:21) and Dan (Josh. 19:1--40). The trouble was, neither tribe drove out the Philistines who inhabited the city. So what you are about to read is a result of the incomplete obedience of the Jews recorded in chapter 1.

Samson ["saw a woman"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). That was a "besetting sin" of his (16:1, 4), and it became his downfall (chap. 16). David got into trouble when he ["saw a woman"]{.class-0} (2 Sam. 11:2). What precipitated the Flood was ["the sons of God"]{.class-0} seeing ["the daughters of men"]{.class-0} and leaving ["their first estate"]{.class-0} to cohabitate with them (Gen. 6:2 cf. Jude 6).

Jesus said, ["Whosoever looketh on a woman to lust after her hath committed adultery with her already in his heart."]{.class-0} Job said, ["I made a covenant with mine eyes; why then should I think upon a maid?"]{.class-0} (Job 31:1). Proverbs tells you not to lust after the beauty of the ["strange woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 6:24--25) because ["beauty is vain"]{.class-0} (Prov. 31:30). What you want for a wife, young man, is not some "super model" that every man gawks and drools over; you need ["a woman that feareth the LORD"]{.class-0} (Prov. 31:30).

Notice that this woman is always called ["a woman"]{.class-0}: verse 1---["a woman,"]{.class-0} verse 2---["a woman,"]{.class-0} verse 3---["a woman,"]{.class-0} verse 7---["a woman."]{.class-0} She is never called a [maiden]{.class-1} or a [virgin.]{.class-1} She's "been around the block." She's like the girls in modern America: she's been pawed over by every boy in high school before she graduates.

Samson's ["lust of the eyes"]{.class-0} (1 John 2:16) leads to direct disobedience. God told those Jews they weren't to marry those heathens in the land: they weren't to give their daughters to the sons of those nations nor take the daughters of those peoples for wives for their sons (Deut. 7:3; Josh. 23:12). The New Testament application is: ["Be ye not unequally yoked together with unbelievers: for what fellowship hath righteousness with unrighteousness? and what communion hath light with darkness?"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 6:14). Samson's lust led to sin, and his sin is going to lead to death (cf. James 1:15).

Verse 3: ["Then his father and his mother said unto him, Is there never a woman among the daughters of thy brethren]{.class-0} \[the Danites\][, or among all my people ]{.class-0}\[Israelites\][, that thou goest to take a wife of the uncircumcised Philistines?"]{.class-0} So this isn't the first time Samson was over in Philistine territory trying to "make time" with the Philistine girls. That Book says, ["evil communications]{.class-0} \[i.e., those with whom you commune, your friends\][ corrupt good manners]{.class-0} \[your manner of living\]["]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 15:33). It says, ["a companion of fools shall be destroyed"]{.class-0} (Prov. 13:20).

Verse 4: ["But his father and his mother knew not that it was of the LORD."]{.class-0} Now how could this be ["of the LORD"]{.class-0} when you just read the direct command of God against it (Deut. 7:3)? Surely this is a "contradiction in the Bible." But the text never says that God [approved]{.class-1} of what Samson was doing. Although ["the wrath of man worketh not the righteousness of God"]{.class-0} (James 1:20)---in other words, Samson was [not right]{.class-1} in this---still God can make ["the wrath of man"]{.class-0} to praise Him (Psa. 76:10)---that is, God can take the wrong a man does and turn it to God's divine purpose.

This is the [permissive will]{.class-1} of God. God did [not tell]{.class-1} Samson to go marry a Philistine woman; He is [allowing]{.class-1} it for the purpose of getting Samson to fight against the Philistines. If Samson had followed the [directive will]{.class-1} of God, he would have stayed away from the Philistines until God said, "Sic 'em!"

That God does not approve of what Samson is doing is obvious by what follows: both Samson's wife and his father-in-law are [killed.]{.class-1} Eventually, Samson dies a suicide. He is [punished]{.class-1} for the wrong that he did, even though God did use it to accomplish His purpose.

5 Then went Samson down, and his father and his mother, to Timnath, and came to the vineyards of Timnath: and, behold, a young lion roared against him.

6 And the Spirit of the LORD came mightily upon him, and he rent him as he would have rent a kid, and he had nothing in his hand: but he told not his father or his mother what he had done.

7 And he went down, and talked with the woman; and she pleased Samson well.

8 And after a time he returned to take her, and he turned aside to see the carcase of the lion: and, behold, there was a swarm of bees and honey in the carcase of the lion.

9 And he took thereof in his hands, and went on eating, and came to his father and mother, and he gave them, and they did eat: but he told not them that he had taken the honey out of the carcase of the lion.

Samson and his parents start out together to go to Timnah, but they don't end up arriving together. Samson ends up in ["the vineyards of Timnath"]{.class-0} (vs. 5) by himself. This begs the question: What was he doing in VINEyards where grapes were grown? As a Nazarite, he wasn't to have anything to do with grapes in any form. Of course, he wasn't [eating]{.class-1} or [drinking]{.class-1} them, but Samson was like a lot of Laodicean Christians: he was trying to get as close as he could to the line between right and wrong without crossing it. Of course when you're that close, it doesn't take much for the Devil to shove you over the line. The verse for the Christian in this regard is 1 Thessalonians 5:22.

"Abstain from all APPEARANCE of evil."

All the corrupt perversions put out since 1880 (including the so-called ["New" KJV]{.class-1}) obliterate the truth of the verse by changing it so you [can appear]{.class-1} to do evil as long as you are not [actually doing]{.class-1} it. They read, ["every kind]{.class-1} (or [form]{.class-1}) [of evil."]{.class-1} That means you can frequent bars and saloons, and as long as you are only drinking sodas, everything's all right. You see how the snow drifts? If Samson had not [appeared]{.class-1} to be breaking his Nazarite vow, he would not have gotten into the trouble in which he is about to get.

["And behold, a young lion roared against him. And the Spirit of the LORD came mightily upon him, and he rent him as he would have rent a kid, and he had nothing in his hand"]{.class-0} (vss. 5--6). This is genuine history from which the Greeks got their mythical strong man "Hercules." The problem was they were about 600 years too late to produce anything original.

A fellow called the Bible Baptist Bookstore one time all upset over the fact that he read a story where Hercules was swallowed by a whale off the coast of Joppa. The implication was that surely the Bible had copied the legend of Hercules when it recorded the story of Jonah. As it turned out, the myth of Hercules came out in 400 B.C. [Jonah was written in 862 B.C.]{.class-1} Every time infidels try to get you to believe the Bible copied mythology, it turns out [mythology plagiarized the Bible.]{.class-1} It's kind of like Mohammed and the [Koran.]{.class-1} Everything Mohammed got for his religion was a perversion of the Old Testament theocracy under the Mosaic Law; he never had an original thought in his life.

Now as Samson passed through the vineyard outside of Timnath, ["a young lion roared against him."]{.class-0} According to Psalm 104:21, ["The young lions roar after their prey"]{.class-0}; Samson is on the menu for this lion. Just then, the Holy Spirit comes on Samson in a mighty way, and with his bare hands, he rips that lion in two.

There's a story I have always liked in regards to Samson and the lion. A little colored boy was looking through the pictures in the family Bible one time, and he said to his mother, "Momma, I thought de lion was de King of beasts." She said to him, "Dat's so." "Well, how come the man in this heah picture is tearin' up this lion?" he asked. His mother replied, "I dunno, but I can tell you one thing, you can be sure no lion painted dat picture."

Now Samson is taking that lion by the jaws and is not just stopping the beast from sinking its teeth into him, but he actually rips the jaws back. He tears the creature apart. A lion generates anywhere from 600--945 pounds per square inch in his jaws, depending on the beast's size. You can see what the Bible means when it says, ["the Spirit of the LORD came mightily"]{.class-0} on Samson (vs. 6).

The account ends on an ominous note, though: ["but he told not his father or his mother what he had done"]{.class-0} (vs. 6). Why? Because when Samson ripped that lion in two, he had a [dead body in his hands.]{.class-1} He had ["defiled the head of his consecration"]{.class-0} (Num. 6:6--9). Momma and daddy would have had him go to the Tabernacle and shave his head and offer the sacrifice. Everyone would know he was no longer a Nazarite. The implication from 16:17, 20 is that once his head was shaven, his strength would go also. With his strength gone, he would be useless as a deliverer of Israel.

I am sure Samson didn't want to disappoint his parents, especially his momma, but more than likely, he was probably proud of his hair (see Absalom in 2 Sam. 14:26). He didn't want to get it cut because all the girls liked it and thought it was "cute" (that's the standard line).

I have seen young men stand in front of a mirror for ten minutes---ten minutes, man!---with a comb, primping their hair. I have never understood that. Why would any man need more than three to five minutes in front of a mirror to take care of everything: shaving, brushing his teeth, and combing his hair?

Back in 1972, a fellow named Mark Spitz won seven gold medals in the Olympics for swimming. I wouldn't have hired the guy to clean up my yard. Why not? Because he was a lazy, good-for-nothing bum; that's why.

I used to swim. I know a competitor can cut time off his laps by shaving his head. Spitz had hair clear down to his collar. That fellow learned he could win without cutting his hair, so he didn't.

Do you know what Bob Jones Sr. used to say? He said, "It is a sin to do less than your best." [Spitz didn't do his best;]{.class-1} he found he could win without doing his best. If he had cut his hair, he could have shaved a second off every fifty yards. That's why I said he was a lazy bum.

Now, Samson met his parents in Timnath at the Philistine woman's house. Evidently this is the first time he even talked to her. Verse 1 says he ["saw"]{.class-0} her, and that sight was enough for Samson to say, ["she pleaseth me well"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). She still ["pleased Samson well"]{.class-0} after he talked with her (vs. 7). But by the end of the chapter, he won't be pleased with her anymore.

["And after a time he returned to take her"]{.class-0} (vs. 8). Samson is going back and forth to Timnath arranging the wedding. On one of those trips, ["he turned aside to see the carcase of the lion."]{.class-0} He finds ["a swarm of bees and honey in the carcase of the lion."]{.class-0}

Now one might overlook Samson killing the lion in regards to defiling his consecration; after all, he had to defend himself or be killed. In addition, he was operating under the power of the Holy Spirit. But what Samson does next has nothing to do with self-defense or the Holy Spirit at all. Samson takes the honey from the dead carcass of the lion, and he defiled his parents by giving them some. As in the case of killing the lion, he told them nothing about where he got the honey. There is no question now of Samson violating his consecration.

If you want to know what eventually led to Samson losing his strength, it was the sin of [secrecy.]{.class-1} Samson is covering up his sin just like Achan back in Joshua 7 and just like David with Bathsheba. Samson keeps his sin secret to spare his momma's feelings, but he should have confessed what he did and fulfilled the word of God concerning it.

It doesn't do any good to keep your sin secret. God sees it and will bring it to judgment (Eccl. 12:14). Psalm 90:8 says, ["Thou hast set our iniquities before thee, our secret sins in the light of thy countenance."]{.class-0}

Proverbs 28:13 says, ["He that covereth his sins shall not prosper: but whoso confesseth and forsaketh them shall have mercy."]{.class-0} Samson should have prayed with David, ["cleanse thou me from secret faults."]{.class-0}

10 So his father went down unto the woman: and Samson made there a feast; for so used the young men to do.

11 And it came to pass, when they saw him, that they brought thirty companions to be with him.

12 And Samson said unto them, I will now put forth a riddle unto you: if ye can certainly declare it me within the seven days of the feast, and find it out, then I will give you thirty sheets and thirty change of garments:

13 But if ye cannot declare it me, then shall ye give me thirty sheets and thirty change of garments. And they said unto him, Put forth thy riddle, that we may hear it.

14 And he said unto them, Out of the eater came forth meat, and out of the strong came forth sweetness. And they could not in three days expound the riddle.

["So his father went down unto the woman"]{.class-0} (vs. 10). The expositors and commentators make all kinds of speculation about why only Samson's father is mentioned as going to the wedding. Mrs. Manoah accompanied her husband back in verse 5 to meet the woman, but here she isn't mentioned.

Now only the father could have been mentioned because he was the head of the household, but more than likely Samson's mother didn't want to have anything to do with her boy marrying a Philistine. Rebekah was ready to die over her son Esau marrying two Hittite women (Gen. 27:46). The marriage here in Judges 14 was a disgrace to Samson's mother, and she wanted nothing to do with it. Notice that the wedding wasn't held at Samson's house, but at the bride's house. This was a sign that the mother and father of the groom did not approve of the marriage.

["And Samson made there a feast."]{.class-0} The feast turns out to be seven days long (vs. 15). This was common in the ancient world. Job celebrated the birthdays of his seven sons in one week (Job 1:4). Ahasuerus held a seven-day feast for the people in his palace (Esth. 1:5--10). Christmas used to be celebrated for twelve days (Christmas on Dec. 25--Epiphany on Jan. 6).

The ["thirty companions"]{.class-0} of verse 11 are known as ["the children of the bridechamber"]{.class-0} in the New Testament (Matt. 9:15; Mark 2:19; Luke 5:34). They are the friends of the bridegroom (cf. John 3:29) who come to help him celebrate at the wedding. Samson has no Jewish friends from his hometown (see our comments on vs. 3), so the Philistines bring in thirty of their own people to keep him company and help him "party." Samson doesn't think much of his ["companions,"]{.class-0} for he comes up with a riddle he knows none of them will get so he can get thirty new suits of clothes out of them (vs. 12).

Orientals are famous for playing games at their weddings, and one of the most common was riddles. One of the first things children do when they learn to read is tell riddles. "What has two hands, runs, and never eats or sleeps? A clock." "What has a mouth, a head, and runs all the time, but is not human or animal? A river." "What is black and white and read (red) all over? A newspaper (or a zebra with sunburn or a penguin with a rash)." "What do you call a ten-foot gorilla? [Sir."]{.class-1} That sort of stuff.

Riddles in literature are famous. There was the "riddle of the Sphinx" in Greek mythology. The Queen had to guess Rumplestilskin's name or lose her baby. Even Tolkien picked up the riddle game and used it in his book [The Hobbit.]{.class-1}

Of course, the best kind of riddle to pose is one to which the guesser isn't privy to the facts behind it. Samson makes reference to getting honey out of the lion's carcass, and none of his "buddies" have any idea about what he was talking because Samson hadn't told anyone what had happened with the lion (vs. 14).

Samson is always playing these little games. He gets with Delilah and leads her on a little at a time to keep her guessing as to the source of his strength. Samson plays around with sin, and his games leave him a [blind, naked suicide.]{.class-1} The Bible says, ["Fools make a mock at sin"]{.class-0} (Prov. 14:9); you had better not play with sin.

The ["garments"]{.class-0} of verse 13 would be the outer garments. The ["sheets"]{.class-0} could be bedsheets, but more likely they are the linen material from which undergarments were made (see Exod. 28:42; Ezek. 44:18).

15 And it came to pass on the seventh day, that they said unto Samson's wife, Entice thy husband, that he may declare unto us the riddle, lest we burn thee and thy father's house with fire: have ye called us to take that we have? is it not so?

16 And Samson's wife wept before him, and said, Thou dost but hate me, and lovest me not: thou hast put forth a riddle unto the children of my people, and hast not told it me. And he said unto her, Behold, I have not told it my father nor my mother, and shall I tell it thee?

17 And she wept before him the seven days, while their feast lasted: and it came to pass on the seventh day, that he told her, because she lay sore upon him: and she told the riddle to the children of her people.

18 And the men of the city said unto him on the seventh day before the sun went down, What is sweeter than honey? and what is stronger than a lion? And he said unto them, If ye had not plowed with my heifer, ye had not found out my riddle.

Verse 15 is given out of chronological order from what follows in verses 16--17. Verse 14 says Samson's companions couldn't guess his riddle in the first three days of the feast; verse 15 skips to the last day of the feast, ["the seventh day."]{.class-0} Well, the companions didn't wait until the last day to get Samson's wife to put the pressure on him to "spill the beans." Verse 17 makes it clear that she was trying to get the answer out of him all seven days. But on the last day, they "put the screws" to the woman. Before she had been helping them out of loyalty to her people; now she has an additional "incentive" to get the answer before it was too late. "Get the answer today, or we'll burn you and your daddy."

Samson's bride weeps "crocodile tears" and says, "You don't love me, or else you would have told me the answer to your riddle." Samson said, "I haven't told my momma and daddy. Why should I tell you?" But with her continual nagging, Samson finally succumbs and tells her what happened.

The Book says that when it comes to sinners, ["Trust ye not in a friend, put ye not confidence in a guide: keep the doors of thy mouth from her that lieth in thy bosom"]{.class-0} (Mic. 7:5). Of course, that could apply to [all]{.class-1} sinners, saved or lost, but it is particularly true of those sinners who care nothing about God or His word. This woman was a heathen Philistine who didn't give the Law of Moses any thought at all when it came to regulating conduct. Samson gave in to the ["continual dropping"]{.class-0} of an unsaved woman (Prov. 19:13, 27:15).

After finally getting the answer out of her husband, Samson's wife goes to the companions and tells them the meaning of the riddle. They wait to the last possible moment for dramatic effect, just like on TV and in the movies, to answer the riddle. Samson makes a rather crude sexual innuendo about his wife: not only does he call her a cow, but he insinuates that by what she had done, she was as unfaithful to him as if she had committed adultery with the companions.

19 And the Spirit of the LORD came upon him, and he went down to Ashkelon, and slew thirty men of them, and took their spoil, and gave change of garments unto them which expounded the riddle. And his anger was kindled, and he went up to his father's house.

20 But Samson's wife was given to his companion, whom he had used as his friend.

Now there is no doubt that Samson has defiled his consecration and has sinned. Nevertheless, God is still using him to accomplish some measure of deliverance for Israel. Up to this point, Samson has [used]{.class-1} the Philistines. He uses the woman for pleasure (vss. 3, 7); he uses the men for friends (see vs. 20). But now God drives a wedge between Samson and the Philistines.

Samson goes to the seacoast town of Ashkelon several miles away and kills thirty men to get the thirty garments for the companions. The implication of the Scripture is that the companions never found out that thirty of their countrymen had been murdered to fulfill the wager.

Samson is so mad at the Philistines in general, and his wife in particular, that he storms out of his father-in-law's house and goes home to momma and daddy. We can infer that the marriage was never consummated, but given the character of the woman and the Philistines, it is irrelevant whether it was or not. Since the bridegroom was gone, everyone figures why waste a perfectly good wedding. So the woman is married off to Samson's "best man."

[]{#section-0_1_5307f6b2d773605f_7099.xhtml}

Chapter 15

15:1 But it came to pass within a while after, in the time of wheat harvest, that Samson visited his wife with a kid; and he said, I will go in to my wife into the chamber. But her father would not suffer him to go in.

2 And her father said, I verily thought that thou hadst utterly hated her; therefore I gave her to thy companion: is not her younger sister fairer than she? take her, I pray thee, instead of her.

3 And Samson said concerning them, Now shall I be more blameless than the Philistines, though I do them a displeasure.

Time goes by and Samson's temper cools off. He takes a kid of the goats as a present and plans to "kiss and make up." It is instructive to note that Judah agrees to give a harlot ["a kid from the flock"]{.class-0} for her services (Gen. 38:17): ["a kid"]{.class-0} was the price of a prostitute. One can't help but think that Samson is trying to "make a point" to his wife with his gift (see our comments on 14:18).

["The time of wheat harvest"]{.class-0} (vs. 1) is in June in the Holy Land.

["But her father would not suffer him to go in."]{.class-0} The woman had been given to another man (vs. 20). Samson's father-in-law offers him the woman's younger, prettier sister as a "consolation prize." This would be a violation of Leviticus 18:18 to a Hebrew. The Law forbade a man from taking his wife's sister as a wife since it would ["vex her"]{.class-0} (the original wife). You can see how this worked out with Jacob before the Law (Gen. 30).

Now Samson turns down the Philistine's offer, but not for any Scriptural reason. You won't find anywhere in the record where Samson operates according to the word of God. Samson refuses the younger sister because [she's not the one he wants.]{.class-1} He's operating according to his own selfish lusts.

What follows is an act of revenge for not getting what he wants. He justifies it figuring the Philistines did to him worse than he is about to do to them (vs. 3). This is still part of God's ["occasion against the Philistines"]{.class-0} (see our comments on 14:4).

4 And Samson went and caught three hundred foxes, and took firebrands, and turned tail to tail, and put a firebrand in the midst between two tails.

5 And when he had set the brands on fire, he let them go into the standing corn of the Philistines, and burnt up both the shocks, and also the standing corn, with the vineyards and olives.

Samson is nothing else if not imaginative. He doesn't just set the Philistines' fields on fire; he sets them on fire in a novel way. He catches 300 foxes; ties the foxes two by two, tail to tail, with a firebrand between them; and sets them loose in the harvested corn (["shocks"]{.class-0}) and unharvested corn (["standing corn"]{.class-0}) of the Philistines.

Now no time element is given for how long it took Samson to catch the foxes, but the implication from verse 5 is that it took place during the wheat harvest (the ["corn"]{.class-0} being ["a corn of wheat"]{.class-0}---John 12:24). Any man who can rip a lion in half wouldn't have any trouble catching 300 foxes in a relatively short period of time. Of course he didn't have to chase them all down and catch them by hand. Undoubtedly he used snares and traps, and kept the captured foxes in cages until he was ready to turn them loose in the Philistines' fields.

6 Then the Philistines said, Who hath done this? And they answered, Samson, the son in law of the Timnite, because he had taken his wife, and given her to his companion. And the Philistines came up, and burnt her and her father with fire.

Having violated his Nazarite oath, you never read of Samson ever confessing his sins, repenting of his sins, or judging his sins. He does not shave his head or bring the required offering. According to Numbers 6:13--14, when the Nazarite's separation was fulfilled, he was to offer a he lamb (male), a ewe lamb (female), and a ram. Without Samson's consent or permission, God is about to force Samson against his will to offer the male and female lambs. And since Samson won't go to the altar, God is going to exact the sacrifices right where they are.

In revenge for Samson burning down their fields, the Philistines burn his estranged wife (the female lamb) and his father-in-law (the male lamb). Later on (16:20), Samson himself will become the ram he was to offer.

Samson is a picture of a disobedient saint who will not do what God tells him to do. God may cover up for a "Samson" like He does here in verse 6, but the Lord ends up killing him ahead of his time (Eccl. 7:17). Sure he made it to Heaven (Heb. 11:32), but what a rough way to go.

7 And Samson said unto them, Though ye have done this, yet will I be avenged of you, and after that I will cease.

8 And he smote them hip and thigh with a great slaughter: and he went down and dwelt in the top of the rock Etam.

More retaliation: tit for tat. Samson's father-in-law gives away Samson's wife; Samson retaliates by burning down the Philistines' fields. The Philistines retaliate against Samson by burning his wife and father-in-law to death. Samson gets vengeance on the Philistines by killing a bunch of them (vs. 8).

Samson says, ["after that I will cease"]{.class-0} (vs. 7). But the cycle of retaliation can only be broken by one or both sides being completely destroyed or repenting. Samson plays with the Philistines. He won't destroy them to the point where they can't launch another attack against Israel, like Barak did to the Canaanites or Gideon did to the Midianites. Samson only kills enough of the Philistines to slake his desire for vengeance. All that does is make the Philistines angry enough to retaliate against Samson, so Samson puts himself in a situation where he [can't]{.class-1}[ "cease."]{.class-0}

["And he smote them hip and thigh"]{.class-0} (vs. 8). The expression ["hip and thigh"]{.class-0} is what is known as an "idiom"; that is, the expression has a meaning which you can't necessarily deduce from the words. A good example is ["cast the same in his teeth"]{.class-0} from Matthew 27:44. Well, the two thieves crucified with Christ weren't in the position to throw anything into Christ's teeth literally. The expression is an English idiom meaning they mocked Him in the same way the scribes and priests did in Matthew 27:41--43.

["Hip and thigh"]{.class-0} is another English idiom meaning "in a ruthless or fierce manner." Samson didn't just kill the Philistines; he killed them ruthlessly and in a fierce manner. After ripping a lion in half, you can imagine what he did to the Philistines.

["And he went down and dwelt in the top of the rock Etam."]{.class-0} Samson ["went down"]{.class-0} in terms of elevation. The place where he slaughtered the Philistines was on a higher elevation than Etam. ["Etam"]{.class-0} was a village of the tribe of Simeon (1 Chron. 4:24, 32). ["Judah"]{.class-0} is involved (vss. 9--11) because Simeon's inheritance was in the territory of Judah (Josh. 19:9). ["The rock Etam"]{.class-0} was a large rock near the village of Etam; it would be like "Stone Mountain" outside of Atlanta, Georgia.

9 Then the Philistines went up, and pitched in Judah, and spread themselves in Lehi.

10 And the men of Judah said, Why are ye come up against us? And they answered, To bind Samson are we come up, to do to him as he hath done to us.

11 Then three thousand men of Judah went to the top of the rock Etam, and said to Samson, Knowest thou not that the Philistines are rulers over us? what is this that thou hast done unto us? And he said unto them, As they did unto me, so have I done unto them.

12 And they said unto him, We are come down to bind thee, that we may deliver thee into the hand of the Philistines. And Samson said unto them, Swear unto me, that ye will not fall upon me yourselves.

13 And they spake unto him, saying, No; but we will bind thee fast, and deliver thee into their hand: but surely we will not kill thee. And they bound him with two new cords, and brought him up from the rock.

["Lehi"]{.class-0} is a good example of the writer of Scripture adding information true in his time which was not the case during the time the event took place (see ["Dan"]{.class-0} in Gen. 14:14). The word ["Lehi"]{.class-0} means "jawbone"; it is obviously a reference to Samson slaughtering the Philistine with ["the jawbone of an ass"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). The place gained its name after the fact (vs. 17), and the writer is recording the name as it was called in his day.

["Then the Philistines went up, and pitched in Judah"]{.class-0} (vs. 9). They are there to fight. Whom? Judah? No, the Philistines are there with an army to fight one man: Samson.

["And the men of Judah said, Why are ye come up against us?"]{.class-0} (vs. 10). ["The men of Judah"]{.class-0} aren't defying the Philistines; they aren't there to fight and drive them out. They are completely compliant with their Philistine masters. Judah has a force of 3,000 men here (vs. 11), and they won't lift a finger against the Philistines. In fact, they are willing to help the Philistines take Samson (vs. 12).

That is a picture of a church that is powerless against the world. The members have all conformed to the world (Rom. 12:2). They don't even try to ["Resist the devil"]{.class-0} (James 4:7). They have reached the point where they are actually helping God's enemies. Examples in the Laodicean church age would be the "seeker-sensitive" churches that take surveys in a community to find out what will bring in people to a church building and then bring in the rock bands, the rap sessions, the new versions, movie clips, coffee shops, snack bars, etc.; and get rid of Bible preaching, sound doctrine, and the Gospel. Other examples are churches that observe Darwin Sunday, "LGBT" (i.e., [sex perverts]{.class-1}) month, Martin Luther King Jr.'s birthday, and "Chrislam." They belong to such organizations as the World Council of Churches and the National Council of Churches that send the tithes and offerings of their parishioners to fund Marxist revolutions overseas.

["To do to him as he hath done to us"]{.class-0} (vs. 10); ["As they did unto me, so have I done unto them"]{.class-0} (11). That's the Philistines retaliating against Samson and Samson retaliating against the Philistines. Both statements are [perversions]{.class-1} of the "Golden Rule" as given by Jesus Christ.

["Therefore all things whatsoever ye would that men should do to you, do ye even so to them"]{.class-0} (Matt. 7:12).

The Bible never gives [carte blanche]{.class-1} to personal vengeance. It teaches vengeance belongs to [God]{.class-1} (Deut. 32:35; Psa. 94:1; Rom. 12:19; Heb. 10:30) and to the powers to whom He dispenses to exercise it under the law (Rom. 13:4). Personal vengeance is [out!]{.class-1}

["Say not, I will do so to him as he hath done to me: I will render to the man according to his work"]{.class-0} (Prov. 24:29).

["Say not thou, I will recompense evil; but wait on the LORD, and he shall save thee"]{.class-0} (Prov. 20:22).

["See that none render evil for evil unto any man; but ever follow that which is good, both among yourselves, and to all men"]{.class-0} (1 Thess. 5:15).

Now Samson is sympathetic toward the plight of Judah. He is not going to fight his own people as long as they don't try to kill him. He allows them to bind ["him with two new cords"]{.class-0} and haul him off to the Philistines.

14 And when he came unto Lehi, the Philistines shouted against him: and the Spirit of the LORD came mightily upon him, and the cords that were upon his arms became as flax that was burnt with fire, and his bands loosed from off his hands.

15 And he found a new jawbone of an ass, and put forth his hand, and took it, and slew a thousand men therewith.

16 And Samson said, With the jawbone of an ass, heaps upon heaps, with the jaw of an ass have I slain a thousand men.

When Samson enters the Philistine camp, a shout of victory goes up from his enemies only to choke in their throats when he snaps the new cords as if they were burnt flax. Then Samson grabs the ["new jawbone of an ass"]{.class-0} (i.e., the jawbone of a donkey that had recently died) to use as a weapon against the Philistines.

The book of Judges has some peculiar weapons. Jael used a tent peg to kill Sisera. Shamgar used an ox goad to kill 600 Philistines. Gideon attacked the Midianites with trumpets, pitchers, and lamps. The idea is God can use [anything]{.class-1} as long as you surrender it to Him. He says to Moses, ["What is that in thine hand?"]{.class-0} (Exod. 4:2). Well, all it was was a rod, a shepherd's staff. But in God's hand, it called down plagues on Egypt and parted the Red Sea. "Little is much when God is in it."

A donkey's jawbone may seem like an unlikely weapon, but it is a formidable one. Before it dries and becomes brittle, it is like iron. Samson was wielding it like a mallet and a hatchet. He's bashing skulls in and breaking Philistine bones with it.

Some infidels cast doubt on one man, armed with only a jawbone, killing a thousand men. The key, though, was not the man, his weapon, or even his fighting skills (in the kung fu movies, one man takes on dozens of men at one time). The reason Samson won was because ["the Spirit of the LORD came mightily upon him"]{.class-0} (vs. 14). The reason Samson could kill a thousand men who had swords, spears, shields, and armor with only ["the]{.class-0} [jawbone of an ass"]{.class-0} as his weapon was the same reason he could rip a lion in two (14:6): [it was the power of the Holy Spirit.]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-28}God is giving Samson supernatural strength, speed, and skill. Samson must have looked like a buzzsaw, man. He was Flash, Superman, and Batman all wrapped up into one.

Verse 16: ["With the jawbone of an ass, heaps upon heaps."]{.class-0} After Samson had killed his first few dozen men, heaps of bodies started piling up, making it harder for the Philistines to attack [en masse. ]{.class-1}After several heaps of bodies, the Philistines could only make their way through a few at a time, making it easier for Samson to take them out.

From a spiritual point of view, it was ["the jawbone of an ass"]{.class-0} God used to rebuke the madness of a false prophet (2 Pet. 2:16). So Samson's weapon is a type of a fool ["for Christ's sake"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 4:10) who practices ["the foolishness of preaching to save them that believe"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 1:21). It should be an encouragement to some of you that God can use ["the jawbone of an ass."]{.class-0}

17 And it came to pass, when he had made an end of speaking, that he cast away the jawbone out of his hand, and called that place Ramathlehi.

18 And he was sore athirst, and called on the LORD, and said, Thou hast given this great deliverance into the hand of thy servant: and now shall I die for thirst, and fall into the hand of the uncircumcised?

19 But God clave an hollow place that was in the jaw, and there came water thereout; and when he had drunk, his spirit came again, and he revived: wherefore he called the name thereof Enhakkore, which is in Lehi unto this day.

20 And he judged Israel in the days of the Philistines twenty years.

Having bragged of his victory, Samson throws away his weapon and names the place where he used the jawbone ["Ramath-lehi"]{.class-0}---"the lifting up of the jawbone," or "jawbone height." But Samson was too quick to get rid of that on which God had put His hand.

It takes a lot out of you to kill a thousand men all by yourself, did you know that? He must have sweat until he couldn't sweat any more. Samson was dying of thirst. To his credit, Samson didn't just gripe and complain about it like the children of Israel did in the wilderness (Exod. 15:22--24, 17:1--3; Num. 20:2--5); he ["called on the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 18). God answered Samson's prayer by cleaving a hollow spot in the jawbone he had just thrown away and letting water flow out of it.

In verse 19, all the new "Bibles" refuse to translate the word ["jaw"]{.class-0}; like the [ASV,]{.class-1} they use the word ["lehi,"]{.class-1} as if the Holy Spirit is talking about the [place]{.class-1} instead of the jawbone. The excuse is that there is no article (["the"]{.class-0}) before [lehi.]{.class-1} But being highly inconsistent in their translating---and [hypocritical,]{.class-1} I might add---when they encounter the same construction with the same word in Isaiah 30:28, they will [add the article]{.class-1} and translate ["in the jaws."]{.class-1} These apostates will violate any rule of English, Greek, or Hebrew to get rid of the God-honored text of 1611. That is the basic, bedrock foundation of every modern translation put out since 1880, [without one exception.]{.class-1}

Having quenched his thirst and revived his spirit, Samson memorializes the spot of the miracle by naming it ["En-hakkore"]{.class-0}---"the well of him that cried." But notice, the name is about [him,]{.class-1} not about the One who answered the prayer. Brethren, the power of prayer is not in the one praying but in the One answering the prayer.

Verse 20: ["And he judged Israel in the days of the Philistines twenty years."]{.class-0} There are two things to notice in this verse. First is the fact that Samson does not deliver Israel from the Philistines. ["He judged Israel IN THE DAYS OF THE PHILISTINES." ]{.class-0}No deliverance. Othniel, Ehud, Barak, Gideon, and Jephthah [delivered]{.class-1} Israel first; [then]{.class-1} they judged. Samson doesn't deliver Israel. With the Philistines [still in charge]{.class-1} and [still oppressing the Jews,]{.class-1} Samson judges Israel. Here's a man full of lust, full of lasciviousness, full of anger, full of vengeance, full of violence; with no repentance, no obedience to the word of God, no getting right. Man, that must have been some term in office.

The second thing to notice is the placement of the verse. The times of the other judges' terms were given at the end of their lives (see 10:2, 12:7, 9--10, 11--12, 14--15). Samson doesn't die until the end of chapter 16. God puts Samson's epitaph [before his ministry was through.]{.class-1} The implication is that God took his "judgeship" from him in 16:1.

[]{#section-0_1_ec3b8a44c07dc000_709a.xhtml}

Chapter 16

16:1 Then went Samson to Gaza, and saw there an harlot, and went in unto her.

2 And it was told the Gazites, saying, Samson is come hither. And they compassed him in, and laid wait for him all night in the gate of the city, and were quiet all the night, saying, In the morning, when it is day, we shall kill him.

3 And Samson lay till midnight, and arose at midnight, and took the doors of the gate of the city, and the two posts, and went away with them, bar and all, and put them upon his shoulders, and carried them up to the top of an hill that is before Hebron.

["Gaza"]{.class-0} was a Philistine city near the Mediterranean coast. It is the city after which the modern "Gaza Strip" is named. That is the territory Bush (the second one) had the Israeli government turn over to the "Palestinians" for "peace." All the Jews got for their trouble was thousands of rockets launched into Israeli territory by Hamas.

Samson is shacked up in a cathouse in the midst of his enemies. When the Philistines in Gaza find out the man who single-handedly murdered over a thousand of their people (see 15:8, 15) is there, they surrounded the place where he was ( ["they compassed him in"]{.class-0}---vs. 2) and put an extra guard at the gate to make sure he wouldn't get out alive. Their plan was to wait until morning and then take him when he came out of the whorehouse.

But Samson foiled their plan. He got up at midnight. The Scriptures gloss over the drama of the situation by simply saying Samson ["took the doors of the gate of the city"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). In order to do that, he would have had to fight his way past the Philistines who ["compassed him in"]{.class-0} and kill all the ones who ["laid wait for him . . . in the gate of the city."]{.class-0} One can't imagine [all ]{.class-1}of the Philistines being asleep "on duty" with Samson hauling away the city gate.

Now think about what all was involved in Samson pulling off what he did in verse 3. Not only did he have to kill a bunch of men, but the structure of ["the doors of the gate of the city, and the two posts"]{.class-0} were anywhere from ten to twelve feet high and twenty to 24 feet across. It could not have possibly weighed any less than [two tons]{.class-1} altogether. Samson doesn't just take the whole city gate, he carries it off to a hill just outside of Hebron. Hebron is about 38 miles away from Gaza. He's picking up a two-ton, bulky structure and hauling it nearly forty miles on his shoulders. Even the Christian weightlifter Paul Anderson, who used to lift an elephant, wouldn't attempt that. Samson is operating under the supernatural power of God.

That being said, Samson is squandering the power God gave him. Why did Samson carry a city gate 38 miles? He's not doing it to deliver Israel from the Philistines. He's doing it to spite his enemies; he's showing off. "Look at me; see what I can do?" There was no spiritual, practical, or military reason for doing what he did. He was just proud and conceited.

Samson is one of the most outstanding examples of grace in the entire Old Testament. He's full of lust and lasciviousness; he's a whoremonger; he's vengeful and murderous; he's proud and conceited; and in all of that, he was completely unrepentant. Salvation was by faith and works in the Old Testament, but Samson had no works until the very end. All of that shows you that if the Holy Spirit had not come back on Samson at the end, that old boy would have gone to Hell. God had grace on Samson.

4 And it came to pass afterward, that he loved a woman in the valley of Sorek, whose name was Delilah.

5 And the lords of the Philistines came up unto her, and said unto her, Entice him, and see wherein his great strength lieth, and by what means we may prevail against him, that we may bind him to afflict him: and we will give thee every one of us eleven hundred pieces of silver.

Once more Samson gets involved with a woman. Although the Bible doesn't outright say, she is undoubtedly a Philistine (see 14:3). What you are about to read is the standard Hollywood plot of the woman betraying her lover (see our remarks on 4:18).

Now up to this point, Samson has violated his Nazarite oath time and time again. He has touched a dead lion, dead men, a dead ass, and [dead women ]{.class-1}if you take the Bible seriously when it says a woman who lives ["in pleasure is dead while she liveth"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 5:6). That old boy could rend a lion in pieces and conquer Philistines, but he couldn't control his own lusts. That Bible says, ["He that hath no rule over his own spirit is like a city that is broken down, and without walls"]{.class-0} (Prov. 25:28).

That's Samson: he can't control his lusts, he can't control his temper, and he can't control a vengeful spirit. He has violated his consecration as a Nazarite over and over again with no confession, no sacrifice, and without getting his hair cut. God is about to call in the barber: it's Delilah.

["The lords of the Philistines"]{.class-0} are [five]{.class-1} in number (3:3); they are the Kings (see 1 Sam. 21:10, 12) of the five main Philistine "city--States": Gaza, Ashdod, Eshkalon, Gath, and Ekron (Josh. 13:3). Five isn't the "number of grace" (the standard Fundamentalist teaching); it is the number of  [death.]{.class-1} The first man dies in Genesis 5:5; the Holy Spirit drops Ananias and Sapphira dead in Acts 5 for lying to Him (see Acts 5:5). The verse about death entering the world through Adam's sin is recorded in Romans 5:12. The only place where grace is connected with the number five is in the "five bleeding wounds He bears, received on Calvary," but it is still connected with [death]{.class-1}---the death of Christ. (For further study, see our work on [Bible Numerics.]{.class-1}) Here, Delilah is paid a total of 5,500 ["pieces of silver"]{.class-0} (vs. 5) to betray Samson to what will end in his [death.]{.class-1}

Notice the Philistines have changed their tactics. Instead of threatening to burn Delilah to get her to betray Samson (see 14:15), they offer her a reward. They offer the "carrot" instead of the "whip." That's because when they used the "whip" back in chapter 14, they got their crops burned down. The old saying is: "You catch more flies with honey than you do with vinegar." Delilah responds to ["the love of money"]{.class-0} (see 1 Tim. 6:10).

["Entice him, and see wherein his great strength lieth"]{.class-0} (vs. 5). That shows you the Philistines knew Samson's strength was unnatural, and they knew the source of his strength was a secret. Samson wasn't some muscular bodybuilder or weightlifter. In all likelihood, he was an average fellow. He was not outstanding in any way that would make you be able to explain his strength naturally. If he had been some muscular giant weighing 400 pounds, they could have explained away why he was so strong. But they knew Samson had a strength beyond his physique.

Well, Samson's secret was that God was with him, but the Philistines couldn't figure that out because they were idolaters. They couldn't admit to themselves that Jehovah was greater than Dagon or Baalzebub, but they are going to (see vss. 23--30; see also 1 Sam. 5).

6 And Delilah said to Samson, Tell me, I pray thee, wherein thy great strength lieth, and wherewith thou mightest be bound to afflict thee.

7 And Samson said unto her, If they bind me with seven green withs that were never dried, then shall I be weak, and be as another man.

8 Then the lords of the Philistines brought up to her seven green withs which had not been dried, and she bound him with them.

9 Now there were men lying in wait, abiding with her in the chamber. And she said unto him, The Philistines be upon thee, Samson. And he brake the withs, as a thread of tow is broken when it toucheth the fire. So his strength was not known.

10 And Delilah said unto Samson, Behold, thou hast mocked me, and told me lies: now tell me, I pray thee, wherewith thou mightest be bound.

11 And he said unto her, If they bind me fast with new ropes that never were occupied, then shall I be weak, and be as another man.

12 Delilah therefore took new ropes, and bound him therewith, and said unto him, The Philistines be upon thee, Samson. And there were liers in wait abiding in the chamber. And he brake them from off his arms like a thread.

13 And Delilah said unto Samson, Hitherto thou hast mocked me, and told me lies: tell me wherewith thou mightest be bound. And he said unto her, If thou weavest the seven locks of my head with the web.

14 And she fastened it with the pin, and said unto him, The Philistines be upon thee, Samson. And he awaked out of his sleep, and went away with the pin of the beam, and with the web.

Now when Delilah asked Samson, ["Tell me, I pray thee, wherein thy great strength lieth"]{.class-0} (vs. 6), Samson should have cut her off right then and told her, "That's none of your business." Instead he begins to play around with her. It's another form of his riddle game from chapter 14. That ended in disaster; this will end worse.

["If they bind me with seven green withs that were never dried"]{.class-0} (vs. 7). A "green with" was a freshly picked fiber used in medieval England for a new bowstring. But with his first answer, he is already revealing a little of the truth. The number ["seven"]{.class-0} is connected in verse 19 with ["the seven locks"]{.class-0} of [his hair.]{.class-1} He goes further in verse 11 with ["new ropes that never were occupied"]{.class-0}---a metaphor for "new hair that had never been cut." Finally in verse 13, he reveals the secret is connected with his hair. Delilah was just too stupid to "connect the dots" and figure the thing out for herself.

Now each time Samson tells Delilah the supposed way to bind him, there are Philistines hiding in the bedroom seeing if he loses his strength. Samson goes to sleep and wakes up bound the way he told Delilah. Each time he woke up to the cry, ["The Philistines be upon thee, Samson"]{.class-0} (vss. 9, 12, 14). As far as we can ascertain from the text, the Philistines hiding in the bedchamber don't attack because Samson breaks his bonds. If they did, it didn't take long for Samson to make "short shrift" of them.

Given what happened each time, what did Samson think was going to happen when he finally ["told her all his heart"]{.class-0} (vs. 18)? But Samson is too busy playing a game with this woman to think straight. Samson figures ["God is love,"]{.class-0} so He wouldn't possibly judge sin to where he (Samson) would have to pay its wages (Rom. 6:23).

["Behold, thou hast mocked me"]{.class-0} (vs. 10; see also vs. 13). The saying taken from William Congreve is: "Hell hath no fury like a woman scorned." She's insulted that Samson would make fun of her so. Of course, the hypocrite is betraying him to enslavement.

15 And she said unto him, How canst thou say, I love thee, when thine heart is not with me? thou hast mocked me these three times, and hast not told me wherein thy great strength lieth.

16 And it came to pass, when she pressed him daily with her words, and urged him, so that his soul was vexed unto death;

17 That he told her all his heart, and said unto her, There hath not come a razor upon mine head; for I have been a Nazarite unto God from my mother's womb: if I be shaven, then my strength will go from me, and I shall become weak, and be like any other man.

18 And when Delilah saw that he had told her all his heart, she sent and called for the lords of the Philistines, saying, Come up this once, for he hath shewed me all his heart. Then the lords of the Philistines came up unto her, and brought money in their hand.

19 And she made him sleep upon her knees; and she called for a man, and she caused him to shave off the seven locks of his head; and she began to afflict him, and his strength went from him.

20 And she said, The Philistines be upon thee, Samson. And he awoke out of his sleep, and said, I will go out as at other times before, and shake myself. And he wist not that the LORD was departed from him.

Now if the Philistines had thought things through, they would have realized Samson was toying with them, and maybe they did. They don't bring the money to Delilah until Samson reveals to Delilah that he has never had a haircut (vs. 18). After all, Samson was bound with ["new cords"]{.class-0} right before he slew a thousand Philistines (15:13), and it would be nothing for a man who hikes 38 miles with a two-ton gate on his back from walking away with a weaver's shuttle and beam attached to his hair (vs. 14).

But both Delilah and the Philistines recognize the truth when Samson tells it. After weeks (probably) of being worn down by Delilah's constant nagging, Samson finally gives in and tells her that he was a Nazarite from the time he was conceived (vs. 17). Delilah immediately ["saw that he had told her all his heart"]{.class-0} (vs. 18). How did she know that? He had lied to her three times in a row.

This time, though, [God]{.class-1} entered the equation: ["I have been a Nazarite UNTO GOD."]{.class-0} It wasn't a good-luck charm or a talisman or a potion that gave him his strength, like the superstitious heathen would assume; it was [God.]{.class-1} Unsaved, wicked sinners know the truth immediately when [God's glory]{.class-1} is brought into the discussion---[even if they don't believe in God.]{.class-1} When the Philistines hear the condition for God giving Samson his great strength, they finally bring the money to pay off Delilah.

Verse 19:[ "And she made him sleep upon her knees."]{.class-0} She's caressing him, whispering "sweet nothings" in his ear, and running her fingers through his pretty hair until he falls asleep on her lap. Then she calls in a barber to give Samson the haircut he should have given himself when he killed the lion.

Once Samson has gotten "buzzed," the gentle lover turns into a violent hellcat:[ "she began to afflict him."]{.class-0} She hadn't done that up to that point. Now that she is confident he has told her the truth and his strength is gone, she doesn't just wake him up with ["The Philistines be upon thee, Samson"]{.class-0} (vs. 20), she begins to slap him and beat on him. The mask of the lover is off, and the devil underneath is revealed.

["And he awoke out of his sleep, and said, I will go out as at other times before . . . And he wist not ]{.class-0}\[i.e., he [knew]{.class-1} not\][ that the LORD was departed from him"]{.class-0} (vs. 20). ["Ichabod"]{.class-0}---["The glory is departed"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 4:21). He thought everything was going along just like normal, but [God had left him.]{.class-1} The source of his power was gone, and [it wasn't his hair.]{.class-1} That was only the [outward symbol.]{.class-1}

Now this is an [Old Testament]{.class-1} thing. The Holy Spirit could [leave]{.class-1} a believer. That's why David prayed, ["take not thy holy spirit from me"]{.class-0} (Psa. 51:11). That has nothing to do with you as a New Testament believer. The Holy Spirit will never[ leave]{.class-1} the born-again child of God (Heb. 13:5; Eph. 4:30; Phil. 1:6). But in the Old Testament, before the Holy Spirit put believers into the Body of Christ (1 Cor. 12:13), the Holy Spirit could and did leave believers. He could have left David, but didn't. He did leave Saul, and He never returned (1 Sam. 16:14, 28:15). He leaves Samson here, but He returns in verses 28--30.

Without God, Samson couldn't do anything. As a New Testament believer, you may not be able to lose the Holy Spirit, but if you don't abide in fellowship with God, you can lose God's power and His blessing. Jesus said:

["I am the vine, ye are the branches: He that abideth in me, and I in him, the same bringeth forth much fruit: for without me ye can do nothing"]{.class-0} (John 15:5).

That's not talking about salvation; it's talking about bearing fruit after salvation. If you don't abide in fellowship with your Saviour, you won't be able to do anything to bear fruit as a believer. You will be as powerless as Samson after his haircut. If God is in a thing, it will work, and if He isn't, it won't work no matter how smart or crafty you are, or how well your plans are laid, or who your "contacts" are.

Samson gets up, stretches, flexes his muscles, and says to himself, "I'll knock 'em out like I always do"; and God says, "No, you won't." Samson had lost his power.

21 But the Philistines took him, and put out his eyes, and brought him down to Gaza, and bound him with fetters of brass; and he did grind in the prison house.

22 Howbeit the hair of his head began to grow again after he was shaven.

The Philistines put out Samson's eyes. Why? That's where all the trouble started (see our remarks under 14:1). Eve[ "saw" ]{.class-0}something, and she ended up eating the forbidden fruit (Gen. 3:6). Abraham [saw]{.class-1} something, and he ended up lying about his wife (Gen. 20:10--13). Achan ["saw"]{.class-0} something, and he ended up taking the accursed thing (Josh. 7:20--21). Those Israelites were told when they entered the Promised Land that they were to destroy the pictures of the heathen so they wouldn't look at them and be drawn to worship them (Num. 33:51--52). Jesus said:

["The light of the body is the eye: therefore when thine eye is single, thy whole body also is full of light; but when thine eye is evil, thy body also is full of darkness" ]{.class-0}(Luke 11:34).

A good preaching outline for verse 21 (which I believe came from R. G. Lee) is that sin will [blind]{.class-1} you, it will [bind]{.class-1} you, and it will [grind]{.class-1} you. After being blinded, Samson is brought to Gaza, where he lay with the whore and carried off the city gates. He is chained in prison and forced to grind at the mill. He is a picture of a Christian suffering for [doing wrong.]{.class-1}

Peter says, ["Yet if any man suffer as a Christian, let him not be ashamed; but let him glorify God on this behalf"]{.class-0} (1 Pet. 4:16). At the same time he says, ["But let none of you suffer as a murderer, or a thief, or as an evildoer, or as a busybody in other men's matters"]{.class-0} (1 Pet. 4:15). If you are going to go to prison as a Christian, let it be for [doing right,]{.class-1} not for [doing wrong.]{.class-1}

It is one thing to go to prison like Lester Roloff because you don't want the State dictating to you how you rehabilitate rebellious teenagers with preaching, Bible study, and Scripture reading and memorization; it's quite another thing to go to prison because you won't pay your taxes like Stewart Crane or Kent Hovind. There are Christians all over this country who ended up in jails or prisons for beating their wife, writing bad checks, shooting their spouse after finding her committing adultery, molesting children, etc. They are [saved;]{.class-1} they aren't lost. Listen, brethren, if you put down your Bible or won't heed the things written in that Book, you can end up in any kind of trouble that an unsaved person can.

Samson ends up grinding meal for the Philistines, walking around a mill like an ox, being slapped or whipped by his guards as he goes by. Why? Because he tried to deliver Israel? No, because he defiled his consecration and wouldn't make it right according to the Scriptures.

["Howbeit the hair of his head began to grow again after he was shaven"]{.class-0} (vs. 22). The sign of his consecration returns. In the law of the Nazarite, if the Nazarite defiled his consecration by a dead body, he was to shave his head and offer a sacrifice. The days before he defiled himself would be lost, but the implication is that he can reconsecrate himself and fulfill his vow (Num. 6:12). That is what God allows Samson to do here.

While Samson is walking around and around that mill, he is in a one-man prayer meeting. He's praying, "God, if you'll get me out of here, I won't mess up again. I promise. Just give me one more chance." I guarantee you that is what he was doing. That Bible says, ["a just man falleth seven times, and riseth up again"]{.class-0} (Prov. 24:16). Samson has fallen, but he's about to get up. God gives him his second chance, but boy, what a payment!

23 Then the lords of the Philistines gathered them together for to offer a great sacrifice unto Dagon their god, and to rejoice: for they said, Our god hath delivered Samson our enemy into our hand.

24 And when the people saw him, they praised their god: for they said, Our god hath delivered into our hands our enemy, and the destroyer of our country, which slew many of us.

25 And it came to pass, when their hearts were merry, that they said, Call for Samson, that he may make us sport. And they called for Samson out of the prison house; and he made them sport: and they set him between the pillars.

26 And Samson said unto the lad that held him by the hand, Suffer me that I may feel the pillars whereupon the house standeth, that I may lean upon them.

27 Now the house was full of men and women; and all the lords of the Philistines were there; and there were upon the roof about three thousand men and women, that beheld while Samson made sport.

28 And Samson called unto the LORD, and said, O Lord GOD, remember me, I pray thee, and strengthen me, I pray thee, only this once, O God, that I may be at once avenged of the Philistines for my two eyes.

29 And Samson took hold of the two middle pillars upon which the house stood, and on which it was borne up, of the one with his right hand, and of the other with his left.

30 And Samson said, Let me die with the Philistines. And he bowed himself with all his might; and the house fell upon the lords, and upon all the people that were therein. So the dead which he slew at his death were more than they which he slew in his life.

Verse 23 is the first mention of the Philistine god ["Dagon."]{.class-0} He was a fish god. He is always pictured as a merman: human from the trunk up, fish from the trunk down. The crown that was on his head looked like a fish head with an open mouth. If you want to see what it looked like, just tune in to the Pope's midnight Mass on Christmas Eve and look at the miters on the heads of the Cardinals and Bishops; you will see the pagan crown of the Philistine fish god sitting on the heads of professing "Christians." Can you imagine a commercial fisherman like Peter wearing something like that on his head?

The Philistines got together for a big shindig to their fish god and said, ["Our god hath delivered Samson into our hand"]{.class-0} (vs. 23). They were giving glory to a devil (Lev. 17:7; Deut. 32:17; 1 Cor. 10:20). It wasn't some merman or devil who turned Samson over to them; it was the Lord God of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob who took His disobedient saint and gave him into the hand of his enemies because of his sins. Dagon had nothing to do with it (see 1 Sam. 5).

Men haven't changed any since 1120 B.C. They still praise their own gods for accomplishing what only God Almighty did or could do. "We won because our factories were better and produced more; we won because we had more and better weapons; we are prosperous because of our capitalistic free enterprise system." They take the glory from God and give it to science, education, money, philosophy, technology, and even their own looks, talents, and skills.

If America is or ever was a great nation, it had nothing to do with democracy, the Constitution, George Washington, Abraham Lincoln, Manifest Destiny, "amber waves of grain," transcontinental railroads, or "American exceptionalism." It was [God Almighty]{.class-1} who made this nation great, and it is [God Almighty]{.class-1} who will bring it down for its sins.

["Our god"]{.class-0} turns out to be the [wrong god.]{.class-1}

Verse 24 takes place chronologically after verse 25, for it says, ["when the people saw him"]{.class-0}---Samson. After they brought Samson ["out of the prison house"]{.class-0} (vs. 25), ["they praised their god"]{.class-0} (vs. 24).

Now the Lord is watching all that. The Bible says, ["I the LORD thy God am a jealous God"]{.class-0} (Exod. 20:5).

It says, ["thou shalt worship no other god: for the LORD, whose name is Jealous, is a jealous God"]{.class-0} (Exod. 34:14).

It says, ["For the LORD thy God is a consuming fire, even a jealous God"]{.class-0} (Deut. 4:24).

God sees those pagans praising their fish god for something He did. Then He looks over there and sees that old, blind saint fettered to that mill, going round and round, praying, "God help me and give me another chance." God sees Samson hauled out there in front of the jeering mob, and a cry goes up from those Philistines, "Three cheers for Dagon! Hip, hip, hooray! Hip, hip, hooray! Hip, hip, hooray! Praise Dagon from whom all blessings flow!" And the Lord God says, "Uh huh! Well, we'll just see about that. I am going to fix their wagon!"

Samson is brought before the mob and is forced to "make sport" for the Philistines; that is, they put him through all kinds of humiliating things for their amusement. Samson has been reduced from a powerhouse for God to entertaining the world.

That is what has happened to the church in America today. It used to be in this country that if a man could speak well, people would go out to hear him. That's why those old-time evangelists could draw such crowds. But with the advent of television, not only could Americans get professional speakers in their living rooms, they could see circus acts, magicians, people being blown up, belly dancers, couples cohabitating together, sports competitions, singers, murders, etc. Well, who would want to go to church and hear a preacher tell them what they're doing wrong when you can stay home and see all that? So to compete with Hollywood, New York, and Chicago, the churches have had to bring in the canned music, the light shows, costumes, make-up, the pretty girls performing in such a way to make any red-blooded male blush, the overhead screens with the scenery behind the words, and all that junk. Why? To draw a crowd. The churches have had to get rid of Bible teaching and Bible preaching and put on some Hollywood production and spectacular extravaganza to get anyone to come to church. That's the church reduced from Holy Ghost power to Hollywood entertainment to compete with the world.

I have gotten bitter about that sort of thing in my ministry. Before my eyes went out on me, I used to draw every Sunday night when I preached. I am not first a chalk artist; I am a [preacher.]{.class-1} Over half my sermons weren't illustrated sermons at all; they were just preaching. Quite frankly, I have always thought the drawing distracted from the preaching, but everyone expected Dr. Ruckman to draw, so watch the clown perform.

I think some people who have watched me draw (whether in person or TV) have expected a commercial or pitch or something like that. But when I preach, I am not there to entertain my audience. [I am after their hides.]{.class-1} I want something out of them, and it's not their money. I want them to [do]{.class-1} something about what they've heard. Entertainment is OUT! ["It pleased God by the foolishness of PREACHING to save them that believe"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 1:24). Entertainment has nothing to do with it.

Now I imagine as Samson trudged around that mill praying, one day the Lord spoke to Samson and said, "Hey, Samson, what's going on?"

Samson was shocked. It had been a long time since he had heard God speak to him. "Oh, God, please get me out of here. I'll behave myself. I'll do exactly what you want."

"Get yourself out," said the Lord.

Samson said, "Now, Lord, don't treat me that way. You know I'm powerless."

"Haven't you noticed anything about your head?" asked the Lord.

Samson shook his head and felt the locks of his hair on his shoulders. He pulled against his fetters and felt the chain begin to give. "You mean I could get out of here anytime?" he said to the Lord.

God replied, "Not yet. You still have that ram to sacrifice."

"But Lord," said Samson, "you know I can't get a hold of a ram here." And then he stopped in his tracks as it hit him. "Oh," he said, "you mean [me]{.class-1}."

"That's right," said the Lord.

"But how am I going to do that?" asked Samson.

"Just wait," said God, "you'll see."

The day came when the Philistines sent a little boy to lead Samson out by a chain to an arena where the Philistines were having a great celebration to Dagon for delivering Samson into their hands. "Come on, donkey," said the boy as he tugged on Samson's chain. The crowd began to yell out humiliating things for Samson to do, and he had to do them.

After one particularly degrading act, Samson said to the boy leading him around, "Son, I'm so tired. I'm used to leaning against the pole of the mill when I grind. Could you please take my hands and put them on the pillars that hold up the house so I can lean against them and catch my breath?"

Now there were 3,000 men and women on the roof looking down into an arena where Samson was. (There could have also been more Philistines seated below the "balcony," as you see in modern church buildings.) The roof rested on two load-bearing pillars that stood close together. Samson positions himself between the pillars with one arm on one pillar and one arm on the other pillar. Then he prays.

Now according to verse 30, even if Samson prayed out loud the prayers of verses 28 and 30, no one survived to pass on the words of his prayer. The only person who could give the words of Samson's prayer was [the One to whom it was addressed.]{.class-1} Verses 28 and 30 are revealed to the writer of Judges by the [inspiration of the Holy Spirit.]{.class-1}

Verse 30: ["And Samson said, Let me die with the Philistines. And he bowed himself with all his might."]{.class-0} Most pictures of Samson's death have him pushing the pillars out, but if ["he bowed himself,"]{.class-0} he could have pulled the pillars in on himself.

Samson dies a suicide, but according to Hebrews 11:32, he's a hero of the faith who is in Heaven right now. The Catholic Church teaches that suicide is a mortal sin; that is, it is a sin for which there is no forgiveness because it is impossible to repent of it. If suicide is murder (and it is), then there is no repenting of it (or "making penance" for it under the Catholic system) before death. In Roman Catholic theology, a suicide does not "die in a state of grace," so he [cannot]{.class-1} go to Heaven.

Nonsense! Here is a suicide under an Old Testament faith-and-works system who [does]{.class-1} end up in Heaven. What makes you think the blood of Christ won't take care of the sin of self-murder; that is, unless you believe you get the blood of Christ from Christian Brothers' distillery?

The people who believe you get saved (or stay saved) by faith and works in this age say that when you trust Christ for salvation, that takes care of all your past sins, but it doesn't take away your future sins. You have to deal with those as they come up. Listen, people, when Jesus Christ died for your sins on the cross, [all your sins were future:]{.class-1} you hadn't even been born yet.

["The blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from ALL sin"]{.class-0} (1 John 1:7); not just all sins but suicide, or all sins but mortal sins, or all sins but sins you haven't repented of at death. That Bible says that when you trust Christ that you are confirmed ["unto the end, that ye may be BLAMELESS in the day of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 1:8), and that ["he which hath begun a good work in you will perform it until the day of Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} (Phil. 1:6).

Now I hope no one reading this page ever commits suicide. Suicide is a terrible thing for a Christian. It leaves emotional and psychological scars on the loved ones of the suicide. It shows a lack of faith in God and His provision on the part of the suicide, and it is a terrible testimony to an unsaved world. You shouldn't commit suicide, but if you do, you won't go to Hell.

I'll be frank with you, there are some circumstances where if a saved person committed suicide, I wouldn't open my mouth in criticism at all. If you are in constant, excruciating pain and commit suicide because you can't take it any more, I understand why you would do that. I don't recommend it, but I can understand it. If you were in a situation like Rommel where the government threatened to send your wife and kids to a concentration camp and torture them to death if you didn't commit suicide, but if you "popped the pill," they would be taken care of financially for life, I wouldn't blame you a bit if you went through with it.

Honest to God, I don't know how some of these Christians in Communist "reeducation camps" make it year in and year out being tortured without committing suicide to end the torment. I know it has to be the grace of God, but I know ending it all and going home to Heaven must cross their minds. But if a Christian slipped up and hung himself because he couldn't take the torture anymore, I wouldn't say anything at all about that. I think it would be better to do that than "rat" on your brethren and cause a lot more Christians to be tortured.

Christian, you had better be careful about being too strong on things like abortion, divorce, and suicide. If you are adamant in your beliefs about those sort of things and look down on a brother or sister who has gone through misfortunes like that, the Devil is likely to get permission from God to let you experience it to see just how strong your "convictions" are. People like that usually have a remarkable naiveté because they are greenhorns who have no experience.

Did you know there are prescription drugs these days that can cause you to commit suicide? What do you do with someone who has to be on a medication like that and is too weak to take the suicidal thoughts? You had better watch out, or [you]{.class-1} might be called to go through something like that.

Back to Judges 16:[ "So the dead which he slew at his death were more than they which he slew in his life"]{.class-0} (vs. 30). That means that all the Philistines he killed in chapters 14 and 15 didn't add up to even 3,000 people. As amazing as killing a thousand men with ["the jawbone of an ass" ]{.class-0}and carrying away a city's gate were, they didn't come anywhere near to what a judge like Gideon did.

Samson had the potential to inspire the men of Judah and Dan to take on the Philistines and whip them to the point where they would never recover, and he wasted the strength God gave him on selfish lusts. Even at the very end, in his prayer for one last show of strength, the glory of God and the salvation of Israel are not to be found. Samson prays for [vengeance]{.class-1} against the Philistines [because they put out his eyes.]{.class-1} How different from David's prayer: ["Deliver me IN THY RIGHTEOUSNESS"]{.class-0} (Psa. 71:2).

31 Then his brethren and all the house of his father came down, and took him, and brought him up, and buried him between Zorah and Eshtaol in the buryingplace of Manoah his father. And he judged Israel twenty years.

This is the epitaph on Samson's life. But even in his ignominious death he still stands out as a type of Christ. Christ certainly "slew" more in His death than He did in His life. When Christ died, He ["spoiled principalities and powers"]{.class-0} (Col. 2:14--15). That wasn't accomplished by His life; it was accomplished by His [death.]{.class-1} Like Christ, Samson died ["with the wicked"]{.class-0} (Isa. 53:9). Samson's ["brethren and all the house of his father"]{.class-0} (vs. 30) had to retrieve his body from the heathen for burial just like Nicodemus and Joseph of Arimathea had to do to the body of Jesus (John 19:39--42). And Samson had no ["burying place"]{.class-0} of his own; he had to be buried in another man's tomb like Christ.

Now there are some lessons Christians can learn from the life of Samson.

1\. If a Christian doesn't bear fruit, he's cast forth as a branch (John 15:6).

2\. God has chosen the base things of this world to confound the mighty (1 Cor. 1:27). No saint in that Book was more base than Samson. He was a crude roughneck who had no redeeming graces, but God used him anyway.

3\. ["A just man"]{.class-0} may fall seven times, but he'll rise again (Prov. 24:16). Samson falls, but he gets back up. He doesn't go to Hell; he's saved.

4\. For a Christian, ["there is a sin unto death"]{.class-0} (1 John 5:16). A Christian can sin to the point where God has to take him home early and in disgrace.

5\. No Christian who covers his sin will prosper (Prov. 28:13). Samson "gets by," but he doesn't prosper as a judge.

6\. The man who prays (vs. 28) is stronger than the man who mocks (vs. 25).

7\. And finally, if you live according to the lusts of the flesh, you'll die (Rom. 8:13; Gal. 6:8).

[]{#section-0_1_7461fb213f153cb6_709b.xhtml}

Chapter 17

Now with the death of Samson, we have come to the end of the book of Judges as given chronologically. In chapters 17--18 and chapters 19--21, there are two accounts that take place at some point during the time period covered by chapters 1 and 2.

17:1 And there was a man of mount Ephraim, whose name was Micah.

2 And he said unto his mother, The eleven hundred shekels of silver that were taken from thee, about which thou cursedst, and spakest of also in mine ears, behold, the silver is with me; I took it. And his mother said, Blessed be thou of the LORD, my son.
