3 And when he had restored the eleven hundred shekels of silver to his mother, his mother said, I had wholly dedicated the silver unto the LORD from my hand for my son, to make a graven image and a molten image: now therefore I will restore it unto thee.

4 Yet he restored the money unto his mother; and his mother took two hundred shekels of silver, and gave them to the founder, who made thereof a graven image and a molten image: and they were in the house of Micah.

5 And the man Micah had an house of gods, and made an ephod, and teraphim, and consecrated one of his sons, who became his priest.

6 In those days there was no king in Israel, but every man did that which was right in his own eyes.

The account of Micah takes place in Mount Ephraim, which was located in central Palestine. Micah is a member of one of the ten northern tribes. He is probably from the tribe of Ephraim or Manasseh.

Micah had stolen 1,100 ["shekels of silver"]{.class-0} from his mother, the story opens with him confessing what he had done and restoring the money. He says to his mother, ["The eleven hundred shekels of silver . . . about which thou cursedst"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). That could mean one of two things. It could mean she put herself under an oath for God to curse her if she didn't keep her oath. Over and over again in the Old Testament you read something to this effect: "The Lord do so to me and more also if I don't do this (whatever the person promised God)"[ ]{.class-0}(see Ruth 1:17; 1 Sam. 3:17, 14:44, 25:22; 2 Sam. 3:35; 1 Kings 2:23; 2 Kings 6:31).

The more likely understanding of the verse, though, is that she cursed when she discovered the money was missing. "What the blankety-blank?! We've been robbed! Some blankety-blank so-and-so took the blankety-blank money." That is a common thing among religious idolaters. During World War II, it was a common thing to hear Catholics cuss and pray in the same breath as they were fighting. "['Our Father which art in heaven']{.class-0} . . . Watch out for that blankety-blank on your left, Joe . . . ['Hallowed be thy name']{.class-0} . . . Get that blankety-blank coming in!" That kind of thing.

It may even have been that she cursed whoever took the money, which is why Micah brought it back. He thought the money was too "hot" to keep and returned it. This would explain why she blessed Micah once he repented and gave her back the money: she was "reversing" her curse.

Notice how piously all this is handled: ["Blessed be thou of the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 2); ["I had wholly dedicated the silver unto the LORD"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). Doesn't that sound pious? [The whole thing is demoniac from start to finish.]{.class-1}

The ironic thing is that the money she had dedicated to the Lord was intended ["to make a graven image"]{.class-0} ---[an idol.]{.class-1} That was absolutely forbidden in the Ten Commandments: ["Thou shalt not make unto thee any graven image"]{.class-0} (Exod. 20:4).

That is the commandment that is eliminated from the Decalogue by the modern descendants of Micah's mother. The Roman Catholic Church gets rid of the second commandment, and splits the tenth one in two, so they can have statues of Mary, Baby Jesus, a pietá (Mary with a [dead Christ]{.class-1}), crucifixes, the "sacred heart of Jesus," "stations of the cross," and images of the saints for "aids to worship." In pious hypocrisy, the Roman Catholic Church says images are to be "revered" and "honored" while pretending they are not "worshiped."

In verse 4, the mother takes 200 of the 1,100 shekels, and gives them ["to the founder"]{.class-0} (the man who cast the metal for the idols), and she gets for her 200 shekels ["a graven image and a molten image."]{.class-0} She either cheated "God" out of 900 shekels, or there were other things associated with the two main idols on which the rest of the money was spent (see vs. 5).

Interestingly enough, the original edition of the Roman Catholic [New American Bible]{.class-1} eliminated verse 4. It got rid of the 200 ["shekels of silver,"]{.class-0} the ["founder,"]{.class-0} and the ["graven image."]{.class-0} If you throw a rock into a pack of dogs, [the hit dog always yells.]{.class-1} Of course, to cover their tracks, they were forced to add the verse back in the "Revised Edition."

The graven image and the molten image could be a reference to [one]{.class-1} idol. An idol was cast first from molten metal, and then its features were fashioned, after it had cooled, with an engraving tool (see Aaron's case in Exod. 32:4). Nevertheless verse 4 does say ["they"]{.class-0}---plural---in regards to the graven image and molten image, so there could indeed have been two different images.

Verse 5: ["And the man Micah had an house of gods, and made an ephod, and teraphim, and consecrated one of his sons, who became his priest."]{.class-0} So this fellow had a little sanctuary in his house; it was an imitation tabernacle, complete with a priest and an ["ephod"]{.class-0} to talk to the gods (see 1 Sam. 30:7--8).

The ["teraphim"]{.class-0} is a plural Hebrew word referring to the lesser idols in addition to the main idol. These other images were of human form (some of them being the size of a man---see 1 Sam. 19:13--16) and may have been connected with ancestor worship. This is a common thing in Oriental homes. There is a "god shelf" with little statues of the household gods. The Roman version of this was the Pantheon, a building that housed all the images of the gods worshiped in the Roman Empire.

The tendency of pagans is to add Jesus or Jehovah to the "god shelf." They don't mind recognizing Jesus as God as long as He is one of many and has no more authority than Buddha, Jupiter, Brahma, Baal, Vishnu, Odin, Ganesh, Krishna, Allah, etc. They don't like that God who ["judgeth among the gods"]{.class-0} (Psa. 82:1) because He ["is God of gods"]{.class-0} (Deut. 10:17) and ["is above all gods"]{.class-0} (Psa. 135:5, 95:3, 96:4, 97:9; 1 Chron. 16:25; 2 Chron. 2:5). They don't want a Jesus who is the [exclusive]{.class-1} way to Heaven (John 14:6; Acts 4:12).

["And consecrated one of his sons, who became his priest."]{.class-0} Micah sets up a fake priesthood like Jeroboam does in 1 Kings 12:31. Hebrews 5:4 says, ["And no man taketh this honour unto himself, but he that is called of God."]{.class-0} Under the Law, the tribe chosen by God to be priests was the tribe of Levi (Deut. 21:5).

In the New Testament Body of Christ, there is no special priest class. If you run into anyone dressed in a Halloween costume, mumbling Latin words, pretending to turn bread and wine into flesh and blood, and claiming that you can only get forgiveness of sins by confessing to him or one of his Baalite buddies, you are looking at a [false priest]{.class-1} with no more legitimacy than Micah's son. This side of the Resurrection, [every]{.class-1} believer in Christ is a priest (1 Pet. 2:5, 9; Rev. 1:5--6).

And then a grim note in verse 6: ["In those days there was no king in Israel, but every man did that which was right in his own eyes."]{.class-0} This is before Saul and David. There is no centralized government. The priests aren't teaching the Law as they were supposed to do (Mal. 2:7), so no one is operating by the word of God as revealed in the Scriptures. Everyone's deciding what is "right" for him. When that happens, you have moral anarchy and chaos.

In the book of Judges, God levies the worst punishment He can on a nation: He just lets Israel run unchecked. When God lets a people run loose, the things they do just keep getting worse and worse. We will see that in chapter 19 here in Judges. If you find that God is not chastening and whipping you for the wrong you are doing, you had better check your salvation first of all (Heb. 12:8). But if you have trusted Christ alone for salvation and He is letting you alone in your sin, you had better get alone and pray God will give you some indication of His approval or [disapproval]{.class-1} of what you're doing. If He doesn't show you and you are in the wrong, you are liable to continue into ruin (1 Cor. 5:5).

7 And there was a young man out of Bethlehemjudah of the family of Judah, who was a Levite, and he sojourned there.

8 And the man departed out of the city from Bethlehemjudah to sojourn where he could find a place: and he came to mount Ephraim to the house of Micah, as he journeyed.

9 And Micah said unto him, Whence comest thou? And he said unto him, I am a Levite of Bethlehemjudah, and I go to sojourn where I may find a place.

10 And Micah said unto him, Dwell with me, and be unto me a father and a priest, and I will give thee ten shekels of silver by the year, and a suit of apparel, and thy victuals. So the Levite went in.

11 And the Levite was content to dwell with the man; and the young man was unto him as one of his sons.

12 And Micah consecrated the Levite; and the young man became his priest, and was in the house of Micah.

13 Then said Micah, Now know I that the LORD will do me good, seeing I have a Levite to my priest.

Here is a fellow who is a Levite, but at the same time he is ["of the family of Judah"]{.class-0} (vs. 7). How could he be from two tribes at the same time? The answer is that his family had married into the tribe of Judah: his mother was from Judah, and his daddy was from Levi. That is the case of the first Levitical high priest: Aaron married a woman from the tribe of Judah (Exod. 6:23 cf. Num. 1:7; 1 Chron. 2:10). There is an affinity between the tribes of Levi and Judah; it is a type of Jesus Christ who is the ["King of the Jews"]{.class-0} (Matt. 2:2) and our ["High Priest"]{.class-0} (Heb. 3:1) at the same time. Unfortunately that picture is marred in this fellow here, as we shall see.

Now this Levite leaves his hometown of Bethlehem in Judah to go find another place to live. Unlike the Levite in Deuteronomy 18:6--7, he's not traveling to the Tabernacle to serve the Lord there. He's looking for any opportunity that presents itself. There's a lot of that that goes on in the ministry.

Pastors move from one church to the other, and many a time it has nothing to do with "the will of God" or "the Holy Spirit's leading." They are following what I call a "green lead": what church offers the greater salary? Don't misunderstand me, there's nothing wrong with a church taking care of its pastor, but the deciding factor for a pastor taking a church should not be salary, health insurance, a parsonage, an expense account, a new car every year, etc. It should be: "Is this where [God]{.class-1} wants me?" If God is in it, He'll take care of you even if the church doesn't.

The Levite comes to Micah's ["house of gods"]{.class-0} (vs. 5), and he is invited by Micah to become ["a father and a priest"]{.class-0} (vs. 10). The origin of the Roman Catholic Church has nothing to do with Simon Peter being the ["rock"]{.class-0} on which Jesus Christ built His Church (Matt. 16:18). It has nothing to do with "the Church Christ founded" or Jesus Christ or the New Testament. The origin of the Roman Catholic Church goes back to 1400 B.C. with priests called "fathers," with a female deity (2:13), with images as "aids to worship," with special "vestments" (2 Kings 10:22), with intoxicating liquor that had nothing to do with the Lord or the Book (Deut. 32:32--33), and with a fake ["rock"]{.class-0} (Deut. 32:31).

Notice the Roman Catholic "oath of poverty" in verse 10. When a Roman Catholic Priest is ordained, he swears he will only take what is necessary for food and clothing. That way he, unlike Protestant ministers and Baptist pastors, can get out of paying taxes. He gets his pastorium free, with the utilities paid by the church. He gets his groceries free. His clothes are free, his hospitalization is free, his retirement is free, his church supplies are free. This is the church that owns 60% stock in Miller beer. The famous Watergate Hotel in Washington, D.C. is owned by the Roman Catholic Church. They own stock in General Motors and IBM, and they have interest in the Chase Manhattan Bank (among others). This is the church whose "first Pope" said, ["Silver and gold have I none"]{.class-0} (Acts 3:9). For further study, get Avro Manhattan's work [Vatican Billions.]{.class-1}

The Levite here got ["ten shekels of silver"]{.class-0} a year, a new suit of clothes every year, and his food (["victuals"]{.class-0}) (vs. 10). That was enough to draw the Levite in. God, the Law, or what was right had nothing to do with it at all.

["And the young man was unto him as one of his sons"]{.class-0} (vs. 11). The Levite is young enough to be one of Micah's sons, and Micah treats him like one of his sons. At the same time,  he's calling him "father." How ridiculous can you get? And like a Roman Catholic celibate Priest, there's no mention of the Levite being married or having any children. "Father" my foot.

["And Micah consecrated the Levite"]{.class-0} (vs. 12). God didn't; the Lord had nothing to do with this mess. When Korah and his bunch tried to usurp the priesthood back there in the wilderness, God sent a fire out of the Tabernacle and devoured them (Num. 16:9--10, 35).

Verse 13: ["Then said Micah, Now know I that the LORD will do me good, seeing I have a Levite to my priest."]{.class-0} Absolute assurance that everything will be all right, and the guy is [completely deluded.]{.class-1} He's "one up" on Jeroboam; Jeroboam's priests weren't even Levites (1 Kings 12:31). Micah thinks that since he has a Levite acting as his priest that that makes what he's doing right. Sorry, "Mike," you've got the wrong priest, the wrong sacrament, the wrong sanctuary, the wrong image, the wrong motive, and the wrong god. The whole set-up is fouled up from start to finish.

A lot of people think that because they are sincere in their beliefs that that makes them right. All it may mean is that you are [deceived,]{.class-1} despite your sincerity. Paul Levin had a tract that said, "Seriously Speaking, You May Be [Sincerely Wrong."]{.class-1} "But I joined the church Christ founded, took the sacraments, and died in a state of grace." [You'll go to Hell.]{.class-1} Sincerity and faith mean nothing unless placed where God chose to effect your salvation. Those Jews in Paul's day had ["a zeal of God"]{.class-0}: they were zealous in their beliefs and practices---AND THEY DIDN'T KNOW ABOUT WHAT THEY WERE TALKING (Rom. 10:2).

["For they being ignorant of God's righteousness, and going about to establish their own righteousness, have not submitted themselves unto the righteousness of God"]{.class-0} (Rom. 10:3).

Unless you come to God [His way]{.class-1} (John 14:6), through [His Priest]{.class-1} (Heb. 3:1), [in the manner He prescribed]{.class-1} (Rom. 5:1; Eph. 2:8--9; Tit. 3:5--6), you will split Hell wide open. Assurance can be a [satanic assurance]{.class-1} unless it is based on [what God said]{.class-1} (1 John 5:13).

[]{#section-0_1_5ae6fcdc69d5c432_709c.xhtml}

Chapter 18

18:1 In those days there was no king in Israel: and in those days the tribe of the Danites sought them an inheritance to dwell in; for unto that day all their inheritance had not fallen unto them among the tribes of Israel.

2 And the children of Dan sent of their family five men from their coasts, men of valour, from Zorah, and from Eshtaol, to spy out the land, and to search it; and they said unto them, Go, search the land: who when they came to mount Ephraim, to the house of Micah, they lodged there.

3 When they were by the house of Micah, they knew the voice of the young man the Levite: and they turned in thither, and said unto him, Who brought thee hither? and what makest thou in this place? and what hast thou here?

4 And he said unto them, Thus and thus dealeth Micah with me, and hath hired me, and I am his priest.

5 And they said unto him, Ask counsel, we pray thee, of God, that we may know whether our way which we go shall be prosperous.

6 And the priest said unto them, Go in peace: before the LORD is your way wherein ye go.

The chapter opens with the observation of 17:6---["In those days there was no king in Israel."]{.class-0} Every tribe is operating on its own. Occasionally they would come together on their own as they do in chapter 20. The judges, generally, only ruled over certain regions of Israel, which means the tribes outside their areas didn't answer to the judge. At this time, there was not only no King, there was no judge. The tribe of Dan is operating independently of the rest of the tribes, with no one to rein them in when they "step over the line."

The Danites, at this time, had received an inheritance from Joshua, but they had not been able to take all of it. Eighteen cities were allotted to the tribe (Josh. 19:40--46), but some of the cities they shared with the tribe of Judah (see our remarks on Timnath under 14:1). Other cities like Timnath and Ekron were still in the hands of the Philistines. The population of Dan seemed to be concentrated in two main cities: Zorah and Eshtaol (Josh. 19:41; Judg. 13:2, 25 18:2). Joshua 19:47 says, ["And the coast of the children of Dan went out too little for them."]{.class-0} That's why they sent out five men to spy out some new territory for them to take.

As the five spies from Dan travel northward, they come to where Micah lived in Mount Ephraim. The passage says ["they lodged there"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). Now they are not actually in the house where Micah lived, because look at the next verse. ["When they were BY the house of Micah"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). So ["house"]{.class-0} can mean more than just a building; it can also mean "household" (see Acts 16:31). Micah's ["house of gods"]{.class-0} turns out to be ["houses"]{.class-0}---plural (vs. 14). ["The house of Micah"]{.class-0} are all the houses occupied by Micah and his extended family. The Danites are either lodging there in the street among the houses (cf. 19:15)---the more likely---or one of Micah's relatives has extended Oriental hospitality to five travelers and invited them into his house.

["When they were by the house of Micah, they knew the voice of the young man the Levite"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). The Danites recognized the voice of the Levite from Judah because, as we have said, Judah shared territory with Dan (Josh. 15:20, 33). They ask, "What are you doing here, man? It looks like you've got a good thing going on here. What's it pay?"

Notice the Levite's answer: ["Micah . . . HATH HIRED ME, and I am his priest"]{.class-0} (vs. 4). This guy isn't a shepherd of the sheep; he's a [hireling]{.class-1} (see our comments on John 10:12--13 in that Commentary). As a hireling, he doesn't care for the sheep, and when push comes to shove, he [flees,]{.class-1} exactly as Jesus said he would (John 10:13).

Interestingly enough, the hireling is called an ["IDOL shepherd"]{.class-0} in Zechariah 11:16--17. He's a shepherd who worships [idols,]{.class-1} exactly as is the case with this Levite. Not only does he worship the outward idol of a graven image, he worships the inward idol of [money]{.class-1} (Luke 16:13; 1 Tim. 6:10). A shepherd placed over the flock by the Chief Shepherd (1 Pet. 5:4) is not to serve ["for filthy lucre"]{.class-0} (1 Pet. 5:2), even though ["the labourer is worthy of his hire"]{.class-0} (Luke 10:7 cf. 1 Tim. 5:17--18).

Verse 5: ["And they said unto him, Ask counsel, we pray thee, of God, that we may know whether our way which we go shall be prosperous."]{.class-0} Now the Levite has already told the spies of his situation with Micah (["Thus and thus dealeth Micah with me"]{.class-0}---vs. 4). They knew about the idols. At the very least they should have moved on at the news and not have had anything to do with Micah or his "priest." Instead they ask the Levite to inquire of God for them. Which God? The graven image or the immortal, invisible One (1 Tim. 6:16) who said, ["Thou shalt not make unto thee any graven image, or any likeness of any thing that is in heaven above, or that is in the earth beneath, or that is in the water under the earth"]{.class-0} (Exod. 20:4)?

Besides that, an Israelite was to ask counsel of God at the Urim and Thummim on the breastplate of the high priest (Num. 27:21; 1 Sam. 28:6). If not there, then before a prophet of God (1 Sam. 9:6). This Levite is a [false priest]{.class-1} and a [false prophet.]{.class-1}

Now what the Levite says to the spies is absolutely true. Of course he does it with [no prayer;]{.class-1} it's all off the top of his head. But the Lord does prosper the tribe of Dan and allows them to take new territory. That being said, look at Deuteronomy 13:1--3.

["If there arise among you a prophet . . . ."]{.class-0} That's what this Levite is doing here: he's prophesying of the success of the Danites' campaign.

[". . . and giveth thee a sign or a wonder ]{.class-0}\[like a fulfilled prophecy\][, And the sign or the wonder come to pass, whereof he spake unto thee, saying, Let us go after other gods, which thou hast not known, and let us serve them . . . ."]{.class-0} That's the result of this Levite's "prophecy": the whole tribe of Dan falls into idolatry.

["THOU SHALT NOT HEARKEN UNTO THE WORDS OF THAT PROPHET . . . ."]{.class-0} Is that clear? Just because he's like a busted clock (right twice a day) doesn't mean he's speaking God's words or speaking them correctly or with the right motive. If what he says is for the purpose of getting you [to go against the Book,]{.class-1} you are to leave him alone---whether what he says is so or not. Just because the Pope can subscribe to the Trinity, the Deity of Christ, and the Virgin Birth doesn't give him the sense God gave a brass monkey when it comes to [the truth,]{.class-1} the [whole]{.class-1} truth, and [nothing but]{.class-1} the truth. Satan is a monotheist (James 2:19) who believes in the Deity of Christ (Luke 4:34). Are you going to trust him to shoot straight with you about what God said? You better hadn't (Gen. 3:1--7).

[". . . for the LORD your God proveth you, to know whether ye love the LORD your God with all your heart and with all your soul."]{.class-0} Why is God putting up with this idolatrous priest? To find out what the Danites think of the Lord and His words. God lets the Catholic Church go on year after year, decade after decade, century after century, to find out if "a good Catholic" loves [Him]{.class-1} or [momma and daddy]{.class-1} more. Does he think more of [God's words]{.class-1} in His Book, or is he more concerned with [where he will be buried?]{.class-1} "Well, I was born a Catholic, I was raised a Catholic, and I'll die a Catholic." Yeah, and you'll go to Hell like a Christ-rejecting Catholic too.

Listen, people, the Devil will give you just enough truth to [damn your soul.]{.class-1} Have you ever looked at what he said to Eve? Genesis 3:5---["For God doth know that in the day ye eat thereof, then your eyes shall be opened . . . ."]{.class-34} They were (Gen. 3:7). [". . . and ye shall be as gods, knowing good and evil."]{.class-0} They did (Gen. 3:22). You say, "What about that part ['Ye shall not surely die']{.class-0} (Gen. 3:4)?" That was the lie, but notice it was foisted on Eve by [three truths.]{.class-1}

That's why you don't just need "the truth," you need "the WHOLE truth" and "NOTHING BUT the truth." You may get "the truth" in the new versions, but you won't get "the whole truth" because they leave out words and whole verses. And you won't get "nothing but the truth" because they retranslate words so you lose truth. There is only one Book that will give you "the truth, the whole truth, and nothing but the truth"; and it's not in an [ASV, NASV, RSV, NRSV, ESV, NIV, NKJV, ]{.class-1}or ["MEV"]{.class-1} (the [Modern English Version]{.class-1}). You'll only get "the truth, the whole truth, and nothing but the truth" in one Book: an [Authorized Version]{.class-1} from 1611.

7 Then the five men departed, and came to Laish, and saw the people that were therein, how they dwelt careless, after the manner of the Zidonians, quiet and secure; and there was no magistrate in the land, that might put them to shame in any thing; and they were far from the Zidonians, and had no business with any man.

8 And they came unto their brethren to Zorah and Eshtaol: and their brethren said unto them, What say ye?

9 And they said, Arise, that we may go up against them: for we have seen the land, and, behold, it is very good: and are ye still? be not slothful to go, and to enter to possess the land.

10 When ye go, ye shall come unto a people secure, and to a large land: for God hath given it into your hands; a place where there is no want of any thing that is in the earth.

["Laish"]{.class-0} (vs. 7) was all the way in northern Palestine, on the border of Lebanon. The inhabitants of Laish were ["Zidonians"]{.class-0} (Phoenicians from the coastal city of Zidon) by nationality, but they ["had no business"]{.class-0} with the people of Zidon. Although Laish was only forty miles from Zidon, it was far enough away that the Zidonians had no control over it.

["They dwelt careless"]{.class-0}---no cares, no worries. ["Quiet and secure"]{.class-0}---they're safe in their little valley (vs. 28) with no threat of war. Their guard is down because of their "cozy" situation.

["And there was no magistrate in the land, that might put them to shame in any thing."]{.class-0} Ain't that the pot calling the kettle black. Here are these Danites who are about to leap headlong into idolatry with no judge or King to stop them, and they're criticizing those Zidonians in Laish for the same thing. Zidon was the seat of Baal worship (1 Kings 16:31--33). So Dan moves into a territory with a religion that links the tribe historically with the ancient roots of Roman Catholicism and prophetically to the Antichrist (Gen. 49:16--17; Deut. 33:22).

The report of the five spies is a "good" one. Like Joshua and Caleb in Numbers 13--14, they say, "The land is good, and the Lord has given it to us. Go get 'em." But they aren't following the promise of God as given by the man of God; they're following the positive message of a false prophet (see Jer. 23:16--17). If they had been following God, they would have driven the Philistines out of the territory God gave them under Joshua. Only after that would they have inquired of God about taking Laish, and they wouldn't have done it through some renegade Levite serving idols.

11 And there went from thence of the family of the Danites, out of Zorah and out of Eshtaol, six hundred men appointed with weapons of war.

12 And they went up, and pitched in Kirjathjearim, in Judah: wherefore they called that place Mahanehdan unto this day: behold, it is behind Kirjathjearim.

13 And they passed thence unto mount Ephraim, and came unto the house of Micah.

14 Then answered the five men that went to spy out the country of Laish, and said unto their brethren, Do ye know that there is in these houses an ephod, and teraphim, and a graven image, and a molten image? now therefore consider what ye have to do.

15 And they turned thitherward, and came to the house of the young man the Levite, even unto the house of Micah, and saluted him.

16 And the six hundred men appointed with their weapons of war, which were of the children of Dan, stood by the entering of the gate.

17 And the five men that went to spy out the land went up, and came in thither, and took the graven image, and the ephod, and the teraphim, and the molten image: and the priest stood in the entering of the gate with the six hundred men that were appointed with weapons of war.

18 And these went into Micah's house, and fetched the carved image, the ephod, and the teraphim, and the molten image. Then said the priest unto them, What do ye?

19 And they said unto him, Hold thy peace, lay thine hand upon thy mouth, and go with us, and be to us a father and a priest: is it better for thee to be a priest unto the house of one man, or that thou be a priest unto a tribe and a family in Israel?

20 And the priest's heart was glad, and he took the ephod, and the teraphim, and the graven image, and went in the midst of the people.

21 So they turned and departed, and put the little ones and the cattle and the carriage before them.

The Danites send an "expeditionary force" of 600 men to take the city of Laish in northern Canaan. They move north and camp ["behind Kirjath-jearim"]{.class-0} (i.e., on the side of the city opposite to the main gate); the name ["Mahaneh-dan"]{.class-0} means "camp of Dan." From there they go to Mount Ephraim where Micah's house was.

There, the five spies tell the others about Micah's ["house of gods."]{.class-0} They say, ["now therefore consider what ye have to do"]{.class-0} (vs. 14). Good advice, but it depends on the basis of the consideration. If they had considered what to do [based on what God said in His written words,]{.class-1} they would beware ["a jealous God"]{.class-0} who forbad idols (Deut. 6:12--15); they would have taken heed not to be deceived by false gods (Deut. 11:6). What they were [commanded]{.class-1} to do in such cases was to [stone]{.class-1} the idolater, whether it was a friend (Deut. 13:6--10) or merely a false prophet (Deut. 18:20). This Levite was [both.]{.class-1}

But the Danites didn't consider [what God said]{.class-1} on the matter; their consideration was based on [superstitious expediency.]{.class-1} They went and stole all of Micah's images and his ephod because they wanted "God's" blessing on their endeavor, and they figured "God" was the graven image, the molten image, the teraphim, and could be consulted through the ephod. They didn't ["consider"]{.class-0} the fact that the real God was in Heaven and that the images were only ["the work of men's hands"]{.class-0} (Psa. 115:3--4).

["They have mouths, but they speak not: eyes have they, but they see not: They have ears, but hear not: noses have they, but they smell not: They have hands, but they handle not: feet have they, but they walk not: neither speak they through their throat. THEY THAT MAKE THEM ARE LIKE UNTO THEM; SO IS EVERY ONE THAT TRUSTETH IN THEM"]{.class-0} (Psa. 115:5--8).

Micah and those Danites were just as deaf, dumb, senseless, and [stupid]{.class-1} as the idols they "venerated." Ditto all Catholics who bow before and pray to a life-size dolly of Mary or Jesus.

Now the "priest" makes a token resistance (he stood in the gate \[vs. 17\] and asked, ["What do ye?"]{.class-0} \[vs. 18\]), but when faced with 600 armed men, he "caves" pretty quickly. The appeal made to the Levite was: "Look, bud, shut up and listen a minute. If you come with us, you will have a bigger congregation. You can expand your ministry and 'reach' more people. Think of all the good you can do." That is the same appeal that was made to Billy Graham, Joel Osteen, and Rick Warren to compromise their message. You water down the Gospel and don't preach the whole ["counsel of God"]{.class-0} (Acts 20:1--7) in order to draw more people in to hear you.

["Be to us a father and a priest"]{.class-0} (vs. 19). That's a religious leader being called a "Father." That's exactly what your Saviour told you [not]{.class-1} to do.

["And call no man your father upon the earth: for one is your Father, which is in heaven"]{.class-0} (Matt. 23:9).

The standard Catholic response to this is: "Well, you call your earthly father, father." To which you can tell the Catholic: "Nuts!" Down South we call him "daddy," not father. But be that as it may, the verse isn't talking about a biological or familial father. It's talking about false religious teachers who walk around ["in long robes"]{.class-0} (Luke 20:46), devouring widows' houses by charging them for "high Masses" to get their dead husbands out of Purgatory (Matt. 23:14), elevating tradition to an equal authority with the Scriptures so they can be the final authority when the two conflict (Mark 7:7--13), and damning their converts to Hell by proselytizing them to a religious system instead of winning them to Christ (Matt. 23:15). The head of such a religious organization will usurp a title reserved for God the Father (["Holy Father"]{.class-0}---John 17:11) just as quick as look at you. You never met a bunch of bigger blasphemers in your life, not even Mohammed and the Moslems.

These rascals are no more "fathers" than Obama is a [laissez-faire]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-28}capitalist; that is, unless they have a bunch of illegitimate children running around. I am more of a father than they are. I have ten children and several grandchildren; you can call me "father Ruckman" in complete legitimacy.

I don't call these birds "Father" anymore. If I have to use the title when I'm writing, I put it in quotations so my readers will know I am speaking "tongue in cheek." If I am talking to one of them, I will call him "mister" or "bud" or "buster." I show little to no respect to them because if I had listened to them, I would be in Hell right now. Why show respect to a man who would have put me in Hell if he could have gotten away with it?

In the New Testament, a [spiritual]{.class-1} father is someone who leads a sinner to Christ (1 Cor. 4:14--15). A Catholic Priest's idea of leading someone to Christ is giving him liquor and a cookie and pretending they're the blood and body of Christ. According to Jesus Christ, that doesn't do the recipient a bit of good (John 6:63). No Catholic Priest, Bishop, Cardinal, or Pope is a "father" in any legitimate sense of the word.

22 And when they were a good way from the house of Micah, the men that were in the houses near to Micah's house were gathered together, and overtook the children of Dan.

23 And they cried unto the children of Dan. And they turned their faces, and said unto Micah, What aileth thee, that thou comest with such a company?

24 And he said, Ye have taken away my gods which I made, and the priest, and ye are gone away: and what have I more? and what is this that ye say unto me, What aileth thee?

25 And the children of Dan said unto him, Let not thy voice be heard among us, lest angry fellows run upon thee, and thou lose thy life, with the lives of thy household.

26 And the children of Dan went their way: and when Micah saw that they were too strong for him, he turned and went back unto his house.

Micah's idolatry has infected his whole community, and his "church" goes to get their "relics" back. Micah is at the head of the "posse."

["Ye have taken away my gods which I made"]{.class-0} (vs. 24). Isn't that a remarkable confession? How could you make a god? How could that be possible? Wouldn't that make [you]{.class-1} God if you made him? After all, anything you make is [inferior]{.class-1} to you.

People are weird, did you know that? They don't reason through things. There's a whole dissertation on this in Isaiah 44. A fellow goes out into the forest and cuts him down a tree. He takes part of the wood and builds a fire to cook himself a meal so he can fill his belly, and with the rest of the wood he carves out an idol and prays to it for deliverance. How is something you can [burn]{.class-1} going to be able to deliver you?

People are strange, did you know that? They will make an idol out of some other person. The news media sets up gods, like Martin Luther King Jr., JFK, Abraham Lincoln, Madonna, Mother Teresa, Hillary Clinton, Obama, et al. Christians are no different; they elevate some "Christian celebrities" to one step just below the Holy Ghost.

They think they have more sense than the Holy Spirit who recorded the words, preserved the words the way He wanted them, guided men in translating those words, and blessed those words for 400 years. Worm food, man! ["For dust thou art, and unto dust shalt thou return"]{.class-0} (Gen. 3:19). You can't make a god out of something you can suck up in a vacuum cleaner.

Micah has lost his gods, his ephod, and his priest. ["What have I more?"]{.class-0} (vs. 24). Nothing, man; you've lost it all. I call that "Micah religion." Do you know what "Micah religion" is? You can't steal my "religion" from me. You say, "I'll burn your Bible." That won't do any good; I've got it hid in my heart (Psa. 119:11). You couldn't separate me from my Saviour if you tried (Rom. 8:38--39; Eph. 5:30; John 10:27--29). You say, "I'll kill your priest." Good luck on that. He was killed nearly 2,000 years ago and arose from the dead. You'd have to get up to the third heaven to get to Him now, because He's at His Father's right hand making intercession for me as my High Priest (Rom. 8:34; Heb. 7:25, 3:1).

Back to Judges 18. The Danites tell Micah and his entourage to run along before he gets himself and his people killed (vs. 25), and Micah turns back empty-handed because he is no match for 600 armed men with swords, spears, and daggers. 27 And they took the things which Micah had made, and the priest which he had, and came unto Laish, unto a people that were at quiet and secure: and they smote them with the edge of the sword, and burnt the city with fire.

28 And there was no deliverer, because it was far from Zidon, and they had no business with any man; and it was in the valley that lieth by Bethrehob. And they built a city, and dwelt therein.

29 And they called the name of the city Dan, after the name of Dan their father, who was born unto Israel: howbeit the name of the city was Laish at the first.

30 And the children of Dan set up the graven image: and Jonathan, the son of Gershom, the son of Manasseh, he and his sons were priests to the tribe of Dan until the day of the captivity of the land.

31 And they set them up Micah's graven image, which he made, all the time that the house of God was in Shiloh.

Now Dan has Micah's idols and priest, so the presumption is they have God's blessing. If they had had God's blessing, they could have driven out the Philistines from their southern inheritance. What Dan is doing here in taking new territory was not wrong in and of itself, but they are not operating with God's blessing. They are going up to a city that is not prepared for war and can get no help  from their own people, the Zidonians. The whole thing is [humanistic.]{.class-1} What you see today in American Christianity are churches operating under humanistic methods and claiming to be enjoying God's blessings on their ministries when it is nothing but successful marketing and promotional techniques. God gets blamed for a lot of things He doesn't do.

Dan takes the city. It is called ["Laish"]{.class-0} here in verse 29 and ["Leshem"]{.class-0} in Joshua 19:47. The name is changed to ["Dan"]{.class-0} after the tribal patriarch. There is nothing unusual for a city to have more than one name. Chicago is called "Chi" and "the Windy City." New York City started out as New Amsterdam, and Constantinople started out as Byzantium and became Istanbul when the Moslems took it over.

In taking the city, Dan violates the Scriptures [again.]{.class-1} When the Israelites went to war against a city that was not part of their inheritance as prescribed in Joshua, they were first to offer a peaceful surrender to the inhabitants and make them tributaries if it was accepted (Deut. 20:10--11). The Danites didn't make the offer. They just went in there and killed everyone and burned the city to the ground.

The city of Dan becomes the northernmost city of Israel. The expression "from Dan to Beersheba" (see Judg. 20:1; 1 Sam. 3:20; 2 Sam. 3:10, 17:11, 24:2, 7, 15; 1 Kings 4:25) means the northern and southern extremities of Israel. Dan was the farthest city in the north; Beersheba was the southernmost city.

Now in verse 30, the text of the [AV]{.class-1} is called into question by the scholars, Jewish and Christian. [Some]{.class-1} Hebrew manuscripts ([not all]{.class-1}) have an elevated [nun]{.class-1} in the name Manasseh. According to all the "recognized" scholars (recognized by each other for correcting the God-honored text of 1611), this was done by Hebrew transcriptionists so that the Hebrew radicals would not identify [Moses]{.class-1} as the father of Gershom, and his descendant as the one who led a whole tribe of Israel into idolatry. The commentators say that the fact that the grandson of Moses did this was sad proof "of the degeneracy of the great Lawgiver's family." In other words, they corrected your [King James]{.class-1} Bible to bring it in line with [their own opinion.]{.class-1}

What are the [facts,]{.class-1} not some scholar's conjecture, on the word ["Manasseh"]{.class-0}? The [fact]{.class-1} is that [no]{.class-1} Hebrew manuscript, whether the [nun]{.class-1} is raised or not, reads "Moses"; they [all]{.class-1} read with the [King James.]{.class-1} The [fact]{.class-1} is that it was the [Talmudists]{.class-1} and [Josephus,]{.class-1} not the writers of Scripture, who put forth the theory that the word was changed from[ Moses]{.class-1} to [Manasseh.]{.class-1} The [fact]{.class-1} is that the "few manuscripts" that read ["Moses"]{.class-1} are the [Septuagint]{.class-1} (written in A.D. 200), the [Vulgate]{.class-1} (translated in A.D. 382), and the Syriac manuscripts that followed Origen's [Hexapla,]{.class-1} from which we get the [Septuagint]{.class-1} (see our work on [The Mythological Septuagint]{.class-1}).

But we didn't need manuscript evidence to tell us that the scholars were full of beans on this point. We have the infallible text of the Holy Scriptures. Just because ["Jonathan"]{.class-0} was ["the son of Gershom"]{.class-0} doesn't mean this Gershom was the son of Moses (Exod. 2:22, 18:3). We have already run into a Gilead back in 11:1--2 who could not have possibly been the grandson of the patriarch Manasseh (Num. 26:29). There is nothing unusual about being named after a famous, historical figure. Gershom the son of Moses was named after another Gershom himself (1 Chron. 6:16 cf. Gen. 46:11).

Second, ["the son of Gershom, the son of Moses"]{.class-0} is clearly named in 1 Chronicles 26:24, and he is [not]{.class-1} Jonathan. He is ["Shebuel,"]{.class-0} and he was over the treasures in the Temple. He wasn't within 400 years of Judges 18. When the sons of Gershom (the son of Levi) are given in 1 Chronicles 6:16--21, no ["Jonathan"]{.class-0} appears in that genealogy either.

Now there are two possibilities for the identity of ["Jonathan,"]{.class-0} and in neither case is ["Gershom"]{.class-0} the direct son of either Levi or Moses. This is a completely different Gershom. If Jonathan is the Levite of Judges 18, then he has a Levitical father named Gershom and a Levitical grandfather named Manasseh. The latter would be a completely different Manasseh from the tribal patriarch. No genealogy of any of these characters would be found in 1 Chronicles because the family did not serve in the Tabernacle or the Temple.

The second possibility, and the one I find more likely, is that Jonathan was [not]{.class-1} the Levite of Judges 18 at all. The Danites could have booted the Levite once they got what they wanted and gotten a priest from the tribe of Manasseh.

Manasseh could indeed be the tribal patriarch, making the priesthood of Jonathan's family like that of Jeroboam's priests in 1 Kings 12. After all, one of Jeroboam's golden calves, the one to which all the people of the northern kingdom went to worship, was at Dan (1 Kings 12:29--30), and none of Jeroboam's priests were Levites (1 Kings 12:31).

Scripture with Scripture, folks. Just believe the text as it stands. There was no need to change the text at all, much less based on two extra-biblical, apostate sources (the [Talmud]{.class-1} and Josephus). When in doubt, throw ALL the scholars OUT! Throw them out no matter how "good," "godly," or "recognized" they are.

["He and his sons were priests to the tribe of Dan until the day of the captivity of the land" ]{.class-0}(vs. 30). Well, ["the captivity of the land"]{.class-0} takes place nearly 700 years later in 2 Kings 17. So verse 30 is either a prophecy given by the author of Judges (possibly Samuel), or it is an historical observation added later on by someone like Ezra.

Dan was in total apostasy for 700 years. For 400 of those years (at least), they served Micah's idol. Verse 31 says, ["all the time that the house of God was in Shiloh."]{.class-0} The Tabernacle was in Shiloh until David moved it to Jerusalem around the time of Solomon (1000 B.C.). If they got rid of that idol when the Temple was built, they still didn't come down to Jerusalem to worship because they had a false priesthood serving them. And it wasn't too long after that when Jeroboam set up his golden calf at Dan, and they simply switched from one idol to another.

The tribe of Dan became inextricably connected with idol worship. It moved as close to the center of Baal and Ashtaroth worship as it could. In prophecy, the tribe is associated with the Antichrist and his image (Gen. 49:16--17; Deut. 33:22). In the Great Tribulation, the tribe, along with the tribe of Ephraim which God also dumps because of its idolatry (Hos. 4:17), is omitted from the list of tribes sealed by God. When God pours out His wrath on the earth, Dan is unprotected, and it is because of its idolatry.

Chapter 19

19:1 And it came to pass in those days, when there was no king in Israel, that there was a certain Levite sojourning on the side of mount Ephraim, who took to him a concubine out of Bethlehemjudah.

2 And his concubine played the whore against him, and went away from him unto her father's house to Bethlehemjudah, and was there four whole months.

3 And her husband arose, and went after her, to speak friendly unto her, and to bring her again, having his servant with him, and a couple of asses: and she brought him into her father's house: and when the father of the damsel saw him, he rejoiced to meet him.

Now you have just gotten through reading about a Levite from Bethlehem in Judah who goes to Mount Ephraim and becomes a false priest for an idolater there. In both chapters 17 and 18, you are told: ["In those days there was no king in Israel"]{.class-0} (17:6, 18:1). This chapter starts out the same way. Everyone was doing what he thought was right with no regard to the written word of God at all.

That Book says, ["There is none righteous, no, not one"]{.class-0} (Rom. 3:10). Without the words of God in Scripture, the only thing you have to guide you is a conscience defiled and seared by sin (Tit. 1:15; 1 Tim. 4:2). Without the Scriptures, the only authority you have for right or wrong is [your opinion]{.class-1} or [someone else's opinion.]{.class-1}

Here in Judges 19, you have another story about a Levite connected with Mount Ephraim and Bethlehem-judah. This one lives ["on the side of mount Ephraim"]{.class-0} and goes down to Bethlehem-judah to get him a concubine.

In ancient societies, a concubine was a "secondary" wife. In the Bible, a concubine was called a ["wife,"]{.class-0} as in the case of Keturah (Gen. 25:1 cf. 1 Chron. 1:32) and David's concubines (2 Sam. 16:21--22 cf. 2 Sam. 12:11). But a concubine didn't have the same status or privileges as a full wife; she was a "second-class" wife. If you Christian ladies ever feel about complaining of your lot in life, you had better be glad you are under grace in the New Testament.

Now this Levite's concubine goes and "plays the whore"; in other words, she goes and commits adultery, probably for remuneration (see Hos. 2:5; Ezek. 16:33). She runs away from her husband back home to daddy, and for good reason: [under the Law, she was to be put to death.]{.class-1}

["They]{.class-0} \[i.e., the Levitical priests---Lev. 21:1\][ shall not take a wife that is a whore, or profane . . . And the daughter of any priest, if she profane herself by playing the whore . . . she shall be burnt with fire"]{.class-0} (Lev. 21:7, 9).

But this Levite isn't going by the ["book of the law"]{.class-0} (Josh. 1:8). He's going by that ["which was right in his own eyes"]{.class-0} (17:6). He goes to his father-in-law's house ["to speak friendly unto her"]{.class-0} and bring her back home (vs. 3). But this woman does indeed end up dying (vss. 26--28), just as the Law said should happen.

Now Israel, as a nation, ends up in the same situation as this concubine. She plays the spiritual harlot (Hos. 2:5). God ends up speaking ["comfortably unto her"]{.class-0} (Hos. 2:14); but not before 500 Jews were crucified outside of Jerusalem and the city was destroyed by the Romans, not before the Romans threw them out of Palestine, not before they were expelled from Gaul in A.D. 62. In the Middle Ages, Roman Catholics forced the Jews to wear yellow clothing to identify them and mark them out for persecution nearly a thousand years before Hitler made them wear yellow stars. They were forced into ghettos by the Catholic Church. Six thousand of them were slain by Moslems in Morocco in 1032, 4,000 were killed in Granada by the Moslems in 1066, 5,000 of them were murdered by the Roman Catholics in Germany in 1096, 500 were killed in France in 1190 by Roman Catholic Crusaders, 3,000 more were killed in France by Crusaders in 1236, and 100,000 were massacred in Austria in 1298. They were expelled from France in 1254, from England in 1290, from France again in 1305 and 1322, from Spain in 1492, from Sicily in 1493, and from Portugal in 1496. The Inquisition went after them; the Russians instituted pogroms against them; Hitler gassed six million of them.

Do you get the picture? The nation suffers for "playing the whore" by being persecuted, humiliated, expelled, and slaughtered. A holocaust is coming up in the future that will make Hitler's look like a Sunday School picnic. Only after that will God ["speak comfortably unto her"]{.class-0} and take the nation back.

In order to destroy the connection to Israel's infidelity to her husband, Adam Clarke goes to the Roman Catholic [Vulgate,]{.class-1} the [Septuagint]{.class-1} (translated a hundred years after the close of the New Testament), the [Targum]{.class-1} ([paraphrases]{.class-1} and [interpretations]{.class-1} by Christ-rejecting Rabbis), and Josephus (an apostate Jew who defected to Rome) to prove the concubine didn't step out on her husband; she was just "upset" with him. The problem is, the Hebrew word for ["played the whore"]{.class-0} ([zanah]{.class-1}) is the same word used of Tamar in Genesis 38:24 when she was caught ["with child by whoredom"]{.class-0}; it means ["to commit adultery."]{.class-1} She wasn't "angry" with her husband or despising him or merely "alienated" from him; she joined her body to another man as a harlot would (see 1 Cor. 6:15--18).

Now the Levite's concubine brings her husband into her father's house, and the father-in-law is glad to see his son-in-law. Undoubtedly the reason is that his son-in-law is not there to kill his wife, the father-in-law's daughter.

4 And his father in law, the damsel's father, retained him; and he abode with him three days: so they did eat and drink, and lodged there.

5 And it came to pass on the fourth day, when they arose early in the morning, that he rose up to depart: and the damsel's father said unto his son in law, Comfort thine heart with a morsel of bread, and afterward go your way.

6 And they sat down, and did eat and drink both of them together: for the damsel's father had said unto the man, Be content, I pray thee, and tarry all night, and let thine heart be merry.

7 And when the man rose up to depart, his father in law urged him: therefore he lodged there again.

8 And he arose early in the morning on the fifth day to depart: and the damsel's father said, Comfort thine heart, I pray thee. And they tarried until afternoon, and they did eat both of them.

9 And when the man rose up to depart, he, and his concubine, and his servant, his father in law, the damsel's father, said unto him, Behold, now the day draweth toward evening, I pray you tarry all night: behold, the day groweth to an end, lodge here, that thine heart may be merry; and to morrow get you early on your way, that thou mayest go home.

10 But the man would not tarry that night, but he rose up and departed, and came over against Jebus, which is Jerusalem; and there were with him two asses saddled, his concubine also was with him.

The concubine's father "retains" his son-in-law for three days: he's holding him there for three days with hospitality. When the Levite gets ready to leave the fourth day, his father-in-law urges him to stay for dinner and then for supper. He starts out the fifth day the same way, and we may infer that if the Levite hadn't insisted on traveling that afternoon that the woman's father would have put them up another night. One is reminded of Samson's seven-day wedding feast back in chapter 14. It is as if the father-in-law is trying to give the couple a "second honeymoon" to guarantee that everything has been "patched up."

There is not much here applicable to the New Testament child of God, except, perhaps, the practical lesson to be hospitable to the saints (Rom. 12:13; 1 Tim. 3:2; Tit. 1:8; 1 Pet. 4:9). If the goal of the father-in-law was to guarantee the reconciliation of his daughter and the Levite, then the practical lesson for the New Testament believer would be the restoration of an erring brother or sister (Gal. 6:1). Certainly the reconciliation of a sinner to the Father is great cause for "making merry" (vs. 6 cf. Luke 15:23--24, 32).

Notice the original name of Jerusalem in verse 10 (cf. Josh. 18:28). Although Judah had taken Jerusalem (1:8), neither they nor the Benjamites with whom they shared the city were able to drive out the Jebusites who inhabited it previously (Josh. 15:63, 18:28). Again, the incomplete obedience of the children of Israel brought disastrous results, as we are about to see.

11 And when they were by Jebus, the day was far spent; and the servant said unto his master, Come, I pray thee, and let us turn in into this city of the Jebusites, and lodge in it.

12 And his master said unto him, We will not turn aside hither into the city of a stranger, that is not of the children of Israel; we will pass over to Gibeah.

13 And he said unto his servant, Come, and let us draw near to one of these places to lodge all night, in Gibeah, or in Ramah.

14 And they passed on and went their way; and the sun went down upon them when they were by Gibeah, which belongeth to Benjamin.

The Levite, along with his servant and concubine, have been traveling from Bethlehem all afternoon, and they have come to Jerusalem as the evening is coming on. The servant urges his master to turn in to Jerusalem to find lodging for the night, but the Levite won't because the place is ["the city of the Jebusites"]{.class-0} (vs. 11). In other words, although there were men from the tribes of Judah and Benjamin in the city, it was still characterized by the [Jebusites]{.class-1} living there.

The Jebusites were descendants of [Ham]{.class-1} (Gen. 10:6, 15), and were one of seven nations God told the nation of Israel to utterly destroy when they came into the land of Canaan (Deut. 7:1; Josh. 3:10). Why? It was not just for their idolatry (Deut. 12:2--3). Those Hamites there in Canaan practiced all sorts of heinous sexual perversions (Lev. 18), one for which God burned Sodom and Gomorrah to the ground (Lev. 18:22 cf. Gen. 13:13, 19:5; Deut. 23:17). (By the way, the original Sodomites were [Hamites]{.class-1} just like the Jebusites \[Gen. 10:19\].) The Bible says the land of Canaan was defiled by the sexual perversions of those Hamites and that the land vomited out its inhabitants because of those perversions (Lev. 18:25). The Jews were to commit genocide on those Hamitic nations like the Jebusites because if they didn't, they would pick up and practice the sexual sins of those heathen until the land spewed them out like it spewed out the Hamites (Lev. 18:26--28). That is what is happening in America right now, and that is what happens here in Judges 19.

The Levite won't lodge with the Jebusites overnight because of their vile practices. What he doesn't know is that the Benjamites in Gibeah who lived near those Jebusites had picked up every filthy habit and "lifestyle" going on in ["Jebus."]{.class-0} Those Jebusites were practicing the sin of Sodom, and the Jews had picked it up.

15 And they turned aside thither, to go in and to lodge in Gibeah: and when he went in, he sat him down in a street of the city: for there was no man that took them into his house to lodging.

16 And, behold, there came an old man from his work out of the field at even, which was also of mount Ephraim; and he sojourned in Gibeah: but the men of the place were Benjamites.

17 And when he had lifted up his eyes, he saw a wayfaring man in the street of the city: and the old man said, Whither goest thou? and whence comest thou?

18 And he said unto him, We are passing from Bethlehemjudah toward the side of mount Ephraim; from thence am I: and I went to Bethlehemjudah, but I am now going to the house of the LORD; and there is no man that receiveth me to house.

19 Yet there is both straw and provender for our asses; and there is bread and wine also for me, and for thy handmaid, and for the young man which is with thy servants: there is no want of any thing.

20 And the old man said, Peace be with thee; howsoever let all thy wants lie upon me; only lodge not in the street.

21 So he brought him into his house, and gave provender unto the asses: and they washed their feet, and did eat and drink.

Do you realize what you are reading here in this passage and in the next (vss. 22--25)? You are reading Genesis 19; you are reading about Lot and the Sodomites.

The Levite, his servant, and his concubine can't find an inn there in Gibeah, so they camp out in the street. They have food for themselves and their beasts, and the weather is agreeable. They figure they have nothing to fear in a city controlled by other Israelites.

But as an old man comes in from a hard day's work in the fields, he sees the three travelers and insists they spend the night in his house. While it is a matter of Oriental hospitality, there is more going on with the old man than that. He lived there long enough to know what was going on in Gibeah. I imagine he hoped he had gotten his visitors off the street in time, before the fruity, Frisco faggots emerged from their trailers like they do in Key West when the sun goes down. Those queers down there look as pale as Dracula because they wait until nightfall to come out so they can practice their sin in the dark (John 3:19).

The old man ushers the three travelers into his house as quickly as he can and goes about caring for their needs and the needs of their beasts. The whole time he listens nervously for the "gay pride parade" that was sure to be gathering in the street if any of the sex perverts had seen the Levite and his manservant enter his house.

22 Now as they were making their hearts merry, behold, the men of the city, certain sons of Belial, beset the house round about, and beat at the door, and spake to the master of the house, the old man, saying, Bring forth the man that came into thine house, that we may know him.

23 And the man, the master of the house, went out unto them, and said unto them, Nay, my brethren, nay, I pray you, do not so wickedly; seeing that this man is come into mine house, do not this folly.

24 Behold, here is my daughter a maiden, and his concubine; them I will bring out now, and humble ye them, and do with them what seemeth good unto you: but unto this man do not so vile a thing.

25 But the men would not hearken to him: so the man took his concubine, and brought her forth unto them; and they knew her, and abused her all the night until the morning: and when the day began to spring, they let her go.

26 Then came the woman in the dawning of the day, and fell down at the door of the man's house where her lord was, till it was light.

27 And her lord rose up in the morning, and opened the doors of the house, and went out to go his way: and, behold, the woman his concubine was fallen down at the door of the house, and her hands were upon the threshold.

28 And he said unto her, Up, and let us be going. But none answered. Then the man took her up upon an ass, and the man rose up, and gat him unto his place.

After having been abused sexually all night long, the woman can only drag herself to the door of the house, where she collapses and dies. There is no doubt of the callousness of this apostate priest. ["None answered"]{.class-0} because she was [dead.]{.class-1} The man showed no grief or remorse for turning her over to the mob. He picked her up like a sack of potatoes and flopped her over the back of her beast and headed home.

Of course, what you are reading here is one of those "exceptions to the rule." The fact is, [no one]{.class-1} in this account (with the possible exception of the father-in-law) was in the right. Chapter 20

20:1 Then all the children of Israel went out, and the congregation was gathered together as one man, from Dan even to Beersheba, with the land of Gilead, unto the LORD in Mizpeh.

2 And the chief of all the people, even of all the tribes of Israel, presented themselves in the assembly of the people of God, four hundred thousand footmen that drew sword.

3 (Now the children of Benjamin heard that the children of Israel were gone up to Mizpeh.) Then said the children of Israel, Tell us, how was this wickedness?

4 And the Levite, the husband of the woman that was slain, answered and said, I came into Gibeah that belongeth to Benjamin, I and my concubine, to lodge.

5 And the men of Gibeah rose against me, and beset the house round about upon me by night, and thought to have slain me: and my concubine have they forced, that she is dead.

6 And I took my concubine, and cut her in pieces, and sent her throughout all the country of the inheritance of Israel: for they have committed lewdness and folly in Israel.

The act of the Levite was so horrific that the whole nation gathers together, from the northernmost city (["Dan"]{.class-0}) to the southernmost city (["Beersheba"]{.class-0}), and all the tribes on the east side of Jordan (["the land of Gilead"]{.class-0}). Notice in verse 1 that Gilead is not just the inheritance of the half tribe of Manasseh on the east of Jordan; here it is a reference to all the eastern tribes, just as Ephraim can refer to the ten northern tribes as well as the individual tribe (Hos. 5:3, 5, 9).

There were several places known as ["Mizpeh"]{.class-0} in the Bible. It is the place in Gilead where Laban and Jacob agreed not to cross over to do one another harm (Gen. 31:44--52); that is where Jephthah lived after being made the head of all Gilead (Judg. 11:11, 34). There was another Mizpeh in the extreme north of Gilead near the base of Mt. Hermon. There is a Mizpeh in Moab (1 Sam. 22:3). The Mizpeh here was a town in Benjamin (Josh. 18:26--28). It became a meeting place for the children of Israel during times of crisis (Judg. 20; 1 Sam. 7, 10). It was part of Samuel's circuit as judge (1 Sam. 7:16).

The whole congregation of Israel gathers together for [war]{.class-1} (vs. 2---["four hundred thousand footmen that drew sword"]{.class-0}). They are ready to "wipe out" the ones responsible for what happened to the concubine. But when all the tribes were assembled, one tribe was missing---Benjamin, the tribe of the sodomites. It was Benjamin's own city, and they refused to come to the general assembly.

Notice the intent of the sodomites in verse 5. It wasn't just rape. They knew that anyone they abused the way they did the concubine would [die]{.class-1} (["thought to have slain me"]{.class-0}). It may have even happened before, with the bodies being disposed of with no one the wiser. Elmer Wayne Henley and Dean Corll were two queers in Houston, Texas, who would lure teenage boys to Corll's home. The boys were then drugged, tied to a board, and tortured and raped over a period of days. They were finally shot to death, and Corll buried their bodies on the beach. He got 28 teenage boys like that before Henley shot him and turned himself in to the police. That's your "gays" for you.

7 Behold, ye are all children of Israel; give here your advice and counsel.

8 And all the people arose as one man, saying, We will not any of us go to his tent, neither will we any of us turn into his house.

9 But now this shall be the thing which we will do to Gibeah; we will go up by lot against it;

10 And we will take ten men of an hundred throughout all the tribes of Israel, and an hundred of a thousand, and a thousand out of ten thousand, to fetch victual for the people, that they may do, when they come to Gibeah of Benjamin, according to all the folly that they have wrought in Israel.

11 So all the men of Israel were gathered against the city, knit together as one man.

["Ye are all children of Israel; give here YOUR advice and counsel"]{.class-0} (vs. 7); ["And all THE PEOPLE arose as one man, saying . . ."]{.class-0} (vs. 8); ["So all the MEN OF ISRAEL were gathered together against the city, knit together as one man"]{.class-0} (vs. 11). Perfect consensus; perfect unity. "United we stand; divided we fall." All of them united against evil. The only problem is [they didn't consult God.]{.class-1}

["Say ye not, A confederacy, to all them to whom this people shall say, A confederacy; neither fear ye their fear, nor be afraid. Sanctify the LORD of hosts himself; and let him be your fear, and let him be your dread"]{.class-0} (Isa. 8:12--13).

It doesn't matter how much "strength in numbers," you have; without the Lord, you will lose your shirt. Here the children of Israel are going up with 400,000 men against one tribe with only 26,700 men: those are odds of fifteen to one. But one tribe is going to whip the combined might of the other eleven tribes.

In preparation to take Gibeah, a tenth of the fighting force is chosen to go ["fetch victual for the people"]{.class-0} (vs. 9). ["Victual"]{.class-0} means "prepared food" ("C" rations, "K" rations, "MREs"; that sort of thing). The old saying is: "An army travels on its stomach." You will usually hear the word [victuals]{.class-1} pronounced "vittles," although how you get vittles out of V-I-C-T-U-A-L-S, I have no idea.

The Israelites are preparing to go to war against the city of Gibeah and to besiege it if necessary. That is why they are creating a "quartermaster corps" to go get supplies for the army.

12 And the tribes of Israel sent men through all the tribe of Benjamin, saying, What wickedness is this that is done among you?

13 Now therefore deliver us the men, the children of Belial, which are in Gibeah, that we may put them to death, and put away evil from Israel. But the children of Benjamin would not hearken to the voice of their brethren the children of Israel:

14 But the children of Benjamin gathered themselves together out of the cities unto Gibeah, to go out to battle against the children of Israel.

15 And the children of Benjamin were numbered at that time out of the cities twenty and six thousand men that drew sword, beside the inhabitants of Gibeah, which were numbered seven hundred chosen men.

16 Among all this people there were seven hundred chosen men lefthanded; every one could sling stones at an hair breadth, and not miss.

17 And the men of Israel, beside Benjamin, were numbered four hundred thousand men that drew sword: all these were men of war.

Following Deuteronomy 13:12--14, the eleven tribes make diligent inquiry of Benjamin about ["the children of Belial . . . in Gibeah"]{.class-0} (vss. 12--13). They are willing to spare the city as a whole if the sodomites are turned over for execution for their crime. That is a reasonable request, but look at Benjamin's reaction: ["But the children of Benjamin would not hearken to the voice of their brethren"]{.class-0} (vs. 13).

Benjamin is ready to go to war with the other eleven tribes to [defend their right to practice sodomy.]{.class-1} Men will die for the right to sin, did you know that? The sodomites in America will march thousands at a time in "gay pride parades" for their "right" to sex perversion. They will get judges to overturn the majority vote of a State for the "right" for two faggots or two dykes to "marry." They will [die]{.class-1} for those "rights"; they will [kill]{.class-1} for those "rights." How do you know? [Judges 20.]{.class-1} If you have a Bible, you will always be ahead of such amateur groups as the American Psychiatric Association.

["The children of Benjamin gathered themselves together out of the cities unto Gibeah, to go out to battle against the children of Israel"]{.class-0} (vs. 14). The Benjamites are not going to let Gibeah be besieged; they are going on the offensive.

We have already commented briefly on the left-handedness of the Benjamites (vs. 16) under 3:15, which see. That is ironic, considering that the name [Benjamin]{.class-1} means "son of my right hand."

In baseball and boxing, a "leftie" is called a south-PAW. Why "paw"? Because the Antichrist is likened to a leopard (Rev. 13:2), and leopards have paws; and as it turns out, the Antichrist will be [left-handed.]{.class-1}

["Woe to the IDOL shepherd]{.class-0} \[a reference to the Antichrist and his image; thus, it has been changed in all the modern translations to cover up for Satan---see Isa. 14:12 in an [NIV]{.class-1}\] [that leaveth the flock! the sword shall be upon his arm, and upon his right eye; his arm shall be clean dried up, and his right eye shall be utterly darkened"]{.class-0} (Zech. 11:17).

The Antichrist has his arm and his eye injured on the right side of his body. Over in 1 Kings 13:4, Jeroboam, another type of the Antichrist, has his arm shriveled up. That thing is pictured by Moses putting his hand in his bosom and bringing it out leprous (Exod. 4:6). So you know what you see Napoleon do? He is always pictured with his hand in his coat. Kaiser Bill had a bad arm, as did Adolf Hitler. All those historical figures are types of the Antichrist. The Antichrist has trouble with one of his arms, and in the Bible it is his right arm. It is pictured by a tribe of left-handers associated with [sodomy]{.class-1}, just like the Antichrist (Dan. 11:37 cf. Rev. 11:8).

Now that doesn't mean that all left-handed people are "of the Devil." You read back in Judges 3 of a left-handed judge who was a picture of [Jesus Christ.]{.class-1} But the Bible is giving you prophecy about what the Antichrist will be like, and the Antichrist will be [a left-handed sodomite.]{.class-1}

Back to Judges 20: ["every one could sling stones at an hair breadth, and not miss"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). Of course you know from the story of David and Goliath how deadly a stone slung from a sling can be. This would not be a "slingshot," but a leather strap with a pouch in the middle. One end was fastened to the wrist and the other was held in the hand, with a stone or lead ball for "shot" in the pouch. The strap was then twirled above the head to gain velocity, and the one end released so the projectile flew towards its target. These 700 Benjamites could hit a target within a hair's breadth. If all you are off is the breadth of a strand of hair, you haven't missed your target; you've hit the bull's-eye "dead on."

A sling in the hand of a skilled user was a deadly weapon. In 2 Kings 3:25, one city was taken down by just slingers. Lead balls were slung with such velocity that the lead was softened in flight (Seneca, book 3, [Quaest-naturalle-57]{.class-1}). Those slings could be deadlier than a musket used in the Revolutionary and Civil Wars.

18 And the children of Israel arose, and went up to the house of God, and asked counsel of God, and said, Which of us shall go up first to the battle against the children of Benjamin? And the LORD said, Judah shall go up first.

19 And the children of Israel rose up in the morning, and encamped against Gibeah.

20 And the men of Israel went out to battle against Benjamin; and the men of Israel put themselves in array to fight against them at Gibeah.

21 And the children of Benjamin came forth out of Gibeah, and destroyed down to the ground of the Israelites that day twenty and two thousand men.

22 And the people the men of Israel encouraged themselves, and set their battle again in array in the place where they put themselves in array the first day.

23 (And the children of Israel went up and wept before the LORD until even, and asked counsel of the LORD, saying, Shall I go up again to battle against the children of Benjamin my brother? And the LORD said, Go up against him.)

24 And the children of Israel came near against the children of Benjamin the second day.

25 And Benjamin went forth against them out of Gibeah the second day, and destroyed down to the ground of the children of Israel again eighteen thousand men; all these drew the sword.

Finally the eleven tribes ["asked counsel of God"]{.class-0} (vs. 18). They prayed and asked God what to do, and He told them. It looks like they are in the will of God, doesn't it? But something is wrong because they are about to "get their hats handed to them"---TWICE!

What's the problem? [They are telling God what to do.]{.class-1} Did you notice that they didn't ask God [if they should go to battle.]{.class-1} They tell God, "We're going to fight against Benjamin. Now how should we go? Which of us first?" When you pray, don't pray like that. Don't make your own plans first and then ask God how to carry them out. Ask God [should]{.class-1} you go (or not go) first and then ask Him to show you why---[His]{.class-1} reason and purpose, not yours. [After that,]{.class-1} you can ask Him [when, where,]{.class-1} and [how;]{.class-1} but get what [He]{.class-1} wants you to do first. David told the prophet, "I'm going to build God a house"; and it wasn't God's will that David build the house at all (2 Sam. 7).

Now the Jews have determined what to do, and they have "prayed about it." God tells them to have Judah go up against Benjamin first. With that, they go out to battle the next day and suffer 22,000 casualties. "God wills it!" as the Catholics said during the Crusades.

There is a joke about a Charismatic who went to Las Vegas. He figured that he couldn't lose because "God was leading him" ("God told me . . . ; God showed me . . ."---that kind of stuff).

Well, you know what happened: he lost everything. As he was hitchhiking out of Las Vegas [because he was broke,]{.class-1} he prayed and said, "Lord, how could you let that happen? I thought you told me . . . ." About that time a voice came from Heaven and said, "Look in your pocket." The Charismatic felt in his pocket and brought up a twenty dollar bill he didn't realize he had left. "Go back and bet the whole thing on red 21 at the roulette wheel," said the voice.

So the Charismatic went back to Las Vegas, went to the nearest casino, and bet the whole twenty dollars on red 21. It came up black 13. As the Charismatic walked dejected down the highway out of the city, he cried, "Lord, I did what you told me to, [and I lost!"]{.class-1} And the Lord came back and said, "Well what do you know. How about that."

That is what happened here: those Jews lost 22,000 men in a day. Well how about that.

But "never say die": they didn't let that discourage them. ["The men of Israel encouraged themselves, and set their battle again in array"]{.class-0} (vs. 22). "If at first you don't succeed, try, try again"---that sort of thing.

But before they did that, they made a partial move in the right direction: ["the children of Israel went up and wept before the LORD until even"]{.class-0} (vs. 23). They are repenting. And this time, they ask the right question: ["Shall I go up again to battle against the children of Benjamin my brother?"]{.class-0} "Lord, do you want me to fight?" God says, "Sic 'em!" [And they lost their shirt again!]{.class-1} Eighteen thousand more die the second day. With the number that died the first day (22,000), they lost 40,000 men---a [tenth]{.class-1} of their force.

Now have you ever wondered why the Bible commanded those Jews to tithe (Mal. 3:8)? Abraham tithes to Melchizedek (Gen. 14:20). Jacob promises to give the tenth to the Lord (Gen. 28:22). Nehemiah takes one of every ten people who returned from captivity in Babylon to live in Jerusalem. Why this constant harping on the tenth, the "tithe"? The answer is found in Isaiah 6:13.

["But yet in it ]{.class-0}\[i.e., the Promised Land---Isa. 6:12\][ shall be A TENTH, and it shall return, and SHALL BE EATEN . . . so the holy seed shall be the substance thereof."]{.class-0}

During the Tribulation, a tenth of the Jews who return to the land of Israel are sacrificed by the Antichrist on the altar of the rebuilt temple (Rev. 6:9). Like the sacrifices prescribed in the Levitical Law (Lev. 6:16, 26, 7:6, 15--16, 10:17--18), they are [eaten]{.class-1} and their blood is offered as a "drink offering" (Psa. 16:4).

Now from a practical standpoint, God allows this slaughter for two reasons. As we shall see, Benjamin is being set up for a devastating defeat: by these victories, they are lured into a false confidence. But God is also clearing out the idolaters from the other eleven tribes. In other words, before sending in the heathen to judge His people, He uses His people to judge themselves. The New Testament application is found in 1 Peter 4:17.

"For the time is come that judgment must begin at the house of God: and if it first begin at us, what shall the end be of them that obey not the gospel of God?"

That's not the self-judgment of the believer on his own sins (1 Cor. 11:31); that's God "cleaning house" among His own people (1 Cor. 11:32).

Now Israel prays, and they pray the way God wants them to pray, and they still lose. What is the problem this time?

Brethren, the Devil is subtle. He won't just try to get you to do the wrong thing; sometimes he will try to get you to do the [right thing]{.class-1} at the [wrong time.]{.class-1} Not too many commentators or expositors realize that is what he did when he tempted Christ. Satan tempted Jesus to turn stones to bread because that is what He will do for Israel in the Tribulation (Mic. 7:14). The Devil tempted Christ to jump from the pinnacle of the Temple because when He comes back at the Second Advent, He comes to the temple (Mal. 3:1). Christ was offered ["all the kingdoms of the world"]{.class-0} at His temptation (Luke 4:5--6); [He gets them at the Second Advent]{.class-1} (Rev. 11:15). Every temptation was a temptation for Christ to do the right thing at the wrong time. You see how subtle that thing is?

Remember that in your Christian life. You are up against a powerful and subtle adversary (1 Pet. 5:8). He can get you praying when you should be witnessing or witnessing when you should be reading your Bible or reading your Bible when you should be studying your Greek or Hebrew (Bible school students) or studying for a test when you should be praying. The Devil's subtle, boy. He can even get you to do the [right thing]{.class-1} at the [right time]{.class-1} but in the [wrong way.]{.class-1} And that is what happens here to Israel. It isn't until verse 26 that the children of Israel go to the Tabernacle to inquire of God and offer sacrifices for their sins.

26 Then all the children of Israel, and all the people, went up, and came unto the house of God, and wept, and sat there before the LORD, and fasted that day until even, and offered burnt offerings and peace offerings before the LORD.

27 And the children of Israel enquired of the LORD, (for the ark of the covenant of God was there in those days,
