28 And Phinehas, the son of Eleazar, the son of Aaron, stood before it in those days,) saying, Shall I yet again go out to battle against the children of Benjamin my brother, or shall I cease? And the LORD said, Go up; for to morrow I will deliver them into thine hand.

And now everything is right. They approach God with[ the right question:]{.class-1} ["Shall I yet again go out to battle . . . OR SHALL I CEASE"]{.class-0} (vs. 28)---that last part wasn't there before. "Lord, I'll do whatever you want, even if it means stop doing what I want."

They approached Him [in repentance.]{.class-1} They approach Him at [the right place:]{.class-1}[ "the house of God"]{.class-0} (vs. 26) where ["the ark of God"]{.class-0} was (vs. 27). They approach Him through [the right person:]{.class-1} the high priest (vs. 28). They approach Him [with sacrifice]{.class-1} (vs. 26); it's not just "give me, give me, give me" this time. A Christian would do well to approach God with ["the sacrifice of praise . . . giving thanks to his name"]{.class-0} (Heb. 13:15) before he starts into the "Lord, I want this, and I need this, and would you do this, etc."

Having approached God in these ways, those Jews get the answer they needed all along. It was not just "Go get 'em"; it was :[ "Go up; for to morrow I WILL DELIVER THEM INTO THINE HAND"]{.class-0} (vs. 28). What they wanted the whole time was the promise of [victory,]{.class-1} and they stopped praying in the two previous instances before they got it. Now they are going to get results.

29 And Israel set liers in wait round about Gibeah.

30 And the children of Israel went up against the children of Benjamin on the third day, and put themselves in array against Gibeah, as at other times.

31 And the children of Benjamin went out against the people, and were drawn away from the city; and they began to smite of the people, and kill, as at other times, in the highways, of which one goeth up to the house of God, and the other to Gibeah in the field, about thirty men of Israel.

32 And the children of Benjamin said, They are smitten down before us, as at the first. But the children of Israel said, Let us flee, and draw them from the city unto the highways.

33 And all the men of Israel rose up out of their place, and put themselves in array at Baaltamar: and the liers in wait of Israel came forth out of their places, even out of the meadows of Gibeah.

34 And there came against Gibeah ten thousand chosen men out of all Israel, and the battle was sore: but they knew not that evil was near them.

35 And the LORD smote Benjamin before Israel: and the children of Israel destroyed of the Benjamites that day twenty and five thousand and an hundred men: all these drew the sword.

The Israelites take a page out of Joshua's playbook when he attacked Ai in Joshua 8. They set an ambushment against Gibeah and lured the Benjamites away from the city by feigning retreat.

Notice the name ["Baal-tamar"]{.class-0} in verse 33. The name means "lord of the palm trees." It was a grove of palm trees set up to Baal. The insinuation is that the idolatry of Benjamin was directly connected to the perversion they practiced (see our remarks under 2:11--13).

Ten thousand men are chosen out of the eleven tribes to draw the Benjamites away from Gibeah. The Benjamites go out against them, and though ["the battle was sore"]{.class-0} (vs. 34), it seemed to be going Benjamin's way: they managed to kill thirty Israelites (vs. 31). But look at the end of verse 34: ["but they knew not that evil was near them."]{.class-0} The Benjamites are about to be cut down from 26,700 men to only 600 men for the whole tribe (vs. 47). ["Twenty-five thousand and an hundred"]{.class-0} Benjamites were killed in one day (vs. 35).

That Bible says, ["For man also knoweth not his time: as the fishes that are taken in an evil net, and as the birds that are caught in the snare; so are the sons of men snared in an evil time, when it falleth suddenly upon them"]{.class-0} (Eccl. 9:12).

It says, ["Therefore shall evil come upon thee; thou shalt not know from whence it riseth: and mischief shall fall upon thee; thou shalt not be able to put it off: and desolation shall come upon thee suddenly, which thou shalt not know"]{.class-0} (Isa. 47:11).

It says, ["For when they shall say, Peace and safety; then sudden destruction cometh upon them, as travail upon a woman with child; and they shall not escape"]{.class-0} (1 Thess. 5:3).

You can be going along thinking everything is just fine and not realize that death is just around the corner to meet you. That rich man there in Luke 12 thought he had ["many years"]{.class-0} (Luke 12:19); [he didn't even have 24 hours]{.class-1} (Luke 12:20). You are told: ["Boast not thyself of to morrow; for thou knowest not what a day may bring forth"]{.class-0} (Prov. 27:1).

Notice why Israel wins this time. Verse 35: ["And the LORD smote Benjamin before Israel."]{.class-0} We have run into this before back in 3:28 (see our comments on that verse). When Joshua fought those five kings back there in Joshua 10, the Scripture says, ["And the LORD discomfited them before Israel"]{.class-0} (Josh. 10:10).

America has forgotten that [God]{.class-1} is in charge of combat. God can cause the foot to slip, the gun to jam, the food to be tainted, the ammunition to run out, etc. He can cause unreasonable fear and panic in the hearts of your troops and destroy their morale. He can set the weather against you (or clear it up like He did for Patton at Bastogne). God can take a nation no bigger than Massachusetts (like Vietnam or Korea) and enable it to defeat the world's greatest superpower (the United States).

I had a buddy in the ministry one time named Ray See. He was Bob Jones Sr.'s nephew. God called him to preach before he was saved, but Ray didn't want to preach, so he wouldn't trust Christ. God made it clear to him in no uncertain terms that if he didn't get saved, he would go to Hell. Ray's attitude was: "O.K., I'll go to Hell, then; I'll go to Hell before I preach."

Well, during World War II, Ray was a Marine who fought in the Pacific Theater. One time he and his squad were going through the jungle when a sniper started picking them off. Ray got behind a rock and poked his head out for several seconds trying to spot the sniper. When he couldn't, he rolled behind a log, and another kid took his place behind the rock. That kid poked his head around that same stone at the same spot at the same angle, and within twenty seconds that sniper drilled that kid right between the eyes at the helmet line.

Ray ended up getting saved after one attack where the gunfire was so thick a butterfly couldn't get through it. Ray temporarily lost his mind and started running around screaming, "You can't hit me!" He was brought back to his senses by one of his buddies yelling, "Mortar!" He looked up to see a mortar shell coming down on him. To get away from it, he dived into a garbage pit right before it hit. That was enough for him. He ended up getting saved, and he went into the ministry.

Now why did Ray survive when his buddy "bought the farm"? Because God is in charge of combat.

36 So the children of Benjamin saw that they were smitten: for the men of Israel gave place to the Benjamites, because they trusted unto the liers in wait which they had set beside Gibeah.

37 And the liers in wait hasted, and rushed upon Gibeah; and the liers in wait drew themselves along, and smote all the city with the edge of the sword.

38 Now there was an appointed sign between the men of Israel and the liers in wait, that they should make a great flame with smoke rise up out of the city.

39 And when the men of Israel retired in the battle, Benjamin began to smite and kill of the men of Israel about thirty persons: for they said, Surely they are smitten down before us, as in the first battle.

40 But when the flame began to arise up out of the city with a pillar of smoke, the Benjamites looked behind them, and, behold, the flame of the city ascended up to heaven.

41 And when the men of Israel turned again, the men of Benjamin were amazed: for they saw that evil was come upon them.

42 Therefore they turned their backs before the men of Israel unto the way of the wilderness; but the battle overtook them; and them which came out of the cities they destroyed in the midst of them.

43 Thus they inclosed the Benjamites round about, and chased them, and trode them down with ease over against Gibeah toward the sunrising.

44 And there fell of Benjamin eighteen thousand men; all these were men of valour.

45 And they turned and fled toward the wilderness unto the rock of Rimmon: and they gleaned of them in the highways five thousand men; and pursued hard after them unto Gidom, and slew two thousand men of them.

46 So that all which fell that day of Benjamin were twenty and five thousand men that drew the sword; all these were men of valour.

The material in this passage is a repetition and expansion of what you just read in verses 29--35 (see our remarks under 5:25 on why God repeats material). Israel follows Joshua's battle plan against Ai all the way down to the "smoke signal" when the ambush took Gibeah (see Josh. 8:8, 19--20).

There is a discrepancy of 100 men killed between verses 35 and 46, so the [Vulgate]{.class-1} and the [Septuagint]{.class-1} try to "help God out" by changing verse 35 to match verse 46. But there was no need for this. Verse 46 is the total of all the Benjamites who were slain in the rout when the Israelites turned on them: 18,000 were killed ["over against Gibeah"]{.class-0} (vss. 43--44), 5,000 were ["gleaned . . . in the highways"]{.class-0} (vs. 45), and 2,000 more were killed as they fled to Gidom. No number is given for the ones slain when ["the liers in wait"]{.class-0} took Gibeah (vss. 37--38). The reasonable conclusion is that the extra 100 men of verse 35 were the men left in Gibeah to guard the city. There was no need to change the text because some scholar, educated beyond his intelligence, was too stupid to figure the thing out.

47 But six hundred men turned and fled to the wilderness unto the rock Rimmon, and abode in the rock Rimmon four months.

48 And the men of Israel turned again upon the children of Benjamin, and smote them with the edge of the sword, as well the men of every city, as the beast, and all that came to hand: also they set on fire all the cities that they came to.

Now if you do the math, after the Israelites got through killing 25,100 Benjamites, that would leave 1,100 of the original force of 26,700. Six hundred of those fled to ["the rock Rimmon"]{.class-0} in the wilderness (vs. 47). Of the remaining 500, verse 48 says, ["And the men of Israel turned again upon the children of Benjamin, and smote them with the edge of the sword."]{.class-0}

So of the original 26,700 Benjamites, now only 600 are left alive. But the other eleven tribes don't stop there. They go to the other cities that belonged to Benjamin and kill all the Benjamites who didn't come out to the battle. Following the instructions of Deuteronomy 13:15--16, they kill everyone in those cities, along with their cattle, and burn the cities to the ground. So as it turned out, the sodomites in Benjamin ended up suffering the same fate as Sodom and Gomorrah, and the other cities of the plain there below the Dead Sea. [That's]{.class-1} what God Almighty thinks of "gay pride," and if you think America is going to fare any better, you are in for one of the most shocking surprises of your life.

The Holy Spirit's commentary on the entire mess of Judges 19--20 is found in Amos 4:11--12.

"I have overthrown some of you, as God overthrew Sodom and Gomorrah, and ye were as a firebrand plucked out of the burning: yet have ye not returned unto me, saith the LORD. Therefore thus will I do unto thee, O Israel: and because I will do this unto thee, PREPARE TO MEET THY GOD, O ISRAEL."

If you want to make the Bible "relevant" to today's "contemporary situation," go ahead and substitute [America]{.class-1} in that last verse for ["Israel."]{.class-0} If God wouldn't let His own chosen people get away with that filth, do you really think He's going to give this country a "pass" on it?

[]{#section-0_1_1adfb75ef33f6680_709f.xhtml}

Chapter 21

21:1 Now the men of Israel had sworn in Mizpeh, saying, There shall not any of us give his daughter unto Benjamin to wife.

2 And the people came to the house of God, and abode there till even before God, and lifted up their voices, and wept sore;

3 And said, O LORD God of Israel, why is this come to pass in Israel, that there should be to day one tribe lacking in Israel?

4 And it came to pass on the morrow, that the people rose early, and built there an altar, and offered burnt offerings and peace offerings.

Now in the last two chapters, we have been covering one of the strangest periods of Israel's history recorded in the Bible. A whole tribe of Israel was nearly destroyed over a city of sodomites raping an apostate priest's concubine. Chapter 21 opens up four months after the civil war between Benjamin and the other eleven tribes (20:47).

The question is, now that they had destroyed Benjamin down to only 600 men for the whole tribe (the women and children had been killed back in 20:48), what was to be done next (vs. 3)? The problem was complicated further over the fact that back in 20:7--18, when the eleven tribes went off "half-cocked" without consulting God to begin with, and then only consulting Him to get approval for their own plans, they had made a foolish, rash vow. Unlike Jephthah's rash vow of chapter 11, there was nothing in the Law to allow them out of it.

Though you aren't told about it back in chapter 20, at some point, the other eleven tribes had vowed not to give any of their daughters to the men of Benjamin to marry. Where did they get that? Nowhere: you won't find anything like that commanded anywhere in the Mosaic Law. They just made it up out of their own heads. Did they pray about it? [No.]{.class-1} Did they ask God's will about it? [No.]{.class-1} They just decided to do it, and they sealed it by making it an oath to God.

Verse 2: ["And the people came to the house of God . . . and lifted up their voices, and wept sore."]{.class-0} You can be sorry about a thing and still be out of the will of God. That was Esau's case. He was sorry for selling his birthright; he wept over it; but he was still out of the will of God (Heb. 12:16--17).

The sorrow of verse 2 is what Paul called ["the sorrow of the world"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 7:10). He said, ["For godly sorrow worketh repentance to salvation not to be repented of: but the sorrow of the world worketh death."]{.class-0}

The tears you shed because you are sorry for your sins are good. The Lord is for that. You ought to be sorry for your sins. But if your sorrow and tears don't cause you to seek God's help in getting rid of your sin, or if they don't cause you to confess and judge your sin, they don't help at all; in fact, they'll do you more harm than good.

Notice in verse 4 that they build an altar. They are [at the Tabernacle]{.class-1} (["the house of God"]{.class-0}---vs. 2). Why aren't they inquiring at the Brazen Altar? [It's right there.]{.class-1} Those Jews weren't suppose to offer their sacrifices on any other altar except ["the altar of the LORD"]{.class-0} (Deut. 12:27), the exceptions commanded by God, notwithstanding (see Gideon's and Manoah's cases in chaps. 6 and 13). God never commanded verse 4 here in chapter 21 at all; these people are completely out of line.

5 And the children of Israel said, Who is there among all the tribes of Israel that came not up with the congregation unto the LORD? For they had made a great oath concerning him that came not up to the LORD to Mizpeh, saying, He shall surely be put to death.

6 And the children of Israel repented them for Benjamin their brother, and said, There is one tribe cut off from Israel this day.

7 How shall we do for wives for them that remain, seeing we have sworn by the LORD that we will not give them of our daughters to wives?

Having asked the Lord why it turned out that a tribe should be ["lacking in Israel"]{.class-0} (vs. 3), the people don't wait for an answer from God. Why not? Because [they were the ones at fault,]{.class-1} not God. They were the ones who had made the stupid vow without asking God's opinion on the matter.

That was compounded by the second rash vow they had made: ["For they had made a great oath concerning him that came not up to the LORD to Mizpeh, saying, He shall surely be put to death"]{.class-0} (vs. 5). Where did God tell them to do that? Nowhere. They were making all these foolish oaths without consulting God one time to find out if that is what He wanted. They were painting themselves into a corner.

["And the children of Israel repented them for Benjamin their brother"]{.class-0} (vs. 6). Nice gesture, but where were the Benjamites repenting for what their people had done? ["The children of Israel repented."]{.class-0} Well, Judas ["repented himself"]{.class-0} (Matt. 27:3), and he went to Hell (Acts 1:25). Like Judas, Israel is not repenting because of the [sin]{.class-1} of Benjamin; they are repenting of the [consequences]{.class-1} of their own foolish vows and rash conduct: ["There is one tribe cut off from Israel this day."]{.class-0} Wrong motive.

["How shall we do for wives for them that remain"]{.class-0} (vs. 7). Again, no prayer, no consulting God for anything, no waiting on God for an answer, no taking responsibility for their own stupidity in the matter. It's just: "We are in a mess. What are we going to do? Well, let's try this. If that doesn't work, then let's try this." That's no way to carry out the Lord's business or to conduct your Christian life.

8 And they said, What one is there of the tribes of Israel that came not up to Mizpeh to the LORD? And, behold, there came none to the camp from Jabeshgilead to the assembly.

9 For the people were numbered, and, behold, there were none of the inhabitants of Jabeshgilead there.

10 And the congregation sent thither twelve thousand men of the valiantest, and commanded them, saying, Go and smite the inhabitants of Jabeshgilead with the edge of the sword, with the women and the children.

11 And this is the thing that ye shall do, Ye shall utterly destroy every male, and every woman that hath lain by man.

12 And they found among the inhabitants of Jabeshgilead four hundred young virgins, that had known no man by lying with any male: and they brought them unto the camp to Shiloh, which is in the land of Canaan.

Now the people are going to solve their dilemma all by themselves without any regard for God's opinion in the matter. The whole mess that takes place in this chapter is summed up in the last verse (vs. 25): ["every man did that which was right IN HIS OWN EYES."]{.class-0}

The infidel will point to what you are reading and say, "Look at that. The Bible is an immoral book."[ God has nothing to do with this mess.]{.class-1} This is man operating by [his own reasoning,]{.class-1} not God's revelation, whether by Scripture or by prophet or by inquiring of the high priest. This is what you get when the ACLU, the Freedom from Religion Foundation, the American Humanist Association, and the American Atheist Association have their way: operating totally [without God, without prayer,]{.class-1} and [without the Bible;]{.class-1} operating completely by [human]{.class-1} reasoning and [human]{.class-1} intellect.

The first solution is to find out who didn't come to the assembly at Mizpeh back in chapter 20 and to kill every one of them except the virgins who had never had carnal knowledge with a man. The one city that had not joined in with the rest of the Israelites was the city of Jabesh in the land of Gilead on the east side of Jordan.

The reason Jabesh-gilead did not come to the assembly was because the people of that city felt a particularly close familial relationship to the tribe of Benjamin. They were Manassites, and Manasseh and Benjamin were directly related to each other through Jacob's wife Rachel. Rachel had two sons she bore herself: Joseph and Benjamin. Joseph had two sons: Manasseh and Ephraim. So Benjamin was Rachel's son, and Manasseh was Rachel's grandson.

That close familial relationship between Jabesh-gilead and Benjamin goes all the way into the era of the kingdom of Israel. When ["Nahash the Ammonite"]{.class-0} came to conquer Jabesh-gilead in 1 Samuel 11, it was King Saul from the tribe of Benjamin who rescued them. When Saul died at the hands of the Philistines in 1 Samuel 31, the men of Jabesh-gilead returned the favor to Saul by reclaiming the bones of their deliverer from the heathens' temple and giving them a decent burial.

Here in Judges 21, 12,000 elite troops are chosen to go up against Jabesh-gilead. They treat the inhabitants of the city like the heathen that lived in that land before the children of Israel conquered it: they killed all the men, all their wives, and all their children; only the virgins were spared (see Num. 31:17--18). There was no reason to do that except for the rash vows the people had made at Mizpeh.

The whole thing was a fleshy operation from start to finish. That's how some pastors build their churches: worldly, fleshy [expediency.]{.class-1} What "works"? That's not Biblical Christianity; that's a worldly philosophy (see Col. 2:8) called "pragmatism." The truth be told, a lot of Christians aren't Bible-believing Christians at all; they're [pragmatic atheists.]{.class-1} They operate by [what works for them]{.class-1} ("situation ethics"), not by what God said in His Book. If preaching against sin and preaching the exclusivity of Jesus Christ and the Gospel won't bring in the crowds, dump 'em and "rap" about finances, how to let your wife run the family, your "love life," and how to "cope and share." If the Bible and hymn books don't appeal to your "community," get rid of them and bring in the twenty-foot plasma screen, the rock band, the "worship team," and all the modern versions. If fellowship and communion among believers of like faith won't fill the auditorium, substitute the coffee shop, the snack bar, the raffle tickets, and the "small groups" in their place. Whatever works for you; [not what God said to do.]{.class-1}

13 And the whole congregation sent some to speak to the children of Benjamin that were in the rock Rimmon, and to call peaceably unto them.

14 And Benjamin came again at that time; and they gave them wives which they had saved alive of the women of Jabeshgilead: and yet so they sufficed them not.

15 And the people repented them for Benjamin, because that the LORD had made a breach in the tribes of Israel.

Having come up with the solution to their problem [without God,]{.class-1} what did it accomplish? After slaughtering a whole city of Israel who, as far as the record goes, hadn't committed any trespass against God Himself, they were still 200 women short of the number of Benjamites who needed wives.

Do they repent of killing the inhabitants of Jabesh-gilead? No. Do they ask God what to do next? No. [They blame God for their own stupidity.]{.class-1}

["And the people repented them for Benjamin, BECAUSE THAT THE LORD HAD MADE A BREACH IN THE TRIBES OF ISRAEL"]{.class-0} (vs. 15).

No He did not! [They had.]{.class-1} You ask, "What do you mean by 'they,' Ruckman?" I mean [the whole nation of Israel.]{.class-1} It was the tribe of Benjamin that raised the ire of the other tribes with their sodomy. It was the prayerlessness, disobedience, and rashness of the other tribes that put them in the situation they now found themselves. Why blame God?

16 Then the elders of the congregation said, How shall we do for wives for them that remain, seeing the women are destroyed out of Benjamin?

17 And they said, There must be an inheritance for them that be escaped of Benjamin, that a tribe be not destroyed out of Israel.

18 Howbeit we may not give them wives of our daughters: for the children of Israel have sworn, saying, Cursed be he that giveth a wife to Benjamin.

19 Then they said, Behold, there is a feast of the LORD in Shiloh yearly in a place which is on the north side of Bethel, on the east side of the highway that goeth up from Bethel to Shechem, and on the south of Lebonah.

20 Therefore they commanded the children of Benjamin, saying, Go and lie in wait in the vineyards;

21 And see, and, behold, if the daughters of Shiloh come out to dance in dances, then come ye out of the vineyards, and catch you every man his wife of the daughters of Shiloh, and go to the land of Benjamin.

22 And it shall be, when their fathers or their brethren come unto us to complain, that we will say unto them, Be favourable unto them for our sakes: because we reserved not to each man his wife in the war: for ye did not give unto them at this time, that ye should be guilty.

The question is raised again: Where would the eleven tribes get the other 200 wives for the remaining Benjamite men (vs. 16)? Once again, no prayer, no consulting God in any way; nothing but pragmatic humanism. The last time they resorted to [murder;]{.class-1} this time they resort to [kidnapping.]{.class-1}

["Behold, there is a feast of the LORD in Shiloh yearly"]{.class-0} (vs. 19). We are not told in the text which feast this is. Some of the expositors say this was the yearly feast commemorating Jephthah's daughter, but that wasn't a ["feast."]{.class-0} It was a lamentation (see 11:40). Lamentation isn't feasting and dancing (vs. 21). It's a time of fasting, sorrow, and mourning.

Also, this ["is a feast of the LORD."]{.class-0} So this isn't something the Israelites instituted. This is one of the seven ["feasts of the LORD"]{.class-0} given by God in Leviticus 23. This is ["the feast of the LORD"]{.class-0} referred to in Hoses 9:5 (see our comments on that verse in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class-1} Vol. I)---it is the Feast of Tabernacles, the feast connected to the Second Advent (Zech. 14:16--19).

The ["dance"]{.class-0} of verse 21 is not a secular dance like you find at sock hops, night clubs, and discos. This is a dance of women with women in a non-sexual way like you find Miriam doing it in Exodus 15:20, and it is a dance to praise God like David did in 2 Samuel 6:16. If you look at that last reference, that dance had nothing to do with "choreography" or seductive moves. It was closer akin to what the lame man did when he was healed in Acts 3:8 than it is to "interpretive dance."

Now what the remaining 200 Benjamites are told is to go kidnap the young ladies who are dancing in praise to God at the Feast of Tabernacles and make them their wives. Do you think God is in a mess like that? Like the teenagers say, "No way!"

The Israelites tell those Benjamites, "Don't you worry about kidnapping those girls. If their fathers or their families come complaining to us about what you've done, we'll speak up for you. We'll say, 'Give them a break for our sakes. We're the war vets, and we promised not to give our daughters to them. Don't you worry about that oath, though, because, technically speaking, you didn't give your daughters to them.'"

You see how devious the mind of a sinner is. It is always trying to find a way out of doing right without being guilty of doing wrong. It looks for the loophole, the technicality, that allows it to get away with its devilment.

A Catholic momma asked her little girl, "What did you give up for Lent, honey?" "Nothing," said the girl. "Why not?" asked the momma. "Well, you didn't give up anything for Lent," replied her daughter. "Yes I did," said the mother, "Your father and I gave up drinking alcohol for Lent." "You did not," said the little girl, "I saw you drink some beer last night at supper." "Yes," said her mother, "but we gave up hard liquor." The little girl said, "Then I'll quit eating hard candy and just have chocolate." That little girl wasn't fooled one bit; she knew momma and daddy were trying to get around their promise.

Back in the days when the Catholic Church used to be stricter than it is today about eating meat on Fridays, a Catholic Priest walked into a cafeteria and asked, "Do you have any shark?" The lady behind the serving counter replied, "No." "Do you have any octopus?" asked the Priest. "No," said the lady. "How about whale?" asked the Priest. "Of course not," said the lady. "Oh well, I tried," said the Priest, "Give me the steak." (That's funny, folks; you can laugh.)

That's the sinful mind trying to justify itself. I experienced that back before I was saved. Looking back on it, it is kind of funny now, but it wasn't funny at the time.

At that time, I was attending the Catholic Church; like any good Catholic, I was trying to [work]{.class-1} my way to Heaven. And I was a good Catholic, boy. I was crossing myself three or four times a day and putting money in the tithe box. (I was tithing before I was saved; some of you Baptists haven't started yet.) On Ash Wednesday, I would put the ashes on my forehead and leave them there all day long while I worked down at the radio station. On Palm Sunday I would take the palm leaf home and put it on my mantle.

But the whole time I was doing all that, I was reading a stolen Bible. One of the things I read was don't forsake the poor and beware and open your hand wide to him (see Deut. 15:7--8). So I was giving out right and left, man. I was going to work my way to Heaven.

Well, one night I was downtown waiting for the bus to get a ride home. I lived only about a mile away, but it was raining, and I didn't want to walk home in the rain. Back then, bus fare was only a dime, and I happened to have one dime in my pocket.

I had the dime in my pocket and saw the bus coming two blocks away. I was leaning up against an awning, waiting on that bus, when around the corner came a blind man with a tin cup in his hand, begging. He was coming right toward me. All I could think of was that Scripture that said not to forget the poor.

I thought to myself, "I have to give him the dime, but if I give him the dime, I'll walk home in the rain." It's kind of funny now; after all, how could some fool think giving away a dime would affect his soul? But if you are a Catholic really trying to get to Heaven by works, you live in terror morning, noon, and night that you aren't doing enough or not doing it right; [you are in bondage.]{.class-1}

Well, that blind man kept getting closer and closer, and the bus started up my block. And wouldn't you know, about that time the rain came down harder. So the old, devious human mind began to work. I said to myself, "If he asks me directly, I'll have to give him the dime, but if he just walks by, I won't have to." That is how the human mind works. When it comes to self-preservation, every man is a genius.

As that blind man got nearer, and as the bus was only forty feet away, I plastered myself up against the wall so that blind man wouldn't know I was there and would just walk on by. As he walked by me, I breathed a sign of relief and started to step toward the bus. That's when that bird swung around and stuck that cup right in my face. Clink! I put the dime in the cup and started to walk off in the rain.

But as I shoved my hands in my pockets, I felt another dime I didn't realize I had. I turned around and got on that bus in a sweat. It's kind of amusing now, but that shows you the self-calculating, scheming nature of the sinful mind. That is why you can't be justified by the works of the Law. It's not just the outward observance; it's the inner motivation behind what you do.

Here, those Jews were looking for a way out of the oath they had sworn. The truth is, they were guilty by "aiding and abetting."

23 And the children of Benjamin did so, and took them wives, according to their number, of them that danced, whom they caught: and they went and returned unto their inheritance, and repaired the cities, and dwelt in them.

24 And the children of Israel departed thence at that time, every man to his tribe and to his family, and they went out from thence every man to his inheritance.

25 In those days there was no king in Israel: every man did that which was right in his own eyes.

Following the instructions of the men of Israel, the remaining 200 Benjamites go and kidnap the young women who danced at the feast in Shiloh. Now all 600 Benjamites had wives. These were all that were left to rebuild the tribe of Benjamin, both in population and the cities the eleven tribes had destroyed (vs. 23 cf. 20:48).

Having solved the problem into which they had gotten themselves, the rest of the tribes returned to their own lands, smug in the fact that [they didn't really need God to take care of their problems.]{.class-1} Remember, all of the events of chapters 19--21 take place [before]{.class-1} Judges 3. If you want to know what contributed to the continuous apostasy of Israel in the book of Judges, it was [that.]{.class-1} As long as the Israelites thought they could get along without God, they continued right on in their idolatry. That is why God sent in those heathen nations to enslave His people: [it drove them back to God.]{.class-1} They couldn't take care of their own problems then; they [had]{.class-1} to seek God.

The last verse of chapter 21 sums up the entire book of Judges.

"In those days there was no king in Israel: every man did that which was right in his own eyes."

["There was no king in Israel."]{.class-0} There was no final authority any higher than every man's own opinion. Do you know what Moses was called in Deuteronomy 33:5? God called Moses a ["KING in Jeshurun."]{.class-0} Although Moses wasn't a King, God gave him the authority of a King, and the authority Moses had as a King came from [the written word of God.]{.class-1}

Deuteronomy 33:4---["Moses commanded us A LAW."]{.class-0} That was the ["BOOK of the law"]{.class-0} Joshua was commanded to go by (Josh. 1:8), and as long as he went by that BOOK, God said He would be with Joshua as He was with Moses (Josh. 1:5). So Joshua had the same authority Moses had (i.e., the authority of a King) as long as he went BY THE BOOK.

Do you know what the Kings of Israel were commanded to do nearly 400 years before Saul or David came along? Each King was commanded by God to make a copy of the Book of the Law and read it ["all the days of his life"]{.class-0} so he would fear God and obey His ["words"]{.class-0} (Deut. 17:19). The Book was to be the "check" on the so-called "divine right of kings" (Deut. 17:20).

So when God said, ["there was no king in Israel,"]{.class-0} He was saying there was no man, like Moses, Joshua, or David, who was teaching and enforcing THE final authority---[God's words in His Book.]{.class-1}

That is the problem with modern Christianity---Christians have abandoned their final authority. The Liberals say the Bible is only a book written by men, and one man's opinion about God is just as good as another's. So the Bible is just one of many "sacred scriptures," and [none of them are the words of God]{.class-1}. So the "emergents" (neo-Liberals) accept Moslems as worshiping the God of Abraham, tacitly deny the virgin birth, define the Trinity in their own human terms, and accept "gay marriage" because the Bible is just a collection of the bigotry and prejudices of ancient men. NO FINAL AUTHORITY.

The Neo-orthodox and Charismatics claim "Jesus" is their final authority, which is saying nothing. "What Would Jesus Do?" (WWJD) is meaningless if you have nothing to tell you what Jesus actually would do or [what Jesus Christ wants you to do.]{.class-1} When you hear someone say "Jesus is my final authority," what is usually meant is: "I THINK this is what Jesus would do or what He wants, so that is what I'll do." Like Voltaire and Mark Twain said, such people create a "Jesus" [in their own image.]{.class-1} The Apostle Paul called such a Jesus ["another Jesus"]{.class-0} that would [damn your soul]{.class-1} (2 Cor. 11:4 cf. Gal. 1:8).

The more theological adherents to this profession will set the words of Jesus Christ in the Gospels against [all the rest of the words of the Holy Ghost in the rest of the Scriptures.]{.class-1} This is a direct attack on the doctrine that ["ALL SCRIPTURE is given by inspiration of God"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 3:16). It also ignores the fact that Jesus Christ gave the Apostle Paul revelation that He did not give Peter, James, John, et al., in the Gospels (Gal. 1:11--12). It is [wrongly]{.class-1}[ "dividing the word of truth"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 2:15). In the end, what you have is someone picking and choosing what words of Jesus Christ in the Gospels he will follow and which ones he won't, based solely on his own personal theological slant. That is, NO FINAL AUTHORITY.

The Fundamentalist and Conservative [profess]{.class-1} belief in a final authority, [without actually believing any book is the final authority.]{.class-1} If your final authority is a pile of lost papers no one living has ever seen, [you have no final authority.]{.class-1} You can profess anything you want about them because [no one can check you out to see if you are telling the truth.]{.class-1}

If your final authority is the Alexandrian text that contradicts the God-honored text in anywhere from 36,000 ([NASV]{.class-1}) to 64,000 ([NIV]{.class-1}) places, [you have no final authority]{.class-1} because you (or your buddies) decide what words belong in the Bible and what words don't. If your final authority is the [Textus Receptus]{.class-1} Greek (or the Masoretic Hebrew), you fare no better, because, in the end, your authority is not the [words]{.class-1} of the Biblical text but the lexicons and commentaries of [men]{.class-1} on the Biblical text. When your profession is "A better translation would be . . ." or "This is an unfortunate rendering . . . ," you have NO FINAL AUTHORITY.

[I have a final authority.]{.class-1} It is in my language. I can hold it in my hand. I can read it, teach it, preach it, memorize it, and [believe it.]{.class-1} I don't have to change one word in my final authority. The Holy Spirit has blessed that Book ([AV]{.class-1} 1611) for over 400 years now; it is the Book that brought about the greatest periods of revival and missionary outreach the world has ever seen.

My final authority isn't in a dead language (koine Greek) or in a language spoken by less than 1% of the world (Hebrew); it is in the universal language of the last days before the return of Jesus Christ. I have a final authority that is inerrant, infallible, and ["given by inspiration of God."]{.class-0} No Fundamentalist or Conservative who believes that "only the originals were inspired" believes [any]{.class-1} Greek manuscript or [any]{.class-1} Greek text is inspired. He believes they [all]{.class-1} have mistakes in them. He doesn't even believe the text he has is necessarily the text of the original autographs since the discovery of new manuscripts can lead scholars to change the text (that is what happened in Nestle's 26th edition of [Novum Testamentum Graece]{.class-1}).

I have a final authority that ["is quick, and powerful, and sharper than any twoedged sword"]{.class-0} (Heb. 4:12) because its ["words"]{.class-0} are ["spirit"]{.class-0} and ["life"]{.class-0} (John 6:63). It's not a dead, impotent beanbag made to generate book sales, like the [ASV, RSV, NASV, NIV, NKJV, NRSV, CEV, Good News for Modern Man, ESV, ]{.class-1}or[ MEV]{.class-1} (the new ["Modern English Version"]{.class-1}). It's the best-selling Book in the history of the world, not because it is the newest piece of junk on the market, but because the Holy Spirit has born witness in the hearts of believers through a period of over 400 years that that Book is ["the holy scriptures"]{.class-0} (Rom. 1:2; 2 Tim. 3:15).

[I have a final authority,]{.class-1} and it is ["THE WORD OF A KING"]{.class-0} (Eccl. 8:4).

Back to Judges 21:25---["every man did that which was right in his own eyes."]{.class-0} So what you have with the children of Israel in the book of Judges is HELL ON WHEELS.

["There is a way WHICH SEEMETH RIGHT UNTO A MAN, but the end thereof are THE WAYS OF DEATH"]{.class-0} (Prov. 14:12).

You thought I was just being rude and crude in my speech again, didn't you (see 2 Cor. 11:6)? "Ruckman's language," you know. No, those Jews were commanded by God NOT to do whatever they thought was right in their own eyes (Deut. 12:8) because it would bring the judgment of God on them (Eccl. 11:9).

In that Book, you are told not to lean on your own understanding (Prov. 3:5), not to rely on your own wisdom (Prov. 3:7, 23:4; Jer. 9:23; Rom. 12:16) or knowledge (1 Cor. 8:1--2), and not to trust your own heart (Prov. 28:26). [Your]{.class-1} understanding and knowledge are [limited. Your]{.class-1} wisdom may not necessarily be [God's]{.class-1} wisdom (1 Cor. 3:18--20; Isa. 55:8--9). Your ["heart is deceitful above all things, and desperately wicked"]{.class-0} (Jer. 17:9).

Your understanding had better come from [God's word]{.class-1} (Psa. 119:169). You had better get ["the wisdom of God"]{.class-0} and ["the righteousness of God"]{.class-0}---the Lord Jesus Christ (1 Cor. 1:24; Rom. 3:22, 10:4; 2 Cor. 5:21). You had better get that deceitful heart purified by faith in Christ (Acts 15:9), your scheming mind renewed by the Holy Ghost (Rom. 12:2; Eph. 4:23), and you had better ["put on the new man . . . created in righteousness and true holiness"]{.class-0} (Eph. 4:24). And if you ever hope to be ["perfect, throughly furnished unto all good works"]{.class-0} (2 Tim. 3:17), you had better NOT go by your own views, opinions, or preferences. You had better go by THE FINAL AUTHORITY (2 Tim. 3:16).

[]{#section-0_1_42ebb642e8ae9d77_70a0.xhtml}

Ruth

Introduction

The book of Ruth is the eighth book in the [Authorized Version]{.class-1} and is included in the historical books. In the Hebrew Bible, though, it is part of the [Kethubim,]{.class-1} the "writings"---what Christ called ["the psalms"]{.class-0} (Luke 24:44).

The book of Ruth is one of only two books in the Bible that bear a woman's name, the other being the book of Esther. The significance of these two books is the [prophetic typology]{.class-1} involved. In Ruth, a Gentile joins the Jews and gets in on the Jewish blessing; that's a picture of the Bride of Christ (Eph. 2:11--19). In Esther, God dumps the Gentiles and brings the Jews back into fellowship with Him (see the Introduction to Esther in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther]{.class-1}). The only two books that are named after women are pictures of the Bride of Christ (the Church) and the bride of Jehovah (Israel). A "coincidence," of course, of course.

So far from being just a "story" in the Old Testament of a Moabite widow returning with her mother-in-law to Israel and finding a husband, what you are reading in the book of Ruth is [prophecy]{.class-1} (2 Pet. 1:20). God can be "tricky" sometimes; He will "hide" things in that Book to see if you will [study]{.class-1} it the right way (2 Tim. 2:15). The Hyperdispensationalist will say, "Israel is the subject of prophecy; the Church is the subject of revelation," meaning there is nothing in the Old Testament about the Church, the Body of Christ (Eph. 1:22--23). Why, you crazy nut, the Church is found, in type, all through the Old Testament, beginning with [Eve]{.class-1} (Eph. 5:25--32).

Brethren, whoever wrote that Book is way ahead of you in 2015. He is sitting up in Eternity (Rev. 21--22) writing [backwards]{.class-1} into time. He is writing about the Bride of Christ before He ever reveals it to the Apostle Paul (Gal. 1; Eph. 2).

The book of Ruth has 4 chapters, 85 verses, and 2,574 words. It takes place during the period of the judges (1:1), sometime between 1322 B.C. and 1186 B.C. The reason that is important is, as you read in the last verse of Judges (21:25): ["In those days there was no king in Israel."]{.class-0} The book of Ruth relates the account of a Gentile woman from whom God chooses His King (4:22). God is going to go from judges to Kings, and He is going to use this Moabite woman Ruth to do that.

But the King goes far beyond just David. Ruth ends up in the [line of Christ]{.class-1} (Matt. 1:5, 17); the book traces the [genealogy of the Messiah.]{.class-1} Ruth doesn't just bring in the King of Israel (Matt. 2:2); she brings in the King of the whole earth (Zech. 14:9).

This Messianic line is what Scofield calls "the godly line of Seth" (see his note under Gen. 6:4). But the Messianic line is not a "godly line" at all; it had some of the most ungodly characters in it about whom you will ever read (see our comments on Matt. 1 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Matthew]{.class-1}). Not only did it have an [adulterer]{.class-1} and [murderer]{.class-1} in it (David---Matt. 1:6), but it also had a woman who committed [incest]{.class-1} with her father-in-law (Tamar---Matt. 1:3) and a [professional whore]{.class-1} (Rahab---Matt. 1:5).

The Messianic line, as recorded in Matthew 1, is also noted for the [Gentile women]{.class-1} in it. Not only was there Ruth, a [Moabitess]{.class-1} (Matt. 1:5 cf. Ruth 1:22), there was a [Canaanite]{.class-1} woman (Tamar---Matt. 1:3 cf. Gen. 38:1--6), an [Amorite]{.class-1} woman (Rahab---Matt. 1:5 cf. Josh 6:25, 5:1, 7:7), and an [Ammonite]{.class-1} woman (Rehoboam's mother---Matt. 1:7 cf. 1 Kings 14:21, 31).

Now Ruth is from the land of Moab (1:4). God says (twice) in the Psalms, ["Moab is my washpot"]{.class-0} (Psa. 60:8, 108:9). Based on that description of Moab, Leroy Wright, a country preacher from Mississippi, came up with this outline for the characters in Ruth 1.

I. Three were [washed up]{.class-1} (Elimelech and his two sons, Mahlon and Chilion, died---1:3).

II\. One was [washed out]{.class-1} (Orpah defected back to her gods---1:14).

III\. One was [washed in]{.class-1} (Ruth got in the right family---1:16--17).

IV\. One was [washed]{.class-1} (Naomi got cleansed by her tribulations---1:20--21).

Unlike its counterpart, Esther, the words [God]{.class-1} and [Lord]{.class-1} appear throughout Ruth. Nevertheless, the [providence]{.class-1} of God is as manifest in Ruth as it is in Esther. Ruth 2:3 says, ["her HAP was to light on a part of the field belonging unto Boaz, who was of the kindred of Elimelech."]{.class-0} But man's ["hap"]{.class-0} is [God's map.]{.class-1}

Although you read of no prophet speaking or of any miracle being performed in the book of Ruth, God is still "behind the scenes" working out circumstances to His own divine purpose. The Christian needs to remember that when he hears some crazy Charismatic talk about "God told me" and "expect your miracle." In this day and age, the Lord speaks to you from [the Scriptures]{.class-1} (2 Pet. 1:19), and He directs the circumstances of your life (even the [bad]{.class-1} ones) to work for your good (Rom. 8:28). If there is any "miracle," it is going to be a "miracle" of [providence,]{.class-1} where God works through men and ordinary, everyday situations to meet your needs. This is the time when ["we walk by faith, not by sight"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 5:7).

With that, we enter into our study of the book of Ruth. It is God's "romance novel." It is the love story of a young widow who comes to faith in the one, true God and finds the "love of her life" in so doing. And in "the fullness of time" (see Gal. 4:4--5), God uses that to manifest His love to a lost world (John 3:16; Rom. 5:8).

["Herein is love, not that we loved God, but that he loved us, and sent his Son to be the propitiation for our sins"]{.class-0} (1 John 4:10).

["We love him, because he first loved us"]{.class-0} (1 John 4:19).

Ruth is what preachers and Bible teachers throughout church history have called "the romance of redemption." In the end, the "hero" of the story is not Ruth at all, but Boaz in his role as "kinsman redeemer," a picture of the One who ["redeemed us from the curse of the law"]{.class-0} (Gal. 3:13) ["out of every kindred, and tongue, and people, and nation"]{.class-0} (Rev. 5:9) by His ["precious blood"]{.class-0} (1 Pet. 1:18--19).

In this book, we learn some great lessons about the ["great love wherewith he loved us"]{.class-0} (Eph. 2:4). And whereas the book of Judges ended in great despair because of the sinfulness of fallen man, the book of Ruth ends in the great expectation of the King, the Lover of our souls, the Lord Jesus Christ.

[]{#section-0_1_25fd3c339395d445_70a1.xhtml}

Chapter 1

1:1 Now it came to pass in the days when the judges ruled, that there was a famine in the land. And a certain man of Bethlehemjudah went to sojourn in the country of Moab, he, and his wife, and his two sons.

2 And the name of the man was Elimelech, and the name of his wife Naomi, and the name of his two sons Mahlon and Chilion, Ephrathites of Bethlehemjudah. And they came into the country of Moab, and continued there.

3 And Elimelech Naomi's husband died; and she was left, and her two sons.

4 And they took them wives of the women of Moab; the name of the one was Orpah, and the name of the other Ruth: and they dwelled there about ten years.

5 And Mahlon and Chilion died also both of them; and the woman was left of her two sons and her husband.

["The days when the judges ruled"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). Archbishop Ussher places the dates for Ruth at between 1322 B.C. and 1312 B.C. (see vs. 4 for the ten-year timespan). If that is so, that would put the events of the book between Judges 3 and 4: between the terms of Ehud and Shamgar, and the term of Deborah.

The ["famine"]{.class-0} of verse 1 is the fourth one listed in the Scriptures. Altogether, there are [thirteen]{.class-1} famines found in the Bible: (1) Genesis 12:10, (2) Genesis 26:1, (3) Genesis 41:54--57, (4) the one here in Ruth 1:1, (5) 2 Samuel 21:1, (6) 1 Kings 18:2, (7) 2 Kings 6:25, (8) 2 Kings 8:1, (9) 2 Kings 25:3, (10) Amos 8:11, (11) Acts 11:27--30, (12) Revelation 6:6--8, and (13) Revelation 18:8.

A famine, of course, is a lack of food, usually due to the crops not growing. When a man's life is threatened, that is the real test of what a man is. When the Devil wanted to test Job to the limit, he told God, ["Skin for skin, yea, all that a man hath will he give for his life"]{.class-0} (Job 2:4). You won't know what human nature really is until you get hungry and can't get food.

Back in the winter of 1846--1847, a group of pioneers known as the "Donner Party" got stuck up in the pass of the Sierra Nevada mountains. The food ran out, and the ones who survived the ordeal did so by [eating]{.class-1} those who had died of starvation and sickness. If you think Americans have changed just because they are more educated and more "advanced" technologically, you had better think again. In 1972, a jet crashed in the Andes Mountains in South America. Sixteen of the 45 passengers survived by eating the frozen remains of the passengers who had died from the elements. A hundred years didn't improve human nature one iota.

Human nature is "survival of the fittest": me first, you next. [That's]{.class-1} human nature. The Devil knows that even if the psychiatrists don't. Of course, he messed up on Job; ditto John the Baptist, Stephen, and the Apostle Paul. The things that made the difference in these "exceptions to the rule" was [a love for God]{.class-1} and [a love for His word]{.class-1} (see Job 1:21, 23:12).

The unsaved, Adamic nature in man is [egocentric.]{.class-1} The more men talk about "helping their fellow man," the more conceited they are. The more frank ones among them, like Hitler, Stalin, and "Chairman Mao," will come right out and tell you, "Since I am going to make the world a better place to live in ([with me in charge,]{.class-1} of course), I have to get rid of everyone who will try to stop me from doing that." In other words, he's an animal in a jungle, operating by brute force, who kills anyone who opposes him.

They appeal to that nature in the people who follow them. If you are a German, then it's Hitler telling you, "Today Germany; tomorrow the world!" He tells the German people, "Join me in conquering Europe, and I'll give you the whole world. You'll be on top like I am."

That's what Mohammed told his followers. The [Koran]{.class-1} is filled with that stuff: "The Arab nation is the greatest nation on earth and chosen by Allah. All the world belongs to Allah and me, his Messenger; someday everyone will be a Moslem like you, my followers" (for documentation, get our work [Will the Real "Allah" Please Stand Up?]{.class-1}). How does a Moslem make that come to pass? By killing the "infidels" who won't "convert." "ISIS" (the Islamic State of Iraq and Syria) is only practicing what Mohammed preached.

The people who talk the most about "love" are the ones who [hate the truth]{.class-1} the most. I get a lot of criticism about "not enough love," but I know real love for God when I see it. Do you give more than the tithe to the Lord's work? Do you love the Lord enough to go out on the street and make a fool out of yourself for Him? Don't talk to me about "love." You don't know about what you are talking.

Most Christians just "play it cool" to preserve themselves. [That's]{.class-1} human nature. Human nature doesn't want to "waste its money" by giving tithes and offerings; it doesn't want to make a fool of itself for anybody.

Do you know to whom I am writing when I make these commentaries? I am addressing the same crowd to whom Noah preached (2 Pet. 2:5). Of course, it is a "select" audience; most of the people who read my works are [saved.]{.class-1} But don't kid yourself, Christian; the Adamic nature in your flesh is the same nature that was in the flesh of everyone who drowned in the Flood. Amen, amen, amen, and AMEN!

If you are saved, the part in you that responds to God, the Holy Spirit, and the Book is the new man in Christ (Eph. 4:24; Col. 3:10). But you have [two natures,]{.class-1} Christian. You still have your [human]{.class-1} nature right alongside the new nature, and [human nature doesn't change.]{.class-1}

That is where the "cross" comes in for the believer. The "cross" is where your natural human tendencies [cross]{.class-1} what God wants, and you [crucify]{.class-1} the desires of the human nature to do what God wants you to do (Gal. 5:24; Rom. 8:13; Col. 3:5; 1 Cor. 15:31). That's denying yourself and bearing your cross cheerfully (Luke 9:23). That [violates]{.class-1} human nature; it takes some [spirituality.]{.class-1}

A famine will show what you are spiritually. We haven't had a real famine in this country (the United States) since it started. Of course, the "Dust Bowl" of the 1930s came the closest, but even then, the government stepped in with measures to feed the poor. Back when the first settlers came to this country, they weren't accustomed to the harsh winters or how to effectively plant crops in the New World. As a result, both the colonies at Plymouth and Jamestown were devastated by famine in their first winter, with over half the colonists dying of starvation. The Pilgrims, of course, learned how to plant maize (corn) from the Indians and how to use fish as fertilizer, so the next winter, the Lord blessed them with an abundance of crops, which is from where our Thanksgiving holiday comes. But since then, there has been no nationwide famine. It is nearly impossible for a healthy person to die of starvation in the United States. If someone does, it is because he won't work, or wastes his money on liquor or drugs, or doesn't avail himself of welfare or other charitable programs.

But brethren, sooner or later, a famine is coming. I got a book which was published back in 1966 by a fellow named Dan Van Gorder; it's entitled [Ill Fares the Land.]{.class-1} The subtitle is: "The Famine Planned for America." It has charts on wheat production, rye production, corn production, the pigs, the cows, the ewes, the chickens, etc.---all the food production in the United States. Those charts show a steady growth in food production from the 1930s to the 1960s, but then he gives you another chart: a [population]{.class-1} chart. The population skyrockets with food production only making modest increases. When the charts are compared, what you are left with is not enough food to feed the populous.

Let enough people lose their jobs and enough people get on "food stamps," and eventually things are going to go to pieces. That's when you will see people as they really are. If people are sure enough hungry, you will see "society" women down at the supermarket with ball bats fighting to get food. In Germany, during the depression of the thirties, when the German mark was severely devalued, something like [three million]{.class-1} middle-aged, middle-class Germans starved to death. The women were going through garbage cans to find food for their families. That is one of the things that led to Hitler coming into power.

Famine will bring raw human nature to the surface, without the refinements of class, education, or "civilization." Sometimes a momma will sacrifice her food to feed her baby, and [sometimes she won't.]{.class-1} Some mommas will [kill ]{.class-1}their babies so they won't have to feed them---more food for the momma. Over in 2 Kings 6, in the famine of Samaria, one woman killed her child and [ate him]{.class-1} to survive. [That's]{.class-1} human nature.

One of the biggest lies told among "Evangelicals" is that all men are created in the image of God. That was true of the [first]{.class-1} man, but Adam sinned and [lost]{.class-1} the image of God. When Seth was born, he wasn't born in God's likeness or image; he was born in his fallen daddy's image (Gen. 5:3). A man doesn't get back God's image until he gets in Christ at salvation (Col. 3:10), because [Jesus Christ is the image of God]{.class-1} (2 Cor. 4:4; Col. 1:15; Heb. 1:3).

Now back during the Depression, the big survival crop was black-eyed peas. If nothing else would grow, you could grow black-eyed peas, can them, and survive on them. Another good survival crop down South is sweet potatoes. I have grown large sweet potatoes in my garden with no pesticides and no fertilizer. I have been told by farmers in Alabama that if stored properly (moderately cool in the summer and moderately warm in the winter), sweet potatoes will stay good for nine months. My son David tells me butternut squash is like that; butternut squash can be stored for fourteen months.

The famine about which you really need to be concerned right now, though, is the famine of Amos 8:11--12.

"Behold, the days come, saith the Lord GOD, that I will send a famine in the land, not a famine of bread, nor a thirst for water, BUT OF HEARING THE WORDS OF THE LORD: And they shall wander from sea to sea, and from the north even to the east, they shall run to and fro to seek the word of the LORD, and shall not find it."

[You are in that famine.]{.class-1} Twice a year, we have special meetings at the Bible Baptist Church called Bad Attitude Baptist Blowouts. We never have any trouble filling up the auditorium during those meetings because Bible believers will travel from all over the country (and in some instances, from [other]{.class-1} countries) to come to those meetings to hear the preaching. Why? Because in many instances, those people aren't getting good, Bible-believing preaching from the [King James]{.class-1} Bible where they are.

It used to be that if a church were independent, Fundamental, and Baptist, the pastor would always preach from the [AV.]{.class-1} That's because, like Bob Jones III, he wanted to be "identified" with the Book that built America and American Christianity---even if he didn't believe it. [He was forced to use a book he didn't believe.]{.class-1}

Not any more, boy. After a hundred years of Christian Colleges, Universities, and Seminaries telling their students the [AV]{.class-1} had mistakes in it and the Alexandrian text of the [ASV]{.class-1} was "clearer" and "more accurate," the pastors trained under that mess finally took the professors at their word and abandoned the [AV]{.class-1} for the [NIV, NKJV, NASV,]{.class-1} and now the [ESV]{.class-1} (the "Conservative" translation of the [RSV]{.class-1} text). After all, why be "identified" with an inferior text when actually [no text]{.class-1} extant is "inspired" or infallible? As a consequence, Bible-believing Christians in some areas have to drive an hour one way to hear ["the words of the LORD,"]{.class-0} and some don't even have a Bible-believing church preaching from the [AV]{.class-1} that close.

What has been the result of this famine of the words of the living God? Women doing belly dances in the aisles of churches (I am exaggerating nothing; I have viewed the video myself of it happening in the biggest Charismatic sideshow ever to pass off as a "revival" here in Pensacola), the divorce rate and abortion rate for "Christians" being equal to that of the lost world, rock music performed from the platform of some of the largest Fundamental works in the country, and "dialogue" on "gay marriage" (sex perversion). [That]{.class-1} is the fruit of the tainted food supply (the modern versions) that produced the current famine of God's words.

Returning to verse 1: ["And a certain man of Bethlehem-judah went to sojourn in the country of Moab."]{.class-0} Now, some of the greatest types found in this chapter can be found in the meanings of the [names. ]{.class-1}Take, for instance, the name ["Bethlehem-judah."]{.class-0} [Beth]{.class-1} is the Hebrew word for "house"; [lehem]{.class-1} is the Hebrew word for "bread." So [Bethlehem]{.class-1} means the "house of bread." Why is that? Because that is where the Bread of Life entered this world (Mic. 5:2 cf. John 6:35, 48).

The name [Judah]{.class-1} means "praising God" (Gen. 29:35). You see that "Ju" at the beginning of the name? That's an abbreviation for [Jehovah]{.class-1} (see Psa. 68:4); as in Joshua and Jesus ("Jehovah saves"), Jehoshaphat, etc. "Ju," "Je," "Jo," and "Ja" are all variations of that abbreviation. So the name ["Bethlehem-judah"]{.class-0} means "the house of bread and praising God."

Here is a fellow named ["Elimelech"]{.class-0}; the name means "God is his King." But Elimelech wasn't living as if God were his King at all. When the famine hit, instead of trusting his King to provide for him in the house of bread and praise, he takes the family and moves to God's ["washpot"]{.class-0} (Moab---Psa. 60:8, 108:9).

That was a bad error. Israel had just come out of subjugation by the Moabites back in Judges 3, and now Elimelech goes there to [God's enemies]{.class-1} to get food to survive the famine. That's what got Abraham into trouble back there in Genesis 12. He went down to Egypt to escape his famine and ended up lying about his wife and almost losing her to Pharaoh. It was in Egypt that he got Hagar, the mother of Ishmael (Gen. 16), and that is from where all the trouble between the Jews and Arabs comes today.

Now look at the wording there in verse 1: Elimelech ["went to SOJOURN in the country of Moab."]{.class-0} A [sojourn]{.class-1} is "a [temporary]{.class-1} stay." But look at the end of verse 2: ["And they came into the country of Moab, and CONTINUED there."]{.class-0} What started out as going down to Moab just long enough for the famine to end, ended up being [ten years]{.class-1} (vs. 4).

There is a great spiritual lesson in that, brethren. It is: you always stay longer out of the will of God than you do in the will of God. Elimelech had no intention of living in Moab that long, but that is what happened. Lot never intended to live among the Sodomites; all he wanted to do was pitch ["his tent toward Sodom"]{.class-0} (Gen. 13:12) so he could get in on the good grazing land for his cattle (Gen. 13:10). But by the time he was through, he not only dumped the tent and bought a house in Sodom (Gen. 19:2), he sat in the gate as one of the "town council" (Gen. 19:1, 9). His heart was so planted in Sodom that the angels had to [drag]{.class-1} him out of the city (Gen. 19:16). The old saying is: "Sin will always take you farther than you wanted to go, keep you longer than you wanted to stay, and cost you more than you wanted to pay."

The picture here with Elimelech is that of a Christian who gets out of the will of God because he is hungering after the things of this world. That was Esau's problem. Esau sold his birthright because he was hungry. That birthright was the right of the firstborn to lead the family as a priest with God. Esau traded his communion with God for a bowl of chili.

Elimelech is a picture of a Christian who is in the center of the will of God, in a "house of bread and praise"; that is, he is in a good church where he is getting fed and praising God for His goodness. Then he leaves, intending to come right back, but he doesn't. Christian, when you get backslidden and go back to the old life, it is always harder to get back than it was to leave. It is always harder to go back up a hill than to slide down it.

Elimelech had no business going to Moab. The Moabites were the descendants of the bastard children of Lot by incest (Gen. 19:37). The children of Israel were to leave the land of the Moabites alone when they entered into Canaan (Deut. 2:9), and the Moabites, along with their cousins the Ammonites, were forbidden from being received ["into the congregation of the LORD"]{.class-0} for ten generations (Deut. 23:3).

The reason for that was because Balak, the King of Moab back there in Numbers 22--24, hired Balaam to curse Israel (Deut. 23:4--5). Because of that, God told those Jews, ["Thou shalt not seek their peace nor their prosperity all thy days for ever"]{.class-0} (Deut. 23:6; that command is repeated in Ezra 9:12).

["Peace"]{.class-0} and ["prosperity"]{.class-0}---two of the gods of modern America. Do you know why America and Europe are turning against Israel? They want [peace]{.class-1} (the Moslems to leave them alone), and they want [prosperity]{.class-1} (Saudi, Iraqi, and Iranian oil). Just like Moab, God is not going to give them either one.

The land of Moab was outside the possessions of Israel, on the east side of Jordan. Today, that land is part of the country of Jordan; the inhabitants are [Moslems.]{.class-1} They are [still]{.class-1} the enemies of Israel to this day.

Back to Ruth 1: ["and the name of his two sons Mahlon and Chilion"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). The name ["Mahlon"]{.class-0} means "sickly"; the name ["Chilion"]{.class-0} means "pining" ([pining]{.class-1} is a painful longing for something due to a broken heart). The names of the boys reflect something wrong spiritually in the lives of Elimelech and Naomi. These boys were given these names when they were born. Something was bad wrong in that family. Paul says ["many"]{.class-0} of the believers in Corinth were ["sickly"]{.class-0} because they wouldn't judge sin in their own lives (1 Cor. 11:30--31). Leviticus 26:39 and Ezekiel 24:23, 33:10 speak of the Israelites pining away in their sins and iniquities.

Elimelech didn't just up and decide to move to Moab when the famine hit; that was merely the excuse he used. He had been struggling with some sin for a while before he ever left the house of bread and praise. Bob Jones Sr. said, "Behind every tragedy of human character is a long process of wicked thinking." A Christian never "falls" into sin; that is, he never enters into it accidently, on a lark, at the spur of the moment. He thinks about it, toys with it, and considers whether he can commit it and get away with it. Elimelech had considered leaving Israel long before the famine.

What Elimelech didn't realize was that he had moved to Moab for [the rest of his life.]{.class-1} He only planned to stay a short time, but he ended up [dying there.]{.class-1} Elimelech's move ended up being [permanent,]{.class-1} not temporary.

Now the one with whom God is dealing in this situation is [Naomi.]{.class-1} She is the one who survives this ten-year "sojourn" in Moab, and she is the one who ends up returning to the house of bread and praise. God is dealing with Naomi, but death doesn't phase her. She loses her husband, but she doesn't return to Israel. Her boys marry "unsaved women," which was forbidden under the Law (Deut. 7:3), and she still didn't return. Her two boys die, but she doesn't return even then. It isn't until she hears there is bread back in Bethlehem that she thinks of returning (vs. 6).

You get the idea from this that it was [Naomi's]{.class-1} idea to leave Israel and go to Moab. Naomi is not motivated by anything God said; she is motivated [by her belly.]{.class-1} She is like those "Christians" about whom Paul talked in the New Testament who served ["their own belly"]{.class-0} instead of Jesus Christ (Rom. 16:18) because their ["God is their belly"]{.class-0} (Phil. 3:19).

What the Holy Spirit is showing you here is how tough some backslidden Christians are, especially [the women.]{.class-1} Before I got saved, I didn't fancy myself a real tough fellow, but I could take a beating. After I got saved, though, I lost all my guts when it came to that sort of thing. I don't mean in regards to taking a beating for Christ's sake; I mean in regards to the chastisement of God (Heb. 12:6). After watching Christians for over sixty years now, I have come to the conclusion that I wasn't as tough as I thought I was. Some Christians I know would put me out of business when it comes to being tough. I have seen God take some Christians and whip them and whip them and whip them until they are nearly dead, and they won't get right. Some of those were [women.]{.class-1}

When I pastored over at Brent, there was a young man who injured his neck diving off a railroad trestle. I visited the boy in the hospital, and the mother asked me, "Dr. Ruckman, why did God let that happen to my boy?" I told her, "Maybe he was doing something wrong God had to deal with him about." That shocked her; she said, "You mean God let that happen to punish him?!" I thought to myself, "You stupid woman, that's the first thing I would have thought of." I mean, if I bump my head on a door going through it, I think I must have been thinking something wrong for that to happen. It's a normal thing to think God might be punishing you for something when something bad happens, but not for that woman.

I once visited the hospital in Atlanta, Georgia. There was a lost fellow there who had just gotten out of jail. He had just married a woman and was driving in his car with her when he had a wreck. He had been drunk and had been driving without a license. He hit the back of a truck and went under it. He was thrown out of the car and slid down the highway on his back; his back looked like he had gone through a potato grater. His wife died, and he ended up with one arm broken and the other amputated.

I tried talking to him. He told me, "Get out of here, preacher; I know what you're going to say. You're going to say if I had gotten saved this probably wouldn't have happened." (Preachers back then were a lot plainer than this modern bunch of "seeker sensitives.") I said, "Yeah, that's exactly what I was going to say." He said, "Run on; I'm doing fine." He was in a hospital bed with one arm gone, his other arm elevated in a sling, facing criminal charges, jail time, and a law suit; but he was doing "fine."

He went on and said, "You're like . . . ," and he named some guy down at the plant where he worked. I don't know who that fellow was, but evidently he had been witnessing to this guy and putting it on him pretty regularly. I must have talked to that guy for thirty minutes, and he wouldn't accept Christ. Tough boy! Too tough for his own good.

I told that fellow, "Listen, buddy, if you think you've had a rough time so far, it's just getting started. If God has His eye on you to save you, you haven't seen hell break loose yet until you get out of here." With that, I had prayer with him and left. He never did a thing about what I told him. Some people just won't learn.

I preached once in Mohawk, Tennessee, and I went to visit a teenage kid named Jimmy. I never will forget that kid as long as I live. Jimmy had a saved mother and an unsaved daddy, and that kid lived a wild life before he was even sixteen years old. Like all those hillbillies up in the mountains, he had heard the Gospel all of his life and had turned it down over and over again. He started smoking at twelve and drinking at fifteen. He got to hanging out with the wrong crowd.

One night, he was in a car with his buddy, and they were both drunk. Jimmy was in the passenger seat, and his friend was driving. Jimmy's buddy decided he would show off how quickly he could drag off up the mountain.

As the car Jimmy was in was going up the mountain and rounding a curve at fifty miles an hour, another car was coming down the mountain at about forty miles an hour on that same curve. Neither driver saw the other one coming until it was too late, and both cars were over the center line just a little, cutting that curve. Both drivers had their left arm on the window sill of the door, with their elbows out the window. As those two cars passed each other, the drivers' elbows hit, and the driver of Jimmy's car had his arm torn out of its socket. He ended up bleeding to death.

That kid screamed, "Jimmy, get the wheel! Jimmy, get the wheel!" Jimmy missed the wheel, and the vehicle went off the side of that mountain, rolling over three times. Jimmy lived, but he had a lot of broken bones. The worse injury, though, was his jaw: it had been pulverized. He had to have holes cut in his cheeks, with wires coming down into those holes to hold up what was left of his jaw.

He got out of the hospital after six months. When I went to visit him, he was still wired up, but he could talk a little. He was sitting on the porch by himself, and I talked to him about forty minutes, trying to get him to receive Christ. But some of the hardest people there are to win to the Lord are those country folk back up there in the mountains. Everybody knows everybody else and all their tricks. They get to watching each other too close and figure they are all right because they wouldn't do what the other fellow is doing. That produces a false sense of security that [damns]{.class-1} a person.

That was Jimmy. He was only about sixteen, but I had never met a harder sinner in my life up to that point. I tried everything I could to get him to receive Christ, and he wouldn't do it. It finally got the best of me. I broke down crying.

When I saw I wasn't getting anywhere with him, I knelt down by him and said, "Jimmy, you may die and go to Hell unsaved, but you're not going to Hell unloved. I love your soul and made a trip up here specifically to talk to you about salvation. There's somebody who loves you; I tried. Won't you accept Christ?" That kid said through that wired jaw, "I ain't ready yet."

I left it at that, but I found out later that a year after I had talked with Jimmy, he got well enough to get out and about. He started driving again and had another car wreck. That kid was too tough for his own good, and he wasn't even eighteen years old.

Now Naomi's two boys ended up marrying women from Moab. That's exactly what God commanded them [not]{.class-1} to do.

["Neither shalt thou make marriages with them; thy daughter thou shalt not give unto his son, nor his daughter shalt thou take unto thy son."]{.class-0} Why not? ["For they will turn away thy son from following me, that they may serve other gods: so will the anger of the LORD be kindled against you, and destroy thee suddenly"]{.class-0} (Deut. 7:3--4).

Those Moabites were [idolaters]{.class-1} (1 Kings 11:33). So this is a picture of a Christian marrying an unsaved spouse. God told those Jews that if they married the heathen, they would be led to worship the false gods those heathen served. That was Solomon's problem.

["Did not Solomon king of Israel sin by these things? yet among many nations was there no king like him, who was beloved of his God, and God made him king over all Israel: nevertheless even him did outlandish women]{.class-0} \[i.e., women outside of the land of Israel, women from places like Moab---1 Kings 11:1\][ cause to sin"]{.class-0} (Neh. 13:26).

Mahlon marries Ruth (see 4:10), and Chilion marries a girl named Orpah (an idol worshipper \[vs. 15\] after whom the New-Age, left-wing black woman Oprah Winfrey is named). And you would think that if you were a Christian momma trying to raise two boys right, and both of them married unsaved women because of something you did, that would motivate you to get right. Not Naomi, boy; she's just as tough as steel. Her two boys die, and that's still not enough to get her back to Bethlehem.

6 Then she arose with her daughters in law, that she might return from the country of Moab: for she had heard in the country of Moab how that the LORD had visited his people in giving them bread.

7 Wherefore she went forth out of the place where she was, and her two daughters in law with her; and they went on the way to return unto the land of Judah.

8 And Naomi said unto her two daughters in law, Go, return each to her mother's house: the LORD deal kindly with you, as ye have dealt with the dead, and with me.

9 The LORD grant you that ye may find rest, each of you in the house of her husband. Then she kissed them; and they lifted up their voice, and wept.

10 And they said unto her, Surely we will return with thee unto thy people.

11 And Naomi said, Turn again, my daughters: why will ye go with me? are there yet any more sons in my womb, that they may be your husbands?

12 Turn again, my daughters, go your way; for I am too old to have an husband. If I should say, I have hope, if I should have an husband also to night, and should also bear sons;

13 Would ye tarry for them till they were grown? would ye stay for them from having husbands? nay, my daughters; for it grieveth me much for your sakes that the hand of the LORD is gone out against me.

14 And they lifted up their voice, and wept again: and Orpah kissed her mother in law; but Ruth clave unto her.

Now Naomi gets right. Of course it's a carnal motive for getting right, but God understands we are carnal, materialistic beings. Did you know sometimes God will appeal to a carnal motive in a sinner to get him right? You take the prodigal son; you know why he got right? He was starving and wanted a good meal (Luke 15:17). Didn't you ever read over there in Matthew 22 and Luke 14 where Christ likens the Gospel invitation to an invitation to a [wedding supper]{.class-1} (cf. Rev. 19:9)? Why, that's sex and food: two of the most carnal motivations you have. So if you won't respond to a spiritual motive to get right, God will allow a carnal motive---AS LONG AS YOU GET RIGHT!

Naomi left Moab to return to Judah, and her two daughters-in-law go with her---at least [part]{.class-1} of the way. But the three came to what I call "the parting of the way." Naomi tells the girls, ["Go, return each to her mother's house"]{.class-0} (vs. 8). She tells them to go back to Moab, find a good husband, and settle down; and she wished them both well (["the LORD deal kindly with you, as ye have dealt with the dead, and with me"]{.class-0}---vs. 8). She then kisses them goodbye, and they all have a good cry together (vs. 9).
