Verse 10: ["And they said unto her, Surely we will return with thee unto thy people."]{.class-0} Both girls say they will go back to Bethlehem with Naomi, but only one of them means it. There's an old riddle that goes like this: eight pigeons were sitting on a fence, and three of them decided to fly away; how many of them were left? The answer is [eight.]{.class-1} You say, "What about the ones that flew away?" I didn't say three of them flew away; I said three of them [decided]{.class-1} to fly away. You can make up your mind to do a thing and not follow through on it.

I talked to an old-timer one time and said, "Why don't you get saved?" That "senior citizen" told me, "Well, I'm aiming to, preacher." I said, "Stop aiming and SHOOT!" You can "aim" yourself right into Hell. The old saying is: "The road to Hell is paved with good intentions." You can have the best intentions of getting saved and wind up in the Lake of Fire.

Naomi tests the motives of the two girls, and the test she gives them deals with [marriage.]{.class-1} In verse 9, she tells them to get remarried; then when they say, "We'll go with you," she says, ["are there yet any more sons in my womb, that they may be your husbands?"]{.class-0} (vs. 11). That's not just rhetorical; she's referring to a command in the Mosaic Law that plays an important role in this book.

Deuteronomy 25:5, ["If brethren dwell together, and one of them die, and have no child, the wife of the dead shall not marry without unto a stranger: her husband's brother shall go in unto her, and take her to him to wife, and perform the duty of an husband's brother unto her."]{.class-0}

That is known as the law of the kinsman redeemer. The idea is that since an inheritance was passed down from father to son, to keep the land God gave those Jews in their own family, if a man died and left no children, his brother or nearest of kin was to marry the widow and beget children through her so the inheritance would stay in the family and not transfer to someone else due to the remarriage of the widow who got her husband's property. That went all the way back before the Law; there was a case similar to what Naomi is saying here in verse 11. Judah's firstborn son Er married Tamar, and God killed him before he could beget a child. The next son refused to perform his duty as a brother, and God killed him too. Judah had another son who was too young to marry Tamar, so Judah told Tamar to wait until he was old enough (Gen. 38:11).

The difference here with Naomi is that she has no more sons to give these two women and has no prospects for producing more. And even if she did, were they really willing to wait a minimum of thirteen years (when a Jewish boy is "bar mitzvahed" into a man), when they would be in their thirties or forties, to marry a boy who was barely a man?

Brethren, that Book has some great revelation on how women work and think. The old joke is the book on "What Men Know About Women": you open it up, and it is [completely blank.]{.class-1} But if you want to understand women, get you a Bible; it talks about fourteen different types of women:

1\. A ["strange woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 2:16).

2\. An ["evil woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 6:24).

3\. ["A whorish woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 6:26).

4\. ["A foolish woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 9:13).

5\. ["A gracious woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 11:16).

6\. ["A fair woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 11:22).

7\. ["A wise woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 14:1).

8.[ "A brawling woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 21:9).

9.[ "An angry woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 21:19).

10\. ["A contentious woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 27:15).

11\. ["An adulterous woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 30:20).

12.[ "An odious woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 30:23).

13\. ["A virtuous woman"]{.class-0} (Prov. 31:10, 12:4).

14\. And a unique woman in Scriptures---["a great woman"]{.class-0} (2 Kings 4:8).

When Naomi puts the test of marriage to Orpah, Orpah backs off when she sees the odds. Naomi knows what the girls want: to get married and have children, like any normal woman would. Orpah sees that Naomi can't present her with any "prospects" for marriage, so she goes back home.

At a meeting up in Maryland, one time, I was invited to this one lady's house. She was in her forties, with three kids, all of them saved. I said to her, "Your husband tells me you didn't get married until you were in your thirties. Why did you wait that long?" She was attractive; she wouldn't have had any problem getting a man.

She told me, "Bro. Ruckman, I was saved as I came through high school and went to College for a couple of years. I watched my classmates all in a rush to get married at eighteen. I watched friend after friend of mine get married at seventeen, eighteen, and nineteen; and their families got busted up in less than five years. I made up my mind and told the Lord, 'If I have to live and die an old maid, I am not going to marry a bum for a husband. If you can't give me a good Christian husband who is going to love me and take care of me, I'm just going to stay single.' I waited on God, and at thirty, I got me a good one."

That woman was right, but that's not your typical American woman. Society and the media say, "Hurry up! Hurry up! Hurry up!" The whole system revolves around [money]{.class-1} (1 Tim. 6:10): get involved with sex as soon as possible so the schools can get funding for sex education, Planned Parenthood can get money for abortions, and businesses can sell you the baby clothes, the diapers, the bottles, the baby food, the crib, the toys, etc., if you decide to have the baby. And if the whole thing busts to pieces, the lawyers are waiting to get your money for the divorce. You'd do better to wait like that Christian woman did.

"Here lies the bones of Mary Jones.

For her life had no terrors.

She lived an old maid; she died an old maid.

No hits, no runs, no errors."

There's nothing wrong with being an old maid. I'd rather my daughters be old maids than have some of the sons-in-law I have seen.

Now back in verse 9, they wept because Naomi kissed them goodbye. In verse 14, they cry again, but the reasons are different between Ruth and Orpah. In verse 14, Orpah kisses her mother-in-law goodbye. She's crying because she is planning to leave, and she won't see her mother-in-law again. Ruth, though, is crying because she doesn't want her mother-in-law to send her away; she is the one who is serious about going with Naomi.

Orpah [kissed]{.class-1} her mother-in-law. There are different types of kisses. There is a [carnal]{.class-1} kiss between lovers. Paul talks about the ["holy kiss"]{.class-0} with which Christian brethren greeted one another (Rom. 16:16; 1 Cor. 16:20; 2 Cor. 13:21; 1 Thess. 5:26). There is a [familial]{.class-1} kiss between relatives. Then there is the [submissive]{.class-1} kiss the rulers of this earth will give Christ when He reigns on earth during the Millennium (Psa. 2:12). The kiss here is a [hypocritical]{.class-1} kiss, like Judas gave to Christ in the Garden of Gethsemane; it's a kiss given with ulterior motives in mind. Orpah is crying "crocodile tears"; she doesn't mean anything by them. She says she'll stay while the whole time she means to leave.

Have you ever met "Orpah"? I have. I know "Orpah." "Orpah" has a husband who never makes anything less than \$150,000 a year. "Orpah" has a big stack of [National Geographic]{.class-1} magazines, [Wall Street Journals,]{.class-1} and [Forbes]{.class-1} magazines, and underneath them somewhere, hidden out of sight, are [True Love, True Romance, True Detective]{.class-1}---that kind of mess. That's "Orpah."

Have you ever met "Orpah"? She reads a bunch of Liberal junk like [The Robe, The Big Fisherman, The Greatest Story Ever Told,]{.class-1} etc. I know "Orpah" because I was raised around her. I know I don't preach like it because I "cut my teeth" preaching in the hills of North Carolina, but I was raised Episcopalian.

"Orpah" may read [The Big Fisherman,]{.class-1} but she never says what the "big fisherman" said. He said, ["Lord, to whom shall we go? thou hast the words of eternal life"]{.class-0} (John 6:68). She reads [The Robe]{.class-1} but never gets close enough to Jesus Christ to ["touch the hem of his garment"]{.class-0} (Matt. 14:36, 9:20).

I know "Orpah": finest of feeling but has worldly friends, anxious to do right but would rob God as quick as look at Him, perfect manners but glares at the pastor, smiling and cheerful but leads her husband around like a poodle on a string. That's "Orpah": the right fork in the right place with the right spoon, but she'll curse a street preacher as she drives by him. She would call "Ruckman" "rude" and "uncouth," but she would pay money to go watch David commit adultery with Bathsheba in a movie theater. I know "Orpah"; I've got her number. She may fool some of you, but she's not going to put one over on me. [I know "Orpah."]{.class-1}

15 And she said, Behold, thy sister in law is gone back unto her people, and unto her gods: return thou after thy sister in law.

16 And Ruth said, Intreat me not to leave thee, or to return from following after thee: for whither thou goest, I will go; and where thou lodgest, I will lodge: thy people shall be my people, and thy God my God:

17 Where thou diest, will I die, and there will I be buried: the LORD do so to me, and more also, if ought but death part thee and me.

18 When she saw that she was stedfastly minded to go with her, then she left speaking unto her.

["Thy sister in law is gone back unto her people, and ]{.class-0}\[get it!\][ UNTO HER GODS"]{.class-0} (vs. 15). Historically, those are idols like ["Chemosh"]{.class-0} (1 Kings 11:33) and ["Baal-peor"]{.class-0} (Num. 25:1--3), but do you know what Orpah's god was [in her heart?]{.class-1} It was[ a husband]{.class-1}---that was the test Naomi gave her back in verses 9--13.

Do you know why Orpah went back to her people and to her gods? Because she would have [rather]{.class-1} gone back than stay with Naomi. People do what they would [rather]{.class-1} do. A person may say, "I would rather not be in church tonight," but he goes anyway because he would rather go to church than pay the consequences for not going.

The old-time Methodist evangelist Sam Jones said, "If I could get your 'druthers' fixed, I'd get you fixed." ["Druthers"]{.class-1} is a Southern term: it is the word [would]{.class-1} and [rather]{.class-1} slurred together. David said, ["I had rather be a doorkeeper in the house of my God, than to dwell in the tents of wickedness"]{.class-0} (Psa. 84:10). If that be the case, he will end up ["a doorkeeper"]{.class-0} (Ezek. 44:1--3, 46:2, 8--10). If you would rather watch the "glass toilet" (the TV) than read the Bible, you will spend time watching the boobtube. If I could get you where you would rather spend time in prayer than spend time in gossip, you will spend time in prayer. The trick is the[ rather.]{.class-1}

You can't always tell who's a Christian and who's not until the person is presented with a choice, and then you will find out what he would rather do. When I used to preach revivals up north in the winter, especially in Kentucky, Ohio, and Indiana, I would always notice a decline in attendance for the meeting on Friday nights. That's because of the Friday night basketball games at the local high schools. Those young people and their parents would rather be at the basketball game than at the revival meeting.

Look, here are two men walking down the sidewalk. Behind them walks a dog, and the dog belongs to one of those two men. How do you know to which of those men the dog belongs? Well, as long as those two men are walking side by side together, you don't, but when one fellow goes one way and the other fellow goes another, [the dog will follow its master.]{.class-1} That's the parting of the way. Those kids who choose the basketball game over the preaching of the word of God are following their master.

Now Orpah returns to her gods. What does Ruth do? She cleaves to her mother-in-law (vs. 14). Why? Verse 16: ["thy people shall be my people, and THY GOD MY GOD."]{.class-0} Ruth is not following Naomi to get a husband, although that is exactly what she gets; she follows Naomi because she knows [Naomi has the right God.]{.class-1} Ruth is "converting."

Verses 16--17 are often used in a Christian marriage ceremony, and that's a nice sentiment. The wife is to follow her husband and not leave him "till death do us part." But, of course, that is not about what the verses are talking at all. A young lady should be a Christian way before a Christian young man asks her to marry him (2 Cor. 6:14--16). And if the husband decides to backslide or apostatize, is the wife to follow him in that? And let's just face it, sister, you may or may not be buried with your husband. Mary Livingstone wasn't buried with her husband in Westminster Abbey. None of Adoniram Judson's three wives are buried with him; he died and was buried at sea.

Ruth's plea in verses 16--17 is the conversion of a pagan to the Lord God. She is giving up her status as a Moabite to become a Jew. Her land now is the Promised Land, not Moab.

That's Old Testament conversion of a Gentile, but it still is a wonderful picture of New Testament salvation. When you get saved, you "cleave" to Jesus Christ (Gen. 2:24; Mark 10:7 cf. Eph. 5:31). You begin to follow Him (Eph. 5:1--2). You "lodge" with Him (Eph. 2:6). You become part of a new "people" because you have a new God (2 Cor. 6:16; Phil. 3:20). As born-again children of God, we are not only dead and buried with our Saviour, we are [risen]{.class-1} with Him as well (Rom. 6:3--4). And better than Ruth, nothing can part us from our Lord, not even physical death (Rom. 8:38--39; 2 Cor. 5:8).

Ruth goes with Naomi and ends up in the line of Christ. She is eternally enshrined in the pages of Scripture (Psa. 119:89; Matt. 24:35; 1 Pet. 1:25). And Orpah?

Orpah goes back to the old crowd. She is greeted with: "How are you doing, Orpah? It's so good to see you, Orpah. We thought you were going to get mixed up with that 'white horse' religion. We're having a cotillion this year, and there are a number of eligible bachelors that will be there. We are so glad you came to your senses, honey."

Orpah married some rich guy, and they ended up getting a divorce. She married another one, and they got divorced. Then she married a third one, and they got divorced. She got alimony from all three of them, so she was "set" for life in her bank account. She got up in years and died in the best hospital for which her money could pay, under anesthetics. AND SHE WOKE UP IN HELL! That's what happened to Orpah.

The great lessons from this passage are:

1\. [Decisions divide domiciles.]{.class-1} When you decide to get saved and live for God, it will sometimes [break up a family.]{.class-1} Jesus said, ["If any man come to me, and hate not his father, and mother, and wife, and children, and brethren, and sisters, yea, and his own life also, he cannot be my disciple"]{.class-0} (Luke 14:26). That's not hatred in the sense of you can't stand them; that's hatred in comparison. You are to love Christ [more]{.class-1} than you love your family (Matt. 10:37).

When you follow Christ over the wishes of your loved ones, that causes division. Jesus said, ["Think not that I am come to send peace on earth; I came not to send peace, but a sword. For I am come to set a man at variance against his father, and the daughter against her mother, AND THE DAUGHTER IN LAW AGAINST HER MOTHER IN LAW]{.class-0} \[as in the case of Orpah\][. And a man's foes shall be they of his own household"]{.class-0} (Matt. 10:34--35).

When I got saved, I saw my momma and daddy drop off me like I was a stranger and not even in the family. When it came to a choice between what was in that Book and my family, I have had one boy and two girls drop off to where there could be no reconciliation. I still love them, of course; and I forgive them, of course. But when it comes to fellowship, I wouldn't phone them up on a rainy day. Why? [Because they're going the wrong way;]{.class-1} I'm going the [other way.]{.class-1} The problem with American Christianity is that it is not taught to put Christ FIRST---above momma, daddy, the wife, and the kids.

2\. [Your supreme affection determines all the decisions you make in life.]{.class-1} Eventually, every decision you make, at any time, anywhere, will be based on what you [love the most.]{.class-1} It will determine where you live, where you go to school, with whom you hang around, whom you marry, what kind of clothes you wear, the kind of music to which you listen---EVERYTHING. Whatever is [first]{.class-1} in your life will guide you.

That's where "the fur hits the fan." That is what prevents a lost man from getting saved. He doesn't love God Almighty above everything else, and he can't and won't make God Almighty his supreme affection. Christians have a hard enough time doing it; how much less the unsaved.

There used to be a great personal worker in this country named Walter Wilson; he was a medical doctor. When Dr. Wilson was a young boy around twelve, he had a chance to work for "Buffalo Bill" Cody and his Wild West Show. The big finale to that circus was when Buffalo Bill would bring out his horse and have it get on its knees and drink water out of his hat.

Walter Wilson witnessed to Buffalo Bill and tried to lead him to Christ, but Buffalo Bill would have none of it. Wilson asked him, "Wouldn't you like to go Heaven when you die, Mr. Cody?" Buffalo Bill said, "No! When I go out there in front of that crowd of people and fill my hat with water and have my horse kneel and drink water out of my hat, and that crowd explodes in applause, [that's all the 'Heaven' I want.]{.class-1}"

And that is all the "Heaven" Bill Cody got. Walter Wilson asked him, "Then you won't accept Jesus Christ as your Saviour?" Old Buffalo Bill said, "I WILL NOT!" And unless something happened before he died, he ended up in [Hell.]{.class-1} Why? Because he rejected Jesus Christ based on what he loved the most---the adulation of the crowds.

Orpah loved her people and her gods, so that's where she went. She ended up in Hell because she didn't love Jehovah enough to leave her family and religion behind. Ruth loved Naomi and Naomi's God, so she traveled to a land that wasn't her own, lived among strangers, worked as a "sharecropper" out gleaning in the fields, AND ENDED UP IN THE LINE OF JESUS CHRIST!

19 So they two went until they came to Bethlehem. And it came to pass, when they were come to Bethlehem, that all the city was moved about them, and they said, Is this Naomi?

20 And she said unto them, Call me not Naomi, call me Mara: for the Almighty hath dealt very bitterly with me.

21 I went out full, and the LORD hath brought me home again empty: why then call ye me Naomi, seeing the LORD hath testified against me, and the Almighty hath afflicted me?

22 So Naomi returned, and Ruth the Moabitess, her daughter in law, with her, which returned out of the country of Moab: and they came to Bethlehem in the beginning of barley harvest.

Back Naomi comes to Bethlehem with her daughter-in-law, and the people barely recognize her: ["Is this Naomi?"]{.class-0} (vs. 19). Well, she had been gone ten years, but even so, the years had not been kind to her.

Naomi says, ["Call me not Naomi"]{.class-0} (vs. 20); the name means "pleasant." ["Call me Mara."]{.class-0} Why? ["For the Almighty hath dealt very BITTERLY with me."]{.class-0} The name [Mara]{.class-1} means "bitter" (cf. Exod. 15:23).

["I went out full"]{.class-0} (vs. 21)---she had a husband and two sons when she left. ["And the LORD hath brought me home again empty."]{.class-0} This is the [third time]{.class-1} Naomi attributes her trouble in Moab to [the Lord.]{.class-1} Back in verse 13, she said, ["the hand of the LORD is gone out against me."]{.class-0} In verse 20, she said, ["the Almighty hath dealt very bitterly with me."]{.class-0} She'll do it a [fourth and fifth time]{.class-1} here in verse 21: ["the LORD hath testified against me, and the Almighty hath afflicted me."]{.class-0} You see that reference to the hand of the Lord being against her in verse 13? That makes her a picture of Israel in apostasy in the book of Judges (see our comments under Judg. 2:15).

Modern American Christians don't like to think God would do anything bad to a people for their rebellion. There are Christian leaders and Bible teachers who are [pro-Israel, premillennial,]{.class-1} and believe in a pre-Tribulational Rapture of the Body of Christ who say God had nothing to do with Hitler's Holocaust. He didn't?! Why, He did with every heathen nation that invaded in the book of Judges. He did with Shalmaneser in 2 Kings 17:3 (Isa. 10:5--6). He did with Nebuchadnezzar (Jer. 25:9). He did with Titus in A.D. 70 (Isa. 5:5 cf. Matt. 21:33--41). What makes you think God stopped whipping His chosen people just because the Canon of the Scripture closed? If you want to know how God treats those Jews for rebelling against Him and His Messiah, read Deuteronomy 28:63--68 and note especially verse 63 in that passage. That wasn't relegated to the times the Scriptures were being written; that stretches all the way to the Tribulation (Hos. 12:2 cf. Jer. 30:7).

That Bible teaches that the bad things that happen to us [come from God]{.class-1} (Lam. 3:38; Job 2:10; Isa. 45:7; Amos 3:6). If it is not in punishment for some wickedness that has been committed against God, then it is to reveal and correct some character flaw in a person, as in the case of Job. Even then, one cannot rule out some divine purpose God may have. When Jim Elliot, Nate Saint, and those other three missionaries were killed by the Auca Indians, God used that to save a lot of folk who read of those martyrs' dedication to Christ and to call a lot more than just five missionaries to the mission field. Atheists and agnostics can't understand that; that's why they reject God, the Bible, and Jesus Christ. They judge the Lord by their own limited understanding.

According to that Book, brethren, famine [comes from God,]{.class-1} drought [comes from God,]{.class-1} floods [come from God, ]{.class-1}disease[ comes from God,]{.class-1} natural disasters[ come from God]{.class-1} (hurricanes, tornadoes, earthquakes, wild fires, volcanoes, electrical storms, etc.). Don't believe me? Read Amos 4:6--11. Don't sit there and blink like an owl; open up your Bible and READ THE PASSAGE! You didn't do it, did you? You're going to go right on with the blather that ["God is love"]{.class-0} and would never do that to anyone, and REJECT WHAT GOD SAYS. Naomi wasn't that stupid.

Back to Ruth 1: ["and they came to Bethlehem in the beginning of barley harvest"]{.class-0} (vs. 22). In the Holy Land, ["the beginning of barley harvest"]{.class-0} is from late March in the lowlands to early May in higher elevations. The reason this is mentioned is that Naomi and Ruth came back to Bethlehem "flat broke." They had no money, no job, and no food.

As we will learn in chapter 2, God's "welfare program" for the poor was [work.]{.class-1} God made allowance for anyone who was poor to get enough food to eat by going out and "gleaning" in the fields of others, and we will cover the Deuteronomic law on that in the next chapter. Suffice it here to say that those Jews weren't allowed to sit around on their dead cans and collect food stamps. The command in that Book is if a man (or woman) won't work, he is not to eat (see 2 Thess. 3:10).

[]{#section-0_1_6c833ff1bbb8d647_70a2.xhtml}

Chapter 2

2:1 And Naomi had a kinsman of her husband's, a mighty man of wealth, of the family of Elimelech; and his name was Boaz.

2 And Ruth the Moabitess said unto Naomi, Let me now go to the field, and glean ears of corn after him in whose sight I shall find grace. And she said unto her, Go, my daughter.

3 And she went, and came, and gleaned in the field after the reapers: and her hap was to light on a part of the field belonging unto Boaz, who was of the kindred of Elimelech.

The real "hero" of the book of Ruth is introduced here: his name is Boaz. The Hebrew scholars vary as to the meaning of the name. Some say it means "swift" ("quickness," "fleetness"). Easton's Bible Dictionary is a little more specific in this regard. He says it means "alacrity"; that is, "a quick and cheerful readiness to do something."

But [Boaz]{.class-1} is not only the name of a person; it is the name of one of the two pillars at the entrance to Solomon's Temple: Boaz and Jachin. In that context, most of the expositors will say [Boaz]{.class-1} means "in strength." [Jachin]{.class-1} means "established," so the idea of the two pillars was that the Lord's house was established in strength.

Now, in the book of Ruth, Boaz is a picture of Jesus Christ, and either meaning of Boaz's name could picture the Lord Jesus Christ. In Psalm 40:8, David, speaking for Jesus Christ prophetically (see Heb. 10:9--10), says, ["I delight to do thy will, O my God."]{.class-0} That's "alacrity."

But also, over and over again in the Psalms, David calls God ["my strength"]{.class-0} (Psa. 18:1--2, 22:19, 28:7, 31:4, 43:2, 59:17, 62:7, 119:14, 144:1; see also Isa. 12:2, 49:5; Jer. 16:19; Hab. 3:19). There are two passages that stand out when it comes to Jesus Christ being the strength of the believer. The first is Psalm 19:14 where the Redeemer is the strength: ["O LORD, my strength, and my redeemer."]{.class-0} The second is Psalm 28:8 where ["the LORD . . . is the saving strength of his anointed"]{.class-0} (Christ, the Messiah). So either meaning of the word Boaz can refer, in type, to the Lord Jesus Christ.

Boaz was ["of the family of Elimelech"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). That could refer to Elimelech's "extended" family (i.e., brothers, uncles, and cousins), or it could refer to the "families" into which the tribes of Israel were divided. Judah was divided into the ["families"]{.class-0} of his three sons: Shelah, Pharez, and Zerah (Num. 26:20). Elimelech and Boaz would belong to ["the family of the Pharzites"]{.class-0} (cf. Ruth 4:18). The family of Pharez was further subdivided into his sons: Hezron and Hamul (Num. 26:21). Elimelech and Boaz were in Hezron's family (Ruth 4:18--19).

Verse 1 here in Ruth 2 says Boaz was ["a mighty man of wealth."]{.class-0} That is a type of Christ. ["The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} was manifested in the fact that ["though he was RICH, yet for your sakes he became poor, that ye through his poverty might be rich"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 8:9). Paul preached ["the unsearchable riches of Christ"]{.class-0} to the Gentiles (Eph. 3:8). The riches of God's grace are ["through Christ Jesus"]{.class-0} (Eph. 2:7), and God supplies our need ["according to his riches in glory by Christ Jesus"]{.class-0} (Phil. 4:19).

But one should not lose the practical implications of the verse. Elimelech and Boaz were in the same family. When the famine hit, Elimelech left the house of bread and praising God to live with God's enemies, and [he lost everything.]{.class-1} Boaz trusted God and rode out the famine in the house of bread and praising God, and as a result, God made him ["a mighty man of wealth."]{.class-0}

That was the situation of Lot and Abraham. Lot chose the well watered plains of Sodom to raise cattle (Gen. 13:10), but he ended up losing everything he had except his salvation (2 Pet. 2:7--8). Abraham, on the other hand, took what Lot didn't want and ended up inheriting [the whole world]{.class-1} (Rom. 4:13). The lesson given by Christ from that account is found in Luke 17:33.

["Whosoever shall seek to save his life shall lose it; and whosoever shall lose his life]{.class-0} \[Christ added ["for my sake"]{.class-0} at this point in Luke 9:24\][ shall preserve it."]{.class-0}

Not only is that the case with Boaz; it is the case with Ruth. Ruth gives up everything in Moab to come live in poverty in Bethlehem, worshiping the true God, and she ends up marrying the richest guy in town.

Back to Ruth 2: ["And Ruth the Moabitess said unto Naomi, Let me now go to the field, and glean ears of corn"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). Notice the use of the word ["corn."]{.class-0} You know it is not corn as we know it (called "maize" by the American Indians) because you were just told in 1:22 that it was ["the beginning of BARLEY harvest."]{.class-0} The Bible, being well able to define its own terms (1 Cor. 2:13), tells you what ["corn"]{.class-0} is in John 12:24.[ "A corn of wheat"]{.class-0} is a [kernel]{.class-1} of wheat. You can have ["a corn of wheat,"]{.class-0} a corn of oat, a corn of rye, a corn of barley (here in 2:2), or a corn of corn. ["Corn,"]{.class-0} in the Bible, can be the kernel of [any]{.class-1} grain. The "ear" of any grain is the "spike" (in the case of maize corn, the cob) to which the kernels are attached.

Now, as I said at the end of chapter 1, God's "welfare program" for those Jews was [work.]{.class-1} If a Jew didn't have money to buy food, he (or in this case, she) could go to someone's field during harvest and pick up the grain left over from the main harvest. The Jewish landowners were commanded by God in the Law to leave the corners of their fields for the poor to glean (Lev. 19:9); they were commanded not to glean their fields themselves but to leave that task for the poor so they would have food (Lev. 23:22); and they were commanded to leave anything they forgot in their harvest for the poor to glean (Deut. 24:9). Under normal circumstances (and we understand that famine and drought were exceptional circumstances), there was no reason for any Jew under the Mosaic Law to starve to death unless he was [lazy]{.class-1} (Prov. 19:24, 26:15) or handicapped in some way (like Mephibosheth---2 Sam. 4:4 cf. 2 Sam. 9:10).

["Let me now go to the field, and glean ears of corn after him in whose sight I shall find grace."]{.class-0} Grace---unmerited favor. In other words, she felt she didn't deserve the benefits of the Mosaic Law because she was a ["Moabitess,"]{.class-0} although the law on gleaning was specifically given for ["the stranger"]{.class-0} (Lev. 23:22; Deut. 24:19). That is our case (and I included myself here) as Gentiles who once were unsaved and ["strangers from the covenants of promise, having no hope, and without God in the world"]{.class-0} (Eph. 2:12). But that is exactly to whom the grace of God through His Son was offered (Eph. 2:7--11). We didn't deserve God's saving grace, but God offers it to us anyway and gives us the faith, as a free gift, to take advantage of that grace (see our comments on Eph. 2:8 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Galatians, Ephesians, Philippians, Colossians]{.class-1}).

["And she said unto her, Go, my daughter."]{.class-0} Notice how the term ["daughter"]{.class-0} in the Scriptures can be used of a [daughter-in-law.]{.class-1} You need to remember that when you hear some educated ass (and I say that with apologies to every four-legged critter out in the pasture) talk about "contradictions" and "mistakes" in the Bible. A person can be a "son" (or a daughter, in this case) without being a literal son. In the Scriptures, a "son" can refer to a son-in-law (like David---1 Sam. 24:16 cf. 1 Sam. 18:21), an adopted or foster son (like Christ---Luke 3:23), or a descendant or successor in a line (Matt. 1:1). There is no contradiction in the Scriptures just because a person won't [believe]{.class-1} what he reads.

Now Ruth wasn't "targeting" anyone when she went out to glean. She wasn't looking for the richest man in Bethlehem in order to catch her a husband. The Bible says it was ["her hap . . . to light on a part of the field belonging unto Boaz, who was of the kindred of Elimelech"]{.class-0} (vs. 3).

The word ["hap"]{.class-0} is archaic English meaning "happenstance," "chance," or "fortune." The text is saying that she just [happened]{.class-1} to pick the field of Boaz in which to glean. She had no idea that he was "available" or that he was rich, and she didn't know that he was related to her late father-in-law. It is doubtful if she even knew exactly in whose field she was.

But as I said in the Introduction, our ["hap"]{.class-0} is [God's map.]{.class-1} This is God leading Ruth in His gracious providence. He knows what Ruth doesn't, and He is directing Ruth's circumstances for her good and His divine purpose (Rom. 8:28).

4 And, behold, Boaz came from Bethlehem, and said unto the reapers, The LORD be with you. And they answered him, The LORD bless thee.

5 Then said Boaz unto his servant that was set over the reapers, Whose damsel is this?

6 And the servant that was set over the reapers answered and said, It is the Moabitish damsel that came back with Naomi out of the country of Moab:

7 And she said, I pray you, let me glean and gather after the reapers among the sheaves: so she came, and hath continued even from the morning until now, that she tarried a little in the house.

Look at verse 4: ["The LORD be with you"]{.class-0}; ["The LORD bless thee."]{.class-0} That would make the ACLU have a "conniption" if a business owner did that today. This country was once so immersed in Scripture that it had it engraved on its monuments and required its teaching in its schools. But with the perversion of the doctrine of "separation of Church and State" (i.e., reading the Bible and prayer in State-run institutions is considered a "Church" and "establishing a religion"), the atheists and agnostics want all recognition of God expunged from society.

Where that leads is to the State telling the churches what they can and can't preach like the Communists did in places like Bulgaria. Haralan Popov said the Communists started out by allowing the preachers to say God was good, but they couldn't say the Devil was bad. It ended up with no preacher being able to say anything without the permission of the atheistic Communist government.

You are seeing that take place now in the United States. In places like New Jersey, no preacher can tell a teenager who is practicing sex perversion and wants to stop it that God can and will deliver him or her from that sin (see 1 Cor. 6:9--11). In Houston, Texas, the dyke Mayor of that city demanded, in a law suit, that the pastors who didn't want sex perverts around their daughters and wives in public restrooms to turn over all their sermons and private correspondence for review. That is completely against everything in the First Amendment of the Bill of Rights to the Constitution.

How much smarter people were 3,000 years ago. The Germans used to have a saying: "Everything depends on God's blessing." If the Lord isn't with you and doesn't bless you in your endeavors, you are doomed to [failure.]{.class-1} The fact that the majority of the people in this country no longer believe that is just proof that you are living in an [apostate dump.]{.class-1}

Now Ruth catches Boaz's eye, and he asks the foreman of the harvest, ["Whose damsel is this?"]{.class-0} (vs. 5). It's not a case of Ruth being "attractive"; the Bible doesn't say anything about Ruth being ["fair to look upon"]{.class-0} (see Gen. 12:11, 26:7; Esth. 1:11, 2:7). Undoubtedly, Ruth stands out because of her [race.]{.class-1} The Moabites were from the Egyptian wife of Lot (whom he got when Abram went down to Egypt in Gen. 12) by his daughter (Gen. 19:36--37), and the Egyptians were [Hamites]{.class-1} (Gen. 10:6 cf. Psa. 105:23, 27, 106:22). Ruth would be what we used to call a "quadroon": someone who is a quarter African. Ruth has a little "color" to her.

Boaz discovers three things about Ruth in verses 6--7. In verse 6, he learns that Ruth is a [loyal]{.class-1} woman: Ruth was loyal to her mother-in-law and left her homeland to be with her. In verse 7, he is told that she is [polite:]{.class-1} she [asked]{.class-1} to glean in Boaz's field; she didn't "demand her rights." Also in verse 7, he can see that she is a [hard worker:]{.class-1} she came to work early (["from the morning"]{.class-0}) and only took a [short]{.class-1} break (["tarried A LITTLE in the house"]{.class-0} ). Ruth is what is called "self-motivated." She decides on her own to go out and glean, and she works without having to be told what to do or be overseen by a "boss."

8 Then said Boaz unto Ruth, Hearest thou not, my daughter? Go not to glean in another field, neither go from hence, but abide here fast by my maidens:

9 Let thine eyes be on the field that they do reap, and go thou after them: have I not charged the young men that they shall not touch thee? and when thou art athirst, go unto the vessels, and drink of that which the young men have drawn.

10 Then she fell on her face, and bowed herself to the ground, and said unto him, Why have I found grace in thine eyes, that thou shouldest take knowledge of me, seeing I am a stranger?

11 And Boaz answered and said unto her, It hath fully been shewed me, all that thou hast done unto thy mother in law since the death of thine husband: and how thou hast left thy father and thy mother, and the land of thy nativity, and art come unto a people which thou knewest not heretofore.

12 The LORD recompense thy work, and a full reward be given thee of the LORD God of Israel, under whose wings thou art come to trust.

["Hearest thou not, my daughter?"]{.class-0} (vs. 8). Here's another use of the word [daughter.]{.class-1} It's a reference to the fact that Boaz had decided to take her "under his wing" and take care of her. In the Old Testament, a leader would refer to a follower under his care as a son or daughter (see Josh. 7:19), and a follower would refer to his leader as a father (see 2 Kings 5:13). This practice was abused by the Pharisees and Sadducees (following the example of pagan religious leaders---see our comments under Judg. 17:10), and so Christ strictly forbids calling any religious leader ["father"]{.class-0} (Matt. 23:9).

["Go not to glean in another field"]{.class-0}---a picture of the Bride of Christ (see our comments on Song of Sol. 1:7--8 in that Commentary). Boaz is telling Ruth, "Don't go begging from field to field to glean there. Stay here, and I'll take care of you and treat you right."

["Abide here fast by my maidens."]{.class-0} The word ["fast"]{.class-0} here means "firmly fixed," "attached"; it's where we get our word [fastened.]{.class-1} Boaz is telling Ruth to stick right beside the young women working his field. In the Middle East during a harvest, the women had certain duties in the field separate from the men. According to verse 9, the women were doing the actual reaping. The men probably bound the grain into sheaves to be transported to the threshingfloor.

Ruth was allowed to follow the women as they reaped and pick up whatever she could, and ["the young men"]{.class-0} weren't allowed to stop her or throw her out of the field (vs. 9). Moreover, there was water drawn and in vessels for the workers which Ruth was allowed to drink, even though she wasn't on the "pay roll."

Naturally, Ruth wants to know why she is getting such favors: ["Why have I found grace in thine eyes, that thou shouldest take knowledge of me, seeing I am a stranger?"]{.class-0} (vs. 10). After all, she is a woman "of color" and not an Israelite, so why is Boaz paying so much attention to her?

The answer is so atypical of what the average American would think in a situation like this. [It has nothing to do with sex.]{.class-1} Boaz isn't trying to "make time" with Ruth. He respects how she treated her mother-in-law---A JEW!

That was the standard for a Jew judging a Gentile in the Old Testament. God told Abraham, ["I will bless them that bless thee, and curse him that curseth thee"]{.class-0} (Gen. 12:3). That promise wasn't just to Abraham personally; it was extended to his descendants through Isaac and Jacob (Gen. 27:29; Num. 24:9)---NOT Ishmael and Esau.

When the Centurion came to Christ wanting Him to heal his servant, the Jews told Jesus that the Centurion ["was worthy"]{.class-0} for Christ to help (Luke 7:4). Why? ["For he loveth our nation, and he hath built us a synagogue"]{.class-0} (Luke 7:5). That Roman had blessed the nation of Israel, so those Jews expected God to keep His promise and bless that Roman.

When Jesus Christ judges the nations at His Second Advent, the basis of judgment has nothing to do with the faith of those Gentiles or Christ's blood atonement for sins at all. ["The King"]{.class-0} tells them, ["Inasmuch as ye have DONE IT]{.class-0} \[[works!]{.class-1}\] [unto the least of these MY BRETHREN, ye have done it unto me"]{.class-0} (Matt. 25:40). Who are His ["brethren"]{.class-0}? Well, they aren't "Christians"; there aren't any "Christians" in Matthew 25 or even in the book of Matthew. "Christians" don't show up until Acts 11:26. The ["brethren,"]{.class-0} in Matthew, are [Jews ]{.class-1}who believe on Jesus as the Messiah (see Matt. 28:10, 23:8, 20:24, 12:46--49).

The ["sheep"]{.class-0} of Matthew 25:32 are a different bunch than the ["brethren."]{.class-0} Christ judges those Gentiles in Matthew 25 based on how they treated those Jews in the Tribulation. He blesses with eternal life the ones who helped those Jews against the Antichrist (Matt. 25:46), and He curses with eternal damnation the ones who ignore the Jews' cry for help (Matt. 25:46, 41).

That being the case, you can write America off. One of the things that made this country great was that it blessed those Jews. George Washington welcomed them into this country when the nations of Europe didn't want anything to do with them. I'll grant you there were some pretty "bumpy" spots in our history where anti-Semitism cropped up in the big cities with the European immigrants, the KKK, and Roosevelt turning a bunch of them away before WWII, and what not; but over all, America welcomed that Jew and took care of him. When the time came for God to restore Israel, He used American troops to liberate the Jews from Hitler's concentration camps and an American President (Harry S. Truman) to shove the resolution to create the State of Israel through the UN.

But with the big push by Clinton, Bush, and Obama to turn the land of Israel over to a bunch of Arab Moslems (erroneously called the "Palestinian State" by the news media; there never has been any "Palestinian State" in 6,000 years of human history), you can kiss the United States good-bye. God is going to curse this nation for cursing His people just as much as He blessed it when it blessed them.

The doctrinal meaning notwithstanding, there is also a wonderful picture of God visiting the Gentiles in this age. Jesus said, ["salvation is OF THE JEWS"]{.class-0} (John 4:22). It doesn't matter who does the witnessing or preaching, the Gentile in this dispensation still learns about the true God---the God of [Israel]{.class-1}---through the [Jew.]{.class-1} ["The oracles of God"]{.class-0} were given to that [Jew]{.class-1} (Rom. 3:1--2), and I don't mean ["the Israel of God"]{.class-0} (Gal. 6:16). No Roman Catholic ever wrote one line of Scripture in either Testament.

Ruth, a Gentile, is receiving the blessing through the [Jews.]{.class-1} Ruth left her homeland to go with the Jews, and Boaz is blessing her for it. But it is much more than that. Look at verse 12.

"The LORD recompense thy work, and a full reward be given thee of the LORD God of Israel, under whose wings thou art come to trust."

That's the verse I give whenever I sign a woman's Bible. In other words, it will not just be Boaz who will bless Ruth for what she's done; God Himself will fulfill the promise He made in Genesis 12:3.[ "The LORD recompense thy work"]{.class-0}---He'll pay you back. The old saying is that you can't outgive God because the Lord will not be a debtor to any man (see Rom. 11:35).

Now that's the Old Testament. The idea is that if you do right, God will pay you back here and now in this life. You will find David talking that way (2 Sam. 22:21, 25; Psa. 18:20, 24). Proverbs 11:31 says, ["Behold, the righteous shall be recompensed IN THE EARTH."]{.class-0} That is why the Jews in the Gospels thought the Pharisees and the Sadducees were so holy; it was because they were so rich. The expectation was that if you did right, the Lord would pay you back by making you rich like He did with Abraham and Job. That's why Job's buddies thought he must have sinned something terrible because God took away everything Job had.

But in the New Testament, things change. The "blessing" isn't necessarily physical or in this life at all. If it were, then John the Baptist and Stephen sure were in a fix. Jesus says to bless the poor who can't pay you back, and ["thou shalt be recompensed at the resurrection of the just"]{.class-0} (Luke 14:14). The "goodies" come on the "other side" (Matt. 5:12; Luke 6:23). You get the rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ and in Christ's Millennial Kingdom; not now. There will be many a poor Indian or African native evangelist, traveling from village to village on a bicycle, preaching, witnessing, and passing out tracts, who "cashes in" at the Judgment Seat of Christ more than these "television evangelists" who rake in hundreds of millions of dollars from Christian suckers who don't have the spiritual discernment God gave a brass monkey.

["A full reward be given thee of the LORD God of Israel."]{.class-0} The writer of Hebrews says God ["is a rewarder of them that diligently seek him"]{.class-0} (Heb. 11:6). Moses gave up his position as ["the son of Pharaoh's daughter"]{.class-0} in order ["to suffer affliction with the people of God"]{.class-0} because ["he had respect unto the recompence of the reward"]{.class-0} (Heb. 11:24--26).

Ruth may not have realized that God would pay her back and reward her for leaving her gods, her family, and her homeland behind to trust in Him and be a part of His people, but she had it "coming to her" anyway. I was like that when I got saved. When I trusted Christ, all I knew is that I wasn't going to Hell. I found out later on that I was going to Heaven, and that was "icing on the cake" and "sauce for the goose." It was "above and beyond" what I expected from the Lord because of how awful of a sinner I was.

Now David says the ["great reward"]{.class-0} comes from keeping God's ["law," "testimony," "statutes," "commandment," "fear,"]{.class-0} and ["judgments"]{.class-0} (Psa. 19:7--11). In the New Testament, this is keeping God's word (Rev. 3:8, 10; John 17:6) and His [words]{.class-1} (John 14:23). If you don't have God's W-O-R-D-S (not just the "word of God" or the "Word of God"), then you can't keep them, and you won't be able to keep God's "word" because the "word" of God is composed of His WORDS. If your "Bible" is missing 500 words ([NKJV]{.class-1}) or 36,000 words ([NASV]{.class-1}) or 64,000 words ([NIV]{.class-1}), then there are some of God's words you aren't keeping; therefore, you can't get ["a full reward"]{.class-0} because you aren't keeping all of God's words.

For the Christian, it is possible to lose part of your rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ by not taking heed to the warnings of Scripture not to be deceived (2 John 7 cf. Matt. 24:4; Luke 21:8; 1 Cor. 6:9, 15:33; Gal. 6:7; Eph. 5:6; 2 Thess. 2:3; 1 John 3:7; Jer. 37:9). You can lose rewards by not having the right motive for service (1 Cor. 3:13--15). Unconfessed and unjudged sin in your life can cause you to lose rewards (2 Cor. 5:10 cf. 1 Cor. 11:31--32). Intemperance in your body can cause you to lose rewards (1 Cor. 9:24--27). And you can lose ["a full reward"]{.class-0} (2 John 8) by not being a good testimony to a lost world and giving them the Gospel (Phil. 2:15--16).

Now there is a great practical lesson here for the Christian woman. I have given you the "doctrine" on the ["full reward"]{.class-0} for the believer, but remember, this is said specifically to a [woman.]{.class-1} Sister, when it seems like you are weighed down by the mundane things of life (like the cooking, the cleaning, the shopping, the washing, taking care of the kids, etc.) and there doesn't seem to be anything you can do spiritually for your Lord, remember what David said in 1 Samuel 30:24.

The Amalekites had raided Ziklag where David lived in exile from Saul and had taken all his wives and stuff, and all the families and stuff of his men. While pursuing the Amalekites to get all their families and things back, 200 of David's men became so exhausted that they couldn't go on, so they stayed behind and guarded the rest of the stuff that had not been taken. When David and the rest of his men had gotten everything and everyone back from the Amalekites, some of the ones who had gone to the battle wanted to send the ones who had stayed behind packing, with no "spoils" but their families. David said, "No, you're not going to do that because under the Law (Num. 31:27), you split even with the ones who stayed behind."

["For who will hearken unto you in this matter? but as his part is that goeth down to the battle, so shall his part be that tarrieth by the stuff: they shall part alike"]{.class-0} (1 Sam. 30:24).

Christian lady, if you do what you do for the Lord, no matter how trivial or mundane it seems, and you are a real helpmeet to a Christian husband who is serving the Lord and is a witness, [you will get your reward.]{.class-1} You will get the same reward as your husband gets. The principle is given by Jesus in Matthew 10:41.

"He that receiveth a prophet in the name of a prophet shall receive a prophet's reward; and he that receiveth a righteous man in the name of a righteous man shall receive a righteous man's reward."

The illustration of that in the Bible is the great woman of Shunem (2 Kings 4:8--11). She was no prophetess, but she took care of Elisha, and God rewarded her for it (2 Kings 4:13--16). Sister, that Book says, ["For God is not unrighteous to forget your work and labour of love, which ye have shewed toward his name, in that ye have ministered to the saints, and do minister"]{.class-0} (Heb. 6:10). You will get your reward.

Back to Ruth 2:12---["Under whose wings thou art come to trust."]{.class-0} The hymn says, "Under His wings I am safely abiding." The Lord likens Himself to two birds: a chicken and an eagle. The eagle speaks of God's leading the believer. God said in Exodus 19:4, ["I bare you on eagles' wings, and brought you unto myself"]{.class-0}; He said He led the children of Israel like an eagle would bear her young ["on her wings"]{.class-0} (Deut. 32:11--12). The chicken speaks of God's care and protection. Jesus said, ["how often would I have gathered thy children together, even as a hen gathereth her chickens under her wings"]{.class-0} (Matt. 23:37). That is the picture here in Ruth 2:12.

13 Then she said, Let me find favour in thy sight, my lord; for that thou hast comforted me, and for that thou hast spoken friendly unto thine handmaid, though I be not like unto one of thine handmaidens.

14 And Boaz said unto her, At mealtime come thou hither, and eat of the bread, and dip thy morsel in the vinegar. And she sat beside the reapers: and he reached her parched corn, and she did eat, and was sufficed, and left.

15 And when she was risen up to glean, Boaz commanded his young men, saying, Let her glean even among the sheaves, and reproach her not:

16 And let fall also some of the handfuls of purpose for her, and leave them, that she may glean them, and rebuke her not.

17 So she gleaned in the field until even, and beat out that she had gleaned: and it was about an ephah of barley.

Seeing that Boaz has already done and said things to comfort and befriend her (["for that thou hast comforted me, and . . . hast spoken friendly unto thine handmaid"]{.class-0}---vs. 13), she asks him to show her yet more favor (["Let me find favor in thy sight"]{.class-0}), even though she is not a Jewess (["though I be not like unto one of thine handmaidens"]{.class-0}). Boaz does indeed show her further favor by allowing her to share in the food he provided to his laborers.

This is a sign that Boaz was "righteous" in an Old Testament sense (see our comments on Luke 1:6 in that Commentary). Job said, "If I have eaten my bread all by myself and haven't given to the poor, widows, and fatherless when they had need, then let my arm fall off and the bones in it break" (Job 31:16--22). James wrote to the twelve tribes of Israel (James 1:1),[ "Pure religion and undefiled before God and the Father is this, To visit the fatherless and widows in their affliction"]{.class-0} (James 1:27); that included [feeding]{.class-1} them where they needed it (James 2:15--16). God promised in the Old Testament to take care of the Jew who did that and to bless him (Isa. 58:10--11).

Boaz allowed Ruth not only to eat the bread prepared for his workers, but to ["dip"]{.class-0} it ["in the vinegar"]{.class-0} (vs. 14); this gave it more flavor and made it more refreshing for working in the warm Spring sun. Hence, "dips" for potato chips and certain meats (like chicken "nuggets"): it comes from a [King James]{.class-1} Bible. You won't get away from that Book no matter how hard you try. God has worked things out so that it is ingrained and embedded in your everyday life.

["And he reached her parched corn"]{.class-0} (vs. 14). The ["parched corn"]{.class-0} was some of the new grain just harvested and roasted right then and there at the noon meal. It was roasted ["in the husk"]{.class-0} (2 Kings 4:42) and rubbed in the hand to get the kernels out to eat (Deut. 23:25 cf. Luke 6:1). With "corn corn," this came out in Southern parlance as "roasting ears."

The word ["reached"]{.class-0} is archaic English coming from the German word [reichen]{.class-1} ("Old English" was originally a [Germanic]{.class-1} language from the Saxons). It means "to give or hand over." Now this is one of those genuinely "archaic" words in a [King James]{.class-1} Bible that can be updated; but the editors, translators, and revisers will use that as an excuse to make as many as 64,000 changes in your Bible (like the [NIV]{.class-1}). These are not merely changes in spellings, punctuation, and orthography like the so-called "70,000 changes" the apostates like to bring up between the editions of the [AV.]{.class-1} Those are omissions of words and sometimes whole verses, the elimination of the word [hell]{.class-1} ("all is well; there is no hell"), kicking the Lord out of His own Book (like the new versions do in Luke 23:42), and attacking every "fundamental of the faith" in the Book. It all begins with the excuse of "updating" the language of the [Authorized]{.class-1} text.

Now you know me. I won't take that first step. If you take the first step, you'll take another and another and another until you have a corrupt, apostate piece of trash masquerading as a "Bible" (like the [NASV]{.class-1} and the [ESV]{.class-1}). When we put together the [Ruckman Reference Bible,]{.class-1} all we had to do to "update" the "archaic language" of the [AV]{.class-1} was put a note in the center column. [We didn't have to change one word of the text.]{.class-1}

["And she did eat, and was sufficed, and left."]{.class-0} Now you can read that one of two ways. The first is the obvious: after she ate her fill, she got up and left the meal. Look at the next verse: ["And when she was risen up to glean"]{.class-0} (vs. 15). But you can also read the ["and left"]{.class-0} as she had grain left over (cf. 2 Kings 4:44). Look at the end of verse 18: ["and she brought forth, and gave to her]{.class-0} \[i.e., to her mother-in-law\] [that she had reserved after she was sufficed."]{.class-0}

Ruth finishes her meal and goes back to work. With Ruth gone, Boaz gives ["his young men"]{.class-0} two prohibitions concerning her: don't ["reproach her"]{.class-0} (vs. 15) and don't ["rebuke her"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). They weren't to make fun of her, and they weren't to get on her for where she gleaned or what she gleaned.

["And let fall also some of the handfuls of purpose for her"]{.class-0} (vs. 16). You would say "handfuls [on]{.class-1} purpose" today, but did you notice that you didn't need a "newer," more "up-to-date" translation to figure the thing out?

Back when there were fewer students at the Pensacola Bible Institute, I used to pass out a list of the 100 archaic words in the [King James]{.class-1} Bible to my Preparation and Delivery of Sermons class. We would then discuss those words and see if the students could figure out what they meant. There were young men in those classes that ranged in education from post-graduate studies to high school dropouts. Of those 100 archaic words, the students had no trouble understanding fifty of them. Of the remaining fifty, the students could figure out what 25 of them meant by the context in which they appeared. When all was said and done, there were only 25 words on that list that the students needed to look up in a dictionary. Are you going to make an average of [one change per verse]{.class-1} to "update" 25 words? Don't give me that gas, man.

Brethren, it has [never]{.class-1} been a matter of not understanding the Bible. Like Mark Twain said, "It's not the things in the Bible I can't understand that bother me; it's the things I do understand." Yeah, you had better believe it. People don't have a problem understanding a [King James]{.class-1} Bible; they have a problem [believing it.]{.class-1} How do you know that is so? Because the last three generations raised on the "clearer" and "more accurate" translations have been some of the biggest [Bible ignoramuses]{.class-1} around. There is a Bible ignorance these days that rivals the Dark Ages. The new versions haven't done one thing to help folks understand God's word.

When I used to do weekly radio broadcasts, I would put out a challenge from time to time. It was this: I challenged the listeners who used the newer translations to show me one thing in a modern version that I couldn't find in a [King James]{.class-1} Bible. They could phone me or write me or come talk to me personally. In over forty years of making that challenge, I never had one "taker." That was with the professors at Pensacola Christian College correcting the [King James]{.class-1} in the classroom with the [New American Standard Version]{.class-1} during that time (they've "backslid" since then and now correct it with the [Textus Receptus]{.class-1} Greek) and with a charismatic outfit off near Gulf Beach Highway somewhere. I didn't have to worry about anybody taking me up on the challenge because that [King James]{.class-1} Bible is so clear that anybody can understand it---even with the archaic words.

There are new translations all over the place, and professing Christians aren't reading them. A survey came out during the 400th anniversary of the publication of the [King James]{.class-1} Bible, and the survey found out that of the number of Christians who read the Bible on a regular basis, 85% of them read the [King James.]{.class-1} Only 15% read the modern versions. There are a bunch of Christians out there with [RSVs, NRSVs, NKJVs, CEVs, Good News Bibles, New Living Translations, NIVs, ]{.class-1}and [ESVs]{.class-1} who aren't reading them. They have no idea what's in them.

Now back to those ["handfuls of purpose."]{.class-0} Christian, haven't you found in your life, if you looked at things with a grateful heart instead of a greedy, griping heart, that God has been awfully good to you? I know we all have trouble, and some more than others, but I'll be right frank with you, the Lord leaves me no room to complain---even when I feel I have a right to. God has given me so many ["handfuls of purpose"]{.class-0} that I can't afford to complain. The Lord dumps things on me that He doesn't give other preachers. Lord knows, I don't deserve them and didn't earn them, but I got them anyway.

I get little things from time to time that I wouldn't trade for money. For example, over in my house, I have eight dollars in a frame (a five and three ones); they have been there over 25 years now. I wouldn't spend that money unless I was down to my last dollar and had no other choice. You say, "Why not, Ruckman?" Because, in a sense, that money is "holy"; it represents [sacrifice.]{.class-1}

You see, that money wasn't a part of any regular church offering. I was preaching one time at the Pot of Gold Ranch in Comfort, Texas. One night after the fourth night of the meeting, a boy about eleven years old called all the other boys in his cabin together and said, "Let's take up an offering for Bro. 'Rupkin' (that's what they called me; I guess they couldn't pronounce "Ruckman")." That kid did  that with no counselor there to suggest it or "egg him on" to do it. Those kids collected eight dollars from their "canteen" money (the money they brought to spend on drinks and snacks). The money was all in change, so they took it to the canteen and had it converted to that five dollar bill and three one dollar bills. Then those kids brought me that offering. I wouldn't trade those four bills for any offering I have gotten from any church, and I have gotten what I consider to be some big offerings in my time.

I'll give you another example. I got a phone call one time about eleven o'clock Saturday night (when a preacher really appreciates them the most, you know) from a drunk buddy of mine from my unsaved days. He was crying and had been in a fight with his wife. They were about ready to break up, and he wanted me to come over and try to "patch things up" between them. I went over.

He answered the door; I could tell he had been crying. His wife was over on the sofa, sitting there just rigid, with her arms folded. He grabbed me by the lapel and said, "Show me Jesus, Pete; show me Jesus!"

I just happened to have a large copy of my illustrated Gospel booklet [Tell It Like It Is.]{.class-1} I turned to the portrait of Christ with the crown of thorns on His head and blood dripping down. I said, "He's right here," and pointed to that picture. He dropped to his knees right there on the floor, and I got down on my knees with him and led the old boy to Christ. It was like we were the only ones in the room.

Meanwhile, his wife was sitting there looking at the whole thing. When my buddy finished getting saved, he said, "Now, Pete, talk to my wife." She sat there frozen and glaring: typical Episcopalian (I should know; I was one growing up).

I asked that guy's wife, "Are you a Christian?"

"I'm an Episcopalian," she replied.

I said, "I was an Episcopalian too before I was saved."

She said, "Well, I was christened."

I said, "I was christened too before I was saved."

Then she began to shift around and get nervous. She blurted out, "But I had a godfather and a godmother."

I said, "I did too before I was saved."

My buddy, who had just gotten saved and was still kneeling over by the door, started laughing. He told his wife, "I told you Pete Ruckman would tell you the d\-\-- truth."

That's the first time I had ever heard a cuss word connected with the truth, but I wouldn't trade that for a degree from Harvard or Princeton. That meant that old drunk knew I was real. He had confidence in me that I would tell the truth.

I'll give you one more. This is the ministry. It's not some air-conditioned faculty lounge behind a barbed-wire fence. I was preaching in a rescue mission over in Mobile, Alabama, one night. After I got through, an old bum came up to me and shook my hand. He said, "You remember me?" I said, "No." "Well, I got saved in your meeting here last year," he said. You could tell the old boy was drunk.

I said, "You ain't doing so good, are you?" He said, "No, I'm not. But I just want to tell you something, preacher. You're the only preacher I could ever understand. I missed a freight train tonight just to hear your preach." I wouldn't take a "purty" for that. That showed me I was down on the level where even a drunken bum like him could [get it.]{.class-1}

Those are all ["handfuls of purpose"]{.class-0} the Lord dropped my way. I am one of the few preachers left in this country (if there are any more left at all) who has never had to preach hard on attendance or giving. Every preacher I ever met had to in order to keep the work going. I never had to because the crowds have always been there and the bills have always been paid. That's ["handfuls of purpose,"]{.class-0} I kid you not; that's not "the norm."

Back to Ruth 2. Ruth gleaned until evening, and after beating out the grain from the husks and stems, she had ["about an ephah of barley."]{.class-0} In contemporary measurements, she had around a bushel of barley grain to make bread. That was exceptional for one woman gleaning. It was obvious from the amount she brought home that someone had given her a "break" (see vs. 19).

18 And she took it up, and went into the city: and her mother in law saw what she had gleaned: and she brought forth, and gave to her that she had reserved after she was sufficed.

19 And her mother in law said unto her, Where hast thou gleaned to day? and where wroughtest thou? blessed be he that did take knowledge of thee. And she shewed her mother in law with whom she had wrought, and said, The man's name with whom I wrought to day is Boaz.

20 And Naomi said unto her daughter in law, Blessed be he of the LORD, who hath not left off his kindness to the living and to the dead. And Naomi said unto her, The man is near of kin unto us, one of our next kinsmen.

21 And Ruth the Moabitess said, He said unto me also, Thou shalt keep fast by my young men, until they have ended all my harvest.

22 And Naomi said unto Ruth her daughter in law, It is good, my daughter, that thou go out with his maidens, that they meet thee not in any other field.

23 So she kept fast by the maidens of Boaz to glean unto the end of barley harvest and of wheat harvest; and dwelt with her mother in law.

Ruth returns to Naomi with her bushel of barley, and gives her mother-in-law supper from her leftovers from lunch. The principle is a younger, able-bodied relative is supposed to take care of the widowed elder. Of course, it is usually taken for granted that it will be a son or near male relative. The Apostle Paul tells Timothy:

["But if any widow have children or nephews, let them learn first to show piety at home, and to requite their parents: for that is good and acceptable before God"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 5:4).

Now as I pointed out, it was apparent to Naomi, from the amount of grain Ruth brought home, that someone was "looking out" for the girl. Naomi was naturally curious about who Ruth's benefactor was. When she found out it was Boaz, she blessed God. Naomi recognized the providential hand of God in guiding Ruth, albeit unwittingly, to the field of Boaz, for Boaz was near kin to Naomi's late husband.

What Naomi has in mind is what is known as the ["levirate]{.class-1} law"; it comes from the Latin word [levir,]{.class-1} meaning "husband's brother." In theological circles, it is called the law of the kinsman redeemer, and it is found in Deuteronomy 25:5--6. In order to keep the land inheritance in the family to whom God gave it in the book of Joshua, if a man died without children, his brother was to marry the widow in order to father children in the name of his brother. The children of such a union would get the dead man's inheritance so the land would remain in the family.

Naomi is getting ready to play "matchmaker" between Ruth and Boaz based on that law. Naomi's advice to her daughter-in-law is to do exactly what Boaz told her back in verse 8: glean only in Boaz's field and stay close to the men and women who worked for him. The idea is to show loyalty and gratefulness to the one who showed her great kindness (see our remarks under Judg. 8:34--35).

Proverbs 27:10 says, ["Thine own friend, and thy father's friend, forsake not."]{.class-0} Of course, we understand that such a command is conditioned on the friend's relationship to God and the love you are to have for Christ [first]{.class-1} (Matt. 10:37 cf. Luke 14:26). But the devotional application in the regard of the believer to his Lord should be obvious. If your Saviour loved you enough to die for your sins and get you out of Hell, can't you show your gratefulness and loyalty to Him by following Him and sticking by those who love Him.

If you love your Saviour, you won't be wandering around in the "fields" of ["this present evil world"]{.class-0} (Gal. 1:4). You were told, as a child of God, not to have ["fellowship with the unfruitful works of darkness"]{.class-0} (Eph. 5:11). As followers of Jesus Christ, we are commanded to ["love one another"]{.class-0} as Christ loved us (John 15:12, 17; 1 Thess. 4:9), and we should love the brethren ["IN THE TRUTH"]{.class-0} (2 John 1; 3 John 1) because charity ["rejoiceth IN THE TRUTH"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 13:6). What is ["the truth"]{.class-0} for the believer? It is ["the scripture"]{.class-0} (Dan. 10:21).

["Sanctify them through the truth: THY WORD IS TRUTH"]{.class-0} (John 17:17).

Ruth 2:23---["So she kept fast by the maidens of Boaz to glean unto the end of barley harvest and of wheat harvest; and dwelt with her mother in law."]{.class-0} Ruth labored in the fields of Boaz through the Spring during the barley harvest and into the Summer, when the wheat harvest began in June.

The interesting thing here, doctrinally, is that the time period of barley harvest and wheat harvest is the time period between Passover and Pentecost (see Lev. 23:5--22). This is the time between Christ's death and resurrection and the coming of the Holy Spirit in Acts 2. This is the time period given for the Rapture of the Bride in Song of Solomon 2:8--13, and you can see our remarks on that passage in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Song of Solomon.]{.class-1}

[]{#section-0_1_301218c1072ba786_70a3.xhtml}

Chapter 3

3:1 Then Naomi her mother in law said unto her, My daughter, shall I not seek rest for thee, that it may be well with thee?

2 And now is not Boaz of our kindred, with whose maidens thou wast? Behold, he winnoweth barley to night in the threshingfloor.

3 Wash thyself therefore, and anoint thee, and put thy raiment upon thee, and get thee down to the floor: but make not thyself known unto the man, until he shall have done eating and drinking.

4 And it shall be, when he lieth down, that thou shalt mark the place where he shall lie, and thou shalt go in, and uncover his feet, and lay thee down; and he will tell thee what thou shalt do.

5 And she said unto her, All that thou sayest unto me I will do.

6 And she went down unto the floor, and did according to all that her mother in law bade her.

["My daughter, shall I not seek rest for thee"]{.class-0} (vs. 1). The ["rest"]{.class-0} there is not sleep or lounging around. Remember back in 1:9 where Naomi told Orpah and Ruth, ["The LORD grant you that ye may find rest, each of you in the house of her husband"]{.class-0}? That ["rest"]{.class-0} is [marriage,]{.class-1} where the husband works and provides for the wife.

The Bible is not against women working outside the home. After all, you just read back in chapter 2 of a bunch of young women out reaping in the field. Acts 16:14 tells you about a business woman who became one of Paul's converts. What the Bible does teach is that when a woman gets married, the [husband]{.class-1} is to be the "breadwinner." The [man]{.class-1} is to provide for his household (1 Tim. 5:8), and the wife is to ["bear children"]{.class-0} and ["guide the house"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 5:14). I know that's considered "sexist" and "chauvinistic" in modern society, but that is the God-ordained pattern for the home. When America followed what God said, there were a lot fewer divorces and busted-up homes.

The ["rest"]{.class-0} of verse 1 is a cessation of work to make a living. It is a picture of the Bride of Christ ceasing from works to be saved.

Jesus said, ["Come unto me, all ye that labour and are heavy laden, and I will give you rest. Take my yoke upon you, and learn of me . . . and ye shall find rest unto your souls"]{.class-0} (Matt. 1:28--29).

["But to him that worketh not, but believeth on him that justifieth the ungodly, his faith is counted for righteousness"]{.class-0} (Rom. 4:5).

Back to Ruth 3:[ "And now is not Boaz of our kindred"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). This is the third mention of this fact in the book (see 2:1, 20). The Bible never tells you how close kin he was. You are told in verse 12 that there is someone else closer kin to Elimelech than Boaz was. The best guess is that he was a cousin.

["Behold, he winnoweth barley to night in the threshingfloor."]{.class-0} Now after grain was harvested, it was threshed. It was taken to the top of a hill with a flattened, paved surface on top. There, oxen or asses would walk around the threshingfloor pulling a heavy platform (with glass and metal on the bottom) that would break the ears of grain from their stalks and loosen the kernels from the husk. That was the [threshing]{.class-1} process.

Then, when a breeze blew across the top of the hill, the grain and the chaff (the husks and stems) were pitched up in the air by a pitchfork or a flat, shallow basket known as "winnowing fan" (see Isa. 30:24, 41:16; Luke 3:17). The wind would blow the lighter chaff away, and the heavy kernels of grain would fall back on the floor. That is the [winnowing process.]{.class-1} Because of the sea breeze coming in from the Mediterranean at night, that is when the winnowing process usually took place in the Holy Land in Bible times.

Now do you know what that pictures? You would never guess unless you read and paid attention to your Bible.[ It pictures the end of the United Nations.]{.class-1} Look at Daniel 2:35.

"Then was the iron, the clay, the brass, the silver, and the gold, broken to pieces together, AND BECAME LIKE THE CHAFF OF THE SUMMER THRESHINGFLOORS; AND THE WIND CARRIED THEM AWAY, that no place was found for them: and the stone that smote the image became a great mountain, and filled the whole earth."

That is the interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's vision of the image of gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay. Each layer represents a [Gentile kingdom,]{.class-1} and the last kingdom of iron and clay is the United Nations under the Antichrist (Rev. 13:1--7). The "smiting stone" of Daniel 2:35 is [Jesus Christ at His Second Advent]{.class-1} (see our comments on Matt. 21:44 in that Commentary). He crushes the Gentile world system and blows the whole thing away. That is found other places in the prophets, not just in Daniel (Isa. 17:13--14, 29:5--8, 41:15--16; Mic. 4:11--13).

Psalm 1:4 says the ["ungodly . . . are like the chaff which the wind driveth away."]{.class-0} John the Baptist said when Jesus Christ showed up, His ["fan"]{.class-0}---that would be a winnowing fan---would be ["in his hand, and he will throughly purge his floor"]{.class-0}---that would be His threshingfloor---["and will gather the wheat in his garner; but the CHAFF he will BURN with FIRE UNQUENCHABLE"]{.class-0} (Luke 3:17)---HELL (Mark 9:44, 46, 48)!

In the Parable of the Wheat and the Tares, Jesus said, ["the tares are the children of the wicked one"]{.class-0} (cf. Eph. 2:1--3; John 8:44), and the wheat is ["the children of the kingdom"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:38). In ["the harvest"]{.class-0} (["the end of the world"]{.class-0}---Matt. 13:39), ["the wheat"]{.class-0} is gathered into the ["barn"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:30), but the tares are gathered in bundles to be [burned]{.class-1} (Matt. 13:30). They are burned in ["a furnace of FIRE"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:42). Everything in that parable is assigned a meaning: the sower ["is the Son of man"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:37); ["The field is the world"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:38); ["The enemy that sowed]{.class-0} \[the tares\][ is the devil"]{.class-0} (Matt. 13:39); etc. Do you know what the ["fire"]{.class-0} is? It's FIRE!

The tares are the United Nations in Zephaniah 3:8. ["For my determination is to gather the NATIONS, that I may ASSEMBLE the kingdoms]{.class-0} \[hence, the [United Nations Assembly]{.class-1})[, to pour upon them mine indignation, even all my fierce anger: for all the earth shall be devoured with the FIRE of my jealousy."]{.class-0} Paul said that Jesus Christ returns ["In flaming FIRE taking vengeance on them that know not God, and obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-0} (2 Thess. 1:8). And just to make sure you don't miss the point, Jesus said that when He judges the nations at His return (Matt. 25:31--32), ["the goats"]{.class-0} (Matt. 25:33, 41) are cast ["into EVERLASTING FIRE, prepared for the devil and his angels"]{.class-0} (Matt. 25:41).

[That ]{.class-1}is what is behind threshing and winnowing. People think the Bible is a "religious" book, and it's not that at all. It's a [history]{.class-1} book: it tells you what takes place in human [history]{.class-1}---both the past and the [future.]{.class-1} That's why the government doesn't want the Book taught to your children: it says God is going to [burn]{.class-1} everyone who turns down His "love" (Rom. 5:8). That's not a "picture" of anything; it's actually going to happen.

Back to Ruth 3:[ "Wash thyself therefore, and anoint thee, and put thy raiment upon thee"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). Ruth has come in from gleaning wheat (2:23). But while the wheat was being harvested, the barley that had been harvested was now being threshed and winnowed. Naomi tells Ruth to wash up, put on some perfume and nicer clothes, and go to the "party" that was always held when the grain was finally winnowed and collected (cf. 2 Sam. 3:23; 1 Sam. 25:4, 36).

But while she was to "crash the party," she was not to go up to Boaz and let him know she was there until he was by himself and asleep. Then she was to uncover his feet while he was asleep, lie down beside him, and wait for him to wake up and tell her what to do.

The significance of uncovering the feet is found in the law of the kinsman redeemer in Deuteronomy 25:8--10. If the kinsman wouldn't perform his duty to raise up children to his brother, the widow was to: ["loose his shoe from off his foot, and spit in his face . . . And his name shall be called in Israel, The house of him that hath his shoe loosed."]{.class-0} By uncovering Boaz's feet, Ruth was saying to him, "You are my near kinsman, and it's your responsibility to marry me and raise up children to your kin who died. You have a choice now: marry me or leave your feet uncovered because your shoe will be loosed off your foot."

["He will tell thee what thou shalt do."]{.class-0} Again, Boaz as a type of Christ. At the wedding at Cana there in John 2, Mary tells those servants of her Son, ["Whatsoever HE saith unto you, do it"]{.class-0} (John 2:5). She doesn't say, "I'm the Mother of God; I'm the Queen of Heaven; I'm the Mother of all the sons of God. If you want to come to my Son, you have to come through me," or any other such Catholic tripe. She refers them directly to her Son. That's because Mary couldn't save a dead horse.

Verses 5--6 are self-explanatory. Ruth is obeying Naomi as she would her own mother.

7 And when Boaz had eaten and drunk, and his heart was merry, he went to lie down at the end of the heap of corn: and she came softly, and uncovered his feet, and laid her down.

8 And it came to pass at midnight, that the man was afraid, and turned himself: and, behold, a woman lay at his feet.

9 And he said, Who art thou? And she answered, I am Ruth thine handmaid: spread therefore thy skirt over thine handmaid; for thou art a near kinsman.
