10 And he said, Blessed be thou of the LORD, my daughter: for thou hast shewed more kindness in the latter end than at the beginning, inasmuch as thou followedst not young men, whether poor or rich.

11 And now, my daughter, fear not; I will do to thee all that thou requirest: for all the city of my people doth know that thou art a virtuous woman.

12 And now it is true that I am thy near kinsman: howbeit there is a kinsman nearer than I.

13 Tarry this night, and it shall be in the morning, that if he will perform unto thee the part of a kinsman, well; let him do the kinsman's part: but if he will not do the part of a kinsman to thee, then will I do the part of a kinsman to thee, as the LORD liveth: lie down until the morning.

["And when Boaz had eaten and drunk, and his heart was merry"]{.class-0} (vs. 7). The word ["drunk"]{.class-0} there doesn't mean Boaz was ["merry"]{.class-0} because he was drunk.[ "Drunk,"]{.class-0} there, is a verb, not an adjective. It is what is known as the "pluperfect" or "past perfect" tense. Boaz ["had . . . drunk."]{.class-0}

I call that to your attention because there are scholars, expositors, commentators, and teachers of all denominations---including Conservatives, Fundamentalists, and even some professing [Bible believers]{.class-1}---who try to tell you Jesus made fermented liquor in John 2. They do that so they can get fermented hootch into the Lord's Supper, with the aim of being able to drink it [anytime]{.class-1} for [any reason.]{.class-1} Of course, they will say, "The only stipulation is you can't get drunk."

But if that's so, then Christ certainly violated that stipulation in John 2. He has those servants fill ["six waterpots . . . containing two or three firkins apiece"]{.class-0} (John 2:6), and then He turns the water in those pots to wine (John 2:9). Well, a [firkin]{.class-1} is about nine gallons (some commentators will go as low as eight; others as high as ten). So each pot contained 18--27 gallons. If Jesus turned that water into alcoholic wine, that would have been from 78-162 gallons of [liquor.]{.class-1} That would be enough "shinny" to get an army drunk if the guests had followed "Standard Operating Procedure" (see John 2:10).

If that were the case, Jesus Christ [broke the Law,]{.class-1} especially in regards to being our High Priest (Heb. 3:1).

["Do not drink wine nor strong drink, thou, nor thy sons with thee, when ye go into the tabernacle of the congregation, lest ye die: it shall be a statute for ever throughout your generations: And that ye may put difference between holy and unholy, and between unclean and clean"]{.class-0} (Lev. 10:9--10).

["Woe unto him that giveth his neighbour drink, that puttest thy bottle to him, and makest him drunken also, that thou mayest look on their nakedness"]{.class-0} (Hab. 2:15).

Jesus didn't make fermented liquor, and He didn't use it at the Lord's Supper---no matter how much the Catholics, the Lutherans, and the Episcopalians try to justify it in their observances. Jesus said, ["I will not drink henceforth of this FRUIT OF THE VINE"]{.class-0} (Matt. 26:29). That's grape juice being squeezed out of the cluster directly into the cup, exactly as you find it in Genesis 40:11. That's called ["the pure blood of the grape"]{.class-0} in Deuteronomy 32:14 because it is ["new wine . . . found IN THE CLUSTER"]{.class-0} (Isa. 65:8).

Now Boaz goes and lies down ["at the end of the heap"]{.class-0} of the winnowed barley. Ruth sees where he is. When she is sure he is asleep, she quietly goes over to him, uncovers his feet, and lays down at them. Boaz wakes up at midnight, and there is a woman laying there at his feet. Of course, this is not like the movies or the TV where there is enough light to see who it is; it is pitch-black with only the stars to give light. There are no "city lights" by which to see. That is why Boaz is "shaken up" (["the man was afraid,"]{.class-0} vs. 8). Wouldn't it shock you if you woke up in the middle of the night with some stranger lying beside you in the dark?

Not being able to tell who it is in the dark, Boaz asks the woman, ["Who art thou?"]{.class-0} (vs. 9).

After identifying herself, Ruth says, ["spread therefore thy skirt over thine handmaid; for thou art a near kinsman."]{.class-0} It is a symbolic gesture, like a hen gathering her chicks under her wings to protect them (Luke 13:34). The idea is, "take me into your care as your wife":[ she's proposing to him.]{.class-1}

God says of Israel in Ezekiel 16:8, ["Now when I passed by thee, and looked upon thee, behold, thy time was the time of love; and I SPREAD MY SKIRT OVER THEE, and covered thy nakedness: yea, I sware unto thee, and entered into a covenant with thee, saith the Lord GOD, and thou becamest mine."]{.class-0}

["Spread therefore thy SKIRT over thine handmaid."]{.class-0} That must come as a shock to the ultra-legalistic Fundamentalists who use Deuteronomy 22:5 to prove a woman shouldn't wear slacks or pants because they ["pertaineth unto a man."]{.class-0} According to what you just read in verse 9 here in Ruth 3 and what you read in 1 Samuel 24:5, [all women today wear a man's clothing.]{.class-1} The command for Christian women in the New Testament is to ["adorn themselves in modest apparel"]{.class-0} (1 Tim. 2:9), and the truth of the matter is that there are times and circumstances when a woman's pants or "culottes" are more modest than a dress.

Verse 10: ["Blessed be thou of the LORD, my daughter: for thou hast shewed more kindness in the latter end than at the beginning."]{.class-0} That is, Ruth showed more kindness in paying attention to him than when she befriended Naomi. She could have been like Orpah and gone looking for a younger man than Boaz or a richer man than Boaz. But Ruth's God wasn't a husband like Orpah's.

Verse 11:[ "for all the city of my people doth know that thou art a virtuous woman."]{.class-0} Important because it gives you insight into Ruth's character, especially in light of what is going on here. Ruth didn't go to Boaz in the middle of the night to fornicate with him. An old saying goes: "Good men praise virtue where bad men practice vice." Boaz is praising the virtue of Ruth and not taking advantage of her and the situation.

Proverbs 31:30 says, ["Favour is deceitful, and beauty is vain: but a woman that feareth the LORD, she shall be praised."]{.class-0}

Ruth is more than just some clothing store dummy. She's a woman of virtue, and she fears the true God.

Verse 12: ["Howbeit there is a kinsman nearer than I."]{.class-0} Now Boaz was a near kin, but he wasn't the nearest kin. There was another man in Bethlehem who was closer in relation to Elimelech than Boaz was. The nearer kin got the first choice to redeem Naomi's property by marrying Ruth. We will get into the nuances of the Mosaic Law and the typology involved in the next chapter.

Boaz tells Ruth to stay where she is until the morning when he will see what the intentions of the nearer kinsman are. If the other relative can't fulfill the role of the redeemer, Boaz is more than willing to do it. In fact, he swears an oath by the Lord: ["then will I do the part of a kinsman to thee, AS THE LORD LIVETH"]{.class-0} (vs. 13).

14 And she lay at his feet until the morning: and she rose up before one could know another. And he said, Let it not be known that a woman came into the floor.

15 Also he said, Bring the vail that thou hast upon thee, and hold it. And when she held it, he measured six measures of barley, and laid it on her: and she went into the city.

16 And when she came to her mother in law, she said, Who art thou, my daughter? And she told her all that the man had done to her.

17 And she said, These six measures of barley gave he me; for he said to me, Go not empty unto thy mother in law.

18 Then said she, Sit still, my daughter, until thou know how the matter will fall: for the man will not be in rest, until he have finished the thing this day.

["And she lay at his feet until the morning."]{.class-0} Notice, she didn't lay [with]{.class-1} him: there is no sex involved. ["Let it not be known that a woman came into the floor."]{.class-0} Why not? Because even though nothing went on, it would give occasion for people to jump to the wrong conclusion and spread false rumors. That's why Paul said, ["Abstain from all APPEARANCE of evil"]{.class-0} (1 Thess. 5:22); not just ["all kinds"]{.class-1} as the new "Bibles" read. Boaz wasn't worried about committing ["evil"]{.class-0}; he hadn't touched Ruth. But he was worried about [appearing]{.class-1} to have committed evil.

Now Boaz swore with an oath to be Ruth's kinsman redeemer if he could, and as an "earnest" of his promise he gives her ["six measures of barley."]{.class-0} The New Testament says God has ["given us the earnest of the Spirit in our hearts"]{.class-0} (2 Cor. 1:22, 5:5). That is, the Holy Spirit is given as the surety of our redemption until the body Christ purchased (1 Cor. 6:19--20) is redeemed at the Rapture (Eph. 1:14; Rom. 8:23).

["And laid it on her."]{.class-0} Hence the popular expression "lay it on me." You couldn't completely get rid of the [King James]{.class-1} Bible if you tried. It is so ingrained in the English language that people quote it at least three to five times a day without even realizing they are doing so. Do you drive down a [highway?]{.class-1} You are quoting Numbers 20:17. Do you drink [beer?]{.class-1} You are quoting Numbers 21:16. Is your wife or little girl your [darling?]{.class-1} You are quoting Psalm 22:20. Did you [miss the boat?]{.class-1} You are quoting 1 Peter 3:20. Do you like the [Star Wars]{.class-1} movies? You are quoting Judges 5:20. Has someone you know [gone to the dogs?]{.class-1} You are quoting 1 Kings 21:23. There are hundreds of expressions like that that are part of the English language because of the Book ([AV]{.class-1} 1611). You have a hard row to hoe if you are going to get rid of it.

["And she went into the city."]{.class-0} And here the destructive critics of the [AV]{.class-1} have a "heyday." This is a famous "contradiction" in the [Authorized]{.class-1} text. It shows you just how "hard up" the apostates are to find a mistake in the [Authorized Version.]{.class-1} You see, some editions of the [AV]{.class-1} read ["she went into the city,"]{.class-0} while others read ["he went into the city."]{.class-0} The faculties and staffs of the leading Christian Colleges, Universities, and Seminaries will point to that and say, "See, there is a contradiction in the editions of the [KJV!]{.class-1} After all, both readings can't possibly be right, can they?" Well, can they?

Now before dealing with that question, let us consider a few things in regards to the critics themselves. These incredible hypocrites who criticize the [AV]{.class-1} for variants will accept a text based on two manuscripts that vary between themselves in [7,000 places.]{.class-1} That is, there are 7,000 differences between [Sinaiticus]{.class-1} and [Vaticanus,]{.class-1} 3,000 of them in the Gospels alone. Having criticized the [AV]{.class-1} for a difference like Ruth 3:15, the translators and revisers of the modern versions will differ from the [Authorized]{.class-1} text anywhere from 500 ([NKJV]{.class-1}) to 36,000 ([NASV]{.class-1}) to 64,000 ([NIV]{.class-1}) times. Ain't that the pot calling the kettle black?

Aside from the fact that what you have here is an example of a printing error and not an actual "error" in the translation or the Biblical text, how would you prove a "contradiction" between the two editions? A contradiction implies that one is right and one is wrong. Why it never occurred to these educated jackasses that [both]{.class-1} could be correct is anybody's guess. You see, not only did [Ruth]{.class-1} go ["into the city"]{.class-0} (vs. 16), [Boaz]{.class-1} did as well (4:1). If push came to shove, you couldn't prove [either]{.class-1} reading was in "error," because both readings are [so]{.class-1} according to the Holy Bible. Nothing like a Bible to clear up a Seminary education, is there?

Verse 16:[ "And when she came to her mother in law, she said, Who art thou, my daughter?"]{.class-0} What do you mean, ["Who art thou,"]{.class-0} Naomi? She's Ruth, of course; she's been living with you for four months. ["Who art thou, my daughter?"]{.class-0} Well, if she wasn't "Ruth," there was only one other person she could have been: [Mrs. Boaz!]{.class-1}

Let's see you explain Naomi's question without believing that a marriage is [flesh joining flesh]{.class-1} (read Gen. 2:24; Deut. 21:10--13, 22:13--30; Matt. 19:5--6; Rom. 7:2--3; 1 Cor. 6:16; Eph. 5:31). Naomi is questioning whether anything has changed in Ruth's "marital status."

Look at Ruth's reply: ["And she told her all that the man had done to her."]{.class-0} What had been ["done"]{.class-0} was the ["six measures of barley"]{.class-0} he gave her as the surety of his promise to redeem her, and NOTHING ELSE. No [marriage]{.class-1} (i.e., no flesh joining flesh) had taken place; she is still [just Ruth.]{.class-1}

Don't go to any Hebrew scholar to figure the thing out. He will screw you up so that you are just as stupid as he is. When you make the marriage a ceremony, you end up making a [sinner]{.class-1} out of God. In the Old Testament, Israel was Jehovah's wife. When the people committed spiritual adultery, God divorced her (Isa. 50:1; Jer. 3:8) and said after He did that, ["She is NOT my wife, NEITHER am I her husband"]{.class-0} (Hos. 2:2). Is that clear? A divorce takes place when a person takes his or her flesh and joins it to the flesh of another beside his or her spouse; the ["bill of divorcement"]{.class-0} (Mark 10:4) is merely a legal formality.

According to Hosea 2:2, when that takes places, the divorced parties are [single.]{.class-1} All this gas about "two living wives" and "three living wives" is a bunch of [baloney.]{.class-1} If you are [loosed]{.class-1} from a wife,[ you aren't married]{.class-1} (1 Cor. 7:27). The commandment for a bishop or a deacon to have one wife (1 Tim. 3:2, 12; Tit. 1:6) is a command against [polygamy;]{.class-1} it has nothing to do with divorce or remarriage. If you are married, you are to be faithful to the spouse you've got, and if a spouse commits adultery and joins his or her flesh to another, and there is no reconciliation (i.e., you end up getting a legal divorce), you do not have "two living wives or husbands" if you get remarried. Why not? [Because the marriage bond was broken.]{.class-1}

Verse 18 is self-explanatory. Ruth is to stay put with her mother-in-law until she finds out what happens between Boaz and the nearer kinsman. The devotional picture is the sinner relying on the finished work of Christ for salvation. Ruth had asked Boaz to be the kinsman redeemer, and that's all she could do. From that point onward, it was all up to Boaz.

Christ came to finish the work His Father gave Him to do (John 4:34, 17:4), and He finished it (John 19:30). He ["offered one sacrifice for sins for ever"]{.class-0} (Heb. 10:12) and became ["the end of the law for righteousness to every one that believeth"]{.class-0} (Rom. 10:4).

[]{#section-0_1_8dc774478a99ab52_70a4.xhtml}

Chapter 4

4:1 Then went Boaz up to the gate, and sat him down there: and, behold, the kinsman of whom Boaz spake came by; unto whom he said, Ho, such a one! turn aside, sit down here. And he turned aside, and sat down.

2 And he took ten men of the elders of the city, and said, Sit ye down here. And they sat down.

3 And he said unto the kinsman, Naomi, that is come again out of the country of Moab, selleth a parcel of land, which was our brother Elimelech's:

4 And I thought to advertise thee, saying, Buy it before the inhabitants, and before the elders of my people. If thou wilt redeem it, redeem it: but if thou wilt not redeem it, then tell me, that I may know: for there is none to redeem it beside thee; and I am after thee. And he said, I will redeem it.

5 Then said Boaz, What day thou buyest the field of the hand of Naomi, thou must buy it also of Ruth the Moabitess, the wife of the dead, to raise up the name of the dead upon his inheritance.

6 And the kinsman said, I cannot redeem it for myself, lest I mar mine own inheritance: redeem thou my right to thyself; for I cannot redeem it.

Now what you are reading here is how legal proceedings were handled back in Bible times. There was no "city hall" or "courthouse"; legal matters were handled at the main gate of a city.

Deuteronomy 16:18 says, ["Judges and officers shalt thou make thee in all thy gates, which the LORD thy God giveth thee, throughout thy tribes: and they shall judge the people with just judgment."]{.class-0} You can see examples of how this was to work in Deuteronomy 17:5, 21:19, and 25:7 (the latter reference being the case here in Ruth 4).

What you have here on the local, municipal level is an example of a [republic.]{.class-1} The people are represented by town elders who decide issues by democratic vote. Those judges were to make rulings in ["the fear of the LORD"]{.class-0} based on the written Law of God (see 2 Chron. 19:5--10). In America, that came out like this:

"Providence \[i.e., God working through men and circumstances\] has given to our people the choice of their rulers, and it is the duty as well as the privilege and interest of our Christian nation to select Christians for their rulers" (John Jay, the first Chief Justice of the Supreme Court).

"It is impossible to rightly govern a nation without God and the Bible" (George Washington, the first President of the United States).

"Our Constitution was made only for a moral and religious people. It is wholly inadequate to the government of any other" (John Adams, second President of the United States).

If that be the case, then this country is shot. It has kicked God and the Bible out of its educational, legislative, and judicial processes. It has divorced its Constitution and laws from this country's Biblical and Christian roots.

The old saying is: "Back to the Bible or back to the jungle." You are in an immoral, sex-obsessed, sex-perverted, integrated, "globalized," "multicultural," Socialistic, Communistic, pagan [jungle]{.class-1} with no sign of going "back."

["And he took ten men of the elders of the city"]{.class-0} (vs. 2). Now ten is the number of the [Gentiles]{.class-1} (Gen. 10 is the table of the Gentile nations; Acts 10 is the first time the Gospel is preached to the Gentiles as a group; Rom. 10 is the missionary call to the Gentiles; etc.). But at the same time, there are a total of [twelve]{.class-1} people involved: the ten elders, Boaz, and the nearer kinsman. So you have a picture of Israel as well (e.g., the twelve patriarchs and the twelve apostles). This "town council" is about to decide the fate of a Gentile woman who has joined ["the commonwealth of Israel"]{.class-0} (cf. Eph. 2:12).

That is the case of the Body of Christ in this age; it is represented by its ["mother"]{.class-0}---New Jerusalem (Gal. 4:26). When Israel, as a nation, rejected the Gospel, the Holy Spirit turned to the Gentiles (see Acts 28:27--28; Rom. 10). So although in Christ there is neither Jew nor Gentile (Gal. 3:28), the Body of Christ is made up, for the most part, of [Gentile]{.class-1} converts. Nevertheless, as we stated under our remarks on 2:11, the Gentiles in this age are still reliant on the Jews (John 4:22; Rom. 3:1--2). So in the New Jerusalem, which is ["the LAMB'S wife"]{.class-0} (Rev. 21:9 cf. 2 Cor. 11:2; Eph. 5:25--32), you read that on the twelve gates to the city ["are the names of the twelve tribes of the children of Israel"]{.class-0} (Rev. 21:12). You get into the city [through that Jew]{.class-1} (John 4:22; Rom. 3:1--2).

Now watch carefully in verses 3--4 the proposition Boaz presents to this nearer kinsman. ["Naomi . . . selleth a PARCEL OF LAND"]{.class-0} (vs. 3). No mention of a marriage yet. Moreover, it is a transaction between two [Jews]{.class-1}---Naomi and the kinsman; there is no mention yet of a [Gentile]{.class-1} being involved. Based on [that,]{.class-1} the other kinsman says, ["I will redeem it"]{.class-0} (vs. 4).

But when Boaz brings up the fact that a marriage is involved, and a marriage to a Gentile at that, the other relative of Elimelech said, ["I cannot redeem it for myself, lest I mar mine own inheritance"]{.class-0} (vs. 6).

The picture here is between God the Father and God the Son. Boaz, of course, is a picture of Jesus Christ---God the Son. That being the case, there would be only one "kinsman" nearer who could redeem us; that would be God the Father. God couldn't redeem the Gentiles personally Himself because He already had a bride who was His inheritance---[the nation of Israel]{.class-1} (see Deut. 32:9; Psa. 28:9, 33:12, 78:62, 94:14; and Hos. 1--3). Ruth is a type of the [Gentile Bride of Christ.]{.class-1} If God the Father had taken "Ruth" to be His wife, He would have violated what He Himself said in Deuteronomy 23:3--6.

Now this is not just a racial or national thing; it goes all the way into eternity, where the saved Jews of the Old Testament and the Tribulation get the new earth as an inheritance (Rom. 4:13) while the Body of Christ gets the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:9). While Jews and Gentiles may be one in Christ [spiritually]{.class-1} right now (Eph. 2:11--17), the "marriage" (Eph. 5:25--32) is not "consummated" (Rev. 19:7--9) until the "nearer Kinsman" (God the Father) takes His shoe off (vs. 7 cf. Deut. 25:10) ["over Edom"]{.class-0} (Psa. 60:8, 108:9) in the Tribulation (see our comments on the book of Obadiah in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class-1} Vol. I). When shoes go off the feet, [slaughter]{.class-1} is sure to follow (see Exod. 3:5; Josh. 5:15).

7 Now this was the manner in former time in Israel concerning redeeming and concerning changing, for to confirm all things; a man plucked off his shoe, and gave it to his neighbour: and this was a testimony in Israel.

8 Therefore the kinsman said unto Boaz, Buy it for thee. So he drew off his shoe.

The passage is obviously a fulfillment of the law in Deuteronomy 25:9; the only difference is that Ruth doesn't spit in the man's face. There are two reasons for this. The first is obvious: [Ruth is not there.]{.class-1} She is not there because, at this point, she has no standing in Israel, even though she has "converted." She married Mahlon while he was out of the Land in Moab; Ruth isn't considered part of ["the commonwealth of Israel"]{.class-0} until she is married to a Jew in the Promised Land.

Secondly, the kinsman is not turning her down just because he doesn't want to marry her. He has a legal reason he can't. He is already married to a Jewess and can't marry a Gentile lest he mess up his own inheritance. Boaz is single and can take Ruth as his wife without violating the rights of a Jewish wife.

9 And Boaz said unto the elders, and unto all the people, Ye are witnesses this day, that I have bought all that was Elimelech's, and all that was Chilion's and Mahlon's, of the hand of Naomi.

10 Moreover Ruth the Moabitess, the wife of Mahlon, have I purchased to be my wife, to raise up the name of the dead upon his inheritance, that the name of the dead be not cut off from among his brethren, and from the gate of his place: ye are witnesses this day.

11 And all the people that were in the gate, and the elders, said, We are witnesses. The LORD make the woman that is come into thine house like Rachel and like Leah, which two did build the house of Israel: and do thou worthily in Ephratah, and be famous in Bethlehem:

12 And let thy house be like the house of Pharez, whom Tamar bare unto Judah, of the seed which the LORD shall give thee of this young woman.

Verse 8:[ "BUY it for thee"]{.class-0}; verse 9: ["I have BOUGHT all that was Elimelech's."]{.class-0} A picture of the atonement of Jesus Christ. The words [redemption]{.class-1} and [redeem]{.class-1} mean "to buy back." In other words, you were under the possession of someone, and a price had to be paid to get you back. The modern picture is a pawn shop where a price must be paid to redeem an object that has been pawned. The object is redeemed by whoever can pay the price.

Before you were saved, you were ["sold under sin"]{.class-0} (Rom. 7:14), and ["the wages of sin is death"]{.class-0} (Rom. 6:23). In your natural state, you were under ["the wrath of God"]{.class-0} (John 3:36 cf. Gal. 3:13). When Jesus Christ died on the cross, He paid your ["wages"]{.class-0} for you in the currency of [His blood]{.class-1} (1 Pet. 3:18, 2:24, 1:18--19; Acts 20:28; Rev. 5:9). That was the only payment that would satisfy God's holiness and justice (Rom. 3:24--25; 1 John 2:2, 4:10).

So when you get saved, the Bible says, ["ye are bought with a price"]{.class-0} (1 Cor. 6:20). It is not just a dowry of a bride; it is the [payment for a slave.]{.class-1} A Christian is a bondslave of Jesus Christ (1 Cor. 7:22), knocked down on the block and sold to the highest bidder (in this case, the Lord Jesus Christ, who made the ultimate payment).

Here, Boaz pays off the money Elimelech owes to get his land and, in so doing, inherits everything that would have fallen to his two sons had they survived. That included Ruth to be his wife (vs. 10).

And then a blessing conferred on Boaz by the witnesses to the transaction: ["The LORD make the woman that is come into thine house like Rachel and like Leah, which two did build the house of Israel"]{.class-0} (vs. 11). Rachel and Leah were Jacob's two wives, and Jacob was Israel (Gen. 32:28). But Rachel and Leah were [Gentiles]{.class-1}---they were [Syrians,]{.class-1} like their aunt (Gen. 25:20).

But that's not all, look at the next verse: ["And let thy house be like the house of Pharez, whom Tamar bare unto Judah"]{.class-0} (vs. 12). Tamar was another Gentile woman (Gen. 38:1--6). Here is a Gentile woman marrying a Jew, and she is likened to three other Gentile women in the lineage of her husband. Again, all pictures of the Gentile Bride of Christ.

Not only that, the child that will be born of this union will be connected, in typology, to [Rachel]{.class-1} and [Tamar.]{.class-1} Rachel gave birth to [Joseph,]{.class-1} a type of Christ in both of His advents (Gen. 49:24). Tamar bare [Judah's]{.class-1} child and the scepter comes through Judah (Gen. 49:10) via Pharez all the way to Christ.

Back to verse 11: ["do thou worthily in Ephratah, and be famous in Bethlehem."]{.class-0} Ephratah (also called ["Ephrath"]{.class-0}---Gen. 35:16, 19) is the region in which Bethlehem was located. And of course, all you just read in verses 11--12 points prophetically to Jesus Christ. As a saved child of God, you were [purchased]{.class-1} (see our remarks above under vs. 9) by a [Judean Jew from the tribe of Judah, born in Bethlehem.]{.class-1}

["But thou, Bethlehem Ephratah, though thou be little among the thousands of Judah, yet out of thee shall he come forth unto me that is to be ruler in Israel; whose goings forth have been from of old, from everlasting"]{.class-0} (Mic. 5:2).

Jesus Christ not only ends up being the ["King of the Jews"]{.class-0} (Matt. 2:2), but [the Saviour and King of the entire earth]{.class-1} (1 John 4:14; Zech. 14:9). Is that ["worthily"]{.class-0} and ["famous"]{.class-0} enough for you? I think so!

13 So Boaz took Ruth, and she was his wife: and when he went in unto her, the LORD gave her conception, and she bare a son.

14 And the women said unto Naomi, Blessed be the LORD, which hath not left thee this day without a kinsman, that his name may be famous in Israel.

15 And he shall be unto thee a restorer of thy life, and a nourisher of thine old age: for thy daughter in law, which loveth thee, which is better to thee than seven sons, hath born him.

16 And Naomi took the child, and laid it in her bosom, and became nurse unto it.

17 And the women her neighbours gave it a name, saying, There is a son born to Naomi; and they called his name Obed: he is the father of Jesse, the father of David.

Notice in verse 13: ["the LORD gave her conception, and she bare a son." ]{.class-0}"The birds and the bees" notwithstanding, it is [the Lord]{.class-1} who "opens the womb" (Gen. 29:31), and it is [the Lord]{.class-1} who closes it (Gen. 20:18). And no matter how often a husband and wife may try to have a child, and no matter how many "fertility drugs" a woman may take, if the Lord doesn't provide ["the fruit of the womb"]{.class-0} (Gen. 30:2), the wife will not be "in a family way."

["Children are an heritage of THE LORD: and the fruit of the womb is HIS reward"]{.class-0} (Psa. 127:3). ["HE maketh the barren woman to keep house, and to be a joyful mother of children"]{.class-0} (Psa. 113:9).

If you are a Christian woman who wants a child but can't seem to have one, all you can do is pray about it (Gen. 20:17, 25:21; 1 Sam. 1:27), and if the Lord says "yes," then praise God. But if He says "no," then [praise God anyway]{.class-1} (Psa. 34:13; 1 Thess. 5:18). I know it is hard, and the government makes you "jump" through all kinds of "hoops," but there are all kinds of children out there either with no momma or with a momma not fit to raise a dog. Maybe you can adopt a child and be a blessing to that boy or girl. After all, [God adopted you]{.class-1} (Rom. 8:15; Gal. 4:5).

I have known several Christian women who adopted a child, and then God gave them children of their own. Of course, that is no guarantee, nor is it a good reason to adopt. But Christian lady, you can be a blessing to some child, somewhere, even if you can't have one yourself.

Verse 14: ["And the women said unto Naomi, Blessed be the LORD, which hath not left thee this day without a kinsman."]{.class-0} Naomi's neighbors are rejoicing ["with them that do rejoice"]{.class-0} (Rom. 12:15).

This is the woman who told her neighbors back in 1:20, ["Call me not Naomi, call me Mara: for the Almighty hath dealt very bitterly with me."]{.class-0} Well, she's not saying that anymore. What happened? [She got right,]{.class-1} and the Lord turned the bitterness into pleasantness again.

Naomi returned to the house of bread and praise, and God gave her a saved daughter-in-law that loved her enough to stick by her through hard times and take care of her (vs. 15). Those Jewish women's opinion of Ruth was high, boy. They said Ruth was better to Naomi ["than seven sons."]{.class-0} That's high praise from a Jewish momma, did you know that?

Not only did God give Naomi a good daughter-in-law, but she also got a rich son-in-law in on the deal who loved the Lord. And now God has given her a grandson to be ["a restorer of thy life, and a nourisher of thine old age"]{.class-0} (vs. 15).

You will remember, back under our comments on 1:21, that Naomi was a picture of Israel in [apostasy.]{.class-1} Here she becomes a picture of Israel [restored.]{.class-1} Isaiah 49:6 says that when Christ returns at the Second Advent, He will ["restore the preserved of Israel."]{.class-0} Before Jesus returned to Heaven, the disciples asked Him, ["Lord, wilt thou at this time restore again the kingdom to Israel?"]{.class-0} (Acts 1:6). That was not a mistake on their part, as many commentators and expositors suppose; [that is the main theme of the Old Testament]{.class-1} (e.g., Isa. 9:6--7; Jer. 23:5--6, 33:15--17, 26; Ezek. 37:24--27; Dan. 2:35, 44, 7:27; Hos. 3:4--5; Obad. 20--21; Mic. 5:2; Zeph. 3:15--17).

Isaiah 1:26--27 says, ["And I will restore thy judges as at the first, and thy counsellors as at the beginning: afterward thou shalt be called, The city of righteousness, the faithful city. Zion shall be redeemed with judgment, and her converts with righteousness."]{.class-0}

Now why did God provide a kinsman redeemer for Naomi, and in type, why will He redeem Israel as a nation? Verse 14: ["that HIS NAME may be famous in Israel."]{.class-0} God restores His people, not for their sakes, but for [His glory.]{.class-1} Passages like Isaiah 49:23; Ezekiel 16:62, 20:42--44, 28:25--26, 34:27, 37:6, 13; Joel 3:17 say God restores Israel so those Jews will know that [He is the Lord.]{.class-1}

Back to Ruth 4:[ "And NAOMI took the child, and laid it in HER bosom, and became nurse unto it. And the women her neighbours gave it a name, saying, There is a son born TO NAOMI"]{.class-0} (vss. 16--17). Now as we pointed out under 2:2, the term [son]{.class-1} or [daughter]{.class-1} in Scripture can be used of a [grandson]{.class-1} or a [granddaughter,]{.class-1} as well as a direct son or daughter. That is the case here in verse 17. Ruth's baby boy isn't Naomi's son, like Mahlon and Chilion were; he is her [grandson.]{.class-1}

But notice how personal the relationship is to Naomi. [She]{.class-1}[ "took the child"]{.class-0}; she ["laid it in HER bosom"]{.class-0}; [she]{.class-1} ["became nurse unto it."]{.class-0} She's treating the child as if it were her very own.

There are some portions of the Bible you will never quite understand until you have experienced them yourself. The relationship between Naomi and Ruth is more like a mother and daughter than it is a mother-in-law and daughter-in-law. There are all kinds of jokes about how hard it is to get along with a mother-in-law, but that is not the case between Naomi and Ruth.

Whenever a momma's "little girl" has a baby of her own, that grandmother, if at all possible, will be right there with her daughter to help her with that new baby. And that new grandma treats that little one as if it is her own baby because it is the baby of her "baby." To Naomi, this is the child God gave her to replace the two sons she lost. It is "her baby" because it came from the daughter-in-law who was ["better"]{.class-0} to her ["than seven sons."]{.class-0}

["And the women her neighbours gave it a name . . . and they called his name Obed."]{.class-0} Notice it is the neighbor women who name the child, not Boaz and Ruth, or even Naomi. They call the child's name ["Obed."]{.class-0} The name means "serving" or "worshiping." It hearkens back to what the ladies said in verse 14: ["Blessed be the LORD . . . that his name may be famous in Israel."]{.class-0}

18 Now these are the generations of Pharez: Pharez begat Hezron,

19 And Hezron begat Ram, and Ram begat Amminadab,

20 And Amminadab begat Nahshon, and Nahshon begat Salmon,

21 And Salmon begat Boaz, and Boaz begat Obed,

22 And Obed begat Jesse, and Jesse begat David.

Now we come to the point of the whole book. It actually begins in verse 17: ["he is the father of Jesse, the father of David."]{.class-0} This is a portion of the Messianic line (see Matt. 1:1--6) from Pharez to David. Pharez was the firstborn son of Tamar, Judah's daughter-in-law who deceived him to have him raise up a son in the place of her dead husband, Judah's son, when Judah wouldn't give her Shelah his son to her when he became old enough (read Gen. 38).

The lineage of Christ was the whole reason for this "love story" and its seemingly mundane details. I mean, Ruth brought an ephah of barley back to her mother-in-law the first day she went out gleaning. Doesn't that make you want to shout and run the bases? Boaz sends back six measures of barley by Ruth to her mother-in-law. Well GLORY! Don't you feel the Spirit of the Lord dealing with you through that passage? No?

Well, why does the Lord put that stuff in His Book? The answer is found in the last five verses of Ruth. The Lord is interested in His Son, and anybody connected with His Son He gives attention to. The Lord will give you the lineages of Ishmael and Esau because they were related to Isaac and Jacob, and the Lord Jesus Christ came through the line of Isaac and Jacob.

Anything connected with God's Son goes in the Book. That is why the Holy Spirit will spend more time telling you about Sarah than He does about Caesar. Who was Sarah? Nobody important in men's eyes. She was just the wife of a Bedouin tramp. Who cares anything about Sarah? [The Lord does.]{.class-1} You see, her son, Isaac, is a type of God's Son, the Lord Jesus Christ.

That's what historians can't stand about that Book; that's why they are always trying to find historical inaccuracies in it. It spends time with seemingly insignificant characters because those characters are connected with [God's Son.]{.class-1} There was nothing special about Ruth, but because she was in the line of Christ, she gets a whole book about her; whereas, God [ignores]{.class-1} Socrates, Aristotle, Plato, Julius Caesar, Archimedes, Homer, Virgil, Pythagoras, Cleopatra, Mark Antony, Nefertiti, Hannibal, Alexander the Great, et al. Why? After all, those were the "movers and shakers" in the ancient world. But they had nothing to do with God's Son, so the Holy Spirit doesn't pay them the time of day.

Brethren, I figured out a long time ago that if I wanted God to pay attention to me, then I had better pay attention to His Son. So I started bragging about the Lord Jesus Christ. Let that be a lesson to you. Are you bragging about Him?

God is interested in His Son. Modern Christians think they are the center of the universe. "Oh, when Jesus was on the cross, He was thinking of [me."]{.class-1} You mean He just let the other ten billion or so people who have lived and died on this planet go to Hell because He was thinking of you?[ "I trow not"]{.class-0} (Luke 17:9).

This modern bunch keeps harping on "God loves me; God loves me; God loves me." Listen, people, if God loves you, it is because [you took His Son as your Saviour]{.class-1} (John 1:12). If you didn't take His Son, don't kid yourself about God loving you. John 3:36---["he that believeth not the Son shall not see life; but the wrath of God abideth on him."]{.class-0}

If the Lord loves unsaved people, why does He let them burn in Hell? Here is how God shows His "love" to the vast majority of the people on this earth (Matt. 7:13):

["Depart from me, ye cursed, into everlasting fire, prepared for the devil and his angels"]{.class-0} (Matt. 25:41).

["Ye serpents, ye generation of vipers, how can ye escape the damnation of hell?"]{.class-0} (Matt. 23:33).

["I never knew you: depart from me, ye that work iniquity"]{.class-0} (Matt. 7:23).

["Ye shall seek me, and shall die in your sins: whither I go, ye cannot come"]{.class-0} (John 8:21).

You understand that all that was said by the One who loved sinners enough to die for them, right? You understand it was said to sinners for whom He died, right? Well, they all went to Hell like a bullet despite that.

What was the problem? They didn't avail themselves of the love of God where He bestowed it. The love of God for sinners is found in [one Person]{.class-1}---Jesus Christ, God's Son (Rom. 8:39); it is found in [one place]{.class-1}---Calvary (Rom. 5:8; 1 John 4:10). Outside of that Person and that place, a sinner knows [nothing]{.class-1} of the love of God. God might show him mercy by giving him chance after chance to get saved; He might show the sinner goodness by providing him food, money, clothing, a place to live, etc.; He might show longsuffering to the Christ-rejector by not sending him to Hell immediately; but [love]{.class-1}? Don't kid yourself.

God gives all this attention to Ruth because she turns out to be the great-grandmother of David, and Christ is ["The Son of David"]{.class-0} (Matt. 22:42).

Now we have reached the end of the book of Ruth. The great historical lesson of the book is the line of the Messiah. The great doctrinal lesson is Christ's work of redemption for the sinner. But there is also a great spiritual lesson for the New Testament believer.

The moral of the story for the believer from the book of Ruth is whoever gives up this world for the sake of Christ and the Gospel (Mark 10:29; Luke 9:24, 17:33) will get it back "in spades." The great example in Scripture is Noah. He went into a box like a coffin, and when he exited it, he became heir of the whole world (Heb. 11:7). He gave up the whole world and got the whole thing back ---literally. The old song goes: "Take the world but give me Jesus." We give up the world for Jesus Christ.

A certain Professor Pinkevich of the USSR once said, "The world is getting too small for that Book. Either that Book must go, or the world must go!" Well, that's easy: [the world will go]{.class-1} (Matt. 24:35; 2 Pet. 3:10; Rev. 20:11). Back in the early 1900s when Halley's Comet was passing near the earth, someone said to Thomas Edison, "The world's going to end." He replied, "That's O.K.; we can do without it."

Folks, if you really want to "live," then give up living for this world and the things it offers, and live for Jesus Christ. Instead of trying to be a bigshot in this world and get a "crown" here, take up your cross now and follow the Lord. Why? Because He'll pay you back someday, and you will get far more than you ever gave up.

Orpah left Naomi and went back to her gods. She went back to the world. What happened to her? [Who knows and who cares.]{.class-1} She becomes a perfect blank. Ruth stuck with Naomi, and that wasn't the end of her. She got her name in a Book---[in both Testaments]{.class-1} (see Matt. 1:5)---that will be here when this present world is an ash heap. When heaven and earth have passed away, Ruth will still be around and remembered because:[ "For ever, O LORD, thy word is settled in heaven"]{.class-0} (Psa. 119:89).

Now isn't that something? If you give up this sin-cursed world to follow Jesus Christ and that Book, you get back [eternity.]{.class-1} You are somebody important after the world is [gone]{.class-1} (Rev. 1:6).

Ruth is a great [picture]{.class-1} of the statement made by the writer of Hebrews:

["For they that say such things declare plainly that they seek a country. And truly, if they had been mindful of that country from whence they came out, they might have had opportunity to have returned ]{.class-0}\[as in Ruth's case\][. But now they desire a better country, that is, an heavenly; wherefore God is not ashamed to be called their God: for he hath prepared for them a city"]{.class-0} (Heb. 11:14--16).

With Ruth, it was a [physical]{.class-1} country, with a [physical]{.class-1} city, but she is a great picture of those of us this side of Calvary---Jews and Gentiles (Eph. 2:11--19)---who have turned our backs on ["this present evil world"]{.class-0} (Gal. 1:4) to seek a heavenly country with a heavenly city. And when we did that, the Holy Spirit put us into Christ's spiritual line (Rom. 8:15--17) just as He put Ruth into Christ's physical line. And just as Ruth went through some hard times only to end up living "happily ever after," we as believers are called to suffer for our Saviour now so that we may reign with Him later (2 Tim. 2:12).

["For I reckon that the sufferings of this present time are not worthy to be compared with the glory which shall be revealed in us"]{.class-0} (Rom. 8:18).
